## Assistant (2026-04-25 09:22:45)

I’ll treat the TeX draft as the authority and the handoff as a proposal to audit against it. I’ll check whether the handoff’s claimed state is actually supported by the draft, then revise the agent split toward the highest-leverage unresolved obligations.

The draft does support the handoff’s broad architecture: Gate A/B are now framed as conditional package-construction layers, not as the final RH mechanism. The main discrepancy is strategic: the proposed agent split underweights auditing the Gate B hypotheses against the actual source model.

_Thought for 1m 50s_

Yes. The handoff is basically correct, but I would revise the agent plan. The current split is too downstream-heavy. It assumes Gate B’s hypotheses are stable enough to build on, while the TeX draft itself repeatedly marks Gate B as conditional on parity/source-frame/full-tower hypotheses and lists remaining theorem obligations for the actual corrected package.  

## Verdict

The best next move is a **two-lane attack**:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Lane 1: harden the conditional local package theorem}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Lane 2: build the package-to-transform bridge}
}
\]

I would not send most agents directly into global RH endgame yet. The local package is now much cleaner, but it is still not fully theoremized: Gate B is conditional, \(Z_j[M_A], Z_j[M_C]\) are not computed, and UV-026 quotient-gauge still needs the connection identities.

## What the handoff gets right

It correctly says Gate A should not be reopened as a live coefficient audit unless someone attacks the homogeneous scalar-grade convention or midpoint parity assumptions. The draft has Gate A closure as aggregate fixed-sector cancellation, not family-by-family \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}\)-gauge.

It correctly identifies Gate B as raw edge-divisibility:

\[
[z^7][\delta^1]\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}
(1-\Pi_{1,1})_{\rm mix}C_{\mathcal W}^{\rm raw}=0,
\]

not a post-edge quotient statement.

It correctly identifies the next concrete local target:

\[
R_7^{(A)}+\sum_{i=1}^7\omega_m(Z_{7-i}[M_A],A_i)=0,
\]

\[
R_7^{(C)}+\sum_{i=1}^7\omega_m(Z_{7-i}[M_C],A_i)=0.
\]

It also correctly warns that reduced package equality does not imply \(\Phi_K\)-visible hidden-state equality because

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}\mapsto A_7^{\mathfrak f}+\chi A_5^{\mathfrak f}
\]

can be \(\Phi_K\)-visible when \(v_5\neq 0\). 

## Main improvement

I would add a **Gate B hypothesis-hardening agent** before the downstream bridge agents. The draft says Gate B closes through order \(7\) only under:

\[
\text{all-subset midpoint parity},
\quad
\text{leading \(Y\)-middle parity},
\quad
\text{moving source-frame telescoping},
\quad
\text{affine boundary removal},
\quad
\text{full-tower-before-truncation}.
\]

Those should not just be accepted as labels. One agent should verify that these hypotheses are actual consequences of the corrected source model, not merely local formal conventions.

## Better agent split

### Agent 1 — Gate B hypothesis hardener

Use this agent to prevent building on a conditional theorem that later collapses.

```text
You are auditing whether Gate B’s hypotheses are genuinely supplied by the actual corrected source model, not merely assumed as formal source-frame conventions.

Work only from the latest paper draft.

Target:
Determine whether Corollary~\ref{cor:gate-b-raw-edge-divisibility-order-seven} is a theorem of the actual corrected package or still conditional on unproved source-model hypotheses.

Focus on:
- all-subset midpoint parity;
- symmetry of same-point subset coefficients;
- leading \(Y\)-middle parity;
- moving homogeneous source-frame telescoping;
- \(2\)-jet affine boundary removal;
- full Taylor source tower before ordinary-order truncation.

Tasks:
1. For each hypothesis, classify it as:
   (a) proved from the corrected block definitions,
   (b) proved only under an explicit convention,
   (c) asserted but not derived,
   (d) false or convention-dependent.
2. Check whether the tagged two-atom pre-whitening source block actually induces the homogeneous scalar-grade source tower used in Gate B.
3. Check whether affine removal is legitimate for the actual \(\mathfrak D_Q\)-scaled source variables, not just for a formal Taylor model.
4. Check whether full-tower-before-truncation creates any upper-boundary terms at ordinary order \(7\).
5. Produce exact LaTeX edits: either promote Gate B language from conditional to theorem, or sharpen the conditional wording.
```

This is probably the most important missing agent.

### Agent 2 — \(Z_j\)-connection table agent

The existing Agent 1 is good, but make it more precise and less “compute everything somehow.”

```text
You are computing the post-Gate-B pre-trivialization connection package.

Work only from the latest paper draft.

Target:
Compute or reduce the two identities
\[
R_7^{(A)}
+
\sum_{i=1}^{7}\omega_m(Z_{7-i}[M_A],A_i)=0,
\]
\[
R_7^{(C)}
+
\sum_{i=1}^{7}\omega_m(Z_{7-i}[M_C],A_i)=0,
\]
where
\[
M_A=\dot r_3r_2\dot r_4,\qquad
M_C=\dot r_3\dot r_2r_4.
\]

Rules:
- Use \(Z_j[M]\), not \(B_j[M]\).
- Work pre-trivialization.
- Do not use determinant scalarization as the quotient definition.
- Do not substitute old raw seven-family residuals for the corrected package table.
- Keep coefficient-normalized and derivative-normalized conventions separate; include binomial factors if derivative-normalized coefficients are used.

Tasks:
1. Extract the transported moving-line coefficients
\[
A_i=[\epsilon^i]\tau_{h\to m}A_5^{\mathfrak f}(h),\qquad 1\le i\le7.
\]
2. Define the finite table needed to compute
\[
Z_j[M_A],\quad Z_j[M_C],\qquad 0\le j\le6.
\]
3. Identify which entries are already supplied by the finite Fréchet coefficient calculus and which source tables are still missing.
4. Compute the connection sum symbolically as far as possible.
5. Determine whether the identity is:
   (a) exact by antisymmetry/parity,
   (b) exact by cancellation with \(R_7^{(A)},R_7^{(C)}\),
   (c) dependent on missing finite source tables,
   (d) likely false under current definitions.
6. Give exact LaTeX insertions.
```

### Agent 3 — UV-026 theorem object audit

This is distinct from Agent 2. It asks whether the package quotient-gauge theorem is even correctly formulated after connection cancellation.

```text
You are auditing the exact theorem object called UV-026 in the latest draft.

Work only from the paper draft.

Target:
Decide whether UV-026 should be stated as:
\[
B_7^{\mathfrak f}(C_{\mathcal W}^{\corr})
\in
\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m),
\]
or whether additional data from the moving edge table, source-bidegree projection, or representative-level trivialization must be included.

Tasks:
1. Trace the sequence:
raw cross-effect
\[
C_{\mathcal W}^{\rm raw}
\]
\(\to\) source-bidegree projection
\(\to\) amplitude normalization
\(\to\) fixed-sector extraction
\(\to\) midpoint trivialization
\(\to\) quotient extractor.
2. Verify that every operation is applied in the correct order.
3. Check whether the quotient class is independent of \(E_m,\ell_h\).
4. Identify any hidden dependence on the good patch \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m)\ne0\).
5. Check whether rank jumps \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}=0\) are treated correctly.
6. Produce exact LaTeX corrections to the UV-026 theorem statement and dependency ledger.
```

### Agent 4 — hidden-state / \(\Phi_K\)-visible bridge

The existing prompt is good, but it should demand a theorem-or-counterexample.

```text
You are attacking the package-to-transform hidden-state bridge.

Work only from the latest paper draft.

Target:
Determine whether quotient package equality implies equality of the first \(\Phi_K\)-visible corrected odd coefficient entering \(\Xi_\zeta^{(N)}\).

Central issue:
The reduced package forgets
\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}\mapsto A_7^{\mathfrak f}+\chi A_5^{\mathfrak f},
\]
but
\[
\Phi_K(A_5^{\mathfrak f})=2v_5.
\]
Therefore quotient equality does not automatically imply hidden-state equality.

Tasks:
1. Define the minimal state needed to determine the first \(\Phi_K\)-visible corrected odd coefficient.
2. Decide whether this state is determined by:
   (a) the quotient class,
   (b) the quotient class plus \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}\),
   (c) the diagnostic tuple \(\widetilde\Psi_{\min}\),
   (d) additional raw septic representative data.
3. Either prove state-locality modulo \(\ker\Phi_K\), or construct a formal countermodel showing why the current reduced data are insufficient.
4. Identify the precise extra theorem needed to make quotient closure feed the two-point and mixed four-point branches.
5. Give exact LaTeX insertions.
```

### Agent 5 — Bottleneck C / diagonal merger

Keep this, but make it more adversarial.

```text
You are attacking Bottleneck C: exceptional-divisor fiber selection.

Work only from the latest draft.

Target:
Determine whether the corrected two-atom package forces
\[
B(m,\kappa)
=
\widetilde\Psi_{\rm red}^{\corr}(m,\kappa,0)
\]
to be independent of \(\kappa\), or whether slope leakage is genuinely possible.

Rules:
- Do not use analyticity, swap-evenness, scalar normalization, or \(B(m,0)=\widehat\Psi(m)\) alone.
- Do not choose a septic representative such as \(v_7=0\) as if that solved the quotient problem.
- Work at the quotient-valued exceptional divisor.

Tasks:
1. Formalize the corrected two-atom collision functor.
2. Determine whether coincidence of the two atoms gives same reduced image germ.
3. Check whether atom-swap symmetry kills only odd \(\kappa\)-terms or also the first nontrivial quotient slope.
4. Construct a formal model with slope leakage unless the paper has an actual theorem excluding it.
5. State the exact missing diagonal merger theorem if not proved.
6. Give exact LaTeX edits.
```

### Agent 6 — mixed four-point carrier after Gate B

This deserves its own agent. It is different from the main two-point obstruction.

```text
You are auditing whether any surviving post-Gate-B residual can create an independent mixed four-point carrier.

Work only from the latest draft.

Accepted context:
Gate A is aggregate-closed.
Gate B is conditionally raw-edge-closed through ordinary order \(7\).
Raw placement-level vanishing is false.
The viable theorem is quotient-line/edge compatibility, not termwise vanishing.

Target:
Determine whether, after Gate B and connection correction, non-\((1,1)\) corrected source terms can create a mixed four-point scalar-exit mechanism independent of the existing two-point/package quotient obstruction.

Tasks:
1. Identify exactly where the mixed four-point branch consumes local package data.
2. Check whether it sees only the quotient class or also hidden \(\Phi_K\)-visible representative data.
3. Determine whether \(M_A,M_C\) connection residuals, if nonzero, would be absorbed by the same scalar-exit mechanism or would generate a new carrier.
4. Separate:
   - pre-\(\Phi_K\) package quotient data;
   - \(\Phi_K\)-visible hidden state;
   - mixed four-point scalar-exit data.
5. Produce either a no-new-carrier theorem or a precise obstruction.
6. Give exact LaTeX insertions.
```

### Agent 7 — finite-core lower model

The current prompt is right but too vague. Make it theorem-shaped.

```text
You are attacking the finite-core lower-model gap.

Work only from the latest draft.

Target:
Replace the current asymptotic pair-like exclusion with a theorem covering non-pair-like finite cores.

Tasks:
1. Define the first surviving corrected odd finite-core coefficient
\[
\Xi_{\core}^{(N)}
\]
in the same normalization used by the zeta-side \(N\)-point formula.
2. Determine whether the current package data control \(\Xi_{\core}^{(N)}\) at size comparable to
\[
(x/B_\zeta)S.
\]
3. If not, identify the missing transfer theorem from local package coefficients to finite-core odd coefficients.
4. Separate pair-like cores from genuinely non-pair-like finite cores.
5. Determine whether a one-sided lower law is plausible from positivity of the \(N\)-point kernel, or whether cancellation among finite-core constituents remains possible.
6. Give exact LaTeX edits distinguishing proved pair-like exclusion from open finite-core closure.
```

### Agent 8 — adversarial consistency / no-go model builder

This is valuable because many false RH attempts die from formal implications that are not actually valid.

```text
You are the adversarial model-checking agent.

Work only from the latest draft.

Target:
Find formal countermodels to any claimed implication that is not forced by the stated hypotheses.

Test the following implications:
1. Gate B hypotheses imply actual corrected source-package edge divisibility.
2. Quotient package equality implies \(\Phi_K\)-visible hidden-state equality.
3. Analyticity plus swap-evenness implies \(\kappa\)-independence of the exceptional-divisor trace.
4. Local \(Z_j\)-connection cancellation implies global package-to-transform closure.
5. Pair-like asymptotic exclusion implies finite-core exclusion.
6. Good-patch determinant scalarization extends across \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}=0\).

For each implication:
- either prove it from draft assumptions;
- or give a small formal model showing it fails;
- or state the missing hypothesis precisely.

Output:
A table of “valid / invalid / unknown” implications and exact LaTeX warnings or theorem-obligation remarks.
```

## Recommended deployment

If you have 4 agents, use: **1, 2, 4, 8**.

If you have 6 agents, use: **1, 2, 3, 4, 5, 8**.

If you have 8 agents, use all of the above.

The most important change is Agent 1. Without that, everyone downstream may be building on a conditional Gate B closure whose hypotheses have not yet been proven to match the actual corrected source model.

## Assistant (2026-04-25 09:26:11)

_Thought for a couple of seconds_

Below is a bird’s-eye summary to send to all agents.

---

# Bird’s-Eye View: Current RH Proof Strategy and Agent Orientation

We are working from the **latest paper draft only**. The proof is not complete. The current situation is that the local corrected-package architecture has become much sharper, but the global bridge to an RH contradiction is still open.

The old local coefficient-audit layer is no longer the main obstruction. The frontier has moved to:

\[
\boxed{
\text{post-Gate-B corrected package completion}
}
\]

and

\[
\boxed{
\text{package-to-transform / hidden-state / finite-core bridge}.
}
\]

Agents should not treat the draft as a completed RH proof. The current endgame should be read as an **asymptotic pair-like branch exclusion**, not yet as a full proof of RH.

---

## 1. Current local proof architecture

The local corrected-package construction is organized around two gates.

---

## Gate A: leading homogeneous cubic audit

Gate A concerns the leading homogeneous cubic non-\((1,1)\) sector at ordinary order \(7\).

The relevant families are:

\[
L_1YR_1,\qquad L_2YR_0,\qquad L_0YR_2,
\]

\[
L_2N_0R_1,\qquad L_1N_0R_2,
\]

\[
L_3N_0R_0,\qquad L_0N_0R_3.
\]

Current status:

\[
\boxed{
F_1^{\mathrm{lead\ cubic}}=0.
}
\]

This is accepted as **aggregate fixed-sector cancellation**, not termwise vanishing and not family-by-family determinant-gauge cancellation.

Mechanism:

1. The \(Y\)-slot families are absent at the relevant homogeneous scalar grade.
2. The pair

\[
L_2N_0R_1+L_1N_0R_2
\]

cancels in aggregate in \(\mathfrak f\).

3. The pair

\[
L_3N_0R_0+L_0N_0R_3
\]

also cancels in aggregate, assuming the relevant midpoint/third-Fréchet parity.

Do **not** reopen Gate A unless attacking one of its actual hypotheses, such as homogeneous scalar-grade convention, midpoint parity, transpose parity, or the asserted aggregate cancellation mechanism.

---

## Gate B: raw edge-divisibility / first-collision theorem

Gate B is the raw edge-divisibility statement for the projected corrected-whitening cross-effect.

The raw object is:

\[
C_{\mathcal W}^{\raw}
=
\mathcal W(\mathcal B_2)
-\mathcal W(\mathcal B_1(a_1,h_1))
-\mathcal W(\mathcal B_1(a_2,h_2))
+\mathcal W(\mathcal B_0),
\]

where

\[
\mathcal W(G_-,N,G_+)=G_-^{-1/2}NG_+^{-1/2}.
\]

The relevant projected raw edge test is:

\[
[z^7][\delta^1]\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}
(1-\Pi_{1,1})_{\rm mix}C_{\mathcal W}^{\raw}=0.
\]

Equivalently, through ordinary order \(7\),

\[
(1-\Pi_{1,1})_{\rm mix}C_{\mathcal W}^{\raw}
=
O(a_1\delta^2)
\]

after fixed-sector projection.

Current status:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate B is conditionally closed through ordinary order }7.
}
\]

The closure depends on the following mechanisms:

\[
\text{Gate A aggregate closure}
\]

\[
+\quad
\text{odd total-grade subset-complement cancellation}
\]

\[
+\quad
\text{moving source-frame telescoping}
\]

\[
+\quad
\text{\(2\)-jet affine-boundary removal}.
\]

This is a major improvement, but agents must keep the word **conditionally** in mind. Gate B is only as strong as the hypotheses feeding it.

The important Gate B hypotheses are:

\[
\text{all-subset midpoint parity},
\]

\[
\text{leading \(Y\)-middle parity},
\]

\[
\text{moving source-frame telescoping},
\]

\[
\text{\(2\)-jet affine-boundary removal},
\]

\[
\text{full-tower-before-truncation}.
\]

A valid attack on Gate B should target these hypotheses directly. Do not simply reopen old \(d\ge4\) transfer-partition lists or lower-shadow tables unless showing that one of these hypotheses fails.

---

# 2. Critical guardrails

## 2.1 Raw placement-level vanishing is false

Individual transfer placements can be nonzero in fixed sector. This is not a contradiction.

The proof uses labelled aggregate cancellation, especially subset-complement symmetry:

\[
I\longleftrightarrow J\setminus I,
\]

together with midpoint parity, source symmetry, and transpose-invariance of \(\pi_{\mathfrak f}\).

A nonzero unsymmetrized subchannel is not a counterexample unless it survives the labelled aggregate sum.

---

## 2.2 Determinant scalarization is not the quotient definition

The quotient line is:

\[
\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m).
\]

If

\[
A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m)=u_5I+v_5S,
\qquad
C=uI+vS,
\]

then

\[
uv_5-u_5v
\]

is only a good-patch coordinate for the quotient.

The actual quotient object is:

\[
[C]\in \mathfrak f_m/\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m).
\]

If

\[
A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m)=0,
\]

the determinant coordinate is unavailable. Such tests are quotient-inconclusive, not automatically zero or false.

---

## 2.3 Do not use post-edge quotient compatibility to prove Gate B

Gate B must be proved at the raw edge level:

\[
[z^7][\delta^1]\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}
(1-\Pi_{1,1})_{\rm mix}C_{\mathcal W}^{\raw}=0.
\]

Do **not** first state or prove it as:

\[
Q_{7,m}^q(C)=Q_{7,m}^q(\Pi_{1,1}C).
\]

That kind of quotient compatibility only makes sense after raw edge-divisibility gives a holomorphic normalized package.

---

## 2.4 Lower shadows are not simply discarded

Grades

\[
0,2,4
\]

are not blanket “baseline data.” They may appear in the moving Taylor source tower.

The intended mechanism is:

1. amplitude terms of total grade \(7\) cancel by odd total-grade subset-complement cancellation;
2. source-motion lower terms cancel by moving source-frame telescoping;
3. the affine grade \(-1\) boundary is removed by \(2\)-jet normalization.

Do not claim that lower shadows are simply absorbed unless proving that for a specific object.

---

## 2.5 \(Z_j[M]\), not \(B_j[M]\), enters the connection formula

After Gate B, the relevant connection formula uses the **pre-trivialization edge table**:

\[
Z_j[M].
\]

The connection identity is:

\[
q_{\mathrm{conn},7}[M]
=
\sum_{i=1}^{7}\omega_m(Z_{7-i}[M],A_i).
\]

Post-trivialization coefficients

\[
B_j[M]
\]

already include the moving-line correction. Using \(B_j[M]\) inside the pre-trivialization connection sum double-counts the connection.

Also distinguish:

\[
Z_j[M](z)\in\mathfrak f_m[z]_{\le7}
\]

from

\[
Z_j[M]=[z^7]Z_j[M](z)\in\mathfrak f_m.
\]

---

# 3. Immediate local frontier

After Gate B, the next concrete local target is no longer another raw seven-family audit. It is the post-Gate-B connection package.

The residual source monomials are:

\[
M_A=\dot r_3r_2\dot r_4,
\qquad
M_C=\dot r_3\dot r_2r_4.
\]

The target identities are:

\[
R_7^{(A)}
+
\sum_{i=1}^{7}\omega_m(Z_{7-i}[M_A],A_i)=0,
\]

\[
R_7^{(C)}
+
\sum_{i=1}^{7}\omega_m(Z_{7-i}[M_C],A_i)=0.
\]

Here

\[
A_i=[\epsilon^i]\tau_{h\to m}A_5^{\mathfrak f}(h),
\qquad
1\le i\le7,
\]

with

\[
\epsilon=h-m.
\]

The missing concrete table is:

\[
Z_j[M_A],
\qquad
Z_j[M_C],
\qquad
0\le j\le6.
\]

The next local theorem should either compute these tables or prove enough structural cancellation to close the two identities.

---

# 4. Global frontier

Even if the \(Z_j\)-connection package closes, the proof is still not done.

The major downstream missing theorem is the package-to-transform bridge.

The key issue is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{quotient package equality does not automatically imply hidden-state equality.}
}
\]

The reduced package forgets the representative freedom:

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}
\longmapsto
A_7^{\mathfrak f}+\chi A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
\]

But

\[
\Phi_K(A_5^{\mathfrak f})=2v_5.
\]

Therefore this forgotten direction can be \(\Phi_K\)-visible unless additional structure kills it.

The missing theorem is not merely “quotient-septic closure.” It is something closer to:

\[
\boxed{
\text{state-locality modulo }\ker\Phi_K.
}
\]

or an equivalent theorem showing that the first \(\Phi_K\)-visible corrected odd coefficient entering the \(N\)-point transform is determined by the corrected local package data.

---

# 5. Bottleneck C: exceptional-divisor fiber selection

Another major open issue is the exceptional-divisor trace:

\[
B(m,\kappa)
=
\widetilde\Psi^{\corr}_{\mathrm{red}}(m,\kappa,0).
\]

Formal properties alone do not force

\[
\partial_\kappa B=0.
\]

In particular, the following are insufficient by themselves:

\[
\text{analyticity},
\qquad
\text{swap-evenness},
\qquad
\text{fixed codomain},
\qquad
\text{scalar normalization},
\qquad
B(m,0)=\widehat\Psi(m).
\]

A real proof must supply one of:

\[
\text{diagonal merger},
\]

\[
\text{same-reduced-image theorem},
\]

\[
\text{collision functoriality of the corrected two-atom package}.
\]

Do not solve this by choosing a diagnostic septic representative such as \(v_7=0\) or \(u_7=0\). The C-side object has already quotiented raw septic representative freedom away.

---

# 6. Mixed four-point issue

There is also a separate mixed four-point question.

Even if Gate B closes locally, we still need to know whether a surviving post-Gate-B or connection-level residual could create an independent mixed four-point carrier.

The core question is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Does the mixed four-point branch see only quotient package data,}
}
\]

or

\[
\boxed{
\text{does it see hidden \(\Phi_K\)-visible representative data?}
}
\]

This must be separated from the two-point obstruction. The mixed four-point scalar-exit mechanism may or may not absorb the same residuals.

---

# 7. Finite-core gap

The current contradiction handles the pair-like branch asymptotically. It does not yet rule out all non-pair-like finite-core behavior.

A remaining possible failure mode is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{the first odd coefficient cancels, but a genuine corrected anomaly survives at a higher odd order.}
}
\]

The proof needs a finite-core lower-model transfer theorem.

Possible target:

\[
\Xi_{\core}^{(N)}
\]

or a one-sided lower law for the first surviving odd finite-core coefficient, fed into the positive-kernel \(N\)-point formula.

Without this, the final theorem should remain phrased as an asymptotic pair-like exclusion, not a full RH proof.

---

# 8. Recommended agent priorities

The highest-value agent split is:

## Agent 1: Gate B hypothesis hardener

Check whether the hypotheses behind Gate B are actually proved from the corrected source model.

Focus:

\[
\text{all-subset midpoint parity},
\]

\[
\text{leading \(Y\)-middle parity},
\]

\[
\text{moving source-frame telescoping},
\]

\[
\text{\(2\)-jet affine-boundary removal},
\]

\[
\text{full-tower-before-truncation}.
\]

Classify each as proved, convention-dependent, asserted, or false.

This is the most important defensive audit.

---

## Agent 2: \(Z_j\)-connection table

Compute or reduce:

\[
Z_j[M_A],
\quad
Z_j[M_C],
\quad
0\le j\le6,
\]

and verify:

\[
R_7^{(A)}
+
\sum_{i=1}^{7}\omega_m(Z_{7-i}[M_A],A_i)=0,
\]

\[
R_7^{(C)}
+
\sum_{i=1}^{7}\omega_m(Z_{7-i}[M_C],A_i)=0.
\]

Must use \(Z_j[M]\), not \(B_j[M]\).

---

## Agent 3: UV-026 theorem-object audit

Check whether the UV-026 quotient statement is formulated at the right level:

\[
\mathfrak f_m/\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m).
\]

Audit the order of operations:

\[
\text{raw cross-effect}
\to
\text{source-bidegree projection}
\to
\text{amplitude normalization}
\to
\text{fixed-sector extraction}
\to
\text{midpoint trivialization}
\to
\text{quotient extractor}.
\]

Check good-patch dependence and rank jumps at \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}=0\).

---

## Agent 4: package-to-transform hidden-state bridge

Determine whether quotient package equality implies equality of the first \(\Phi_K\)-visible corrected odd coefficient.

Central obstruction:

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}
\mapsto
A_7^{\mathfrak f}+\chi A_5^{\mathfrak f},
\qquad
\Phi_K(A_5^{\mathfrak f})=2v_5.
\]

Either prove state-locality modulo \(\ker\Phi_K\), or construct a formal countermodel showing the reduced data are insufficient.

---

## Agent 5: Bottleneck C / diagonal merger

Attack:

\[
B(m,\kappa)
=
\widetilde\Psi^{\corr}_{\mathrm{red}}(m,\kappa,0).
\]

Determine whether actual corrected-package collision functoriality forces:

\[
\partial_\kappa B=0.
\]

Do not rely only on analyticity or symmetry.

---

## Agent 6: mixed four-point carrier

Determine whether non-\((1,1)\) corrected source terms can create an independent mixed four-point carrier after Gate B and connection correction.

Separate:

\[
\text{package quotient data},
\]

\[
\Phi_K\text{-visible hidden state},
\]

\[
\text{mixed four-point scalar-exit data}.
\]

---

## Agent 7: finite-core lower model

Attack the non-pair-like finite-core gap.

Determine whether the local corrected package controls:

\[
\Xi_{\core}^{(N)}
\]

or whether a higher odd finite-core anomaly can survive after pair-like exclusion.

---

## Agent 8: adversarial no-go model builder

Try to construct formal countermodels to any implication that is not actually forced by the draft.

Test especially:

1. Gate B hypotheses \(\Rightarrow\) actual corrected source-package edge divisibility.
2. Quotient package equality \(\Rightarrow\) \(\Phi_K\)-visible hidden-state equality.
3. Analyticity plus swap-evenness \(\Rightarrow\) \(\kappa\)-independence.
4. Local connection cancellation \(\Rightarrow\) global transform closure.
5. Pair-like asymptotic exclusion \(\Rightarrow\) finite-core exclusion.
6. Good-patch determinant scalarization \(\Rightarrow\) global quotient statement.

This agent should be adversarial. Their output should be a table of:

\[
\text{valid / invalid / unknown}
\]

for each implication.

## 1. Insert the status remark now

This part is high-value and stable:

```latex
\begin{remark}[Status of the \(M_A,M_C\) connection identities]
\label{rem:status-ma-mc-connection-identities}
The identities
\[
R_7^{(A)}
+
\sum_{i=1}^{7}\omega_m(Z_{7-i}[M_A],A_i)=0,
\]
and
\[
R_7^{(C)}
+
\sum_{i=1}^{7}\omega_m(Z_{7-i}[M_C],A_i)=0
\]
are not proved in the present draft by parity alone.  The available
antisymmetry and subset-complement mechanisms are Gate~B edge mechanisms;
they do not by themselves evaluate the post-Gate-B moving-line connection
sum.

The viable closure mechanism is cancellation between the direct corrected
order-\(7\) residuals \(R_7^{(A)},R_7^{(C)}\) and the connection
contributions computed from the lower pre-trivialization table
\(Z_j[M_A],Z_j[M_C]\).  Therefore the current status is:
\[
\boxed{
\text{connection closure depends on the missing finite }Z_j\text{-tables
and corrected }R_7\text{-tables.}
}
\]
In particular, \(R_7^{(A)}\) and \(R_7^{(C)}\) must be corrected-package
residuals in the same pre-\(\Phi_K\), pre-determinant convention.  Old raw
seven-family residuals must not be substituted for these quantities.
\end{remark}
```

This should go after `rem:next-package-table-connection-correction`.

## 2. Insert the reduction remark, but fix the derivative-normalization wording

Agent 2’s coefficient-normalized formula is good:

\[
q_{\mathrm{conn},7}[M_X]
=
\sum_{i=1}^{7}
\left(
u_{7-i}^{X}\beta_i-\alpha_i v_{7-i}^{X}
\right).
\]

But the derivative-normalized version needs to be phrased carefully. The binomial expression gives the **seventh derivative normalization**, not the coefficient-normalized \([ \epsilon^7]\) coefficient unless divided by \(7!\).

Use this version:

```latex
\begin{remark}[Connection table reduction for the residual monomials]
\label{rem:connection-table-reduction-residual-monomials}
The post-Gate-B connection identities for
\[
M_A=\dot r_3r_2\dot r_4,
\qquad
M_C=\dot r_3\dot r_2r_4
\]
are finite pre-trivialization table identities.  They are not raw
seven-family identities and they must not be tested using the
post-trivialization coefficients \(B_j[M]\).

Write
\[
\epsilon=h-m,
\qquad
A_h^m:=\tau_{h\to m}A_5^{\mathfrak f}(h)
       =\sum_{i\ge0}\epsilon^iA_i,
\]
so that
\[
A_i=[\epsilon^i]\tau_{h\to m}A_5^{\mathfrak f}(h),
\qquad 1\le i\le7.
\]
If
\[
A_i=\alpha_i I+\beta_iS,
\]
and
\[
Z_j[M_X]=u_j^X I+v_j^X S,
\qquad X\in\{A,C\},
\]
then the coefficient-normalized connection contribution is
\[
q_{\mathrm{conn},7}[M_X]
=
\sum_{i=1}^{7}
\omega_m(Z_{7-i}[M_X],A_i)
=
\sum_{i=1}^{7}
\left(
u_{7-i}^X\beta_i-\alpha_i v_{7-i}^X
\right).
\]
Thus the two required scalar identities are
\[
R_7^{(A)}
+
\sum_{i=1}^{7}
\left(
u_{7-i}^A\beta_i-\alpha_i v_{7-i}^A
\right)
=0,
\]
and
\[
R_7^{(C)}
+
\sum_{i=1}^{7}
\left(
u_{7-i}^C\beta_i-\alpha_i v_{7-i}^C
\right)
=0.
\]

If instead the table uses derivative-normalized coefficients
\[
\mathsf A_i
=
\partial_\epsilon^i
\left(\tau_{m+\epsilon\to m}A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m+\epsilon)\right)
\big|_{\epsilon=0},
\qquad
\mathsf Z_j[M]
=
\partial_\epsilon^j Z[M](m+\epsilon)\big|_{\epsilon=0},
\]
then
\[
A_i=\frac{\mathsf A_i}{i!},
\qquad
Z_j[M]=\frac{\mathsf Z_j[M]}{j!}.
\]
Consequently the coefficient-normalized order-\(7\) term is
\[
q_{\mathrm{conn},7}[M_X]
=
\frac{1}{7!}
\sum_{i=1}^{7}
\binom{7}{i}
\omega_m(\mathsf Z_{7-i}[M_X],\mathsf A_i).
\]
Equivalently, after applying \(\partial_\epsilon^7|_{\epsilon=0}\) to the
whole order-\(7\) identity, the derivative-normalized connection term is
\[
\sum_{i=1}^{7}
\binom{7}{i}
\omega_m(\mathsf Z_{7-i}[M_X],\mathsf A_i).
\]
The coefficient-normalized and derivative-normalized conventions must not be
mixed.
\end{remark}
```

## 3. Insert the finite \(Z_j\)-table contract, but mark it as a contract, not a theorem

This is also worth adding now, because it tells future agents exactly what table must be computed. I would slightly soften the “contract” language so it does not look like the table exists yet.

```latex
\begin{definition}[Finite \(Z_j\)-table target for \(M_A\) and \(M_C\)]
\label{def:finite-zj-table-target-ma-mc}
For \(X\in\{A,C\}\), set
\[
M_A=\dot r_3r_2\dot r_4,
\qquad
M_C=\dot r_3\dot r_2r_4.
\]
The required pre-trivialization table entries are
\[
Z_j[M_X]
=
-[z^7][\epsilon^j\delta^2M_X]\,
a_1^{-1}\tau_{h\to m}
\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}
(1-\Pi_{1,1})_{\mathrm{mix}}C_{\mathcal W}^{\mathrm{raw}},
\qquad
0\le j\le6.
\]
Equivalently, after Gate~B edge divisibility has supplied the holomorphic
edge-normalized package,
\[
Z_j[M_X]
=
[z^7][\epsilon^jM_X]\,
\tau_{h\to m}\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}
\widehat C_{\mathcal W}^{\mathrm{amp}}.
\]

To compute these entries from the finite Fr\'echet/Sylvester calculus, one
must keep the labelled source slots through the computation.  For the
labelled source triple \(J=(3,2,4)\), the \(N_0\)-middle contribution has
the schematic contract
\[
\sum_{I\subseteq J}
\sum_{\alpha+\beta+\gamma=7}
\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}
\left(
L^-_{I,\alpha}N^{(0)}_{\beta}
R^+_{J\setminus I,\gamma}
\right),
\]
and the \(Y\)-middle contribution has the schematic contract
\[
\sum_{m_0\in J}
\sum_{I\subseteq J\setminus\{m_0\}}
\sum_{\alpha+\beta+\gamma=7}
\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}
\left(
L^-_{I,\alpha}Y_{m_0,\beta}
R^+_{J\setminus(I\cup\{m_0\}),\gamma}
\right).
\]
The operator
\[
-[\epsilon^j\delta^2M_X]\,a_1^{-1}\tau_{h\to m}
(1-\Pi_{1,1})_{\mathrm{mix}}
\]
is then applied to the labelled aggregate before determinant scalarization
and before midpoint trivialization.

The current finite Fr\'echet recurrences supply the formal \(L\)- and
\(R\)-coefficient infrastructure and the baseline \(N^{(0)}\)-coefficient
infrastructure.  What remains to be supplied for this table is the actual
\(\delta^2\)-edge source expansion for \(M_A,M_C\), including the
\(\epsilon^j\)-coefficients for \(0\le j\le6\), the corresponding
\(Y\)-middle source-linear table in the same normalization, and the
transported moving-line coefficients \(A_i\) through \(i=7\).
\end{definition}
```

I changed “contract” to “target” and “has the contract” to “has the schematic contract” because the exact source-labelling/sign conventions may still be probed.

## 4. Yes, fix the stale-reference note

```latex
Here \(Z_j[M]\) denotes the pre-trivialization edge coefficient of
Definition~\ref{def:lower-moving-package-coefficients}
(equivalently Definition~\ref{def:pre-trivialization-edge-table-after-gate-b});
it is not the post-trivialization coefficient \(B_j[M]\).
```

# Edit 1 — UV-026: good-patch quotient object

Agent 3 has a real correction: UV-026 can be stated as

\[
B_7^{\mathfrak f}(C_{\mathcal W}^{\corr})
\in
\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m),
\]

but only if \(C_{\mathcal W}^{\corr}\) is already the projected, amplitude-normalized, fixed-sector, midpoint-trivialized package representative. Also, this is a good-patch statement; rank jumps are not covered. 

Insert after `rem:naming-convention-uv026`, or replace any bare UV-026 theorem with:

```latex
\begin{theorem}[Corrected UV-026 quotient-gauge theorem on the quintic-good patch]
\label{thm:uv026-corrected-package-quotient-gauge}
Work on a good patch on which
\[
A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m)\ne0.
\]
Assume that Gate~B raw edge-divisibility has supplied the holomorphic
edge-normalized object
\[
\widehat C_{\mathcal W}^{\mathrm{amp}}
=
-a_1^{-1}\delta^{-2}
(1-\Pi_{1,1})_{\mathrm{mix}}
C_{\mathcal W}^{\mathrm{raw}}
\]
through ordinary order \(7\) on the collision chart.  Let
\(C_{\mathcal W}^{\corr}\) denote the fixed-target fixed-sector package
representative obtained from this object by
\[
C_{\mathcal W}^{\corr}
=
B_{\mathrm{pkg}}^{\mathfrak f}(h;z)
=
\sum_{n=0}^{7}
z^n\operatorname{Triv}_{h\to m} Z_n(h),
\]
where
\[
\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}[z^{\le7}]
\widehat C_{\mathcal W}^{\mathrm{amp}}(h)
=
\sum_{n=0}^{7}z^n Z_n(h).
\]
Then the corrected UV-026 statement is
\[
B_7^{\mathfrak f}(C_{\mathcal W}^{\corr})
:=
[z^7]B_{\mathrm{pkg}}^{\mathfrak f}(m;z)
\in
\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m),
\]
equivalently
\[
Q_{7,m}^q(C_{\mathcal W}^{\corr})
=
0
\quad\text{in}\quad
\mathfrak f_m/\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m).
\]
\end{theorem}
```

Then add immediately after:

```latex
\begin{remark}[UV-026 theorem object versus proof data]
\label{rem:uv026-object-versus-proof-data}
The theorem object in UV-026 is the quotient class
\[
Q_{7,m}^q(C_{\mathcal W}^{\corr})
\in
\mathfrak f_m/\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m).
\]
The source-bidegree projection, amplitude normalization, fixed-sector
extraction, and midpoint trivialization are part of the definition of
\(C_{\mathcal W}^{\corr}\).  They should not be applied again to
\(C_{\mathcal W}^{\corr}\).

The pre-trivialization edge table \(Z_j[M]\) is not extra output data in the
UV-026 statement.  It is proof data needed to verify the connection
cancellation for
\[
M_A=\dot r_3r_2\dot r_4,
\qquad
M_C=\dot r_3\dot r_2r_4.
\]
The required proof identities are
\[
R_7^{(A)}
+
\sum_{i=1}^{7}\omega_m(Z_{7-i}[M_A],A_i)=0,
\]
and
\[
R_7^{(C)}
+
\sum_{i=1}^{7}\omega_m(Z_{7-i}[M_C],A_i)=0.
\]
Replacing \(Z_j[M]\) by post-trivialization \(B_j[M]\) inside this connection
sum double-counts the moving-line correction.
\end{remark}
```

Add the rank-jump warning after `rem:good-patch-convention-quotient-coordinate`:

```latex
\begin{remark}[Rank-jump locus is not covered by the good-patch quotient theorem]
\label{rem:rank-jump-locus-not-covered-uv026}
The corrected UV-026 theorem is a good-patch statement.  The
representative-level midpoint trivialization uses a nonzero quintic line
\[
A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m)\ne0
\]
to identify the quotient
\[
\mathfrak f_m/\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m).
\]
On the rank-jump locus
\[
A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m)=0,
\]
the determinant coordinate is unavailable.  Moreover, the literal inclusion
\[
B_7^{\mathfrak f}(C_{\mathcal W}^{\corr})
\in
\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m)
\]
would reduce to the stronger assertion
\[
B_7^{\mathfrak f}(C_{\mathcal W}^{\corr})=0.
\]
That zero statement is not supplied by the good-patch quotient theorem.
Rank-jump cases therefore require a separate extension, blow-up, or limiting
quotient-line theorem.
\end{remark}
```

# Edit 2 — \(\Phi_K\)-visible hidden-state non-descent

This is the most important downstream correction from Agent 4. Quotient closure does **not** imply transform-visible closure, because the quotient forgets

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}\mapsto A_7^{\mathfrak f}+\chi A_5^{\mathfrak f},
\]

while

\[
\Phi_K(A_5^{\mathfrak f})=2v_5.
\]

This is a formal obstruction, not merely a missing computation. 

Insert after `rem:reduced-package-equality-not-hidden-state-equality`:

```latex
\begin{definition}[\(\Phi_K\)-visible septic state]
\label{def:phik-visible-septic-state}
On the fixed target fiber
\[
\mathfrak f_m=\mathbf C I\oplus \mathbf C S,
\]
write
\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}=u_7I+v_7S.
\]
The \(\Phi_K\)-visible septic state is the class
\[
[A_7^{\mathfrak f}]_{\Phi}:=
A_7^{\mathfrak f}\bmod \ker(\Phi_K|_{\mathfrak f_m}),
\]
equivalently the scalar
\[
\phi_7:=\Phi_K(A_7^{\mathfrak f})=2v_7.
\]
If the \(c\)-normalized package is being used, the normalized visible septic
state is
\[
\theta_7:=\frac{\phi_7}{c}=\frac{2v_7}{c}.
\]
\end{definition}

\begin{proposition}[Formal non-descent of the \(\Phi_K\)-visible septic state]
\label{prop:formal-non-descent-phik-visible-septic-state}
On the generic locus \(v_5\neq0\), the quotient class
\[
[A_7^{\mathfrak f}]
\in
\mathfrak f_m/\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m)
\]
does not determine the \(\Phi_K\)-visible septic state
\[
[A_7^{\mathfrak f}]_{\Phi}
\in
\mathfrak f_m/\ker(\Phi_K|_{\mathfrak f_m}).
\]
In particular, quotient package equality does not imply equality of the first
\(\Phi_K\)-visible corrected odd coefficient.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Write
\[
A_5^{\mathfrak f}=u_5I+v_5S,
\qquad
A_7^{\mathfrak f}=u_7I+v_7S.
\]
The quotient identifies
\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}
\sim
A_7^{\mathfrak f}+\chi A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
\]
However
\[
\Phi_K(A_7^{\mathfrak f}+\chi A_5^{\mathfrak f})
-
\Phi_K(A_7^{\mathfrak f})
=
\chi\Phi_K(A_5^{\mathfrak f})
=
2\chi v_5.
\]
Thus, if \(v_5\neq0\), the forgotten quotient direction is visible to
\(\Phi_K\).

Equivalently, take the formal model
\[
A_5^{\mathfrak f}=S,
\qquad
A_7^{\mathfrak f,\chi}=\chi S.
\]
Then
\[
[A_7^{\mathfrak f,\chi}]=0
\quad\text{in}\quad
\mathfrak f_m/\mathbf C S
\]
for every \(\chi\), but
\[
\Phi_K(A_7^{\mathfrak f,\chi})=2\chi.
\]
Hence the reduced quotient package does not determine the
\(\Phi_K\)-visible septic state.
\end{proof}
```

Then add near downstream obligations:

```latex
\begin{remark}[Needed package-to-transform state-locality theorem]
\label{rem:needed-package-to-transform-state-locality-theorem}
The theorem needed downstream is not merely quotient-septic closure.  It must
identify the first transform-visible corrected odd coefficient as a function
of the reduced corrected package.

A sufficient form is the following state-locality statement.  If two actual
corrected packages \(P,P'\) have the same reduced package datum, then
\[
A_{7,\Xi}^{\mathfrak f}(P')-A_{7,\Xi}^{\mathfrak f}(P)
\in
\ker\Phi_K.
\]
Equivalently, there should exist a package-local functional
\[
\Theta_{\Phi,7}
\]
such that
\[
\Phi_K\!\left(A_{7,\Xi}^{\mathfrak f}(P)\right)
=
\Theta_{\Phi,7}\!\left(\widehat\Psi_{\mathrm{red}}(P)\right).
\]
Only such a theorem allows the corrected quotient package to feed the
two-point and mixed four-point transform branches.
\end{remark}
```

---

# Edit 3 — Bottleneck C: \(\kappa\)-slope leakage

Agent 5 gives a real no-go: atom-swap symmetry does **not** impose \(\kappa\mapsto-\kappa\) on the exceptional divisor, so formal symmetry does not kill \(\partial_\kappa B\). The paper should contain this. 

Insert after the current C-side warning, probably after `rem:formal-c-properties-do-not-rule-out-slope-leakage`:

```latex
\begin{remark}[Atom swap does not impose \(\kappa\mapsto-\kappa\) on the exceptional divisor]
\label{rem:atom-swap-does-not-kill-kappa-slope}
In the collision chart
\[
h_1=m-\frac{\delta}{2},
\qquad
h_2=m+\frac{\delta}{2},
\qquad
a_2=-a_1(1+\kappa\delta),
\]
interchanging the two labelled atoms gives
\[
\delta\longmapsto-\delta,
\qquad
a_1\longmapsto -a_1(1+\kappa\delta),
\qquad
\kappa\longmapsto \frac{\kappa}{1+\kappa\delta}.
\]
Hence on the exceptional divisor \(\delta=0\), the slope coordinate is fixed:
\[
\kappa\longmapsto\kappa.
\]
Therefore atom-swap symmetry does not force the exceptional trace
\[
B(m,\kappa)
\]
to be even in \(\kappa\), and in particular it does not force
\[
\partial_\kappa B(m,\kappa)=0.
\]
Swap symmetry removes the wrong-parity terms in the transverse collision
variable; it does not remove quotient-visible dependence on the exceptional
slope.
\end{remark}
```

Then add the missing theorem target:

```latex
\begin{remark}[Missing theorem: quotient-valued diagonal merger]
\label{rem:missing-quotient-valued-diagonal-merger}
Bottleneck~C requires a quotient-valued diagonal merger theorem.  On every
good patch on which
\[
c(m)\ne0,
\qquad
A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m)\ne0,
\]
the corrected two-atom collision package must factor through the blow-down of
the exceptional divisor:
\[
(m,\kappa,0)\longmapsto m.
\]
Equivalently,
\[
B(m,\kappa)
=
B(m,0)
=
\widehat\Psi(m)
\qquad
\text{for all sufficiently small }\kappa.
\]
At the order-\(7\) quotient level this means
\[
B_7^{\mathfrak f}(m,\kappa,0)
-
B_7^{\mathfrak f}(m,0,0)
\in
\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m).
\]

This is stronger than choosing a local septic gauge such as \(v_7=0\) or
\(u_7=0\).  Such a gauge selects a representative inside a fixed quotient
class; it does not prove that the quotient class itself is independent of the
exceptional slope \(\kappa\).
\end{remark}
```

I would **not** insert Agent 5’s full formal leakage model unless you want a more adversarial paper. The swap-coordinate calculation plus missing theorem statement is enough.

# Edit 4 — finite-core lower-transfer gap

Agent 7 is a major downgrade: the current final theorem is pair-like only; it is not finite-core closure. This should be explicit. 

Insert after `rem:xi-zeta-finite-core-localization-asymptotic`:

```latex
\begin{definition}[Finite-core \(N\)-point scalar]
\label{def:finite-core-npoint-scalar}
Fix a finite same-scale core \(\mathcal C\) of zero pairs around the midpoint
\(m\), and let
\[
H_{\core,m}(s)
:=
\Phi_K\!\bigl(\widehat\Omega_{\core}^{\corr}(s;m)\bigr)
\]
denote the corrected transverse scalar contributed by this core, in the same
finite-\(s\) normalization as \(H_m(s)\).  For \(N\ge1\), define
\[
\Xi_{\core}^{(N)}(m)
:=
\sum_{j=1}^N a_j^{(N)}H_{\core,m}(j/Q^2).
\]
If
\[
H_{\core,m}(z/Q^2)
=
\sum_{r\ge 0}
c_{\core,2r+1}(m)\frac{z^{2r+1}}{Q^{2r+4}},
\]
then the \(N\)-point moment cancellations give
\[
\Xi_{\core}^{(N)}(m)
=
(-1)^{N+1}(2N-1)N!(N-1)!
\sum_{k\ge0}
c_{\core,2N-1+2k}(m)
h_k(1^2,\dots,N^2)
Q^{-(2N+2k+2)}.
\]
Thus the first finite-core coefficient seen by the \(N\)-point projector at
depth \(N\) is
\[
c_{\core,2N-1}(m).
\]
\end{definition}

\begin{remark}[Finite-core localization is not a lower law]
\label{rem:finite-core-localization-not-lower-law}
Corollary~\ref{cor:xi-zeta-finite-core-localization} is an upper/localization
statement.  It does not supply a lower bound for
\[
\Xi_{\core}^{(N)}(m).
\]
In particular, it does not rule out cancellation among the finitely many core
constituents:
\[
c_{\core,2N-1}(m)=0
\]
or cancellation of several consecutive \(N\)-visible odd coefficients.
A separate finite-core lower-transfer theorem is required before the
\(N\)-point contradiction can be applied to genuinely non-pair-like cores.
\end{remark}
```

Then add near `rem:relation-to-package-to-jet-bridge`:

```latex
\begin{remark}[Open theorem target: finite-core lower transfer]
\label{rem:open-finite-core-lower-transfer}
The finite-core branch would be closed by a theorem of the following form.

\emph{Finite-core lower-transfer theorem.}
Let \(\mathcal C\) be a normalized genuinely finite same-scale core whose
corrected package anomaly is nonzero after all quotient and hidden-state
identifications relevant to \(\Phi_K\).  Then there exist an admissible
\(N=N(m)\), a sign \(\sigma_{\mathcal C}\in\{\pm1\}\), and a constant
\(c_{\mathcal C}>0\), stable on the compact core-parameter patch, such that
\[
|\Xi_{\core}^{(N)}(m)|
\ge
c_{\mathcal C}\frac{x}{B_\zeta(m)}S(m).
\]

The present draft does not prove this theorem.  The corrected order-\(7\)
package controls the local quotient construction and removes the known
two-point/package quotient residuals, but it does not by itself determine the
\(N\)-visible coefficient
\[
c_{\core,2N-1}(m)
\]
for a genuinely non-pair-like finite core, nor does it rule out cancellation
among finite-core constituents.
\end{remark}
```

Also refine the final theorem statement if it still overclaims:

```latex
\begin{theorem}[Asymptotic calibrated \(N\)-point contradiction in the pair-like branch]
\label{thm:final-contradiction}
Assume the pair-like branch hypothesis and assume that the pair-like
package-to-\(\Xi\) bridge identifies the calibrated local two-point package
with the toy normal form entering Proposition~\ref{prop:toy-n-point-direct}.
Then, for \(Q\) sufficiently large, no fixed off-line toy anomaly can occur in
the pair-like branch.

This theorem is not a finite-core closure theorem.  The genuinely non-pair-like
finite-core branch remains open pending the lower-transfer theorem described in
Remark~\ref{rem:open-finite-core-lower-transfer}.
\end{theorem}
```

If the title/abstract still claim a proof of RH, I would downgrade them now. That is not a cosmetic change; it is a correctness correction.

# Edit 5 — mixed four-point: short no-new-carrier remark only

Agent 6’s result is useful but should not become a long theorem right now. It is conditional on Gate B plus the \(M_A,M_C\) connection correction closing. The useful part is the caution: a residual that survives does not become a new mixed four-point carrier; it enters through the existing quotient determinant \(\Delta_7\). 

Insert after `rem:mixed-four-point-sensitivity-to-gate-b`:

```latex
\begin{remark}[No separate mixed four-point carrier beyond the quotient determinant]
\label{rem:no-separate-mixed-four-point-carrier}
Assume Gate~B and the post-Gate-B connection correction close at the quotient
line.  Then a non-\((1,1)\) order-\(7\) fixed-sector residual
\[
E=eI+fS
\]
is seen by the mixed four-point branch only through its quotient determinant
\[
\omega_h(E,A_5^{\mathfrak f}(h))=ev_5-u_5f.
\]
If
\[
E\in \mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}(h),
\]
then it does not change the canonical septic determinant
\[
\Delta_7=u_7v_5-u_5v_7
\]
and hence creates no mixed four-point carrier beyond the already-defined
scalar exits.

If the residual is not quotient-line absorbed, the obstruction is precisely
the failure of the quotient-septic connection identity, for example
\[
R_7^{(A)}
+
\sum_{i=1}^{7}\omega_m(Z_{7-i}[M_A],A_i)
\]
or the corresponding \(M_C\) expression.  It is not a new mixed four-point
mechanism; downstream it enters only through the induced change of
\(\Delta_7\).

This does not solve the separate \(\Phi_K\)-visible hidden-state problem,
since a line shift \(E=\chi A_5^{\mathfrak f}\) is quotient-invisible but may
still satisfy
\[
\Phi_K(E)=2\chi v_5.
\]
\end{remark}
```

Also make the two minor cleanups Agent 6 found:

1. Remove duplicate `\end{corollary}` around `cor:explicit-four-point-determinant-form-vpatch`.
2. Remove duplicate sentence near the tagged slice proof beginning “It cannot occur in \(c(h)\), since \(c\) is cubic...”.

```latex
\[
```

\[

```text
through ordinary order \(7\), its edge coefficient is represented by the homogeneous moving Taylor source tower satisfying the Gate B hypotheses.

not captured by the formal homogeneous tower.
```

# Agent 4 — Bottleneck C: quotient-valued diagonal merger

```text
You are attacking Bottleneck C: exceptional-divisor fiber selection.

Goal:
Prove or refute that the exceptional-divisor trace
\[
B(m,\kappa)=\widetilde\Psi_{\rm red}^{\corr}(m,\kappa,0)
\]
is independent of \(\kappa\).

Known warning:
Analyticity, swap symmetry, fixed codomain, scalar normalization, and
\[
B(m,0)=\widehat\Psi(m)
\]
do not by themselves imply \(\partial_\kappa B=0\).

Collision chart:
\[
h_1=m-\frac{\delta}{2},
\qquad
h_2=m+\frac{\delta}{2},
\qquad
a_2=-a_1(1+\kappa\delta).
\]

Atom swap gives:
\[
\delta\mapsto-\delta,
\qquad
\kappa\mapsto\frac{\kappa}{1+\kappa\delta},
\]
so on \(\delta=0\), \(\kappa\mapsto\kappa\). Thus swap does not kill \(\kappa\)-slope.

Target theorem:
Prove quotient-valued diagonal merger:
\[
B(m,\kappa)=B(m,0)=\widehat\Psi(m)
\]
or equivalently
\[
B_7^{\mathfrak f}(m,\kappa,0)
-
B_7^{\mathfrak f}(m,0,0)
\in
\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m).
\]

Tasks:
1. Formalize the corrected two-atom collision functor as the ordered composite:
\[
\mathcal B_2
\to
C_{\mathcal W}^{\rm raw}
\to
(1-\Pi_{1,1})_{\rm mix}
\to
-a_1^{-1}\delta^{-2}
\to
\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}[z^{\le7}]
\to
\tau_{h\to m}
\to
[z^7]
\to
\mathfrak f_m/\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m).
\]
2. Check whether this functor factors through the blow-down
\[
(m,\kappa,0)\mapsto m.
\]
3. Identify any actual package property that kills the formal leakage model
\[
\delta^2 Z_0(m)+2\varepsilon\omega\delta E_m,
\qquad
\kappa=2\omega/\delta.
\]
4. Determine whether the \(a_2=-a_1(1+\kappa\delta)\) balancing condition imposes a hidden derivative constraint at \(\delta=0\).
5. Check whether quotienting by \(\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}\) removes or preserves the possible \(\kappa\)-slope.

Deliverable:
Either a proof of diagonal merger, or a formal quotient-visible leakage model compatible with all current assumptions, plus the exact missing theorem needed to exclude it.
```

# Agent 5 — Finite-core lower transfer

```text
You are attacking the genuinely non-pair-like finite-core branch.

Goal:

\Xi_{\core}^{(N)}(m)

or isolate why the current machinery only excludes the pair-like branch.

Current status:
The pair-like toy model has an asymptotic contradiction, but arbitrary finite cores may cancel the first visible odd coefficient and survive at higher odd order.

Let
\[
H_{\core,m}(s)
=
\Phi_K(\widehat\Omega_{\core}^{\corr}(s;m)).
\]
Define
\[
\Xi_{\core}^{(N)}(m)
=
\sum_{j=1}^N a_j^{(N)}H_{\core,m}(j/Q^2).

\[

=
```

# Agent 7 — Finite-dimensional algebraic no-cancellation search

```text
You are attacking the finite-core problem from a purely finite-dimensional algebraic angle.

Goal:
Find a structural non-cancellation theorem for finite cores, or build a countermodel showing why such a theorem is false under current assumptions.

Set-up:
A finite core produces an odd scalar expansion
\[
H_{\core,m}(z/Q^2)
=
\sum_{r\ge0}
c_{\core,2r+1}(m)\frac{z^{2r+1}}{Q^{2r+4}}.
\]
The \(N\)-point operator detects \(c_{\core,2N-1}\) first.

Question:
If the corrected package anomaly is nonzero, must there exist an admissible \(N\) such that
\[
c_{\core,2N-1}\ne0
\]
with a controlled sign/size? Or can a nonzero finite-core anomaly be hidden from all admissible \(N\)-point projectors up to the required depth?

Tasks:
1. Abstract the finite core as a finite sum of atoms/interactions with coefficients satisfying the symmetries in the paper.
2. Model the first several odd coefficients as polynomial functionals on finite-core parameters.
3. Search for linear/algebraic constraints forcing all \(c_{\core,2r+1}\) to vanish unless the anomaly is zero.
4. Conversely, search for finite-dimensional cancellation families where early odd coefficients vanish but a higher odd coefficient survives.
5. Determine whether compactness of the finite-core parameter patch gives a uniform lower bound after quotienting by the zero-anomaly locus.
6. Identify whether the required \(N\) might grow with core complexity or can be bounded by core size.

Deliverable:
A theorem candidate or a countermodel:
\[
\text{nonzero finite-core anomaly}
\Rightarrow
\exists N\le N_0(\#\mathcal C)
:
|\Xi_{\core}^{(N)}|\gtrsim (x/B_\zeta)S,
\]
or a demonstration that such a statement fails without extra positivity/ECT assumptions.
```

---

# Agent 8 — Search for a direct diagonal-merger mechanism in the source algebra

```text
You are attacking Bottleneck C from the source-algebra side.

Goal:
Find a direct reason inside the two-atom source algebra that the exceptional slope \(\kappa\) cannot survive in the quotient-valued corrected package.

Do not rely on abstract symmetry alone; we already know atom swap does not send \(\kappa\mapsto-\kappa\) on the exceptional divisor.

Possible mechanisms to investigate:
1. The balancing condition
\[
a_2=-a_1(1+\kappa\delta)
\]
may force first moment cancellation that removes \(\kappa\)-slope.
2. The \((1-\Pi_{1,1})_{\rm mix}\) projection may kill the slope term.
3. The \(\delta^{-2}\) edge normalization may convert slope dependence into a line-gauge term.
4. The source-bidegree projection may remove the only quotient-visible \(\kappa\)-term.
5. The corrected whitening transfer may make the exceptional trace depend only on the merged second jet.

Tasks:
1. Expand the two-atom source moment data in \((a_1,\delta,\kappa)\) through the order needed for \(z^7\delta^2\).
2. Identify all terms linear in \(\kappa\) after imposing cancellation.
3. Track which of these terms survive:
\[
(1-\Pi_{1,1})_{\rm mix},
\quad
\pi_{\mathfrak f},
\quad
\tau_{h\to m},
\quad
\mathfrak f_m/\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
\]
4. Determine whether all surviving \(\kappa\)-linear terms are multiples of \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}\).
5. If yes, formulate the diagonal-merger proof.
6. If no, produce the first quotient-visible \(\kappa\)-linear term.

Deliverable:
A source-algebra proof of
\[
\partial_\kappa B(m,\kappa)=0
\]
in the quotient, or the explicit first surviving quotient-visible \(\kappa\)-term.
```

# Agent 9 — Search for an \(A_5\)-line lift fixed by normalization

```text
You are attacking the hidden-state problem by searching for a canonical lift of the quotient package.

Goal:
Determine whether the paper’s normalizations secretly fix the affine lift
\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}
\mod \mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}
\]
well enough to determine
\[
\Phi_K(A_7^{\mathfrak f}).
\]

Problem:
The quotient class alone loses
\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}\mapsto A_7^{\mathfrak f}+\chi A_5^{\mathfrak f},
\]
and this is \(\Phi_K\)-visible when \(v_5\ne0\).

Potential lift-fixing mechanisms:
1. \(c\)-normalization.
2. The value gauge.
3. Midpoint representative choice.
4. Determinant normalization \(\Delta_7/(cv_5)\).
5. Orthogonality or symplectic normalization against a dual line.
6. The \(2\)-jet affine removal convention.
7. Compatibility with the zeta-side finite-\(s\) block.

Tasks:
1. Examine every normalization that occurs before \(A_7^{\mathfrak f}\) is fed to \(\Phi_K\).
2. Check whether any normalization imposes a condition equivalent to fixing \(v_7\), \(u_7\), or \(\Phi_K(A_7^{\mathfrak f})\).
3. Distinguish diagnostic gauges from canonical theorem objects.
4. If a canonical lift exists, define it invariantly.
5. If no canonical lift exists, prove that an additional hidden-state coordinate is unavoidable.

Deliverable:
Either a canonical lift theorem, or a proof that \(\widetilde\Psi_{\min}\)-type data must be added as genuine hidden state before the package can feed the transform.
```

# Agent 10 — Attack the pair-like-to-finite-core bridge

```text
You are attacking whether every finite core can be reduced to a controlled sum of pair-like components.

Goal:
Close or refute the idea that non-pair-like finite cores can be decomposed into pair-like toy anomalies whose signs cannot all cancel.

Tasks:
1. Identify the pair-like toy normal form used in the final contradiction.
2. For a finite same-scale core with \(k\) zero pairs, attempt to decompose its corrected transverse scalar into pairwise toy contributions plus higher interaction error.
3. Determine whether the pairwise contributions have a common sign after calibration.
4. If not, classify interaction terms that can reverse or cancel the pairwise lower law.
5. Check whether ECT / Chebyshev / total positivity methods in the draft can force a sign variation bound.
6. Determine whether a non-pair-like core can be continuously deformed to a pair-like one without crossing the zero-anomaly locus.
7. If yes, attempt a homotopy/degree argument for nonvanishing.
8. If no, identify the obstruction stratum.

Deliverable:
Either:
- a reduction of finite-core lower transfer to finitely many pair-like toy lower laws plus controlled errors, or
- a concrete finite-core cancellation scenario showing why pair-like exclusion cannot be generalized directly.
```

_Thought for 23s_

The 10-agent round did **not** close a new theorem. It did sharpen the attack surface substantially.

The most important outcome is that the proof now has **five precise obstruction targets**, and one branch has been downgraded from “possible independent danger” to “dependency-only.”

## Consolidated verdict

### 1. Gate B is still conditional, but the obstruction is now precise

Agent 1 reduced the actual-source Gate B upgrade to a single defect:

\[
\Theta_7^{\actual}
=
[z^7][\delta^1]\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}
(1-\Pi_{1,1})_{\rm mix}
\left(
C_{\mathcal W,\actual}^{\rm raw}
-
C_{\mathcal W,\mathrm{tower}}^{\rm raw}
\right).
\]

The formal homogeneous tower already has zero Gate B edge coefficient. The missing theorem is exactly:

\[
\boxed{\Theta_7^{\actual}=0.}
\]

Useful positive information: functional calculus itself is probably not the obstruction. If endpoint parity is supplied at the actual source-block level, analytic \(G^{-1/2}\) preserves the subset parity and symmetry needed downstream. The real gap is showing that the actual \(\mathcal K\)-degree \(\ge2\) pre-whitening remainders either obey the same tower/parity/telescoping, are too high-order, or vanish after projection.  

**Attack priority:** high.

---

### 2. The \(M_A,M_C\) connection identities are not formal

Agent 2 confirmed that the connection identities reduce to a finite \(Z_j\)-table, but are not closed by parity or antisymmetry alone:

\[
R_7^{(A)}
+
\sum_{i=1}^{7}\omega_m(Z_{7-i}[M_A],A_i)=0,
\]

\[
R_7^{(C)}
+
\sum_{i=1}^{7}\omega_m(Z_{7-i}[M_C],A_i)=0.
\]

The missing concrete objects remain:

\[
Z_j[M_A],\quad Z_j[M_C],\quad A_i,\quad R_7^{(A)},\quad R_7^{(C)}.
\]

Agent 2’s strongest useful reframing is “moving-line orthogonality”:

\[
[\epsilon^7]\,
\omega_m\!\left(
[z^7]Z(h;z;M_X),
A_h^m
\right)
=0.
\]

This is better than raw coefficient hunting because it identifies the structural statement the table must prove. Agent 2 also gave a formal countermodel showing the identity is not forced by typing/parity alone.  

**Attack priority:** high and concrete.

---

### 3. The hidden-state bridge is genuinely not solved

Agents 3 and 9 agree: the reduced quotient package does **not** determine the first \(\Phi_K\)-visible corrected odd coefficient.

The obstruction is:

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}
\sim
A_7^{\mathfrak f}+\chi A_5^{\mathfrak f},
\]

but

\[
\Phi_K(\chi A_5^{\mathfrak f})=2\chi v_5.
\]

So on \(v_5\neq0\), the quotient-forgotten line is transform-visible. The exact missing datum is locally

\[
T=\frac{v_7}{c},
\]

or equivalently

\[
\theta_7=\frac{\Phi_K(A_7^{\mathfrak f})}{c}.
\]

No current normalization fixes this lift. \(c\)-normalization, determinant normalization, midpoint trivialization, and \(2\)-jet affine removal do not fix \(v_7\).  

**Attack priority:** high, but likely requires a new theorem rather than more local table work.

---

### 4. Bottleneck C is now sharper: it is a weighted edge derivative problem

Agents 4 and 8 both found formal \(\kappa\)-slope leakage models. The strongest new formulation comes from Agent 8.

Let

\[
F(a_1,a_2,\delta)
=
[z^7]\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}
(1-\Pi_{1,1})_{\rm mix}
C_{\mathcal W}^{\rm raw}
(a_1,h-\delta/2;\,a_2,h+\delta/2).
\]

Gate B gives only:

\[
[\delta^1]F(a_1,-a_1,\delta)=0.
\]

But diagonal merger needs the stronger weighted derivative condition:

\[
[\delta^1]\partial_{a_2}F(a_1,-a_1,\delta)
\in
\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m).
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\partial_\kappa Q_{7,m}^q(m,\kappa,0)=0.
\]

Agent 8’s countermodel shows unweighted balanced cancellation can hold while the weighted derivative survives in the quotient. This is a major sharpening: Bottleneck C is no longer vague “exceptional fiber selection”; it is a **weighted source-bidegree edge cancellation** theorem. 

**Attack priority:** very high. This is probably the cleanest next theorem to attack.

---

### 5. Mixed four-point branch is not a separate local carrier

Agent 6 gives a useful positive result: the mixed four-point branch consumes only

\[
c,\quad u_5,\quad v_5,\quad \Delta_7,
\]

where

\[
\Delta_7=u_7v_5-u_5v_7.
\]

A residual

\[
E=eI+fS
\]

enters only through

\[
\omega_h(E,A_5^{\mathfrak f})=ev_5-u_5f.
\]

So if \(E\in \mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}\), it is invisible to mixed four-point geometry. If not, it shifts \(\Delta_7\), i.e. it is the existing quotient determinant obstruction, not a new mixed four-point mechanism.  

This is good news. Mixed four-point should be **deprioritized** as an independent attack. It depends on quotient determinant closure plus the separate hidden-state bridge.

**Attack priority:** low, unless quotient closure changes.

---

### 6. Finite-core closure is still wide open

Agents 5, 7, and 10 all converge: the pair-like lower law does not generalize automatically to finite same-scale cores.

There are two distinct missing inputs:

\[
\boxed{\text{finite odd-germ determinacy}}
\]

and

\[
\boxed{\text{scale-normalized package-to-}\Xi_{\core}^{(N)}\text{ transfer}.}
\]

Agent 5 gives the “upper not lower” diagnosis: finite-core localization tells us where \(\Xi_\zeta^{(N)}\) comes from, but gives no lower bound. Agent 7 gives delayed-cancellation countermodels. Agent 10 shows pair-like toy contributions can cancel their first odd channel, with interaction terms surviving at higher odd order.   

This branch is fundamental but currently too broad unless we first solve hidden-state/diagonal-merger issues.

**Attack priority:** medium/long-term. Do not spend all agents here yet.

---

## Prompt 1 — Bottleneck C weighted edge derivative

```text
You are attacking Bottleneck C in its sharpened source-algebra form.

Work only from the latest draft.

Define
\[
F(a_1,a_2,\delta)
=
[z^7]\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}
(1-\Pi_{1,1})_{\rm mix}
C_{\mathcal W}^{\rm raw}
(a_1,h-\delta/2;\,a_2,h+\delta/2).
\]

Gate B gives
\[
[\delta^1]F(a_1,-a_1,\delta)=0.
\]

But quotient-valued diagonal merger requires the stronger weighted derivative law
\[
[\delta^1]\partial_{a_2}F(a_1,-a_1,\delta)
\in
\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m).
\]

Equivalently,
\[
\partial_\kappa Q_{7,m}^q(m,\kappa,0)=0.
\]

Tasks:
1. Decompose the non-\((1,1)\) mixed edge coefficient into source bidegrees:
\[
[\delta^1][z^7]\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}
(1-\Pi_{1,1})_{\rm mix}
C_{\mathcal W}^{\rm raw}
=
\sum_{p,q}a_1^pa_2^qE_{p,q}(m).
\]
2. Gate B gives the unweighted balanced identity:
\[
\sum_{p,q}a_1^p(-a_1)^qE_{p,q}(m)=0.
\]
Check whether the weighted identity
\[
\sum_{p,q}q\,a_1^p(-a_1)^{q-1}E_{p,q}(m)
\in
\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m)
\]
follows from the actual source algebra.
3. Identify whether subset-complement parity gives weighted cancellation, or only unweighted cancellation.
4. Track the candidate countermodel:
\[
a_1a_2^3\delta E-a_1^3a_2\delta E.
\]
Determine whether actual corrected whitening permits or forbids such a source-bidegree pattern.
5. If forbidden, state the exact structural reason. If permitted, produce the first quotient-visible \(\kappa\)-slope term.

Deliverable:
A proof of weighted edge cancellation, or the exact surviving source-bidegree obstruction.
```

## Prompt 6 — Finite-core scale transfer only

```text
You are attacking finite-core scale transfer, assuming finite determinacy.

Work only from the latest draft.

Assume some \(N\) has

c_{\core,2N-1}\neq0.
\]

\[

\gtrsim

\[

=

h_k(1^2,\dots,N^2)
Q^{-(2N+2k+2)}.
\]
2. Determine the required lower bound on \(c_{\core,2N-1}\).
3. Prove or refute tail domination:
\[
\sum_{k\ge1}
|c_{\core,2N-1+2k}h_kQ^{-2k}|
\le
\frac12|c_{\core,2N-1}|.
\]
4. Relate the finite-core normalization to the zeta calibration scale
\[
(x/B_\zeta)S.
\]
5. Check whether the positive kernel gives anything beyond sign transfer once a one-sided derivative law is known.

Deliverable:
A scale-transfer theorem conditional on finite determinacy, or the exact missing calibration estimate.
```

through ordinary order \(7\).

\[
A_+^{[g]}=(-1)^gA_-^{[g]}.

Either a proof of

\]

or the first explicit actual-source defect term.

## User (2026-04-25 10:05:54)

ELI what we are doing in this attack overall

## Assistant (2026-04-25 10:05:55)

We are trying to turn a promising RH proof draft from a **local formal mechanism** into a **global contradiction**.

Right now the draft has several impressive-looking local cancellations. The danger is that local cancellations can be true but still not imply RH. So the attack is not “compute random more coefficients.” It is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Find the exact bridges needed from local algebra to global RH contradiction.}
}
\]

Here is the simple map.

---

## 1. The proof has a local engine

The local engine studies what happens near a hypothetical off-line zero configuration. It builds matrix/block packages and tries to show that certain “bad” local anomalies must cancel.

The main local gates are:

\[
\text{Gate A}
\]

and

\[
\text{Gate B}.
\]

Gate A is basically closed. It says the first scary cubic obstruction cancels in the fixed sector.

Gate B is almost closed, but only for a **formal homogeneous tower model**. The first big attack is to show that the **actual zeta-side corrected source package** really behaves like that tower.

So one attack is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Does the real object equal the formal object at the Gate B coefficient?}
}
\]

That is the defect:

\[
\Theta_7^{\actual}=0.
\]

If this fails, Gate B was only a beautiful formal cancellation, not a theorem about zeta.

---

## 2. After Gate B, two residual monomials remain structurally important

The two named residuals are:

\[
M_A=\dot r_3r_2\dot r_4,
\qquad
M_C=\dot r_3\dot r_2r_4.
\]

They are not supposed to be killed by raw parity alone. They need a **connection correction**, using lower table data:

\[
Z_j[M].
\]

So the second attack is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Compute the actual }Z_j[M_A],Z_j[M_C]\text{ tables and prove the connection identity.}
}
\]

The target is:

\[
R_7^{(A)}
+
\sum_{i=1}^{7}\omega_m(Z_{7-i}[M_A],A_i)=0,
\]

\[
R_7^{(C)}
+
\sum_{i=1}^{7}\omega_m(Z_{7-i}[M_C],A_i)=0.
\]

In plain English: there is a moving reference line. Some residuals may look nonzero before you account for the line moving. We are checking whether the residual plus the line-motion correction cancels exactly.

---

## 3. The quotient package may forget something the global transform sees

The local package often works modulo the line:

\[
\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
\]

So two representatives are treated as the same if they differ by:

\[
\chi A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
\]

But the global transform uses a scalar functional:

\[
\Phi_K.
\]

And:

\[
\Phi_K(\chi A_5^{\mathfrak f})=2\chi v_5.
\]

So the quotient may say “same,” while the transform says “different.”

This is one of the most important gaps.

In plain English:

\[
\boxed{
\text{The local proof may be throwing away information that the global RH contradiction still needs.}
}
\]

The hidden coordinate is basically:

\[
T=\frac{v_7}{c}.
\]

So the third attack is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Does the actual transform canonically recover this hidden state, or must we add it?}
}
\]

---

## 4. Bottleneck C is about collision directions

The proof considers two nearby source atoms colliding:

\[
h_1=m-\frac{\delta}{2},
\qquad
h_2=m+\frac{\delta}{2}.
\]

There is also a slope parameter:

\[
\kappa.
\]

When \(\delta\to0\), many different collision paths collapse to the same point \(m\). For the proof to work, the reduced package should not depend on the collision slope \(\kappa\). That desired statement is:

\[
B(m,\kappa)=B(m,0).
\]

But symmetry alone does not prove this.

The sharper version is:

\[
[\delta^1]\partial_{a_2}F(a_1,-a_1,\delta)
\in
\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m).
\]

In plain English:

\[
\boxed{
\text{When two atoms merge, does the package forget the path of merger?}
}
\]

If it remembers the path, then a hidden \(\kappa\)-slope survives and the global argument breaks.

This is probably the cleanest next serious target.

---

## 5. Mixed four-point is less scary now

One concern was: even if the two-point package closes, maybe a mixed four-point obstruction survives independently.

Agent 6 basically says no: the mixed four-point branch only sees the usual quotient determinant:

\[
\Delta_7=u_7v_5-u_5v_7.
\]

So if the quotient determinant closes, there is no extra mixed four-point carrier.

In plain English:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Mixed four-point is probably not a separate monster.}
}
\]

It depends on the same quotient determinant closure plus the hidden-state bridge.

---

## 6. The final global contradiction is only pair-like so far

The draft has a final contradiction for a “pair-like” configuration. That means the off-line anomaly looks essentially like a two-point toy model.

But general finite cores may be more complicated. Multiple components can cancel the first visible odd term, while a higher odd anomaly survives.

So the final attack is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Can every non-pair-like finite core still be detected by some }N\text{-point test?}
}
\]

This splits into two subproblems:

### A. Finite determinacy

If the finite-core anomaly is nonzero, does some bounded odd coefficient detect it?

\[
H_{\core}\not\equiv0
\Rightarrow
\exists N:
c_{\core,2N-1}\neq0.
\]

### B. Scale transfer

Once a coefficient is nonzero, is it large enough to give the RH contradiction?

\[
|\Xi_{\core}^{(N)}|
\gtrsim
\frac{x}{B_\zeta}S.
\]

In plain English:

\[
\boxed{
\text{The pair-like contradiction is not enough; we need to catch all finite-core shapes.}
}
\]

---

# Overall attack strategy

We are not trying to “finish RH by optimism.” We are stress-testing the proof at the exact places where local-to-global arguments usually fail.

The five major attack points are:

\[
\boxed{1.\ \Theta_7^{\actual}=0}
\]

Does the actual zeta package match the formal Gate B tower?

\[
\boxed{2.\ Z_j[M_A],Z_j[M_C]\text{ connection closure}}
\]

Do the remaining residual monomials cancel after moving-line correction?

\[
\boxed{3.\ \Phi_K\text{-visible hidden-state bridge}}
\]

Does the quotient package retain all information the global transform sees?

\[
\boxed{4.\ \kappa\text{-slope / diagonal merger}}
\]

When two atoms collide, does the reduced package forget the collision path?

\[
\boxed{5.\ \text{finite-core lower transfer}}
\]

Does the final \(N\)-point contradiction catch every possible finite core, not just pair-like ones?

---

# The strategic meaning

If all five attacks close, the draft would move from:

\[
\text{“local corrected package plus pair-like contradiction”}
\]

to something much closer to:

\[
\text{“global off-line zero exclusion.”}
\]

If any one fails, that tells us exactly where the proof attempt breaks.

So the current work is a **gap-isolation and bridge-building campaign**. We are not merely polishing the paper; we are trying to determine whether the local package machinery actually reaches RH.

# 1. Agent 1: actual-source Gate B narrowed

Agent 1 first identified a plausible actual-source obstruction from the nonlinear \(q^3\) term in

\[
G_{\pm}^{\corr}.
\]

Specifically, the same-point cubic terms

\[

\qquad

\]

inside \(G_{\pm,22}^{\corr}\) looked like a \((2,1)/(1,2)\) source-bidegree defect not represented by the formal homogeneous tower. But the continued calculation then showed that the **single-insertion first Fréchet response of this defect vanishes** after fixed-sector projection, by endpoint swap and transpose-invariance. 

So the correct status is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{The same-point cubic \(q^3\) single-insertion defect is killed.}
}
\]

But this does **not** prove

\[
\Theta_7^{\actual}=0.
\]

The remaining actual-source candidates are now narrower:

\[

\]

and nonlinear mixed-block Taylor remainders in

\[
