\]

**Next attack:** check whether the same endpoint-swap/transpose mechanism kills all higher Fréchet responses involving \(P_\pm\), and then separately table nonlinear mixed-block remainders.

---

# 2. Agent 2: \(M_A,M_C\) connection reduced to one sharp \(Y\)-middle parity lemma

Agent 2 made real progress. The \(N_0\)-middle part of the \(J=(3,2,4)\) table cancels under the usual complement parity because the source-edge weights are complement-invariant and \(|J|=9\) is odd. 

The whole \(M_A,M_C\) table now reduces to the edge-refined \(Y\)-middle transpose parity:

\[
\boxed{
\left(Y_{g,\beta}^{\langle e\rangle}\right)^T
=
(-1)^{g+e}Y_{g,\beta}^{\langle e\rangle}.
}
\]

Here \(e=0\) means the middle source is undotted, and \(e=1\) means the middle source supplies one endpoint-edge derivative.

If this holds, then:

\[
Z_j[M_A]=Z_j[M_C]=0,
\qquad
0\le j\le7,
\]

and the connection identities close exactly. 

If it fails, the first explicit defects are:

\[
D_A
\quad\text{from}\quad
Y_4^{\langle1\rangle},
\]

and

\[
D_C
\quad\text{from}\quad
Y_2^{\langle1\rangle}.
\]

**Next attack:** prove or refute the actual mixed-block swap identity

\[
Y_g(h-\delta/2,h+\delta/2)^T
=
(-1)^gY_g(h+\delta/2,h-\delta/2),
\]

then extract the \(\delta^e\)-coefficient to get the extra \((-1)^e\).

This is one of the cleanest local targets now.

---

# 3. Agents 3 and 9: hidden state is unavoidable unless we augment the package

Agents 3 and 9 converged strongly. The reduced quotient package cannot determine the \(\Phi_K\)-visible septic coefficient. The obstruction is exact:

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}
\sim
A_7^{\mathfrak f}+\chi A_5^{\mathfrak f},
\]

but

\[
\Phi_K(\chi A_5^{\mathfrak f})=2\chi v_5.
\]

Thus \(\Phi_K\) descends to the quotient

\[
\mathfrak f_m/\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}
\]

if and only if

\[
v_5=0.
\]

On the generic \(v_5\neq0\) patch, descent is algebraically impossible from the reduced quotient package alone. 

The actual finite-\(s\) germ does give a canonical value of the transform-visible coefficient, but only because it contains more data than the reduced package. Therefore the minimal repaired package is:

\[
\boxed{
\widehat\Psi_{\rm red}^{+}
=
(\widehat\Psi_{\rm red},T),
\qquad
T=\frac{v_7}{c}.
}
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\theta_{\Phi,7}
=
\frac{\Phi_K(A_7^{\mathfrak f})}{c}
=
2T.
\]

Agent 3 also checked that the \(N=4\) moment operator sees the septic hidden state; it does not cancel it.  Agent 9 confirmed that finite-\(s\) compatibility does not define a lift from reduced data alone; the finite-\(s\) germ must be admitted as extra data or encoded through \(T\). 

**Conclusion:** stop trying to prove quotient-only state-locality on the generic patch. The viable path is to **augment the package**.

---

# 4. Agents 4 and 8: Bottleneck C is double balanced divisibility

Agents 4 and 8 sharpened Bottleneck C substantially.

The right object is the edge polynomial

\[
P_{7,m}(a_1,a_2)
=
[z^7][\delta^1]\tau_{h\to m}\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}
(1-\Pi_{1,1})_{\rm mix}
C_{\mathcal W}^{\rm raw}.
\]

Gate B gives a simple balanced zero:

\[
\overline P_{7,m}(a_1,-a_1)=0
\]

in the quotient

\[
V_m=\mathfrak f_m/\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m).
\]

Bottleneck C requires the stronger condition:

\[
\partial_{a_2}\overline P_{7,m}(a_1,-a_1)=0.
\]

Equivalently:

\[
\boxed{
\overline P_{7,m}(a_1,a_2)
\in
(a_1+a_2)^2V_m[a_1,a_2].
}
\]

So Bottleneck C is **double balanced divisibility modulo the quotient line**. 

Important refinement: the earlier formal \((1,3)/(3,1)\) countermodel is not compatible with the homogeneous tower, because the tower forces the compensating bidegree structure needed for double divisibility. So the homogeneous tower likely closes Bottleneck C. The remaining issue is actual-source deviation from the homogeneous tower:

\[
\boxed{
\overline P_{7,m}^{\actual}
-
\overline P_{7,m}^{\tower}
\in
(a_1+a_2)^2V_m[a_1,a_2]?
}
\]

Agent 8 still emphasizes the generic algebraic danger: Gate B’s simple zero does not imply the weighted derivative condition.  But Agent 4’s continuation refines this: the tower has the stronger double zero, so leakage can only come from actual-source deviations. 

**Next attack:** combine Agent 1 and Agent 4. Prove every nonlinear actual-source remainder has a double balanced zero modulo \(\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}\).

This is now the central Bottleneck C / actual-source joint target.

---

# 5. Agent 5: finite-core scale transfer is exponentially sensitive

Agent 5 separated finite determinacy from scale transfer and showed scale transfer is much harder than “some coefficient is nonzero.”

The exact \(N\)-point expansion is:

\[
\Xi_{\core}^{(N)}
=
(-1)^{N+1}C_NQ^{-(2N+2)}
\left(
c_{\core,2N-1}+T_N
\right),
\]

where

\[
C_N=(2N-1)N!(N-1)!
\]

and

\[
T_N=
\sum_{k\ge1}
c_{\core,2N-1+2k}
h_k(1^2,\dots,N^2)Q^{-2k}.
\]

So the actual lower bound requires a filtered coefficient estimate:

\[
\left|
c_{\core,2N-1}
+
\sum_{k\ge1}
c_{\core,2N-1+2k}
h_kQ^{-2k}
\right|
\gtrsim
\frac{Q^{2N+2}}{C_N}
\frac{x}{B_\zeta}S.
\]

At linear depth \(N=\alpha Q\), this becomes exponentially sensitive through the factor

\[
\left(\frac{e}{\alpha}\right)^{2\alpha Q}.
\]

Agent 5’s key conclusion is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{finite-core scale transfer needs a scale-normalized anti-Cauchy lower theorem.}
}
\]

Finite determinacy is not enough. Tail domination or a one-sided positive-kernel derivative lower law is required. 

**Next attack:** not “prove nonzero coefficient.” Instead prove a one-sided derivative lower law or filtered coefficient lower bound at the calibrated zeta scale.

---

# 6. Agent 6: mixed four-point branch is dependency-only

Agent 6 again confirms that there is no independent mixed four-point carrier. A residual

\[
E=eI+fS
\]

affects mixed four-point geometry only through

\[
\omega_h(E,A_5^{\mathfrak f})=ev_5-u_5f.
\]

A line shift

\[
E=\chi A_5^{\mathfrak f}
\]

is mixed-four-point invisible, even though it may be \(\Phi_K\)-visible. 

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
\text{mixed four-point closure}
\Longleftarrow
\text{quotient determinant closure}
+
\text{separate hidden-state bridge}.
}
\]

**Action:** deprioritize mixed four-point as an independent attack. It is now a dependency audit, not a live main branch.

---

# 7. Agent 7: finite determinacy is actually available on compact analytic strata

This is the strongest positive result in the finite-core direction.

Agent 7 corrected the previous overly formal delayed-cancellation countermodel. If a fixed \(k\)-core lives on a compact nonsingular actual-source analytic stratum, then the family

\[
\theta\mapsto H_{\core,\theta}(z)
\]

is analytic in \((\theta,z)\). By Noetherianity of local analytic rings and compactness, the zero-anomaly locus is cut out by finitely many odd coefficients. Therefore there exists some finite

\[
R_{\Theta_k}
\]

such that

\[
c_{\core,1}=\cdots=c_{\core,2R_{\Theta_k}+1}=0
\]

implies

\[
H_{\core,\theta}\equiv0.
\]

So:

\[
\boxed{
\text{finite determinacy is available on compact nonsingular actual-source strata.}
}
\]

But it is non-quantitative: no usable \(R_k\), no lower bound, no sign law, no scale transfer. 

**Next attack:** use this as a structural reduction, then hand off the quantitative burden to Agent 5’s scale-transfer theorem.

---

# 8. Agent 10: finite-core stratification still has an unresolved interaction-cancellation stratum

Agent 10 found a useful positive fact:

\[
K(d)=\Phi_K(M(d))
\]

has

\[
\Re K(d)>0
\qquad(d>0).
\]

So positive real sums of pair-like toy coefficients cannot cancel in the first odd channel. 

But actual finite cores are not known to be positive sums of pair-like terms. They include interaction terms

\[
\mathcal I_{\ge2},
\]

and those can cancel the first odd pair-like channel without forcing any of the already-controlled geometric incidence strata:

\[
M=0,\quad W=0,\quad K_v=0,\quad T_v=0,
\]

or collision / patch-boundary / endpoint-gap strata.

Agent 10 isolates the unresolved stratum:

\[
\boxed{
\mathfrak Z_{\mathrm{int}}
=
\text{interaction-driven first-odd cancellation away from controlled strata.}
}
\]

So the finite-core stratification must include an unresolved interaction-cancellation stratum unless a new rigidity theorem proves it collapses into controlled geometry or higher-odd lower law. 

**Next attack:** prove an interaction rigidity theorem, not a generic pair-like summation theorem.

# 1. Actual-source Gate B / Bottleneck C: first live carrier found

Earlier we suspected the same-point cubic defect

\[
P_\pm\sim d_1^2d_2+d_1d_2^2
\]

might break actual-source Gate B. Agent 1 now shows that all same-point-only higher Fréchet responses involving \(P_\pm\) are killed by endpoint-swap / transpose symmetry. So that is no longer the live obstruction. 

The first live channel is instead:

\[
Y_{12}^{(2)}
=
D^2N_0[\xi_1,\xi_2],
\]

the \(\mathcal K^2\), source-bidegree \((1,1)\) nonlinear mixed-block Taylor remainder, **promoted** to non-\((1,1)\) by coupling to one same-point linear whitening slot:

\[
D(G_-^{-1/2})[A_-]\,
Y_{12}^{(2)}\,
R_0
+
L_0\,
Y_{12}^{(2)}\,
D(G_+^{-1/2})[B_+].
\]

This has amplitude factor:

\[
a_1a_2(a_1+a_2).
\]

So it passes Gate B’s simple balanced zero:

\[
a_1a_2(a_1+a_2)\big|_{a_2=-a_1}=0,
\]

but fails Bottleneck C’s double-balanced condition because

\[
\partial_{a_2}\bigl(a_1a_2(a_1+a_2)\bigr)\big|_{a_2=-a_1}
=
-a_1^2.
\]

Thus the precise local obstruction is:

\[
\boxed{
E_{A,Y}\in \mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m)?
}
\]

where

\[
E_{A,Y}
=
[z^7]\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}
\left(
D(G_-^{-1/2})[A_-]\,
Y_{12}^{(2)}\,
R_0
+
L_0\,
Y_{12}^{(2)}\,
D(G_+^{-1/2})[B_+]
\right).
\]

If this is line-gauge, the first live carrier dies. If not, actual-source double-balanced divisibility fails.  

## Next target

Do **not** broadly attack all nonlinear remainders yet. First attack:

\[
\boxed{
[z^7]\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}
\left(
D(G_-^{-1/2})[A_-]\,
Y_{12}^{(2)}\,
R_0
+
L_0\,
Y_{12}^{(2)}\,

\right)
\in

}
\]

This is the cleanest next local theorem.

# 2. \(M_A,M_C\) connection closure: reduced to actual mixed-block swap parity

Agent 2 reduced the whole \(M_A,M_C\) connection problem to one actual-source functoriality lemma. If the actual corrected mixed block satisfies

\[
N^{\corr}(h_-,h_+)^T=N^{\corr}(h_+,h_-),
\]

and the source-linear grade extraction gives

\[
Y_g(h_-,h_+)^T=(-1)^gY_g(h_+,h_-),
\]

then extracting \(\delta^e\) gives the edge-refined parity:

\[
\boxed{
\left(Y_{g,\beta}^{\langle e\rangle}\right)^T
=
(-1)^{g+e}Y_{g,\beta}^{\langle e\rangle}.
}
\]

That parity closes the \(J=(3,2,4)\) table exactly:

\[
Z_j[M_A]=Z_j[M_C]=0,
\qquad
0\le j\le7.
\]

So the connection identities close:

\[
R_7^{(A)}
+
\sum_{i=1}^7\omega_m(Z_{7-i}[M_A],A_i)=0,
\]

\[
R_7^{(C)}
+
\sum_{i=1}^7\omega_m(Z_{7-i}[M_C],A_i)=0.
\]

If the identity fails, the first surviving wrong-parity pieces are:

\[
\operatorname{Sym}_+(Y_4^{\langle1\rangle})
\quad\text{for }M_A,
\]

and

\[
\operatorname{Sym}_+(Y_2^{\langle1\rangle})
\quad\text{for }M_C.
\]

## Next target

Prove directly from the formula for \(N^{\corr}\):

\[
\boxed{
N^{\corr}(h_-,h_+)^T=N^{\corr}(h_+,h_-)
}
\]

including all actual nonlinear source corrections. Then verify grade extraction contributes exactly \((-1)^g\).

This is probably the fastest local win.

---

# 3. Hidden-state bridge: the augmented package is now mandatory

Agents 3 and 9 converge: the old package object

\[
\widehat\Psi_{\rm red}
\]

is insufficient. The corrected object must be:

\[
\boxed{
\widehat\Psi_{\rm red}^{+}
=
(\widehat\Psi_{\rm red},T),
\qquad
T=\frac{v_7}{c}.
}
\]

Equivalently:

\[
\theta_{\Phi,7}
=
\frac{\Phi_K(A_7^{\mathfrak f})}{c}
=
2T.
\]

This is not cosmetic. The quotient package forgets the line direction:

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}
\mapsto
A_7^{\mathfrak f}+\chi A_5^{\mathfrak f},
\]

but the transform sees it:

\[
\Phi_K(\chi A_5^{\mathfrak f})=2\chi v_5.
\]

On \(v_5\neq0\), there is no quotient-only descent theorem. Adding \(T\) repairs the local two-point transform readout, because

\[
\Phi_K(A_7^{\mathfrak f})=2cT.
\]

 

## But this creates a new Bottleneck C obligation

Quotient diagonal merger controls \(\Delta_7\), not \(T\). Therefore augmented diagonal merger must require both:

\[
\partial_\kappa Q_{7,m}^q(m,\kappa,0)=0,
\]

and

\[
\boxed{
\partial_\kappa T(m,\kappa,0)=0.
}
\]

So Bottleneck C splits into:

\[
\boxed{\text{quotient-horizontal merger}}
\]

and

\[
\boxed{\text{\(T\)-horizontal / transform-visible merger}.}
\]

The first is local quotient geometry. The second is finite-\(s\) scalar geometry.

---

# 4. Mixed four-point: remains closed as dependency audit

Agent 6 confirms that adding \(T\) does **not** create a new mixed four-point carrier.

Mixed four-point sees:

\[
c,\quad u_5,\quad v_5,\quad \Delta_7,
\]

but not

\[
T=\frac{v_7}{c}.
\]

A residual

\[
E=eI+fS
\]

has two separate effects:

\[
\text{mixed four-point effect}
=
ev_5-u_5f,
\]

while

\[
\Phi_K\text{-visible hidden effect}
=
\frac{f}{c}.
\]

For a line shift

\[
E=\chi A_5^{\mathfrak f},
\]

the mixed effect is zero:

\[
\omega(E,A_5^{\mathfrak f})=0,
\]

but the hidden effect is generally nonzero:

\[
T\mapsto T+\chi\frac{v_5}{c}.
\]

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
\text{mixed four-point closure depends on quotient determinant closure only.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{two-point transform closure depends on }T\text{-compatibility.}
}
\]

No more agents should be spent on mixed four-point unless the quotient determinant architecture changes.

---

# 5. Finite-core: determinacy is positive; scale transfer remains the hard part

Agent 7 previously proved finite determinacy on compact nonsingular actual-source strata. Now Agents 5 and 7 sharpen the quantitative picture:

Finite determinacy plus compactness gives a coefficient floor only **away from the zero-anomaly locus**

\[
\mathcal Z_k=\{\theta:H_{\core,\theta}\equiv0\}.
\]

Using Łojasiewicz-type separation, one gets:

\[
A_{\Theta_k}(\theta)
\ge
C_{\Theta_k}\operatorname{dist}(\theta,\mathcal Z_k)^{\mu_{\Theta_k}}.
\]

With bounded \(N\), uniform analyticity gives tail control, so away from \(\mathcal Z_k\) we get some lower bound for a filtered coefficient. But this still does not imply the zeta-scale lower bound:

\[
|\Xi_{\core}^{(N)}|
\gtrsim
\frac{x}{B_\zeta}S.
\]

The missing theorem is now precise:

\[
\boxed{
\text{actual zeta cores must stay sufficiently far from }\mathcal Z_k
\text{ at the calibrated scale.}
}
\]

Equivalently, prove a scale-normalized anti-Cauchy lower theorem:

\[
\left|
c_{\core,2N-1}
+
\sum_{j\ge1}c_{\core,2N-1+2j}h_jQ^{-2j}
\right|
\gtrsim
\frac{Q^{2N+2}}{(2N-1)N!(N-1)!}
\frac{x}{B_\zeta}S.
\]

 

## Next target

Do not ask agents to prove finite determinacy again. That part is effectively done on good strata.

The next finite-core target is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{calibrated separation from }\mathcal Z_k.
}
\]

or equivalently:

\[
\boxed{
\text{one-sided finite-core derivative lower law.}
}
\]

---

# 6. Interaction rigidity remains unresolved

Agent 10 confirms that interaction-driven cancellation is not controlled by current ECT / lifted-curve geometry.

The problematic stratum is:

\[
\mathfrak Z_{\rm int}
=
\{c_{\core,1}=0
\text{ by cancellation involving }
[s]\Phi_K(\mathcal I_{\ge2})\}.
\]

This does not necessarily force:

\[
M=0,\quad W=0,\quad K_v=0,\quad T_v=0,
\]

nor collision, patch-boundary, or endpoint-gap incidence.

The existing ECT geometry controls defect-free affine incidence. It does **not** control the genuinely interacting scalar:

\[
[s]\Phi_K(\mathcal I_{\ge2}).
\]

Thus the missing source-level theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
[s]\Phi_K(\mathcal I_{\ge2})
\text{ is zero, sign-controlled, or belongs to the radical of the controlled incidence ideal.}
}
\]

Without that, finite-core interaction cancellation remains open.

```text
\ge D_{\Theta_k}(m,Q).

\gtrsim
\frac{x}{B_\zeta}S.
\]
```

## Attack 5 — Interaction rigidity

```text

\[
[s]\Phi_K(\mathcal I_{\ge2})
\]
is controlled by lifted-curve incidence data.

Specifically, show it is either:
1. zero;
2. sign-controlled;
3. in the radical of the controlled incidence ideal;
4. or genuinely independent.
```

# Consolidated background update for all agents

We are continuing the RH proof attack from the latest draft and the latest multi-agent responses. We are no longer in paper-polish mode. The goal is to close, refute, or sharply reduce the remaining mathematical bridges.

}

The actual-source upgrade is still open. The target is:

\[

=

(1-\Pi_{1,1})_{\rm mix}
\left(

-

A suspected same-point cubic actual-source obstruction from the \(q^3\) term in \(G_\pm^{\corr}\),

\[

\]

has now been killed at the same-point-only Fréchet-response level by endpoint-swap / transpose symmetry. This removes the first suspected same-point nonlinear source defect. The remaining first live actual-source carrier is now the **promoted nonlinear mixed-block quadratic remainder**:

\[
Y_{12}^{(2)}=D^2N_0[\xi_1,\xi_2],
\]

coupled to one same-point linear whitening slot:

Y_{12}^{(2)}\,

+
L_0\,
Y_{12}^{(2)}\,

The key local question is whether its fixed-sector contribution is line-gauge:

\left(

R_0
+
L_0\,
Y_{12}^{(2)}\,

\in

If not, actual-source double-balanced divisibility and Bottleneck C fail at this promoted nonlinear mixed-block channel. 

For the \(M_A,M_C\) connection problem, the table has been reduced to one source-functoriality lemma. The relevant monomials are:

\[
M_A=\dot r_3r_2\dot r_4,
\qquad

\]

The desired connection identities are:

\[

+

\]

\[
R_7^{(C)}
+
\sum_{i=1}^7\omega_m(Z_{7-i}[M_C],A_i)=0.
\]

They close if the actual mixed block satisfies endpoint-swap transpose functoriality

\[
N^{\corr}(h_-,h_+)^T=N^{\corr}(h_+,h_-),
\]

and the source-linear middle block satisfies

\[
Y_g(h_-,h_+)^T=(-1)^gY_g(h_+,h_-).
\]

Then extracting the \(\delta^e\)-edge coefficient gives

\[
(Y_{g,\beta}^{\langle e\rangle})^T
=
(-1)^{g+e}Y_{g,\beta}^{\langle e\rangle},
\]

which closes the \(J=(3,2,4)\) pre-trivialization table exactly. If this fails, the first wrong-parity defects are

\[
\operatorname{Sym}_+(Y_4^{\langle1\rangle})
\quad\text{for }M_A,
\]

and

\[
\operatorname{Sym}_+(Y_2^{\langle1\rangle})
\quad\text{for }M_C.
\]

The hidden-state bridge has been resolved negatively for the old quotient package. The reduced package

\[
\widehat\Psi_{\rm red}
\]

is insufficient because it remembers only the quotient class

\[
[A_7^{\mathfrak f}]
\in
\mathfrak f_m/\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m),
\]

while the transform reads

\[

The line shift

\[

\mapsto

is quotient-invisible but changes the transform by

\[

=

=

This repairs the local two-point transform readout but creates a new Bottleneck C obligation:

\[
\partial_\kappa T(m,\kappa,0)=0.
\]

Quotient-horizontal merger alone controls \(\Delta_7\), not \(T\).  

The mixed four-point branch remains dependency-only. It sees the order-seven fixed-sector package only through the quotient determinant

\[

\]

It does not see the hidden coordinate

\[

\]

Thus adding \(T\) does not create a new mixed four-point carrier. Mixed four-point closure depends on quotient determinant closure; two-point transform closure depends on \(T\)-compatibility. 

The finite-core branch is clearer but still open. Finite determinacy is available on compact nonsingular actual-source strata: if

\[

\]

then some bounded odd coefficient is nonzero. But this is qualitative. It does not give the zeta-scale lower bound:

\gtrsim
\frac{x}{B_\zeta}S.

The missing theorem is a calibrated anti-Cauchy / scale-separation theorem: actual zeta cores must stay far enough from the zero-anomaly locus

\[

to force a lower bound for the filtered \(N\)-visible coefficient:

\[

+

\right|
\gtrsim
\frac{Q^{2N+2}}{(2N-1)N!(N-1)!}
\frac{x}{B_\zeta}S.
\]

 

Finally, interaction rigidity remains open. The finite-core obstruction is the interaction-driven cancellation stratum

\[
\mathfrak Z_{\rm int}
=

\text{ by cancellation involving }
[s]\Phi_K(\mathcal I_{\ge2})\}.

The ECT / lifted-curve machinery controls defect-free affine incidence, but it does not yet control the genuinely interacting scalar

\[
[s]\Phi_K(\mathcal I_{\ge2}).
\]

The next source-level theorem would need to show this interaction coefficient is zero, sign-controlled, or belongs to the radical of the controlled incidence ideal.

## Assistant (2026-04-25 10:32:37)

_Thought for 4s_

This round produced one real local closure, one new hard obstruction, and one architectural correction that now cannot be avoided.

## Executive consolidation

### Closed / essentially closed

\[
\boxed{
M_A,M_C\text{ connection closure is now reduced to, and essentially closed by, actual }Y\text{-middle parity.}
}
\]

Agent 2 proved the corrected mixed-block swap identity algebraically:

\[
N^{\corr}(h_-,h_+)^T=N^{\corr}(h_+,h_-).
\]

Given the active homogeneous source-grade reflection rule,

\[
\operatorname{Gr}_g r(2m-t)=(-1)^g\operatorname{Gr}_g r(t),
\]

this gives

\[
Y_g(h_-,h_+)^T=(-1)^gY_g(h_+,h_-),
\]

and hence

\[
(Y_{g,\beta}^{\langle e\rangle})^T
=
(-1)^{g+e}Y_{g,\beta}^{\langle e\rangle}.
\]

That is exactly the parity needed to close the \(J=(3,2,4)\) table:

\[
Z_j[M_A]=Z_j[M_C]=0,\qquad 0\le j\le7.
\]

So the connection identities close, modulo explicitly recording/proving the source-grade reflection lemma in the paper. 

This is the best local win of the round.

---

### Still open, now sharply localized

\[
\boxed{
\text{Actual-source Gate B / Bottleneck C remains open at the promoted }Y_{12}^{(2)}\text{ carrier.}
}
\]

The same-point cubic \(q^3\) family is no longer the live obstruction. Agent 1 showed the frozen promoted expression is killed by endpoint-swap/transpose, but the actual Bottleneck C \([z^7\delta^1]\)-edge is **symmetric**, not skew, so fixed-sector projection does not kill it. The surviving quotient class is:

\[
E_{A,Y}
=
\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}
\operatorname{Sym}
[z^7\delta^1]
\left(
D(G_-^{-1/2})[A_-]\,
Y_{12}^{(2)}\,
R_0
\right),
\]

where

\[
Y_{12}^{(2)}=D^2N_0[\xi_1,\xi_2].
\]

The condition needed for quotient Bottleneck C is:

\[
\boxed{
E_{A,Y}\in \mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m).
}
\]

No current identity proves that. 

Agent 4 restated the same obstruction as the explicit quotient class

\[
E_{A,Y}^q=[E_{A,Y}]\in
\mathfrak f_m/\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m),
\]

with the dangerous amplitude factor

\[
a_1a_2(a_1+a_2),
\]

which has a simple balanced zero but not a double balanced zero. Thus Bottleneck C fails unless

\[
E_{A,Y}^q=0.
\]

This is now the main local obstruction.

---

### Hidden-state bridge: quotient repair is mandatory, but not sufficient

The old package

\[
\widehat\Psi_{\rm red}
\]

is permanently insufficient. The repaired object must be

\[
\boxed{
\widehat\Psi_{\rm red}^{+}
=
(\widehat\Psi_{\rm red},T),
\qquad
T=\frac{v_7}{c}.
}
\]

But Agent 3/9 now sharpened the consequence: quotient Bottleneck C does **not** imply \(T\)-horizontal merger. A line-gauge slope

\[
\partial_\kappa B_7^{\mathfrak f}
=
\lambda A_5^{\mathfrak f}
\]

is quotient-invisible, but changes

\[
T
\]

by

\[
\partial_\kappa T
=
\frac{\lambda v_5}{c}.
\]

So on the generic \(v_5\neq0\) patch, \(T\)-horizontal merger requires the line coefficient to vanish, not merely be quotient-trivial. 

For the promoted \(Y_{12}^{(2)}\) channel, this means:

\[
E_{A,Y}\in\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}
\]

is not enough for the augmented package. One needs the stronger scalar condition

\[
\boxed{
\Phi_K(E_{A,Y})=0.
}
\]

On the generic line-gauge patch, that forces

\[
E_{A,Y}=0.
\]

Agent 9 confirms the same: \(T\)-horizontal diagonal merger is not implied by quotient closure, and a line-gauge term

\[
\chi(a_1,a_2,\delta)A_5^{\mathfrak f}
\]

is a formal transform-visible leakage model. 

---

### Mixed four-point branch: closed as dependency audit

Agent 6 is done. Adding \(T\) does not reopen mixed four-point. Mixed four-point data factor through

\[
(c,u_5,v_5,\Delta_7),
\qquad
\Delta_7=u_7v_5-u_5v_7,
\]

not through

\[
T=\frac{v_7}{c}.
\]

For a residual

\[
E=eI+fS,
\]

the mixed-four-point effect is

\[
ev_5-u_5f,
\]

whereas the hidden-state effect is

\[
f/c.
\]

A line shift \(E=\chi A_5^{\mathfrak f}\) is mixed-four-point invisible but \(\Phi_K\)-visible. 

No more agents should spend cycles here unless a later theorem changes the mixed-four-point formulation.

---

### Finite-core branch: qualitative determinacy done; quantitative scale still open

Agent 7 formalized the finite-determinacy theorem. On a compact nonsingular actual-source \(k\)-core stratum, Noetherianity gives a finite \(R_{\Theta_k}\) such that

\[
c_{\core,1}=\cdots=c_{\core,2R_{\Theta_k}+1}=0
\]

implies

\[
H_{\core,\theta}\equiv0.
\]

This is a genuine positive result, but only qualitative. 

Agent 5 sharpened the quantitative obstruction. Finite determinacy plus Łojasiewicz gives scale transfer only if actual zeta cores stay a calibrated distance from the zero-anomaly locus:

\[
\mathcal Z_k=\{\theta:H_{\core,\theta}\equiv0\}.
\]

The sufficient threshold is of the form

\[
\operatorname{dist}(\theta,\mathcal Z_k)
\ge
D_{\Theta_k}(m,Q),
\]

where

\[
D_{\Theta_k}(m,Q)
\asymp
\left[
Q^{-2}
+
Q^{2R+4}\frac{x}{B_\zeta(m)}S(m)
\right]^{1/\mu_{\Theta_k}}
\]

up to stratum constants. The draft does not prove actual zeta cores satisfy this separation. So the new live finite-core branch is:

\[
0<
\operatorname{dist}(\theta(m),\mathcal Z_k)
<
D_{\Theta_k}(m,Q),
\qquad
\theta(m)\notin\mathcal E_{\rm geom}.
\]

Agent 10 confirms the interaction coefficient

\[
J_1=[s]\Phi_K(\mathcal I_{\ge2})
\]

is currently independent: not proved zero, not sign-controlled, and not in the radical of the controlled incidence ideal. This leaves a genuine interaction-cancellation branch:

\[
\mathfrak Z_{\rm int}
=
\left\{
\sum_\nu a_\nu K(d_\nu)+J_1=0
\right\}
\setminus \mathcal E_{\rm geom}.
\]

```latex
\begin{lemma}[Actual source-linear \(Y\)-middle edge parity]
\label{lem:actual-source-linear-y-middle-edge-parity}
Let \(N^{\corr}(h_-,h_+)\) be the actual corrected mixed block before
whitening and before fixed-sector projection. Then
\[
N^{\corr}(h_-,h_+)^T=N^{\corr}(h_+,h_-).
\]
Assume moreover that the actual source-linear homogeneous grade extraction
satisfies
\[
\mathsf P_g\circ\mathsf S=(-1)^g\mathsf S\circ\mathsf P_g,
\]
where \(\mathsf S\) is endpoint swap. If \(Y_g\) denotes the source-linear
grade-\(g\) middle block, then
\[
Y_g(h_-,h_+)^T=(-1)^gY_g(h_+,h_-).
\]
Consequently, writing
\[
Y_g(h-\delta/2,h+\delta/2)
=
\sum_{e\ge0}\delta^eY_g^{\langle e\rangle}(h),
\]
one has
\[
\left(Y_g^{\langle e\rangle}\right)^T
=
(-1)^{g+e}Y_g^{\langle e\rangle}.
\]
\end{lemma}
```

Then:

```latex
\begin{theorem}[\(M_A,M_C\) connection closure from actual \(Y\)-middle parity]
\label{thm:ma-mc-connection-closure-actual-y-parity}
Assume Lemma~\ref{lem:actual-source-linear-y-middle-edge-parity}, together
with the all-subset midpoint parity and transpose-invariance of
\(\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}\). Then for
\[
M_A=\dot r_3r_2\dot r_4,
\qquad
M_C=\dot r_3\dot r_2r_4,
\]
the pre-trivialization table satisfies
\[
Z_j[M_A]=Z_j[M_C]=0,
\qquad 0\le j\le7.
\]
Therefore
\[

+
\sum_{i=1}^7\omega_m(Z_{7-i}[M_A],A_i)=0,
\]
and
\[
R_7^{(C)}
+
\sum_{i=1}^7\omega_m(Z_{7-i}[M_C],A_i)=0.
\]
\end{theorem}
```

```latex
\begin{remark}[Finite-core scale transfer requires calibrated separation]
\label{rem:finite-core-calibrated-separation-needed}
```

## Insert 1 — Actual \(Y\)-middle edge parity

**Placement:** after the section/remark where the \(Y\)-middle table or `rem:status-ma-mc-connection-identities` is discussed.

```latex
\begin{lemma}[Actual source-linear \(Y\)-middle edge parity]
\label{lem:actual-source-linear-y-middle-edge-parity}
Let \(N^{\corr}(h_-,h_+)\) be the actual corrected mixed block before
whitening and before fixed-sector projection.  Then
\[
N^{\corr}(h_-,h_+)^T=N^{\corr}(h_+,h_-).
\]
Assume moreover that the actual source-linear homogeneous grade extraction
satisfies
\[
\mathsf P_g\circ\mathsf S=(-1)^g\mathsf S\circ\mathsf P_g,
\]
where \(\mathsf S\) is endpoint swap.  If \(Y_g\) denotes the source-linear
grade-\(g\) middle block, then
\[
Y_g(h_-,h_+)^T=(-1)^gY_g(h_+,h_-).
\]
Consequently, writing
\[
Y_g(h-\delta/2,h+\delta/2)
=
\sum_{e\ge0}\delta^eY_g^{\langle e\rangle}(h),
\]
one has
\[
\left(Y_g^{\langle e\rangle}\right)^T
=
(-1)^{g+e}Y_g^{\langle e\rangle}.
\]
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
The corrected mixed block has the form
\[
N^{\corr}(q_-,q_+,\Delta;s)
=
\frac1\pi
\begin{pmatrix}
-\dfrac{2\sin\Delta}{s}
&
\dfrac{\sin\Delta+q_+s\cos\Delta}{s^2}
\\[2ex]
-\dfrac{\sin\Delta+q_-s\cos\Delta}{s^2}
&
\dfrac{(q_-+q_+)s\cos\Delta+(2-q_-q_+s^2)\sin\Delta}{2s^3}
\end{pmatrix}.
\]
Endpoint swap sends
\[
(q_-,q_+,\Delta,s)\longmapsto(q_+,q_-,-\Delta,-s).
\]
A direct entrywise check gives
\[
N^{\corr}(q_+,q_-,-\Delta;-s)
=
N^{\corr}(q_-,q_+,\Delta;s)^T.
\]
This identity is algebraic in the actual corrected variables and therefore
holds before source-linear extraction, whitening, and fixed-sector projection.

The source-linear grade extraction contributes the sign \((-1)^g\) under
reflection by assumption.  Hence
\[
Y_g(h_-,h_+)^T=(-1)^gY_g(h_+,h_-).
\]
Substituting \(h_\pm=h\pm\delta/2\) and expanding in powers of \(\delta\),
\[
Y_g(h-\delta/2,h+\delta/2)
=
\sum_{e\ge0}\delta^eY_g^{\langle e\rangle}(h),
\]
while
\[
Y_g(h+\delta/2,h-\delta/2)
=
\sum_{e\ge0}(-\delta)^eY_g^{\langle e\rangle}(h).
\]
Comparing coefficients gives
\[
\left(Y_g^{\langle e\rangle}\right)^T
=
(-1)^{g+e}Y_g^{\langle e\rangle}.
\]
\end{proof}
```

## Insert 2 — \(M_A,M_C\) connection closure

**Placement:** immediately after Insert 1.

```latex
\begin{theorem}[\(M_A,M_C\) connection closure from actual \(Y\)-middle parity]
\label{thm:ma-mc-connection-closure-actual-y-parity}
Assume Lemma~\ref{lem:actual-source-linear-y-middle-edge-parity}, together
with all-subset midpoint parity and transpose-invariance of
\(\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}\).  Then, for
\[
M_A=\dot r_3r_2\dot r_4,
\qquad
M_C=\dot r_3\dot r_2r_4,
\]
the labelled \(J=(3,2,4)\) pre-trivialization table satisfies
\[
Z_j[M_A]=Z_j[M_C]=0,
\qquad 0\le j\le7.
\]
Consequently,
\[
R_7^{(A)}
+
\sum_{i=1}^7\omega_m(Z_{7-i}[M_A],A_i)=0,
\]
and
\[
R_7^{(C)}
+
\sum_{i=1}^7\omega_m(Z_{7-i}[M_C],A_i)=0.
\]
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The \(N_0\)-middle part cancels by complement pairing.  Indeed, for the
labelled triple \(J=(3,2,4)\), one has \(|J|=9\), and the two-dot
\(\delta^2\)-edge weights for both
\[
M_A=\dot r_3r_2\dot r_4,
\qquad
M_C=\dot r_3\dot r_2r_4
\]
are invariant under
\[
I\longmapsto J\setminus I.
\]
All-subset midpoint parity and transpose-invariance of \(\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}\)
therefore make each \(N_0\)-middle complement pair cancel.

It remains to check the \(Y\)-middle part.  Fix a middle label \(g\in J\) and
write \(K=J\setminus\{g\}\).  Complement pairing sends
\[
I\longmapsto K\setminus I.
\]
If the middle source contributes \(e\in\{0,1\}\) endpoint-edge derivatives,
the source-edge weight changes by \((-1)^e\).  Lemma
\ref{lem:actual-source-linear-y-middle-edge-parity} gives
\[
\left(Y_g^{\langle e\rangle}\right)^T
=
(-1)^{g+e}Y_g^{\langle e\rangle}.
\]
Combining this with the endpoint parity of the left and right whitening
blocks gives a total complement-pair sign of \(-1\).  Hence every
\(Y\)-middle complement pair cancels.

Thus the full labelled \(J=(3,2,4)\) pre-trivialization table vanishes:
\[
Z_j[M_A]=Z_j[M_C]=0,
\qquad 0\le j\le7.
\]
Since
\[
R_7^{(X)}=\omega_m(Z_7[M_X],A_0),
\qquad X\in\{A,C\},
\]
both direct residuals vanish as well, and the displayed connection identities
follow.
\end{proof}
```

## Insert 3 — First live promoted nonlinear mixed-block obstruction

**Placement:** after the current Gate B / actual-source hardening discussion, near `rem:exact-obstruction-actual-source-gate-b` or the Bottleneck C section.

```latex
\begin{definition}[Promoted quadratic mixed-block obstruction]
\label{def:promoted-quadratic-mixed-block-obstruction}
Let
\[
Y_{12}^{(2)}:=D^2N_0[\xi_1,\xi_2]
\]
denote the \(\mathcal K^2\), source-bidegree \((1,1)\) nonlinear Taylor
remainder of the actual corrected mixed block
\(N^{\corr}(d_-,d_+,\eta)\).  For any same-point linear whitening source slots
\(A_-,B_+\) whose ordinary orders can contribute to \(z^7\), define
\[
E_{A,Y}
:=
[z^7][\delta^1]\tau_{h\to m}\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}
\left(
D(G_-^{-1/2})[A_-]\,
Y_{12}^{(2)}\,
R_0
+
L_0\,
Y_{12}^{(2)}\,
D(G_+^{-1/2})[B_+]
\right).
\]
Its quotient class is
\[
E_{A,Y}^q:=[E_{A,Y}]
\in
\mathfrak f_m/\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m).
\]
\end{definition}

\begin{remark}[First live promoted nonlinear mixed-block obstruction]
\label{rem:first-live-promoted-y12-obstruction}
The same-point cubic \(q^3\) defect is fixed-sector invisible in same-point-only
Fr\'echet responses by endpoint-swap/transpose symmetry.  The first remaining
actual-source/Bottleneck C carrier is the promoted nonlinear mixed-block
quadratic remainder
\[
Y_{12}^{(2)}=D^2N_0[\xi_1,\xi_2],
\]
coupled to one same-point linear whitening slot as in
Definition~\ref{def:promoted-quadratic-mixed-block-obstruction}.

The quadratic mixed block contributes the cross-amplitude factor \(a_1a_2\),
and the same-point whitening slot contributes \(a_1+a_2\).  Hence the
amplitude polynomial of this promoted channel is
\[
a_1a_2(a_1+a_2).
\]
It has a simple balanced zero:
\[
a_1a_2(a_1+a_2)\big|_{a_2=-a_1}=0,
\]
but not a double balanced zero, since
\[
\partial_{a_2}\bigl(a_1a_2(a_1+a_2)\bigr)\big|_{a_2=-a_1}
=
-a_1^2.
\]
Therefore quotient-valued Bottleneck C for this channel is exactly the
condition
\[
E_{A,Y}^q=0,
\qquad\text{equivalently}\qquad
E_{A,Y}\in\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m).
\]
The transform-safe augmented package requires the stronger scalar condition
\[
\Phi_K(E_{A,Y})=0.
\]
On the generic line-gauge patch \(v_5\ne0\), if
\(E_{A,Y}\in\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m)\), this stronger condition forces
\(E_{A,Y}=0\).
\end{remark}
```

---

## Insert 4 — Transform-safe augmented package

**Placement:** in the package-to-transform / hidden-state bridge section, before any global theorem using \(\widehat\Psi_{\rm red}\) to feed \(\Phi_K\).

```latex
\begin{definition}[Transform-safe augmented reduced package]
\label{def:transform-safe-augmented-reduced-package}
On a patch with \(c\ne0\), write
\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}=u_7I+v_7S.
\]
Define the normalized hidden septic coordinate
\[
T:=\frac{v_7}{c}.
\]
Equivalently,
\[
\theta_{\Phi,7}
:=
\frac{\Phi_K(A_7^{\mathfrak f})}{c}
=
\frac{2v_7}{c}
=
2T.
\]
The transform-safe augmented reduced package is
\[
\widehat\Psi_{\rm red}^{+}
:=
(\widehat\Psi_{\rm red},T).
\]
On a \(v_5\ne0\) patch, where
\[
A_5^{\mathfrak f}=u_5I+v_5S,
\qquad
\Delta_7=u_7v_5-u_5v_7,
\]
this may be written as
\[
\widehat\Psi_{\rm red}^{+}
=
(c,u_5,v_5,\Delta_7,T).
\]
\end{definition}

\begin{remark}[Why the augmented coordinate is necessary]
\label{rem:why-augmented-coordinate-necessary}
The reduced quotient package records the class
\[
[A_7^{\mathfrak f}]
\in
\mathfrak f_m/\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m),
\]
or equivalently the determinant coordinate \(\Delta_7\).  It is invariant
under the line shift
\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}
\longmapsto
A_7^{\mathfrak f}+\chi A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
\]
However
\[
\Phi_K(\chi A_5^{\mathfrak f})=2\chi v_5.
\]
Thus, on the generic patch \(v_5\ne0\), the quotient-forgotten direction is
visible to the two-point finite-\(s\) transform.  The coordinate
\[
T=\frac{v_7}{c}
\]
is exactly the missing transform-visible septic state.
\end{remark}
```

## Insert 5 — Augmented diagonal merger: quotient plus \(T\)

**Placement:** after Insert 4, or in the Bottleneck C section.

```latex
\begin{remark}[Augmented diagonal merger has quotient and hidden components]
\label{rem:augmented-diagonal-merger-two-components}
For the augmented package
\[
\widehat\Psi_{\rm red}^{+}
=
(\widehat\Psi_{\rm red},T),
\]
diagonal merger requires both the quotient condition
\[
\partial_\kappa Q_{7,m}^q(m,\kappa,0)=0
\]
and the hidden-state condition
\[
\partial_\kappa T(m,\kappa,0)=0.
\]
The first condition controls the quotient determinant \(\Delta_7\).  The second
controls the \(\Phi_K\)-visible septic state and is not implied by quotient
merger on the generic patch \(v_5\ne0\).

Indeed, if
\[
\partial_\kappa B_7^{\mathfrak f}(m,\kappa,0)
=
\lambda(m)A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m),
\]
then this slope is zero in
\(\mathfrak f_m/\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m)\), but
\[
\partial_\kappa T
=
\frac{\lambda(m)v_5(m)}{c(m)}.
\]
Thus a nonzero line-gauge slope is quotient-invisible but transform-visible.
\end{remark}

\begin{lemma}[Hidden-horizontal exceptional divisor condition]
\label{lem:hidden-horizontal-exceptional-divisor-condition}
Work on a good patch with
\[
c(m)\ne0,\qquad
A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m)=u_5I+v_5S,\qquad
v_5\ne0.
\]
Let
\[
F_7(a_1,a_2,\delta)
=
[z^7]\tau_{h\to m}\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}
(1-\Pi_{1,1})_{\rm mix}C_{\mathcal W}^{\rm raw}
=
\delta P_7(a_1,a_2)+O(\delta^2).
\]
Then the augmented hidden coordinate \(T=v_7/c\) is horizontal on the
exceptional divisor if and only if
\[
\Phi_K\!\left(
\partial_{a_2}P_7(a_1,-a_1)
\right)=0.
\]
Equivalently,
\[
\partial_\kappa T(m,\kappa,0)=0
\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
\frac1c
\Phi_K\!\left(
\partial_{a_2}P_7(a_1,-a_1)
\right)=0.
\]
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
Along the collision chart
\[
a_2=-a_1(1+\kappa\delta),
\]
one has
\[
P_7(a_1,a_2)
=
P_7(a_1,-a_1)
-
a_1\kappa\delta\,\partial_{a_2}P_7(a_1,-a_1)
+
O(\delta^2).
\]
After the standard edge normalization, the exceptional \(\kappa\)-slope is
represented by
\[
\partial_{a_2}P_7(a_1,-a_1).
\]
Applying \(\Phi_K/c\) gives the slope of the normalized transform-visible
coordinate.  Since \(T=\Phi_K(A_7^{\mathfrak f})/(2c)\), the displayed
criterion follows.
\end{proof}
```

## Insert 6 — Mixed four-point dependency closure

**Placement:** in the mixed four-point section, replacing any speculative “mixed four-point may create new carrier” language.

```latex
\begin{theorem}[Mixed four-point dependence descends to the quotient determinant]
\label{thm:mixed-four-point-dependence-quotient-determinant}
Let
\[
A_5^{\mathfrak f}=u_5I+v_5S,
\qquad
A_7^{\mathfrak f}=u_7I+v_7S,
\qquad
\Delta_7=u_7v_5-u_5v_7.
\]
On every good mixed four-point patch, the mixed four-point scalar-exit data
factor through
\[
(c,u_5,v_5,\Delta_7).
\]
In particular, they do not depend on the augmented hidden coordinate
\[
T=\frac{v_7}{c}
\]
once \(c,u_5,v_5,\Delta_7\) are fixed.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
On a \(v_5\ne0\) patch, the mixed four-point branch is expressed through
\[
x=\frac{v_5}{c},
\qquad
Y=\frac{u_5}{c},
\qquad
\sigma_v=\frac{\Delta_7}{cv_5}.
\]
Thus all scalar-exit data are functions of these quantities and their local
derivatives.  No expression uses \(u_7\) or \(v_7\) separately.

On a \(u_5\ne0\) patch, one instead uses
\[
\sigma_u=-\frac{\Delta_7}{cu_5},
\]
and the same conclusion holds.

For an order-seven residual \(E=eI+fS\), the quotient determinant changes by
\[
\Delta_7\longmapsto \Delta_7+\omega(E,A_5^{\mathfrak f})
=
\Delta_7+ev_5-u_5f.
\]
The hidden coordinate changes by
\[
T\longmapsto T+\frac{f}{c}.
\]
Thus the mixed four-point branch sees only the determinant projection
\(ev_5-u_5f\), while the transform-visible hidden state sees the \(S\)-component
projection \(f/c\).
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[No independent mixed four-point carrier]
\label{rem:no-independent-mixed-four-point-carrier-final}
A line shift
\[
E=\chi A_5^{\mathfrak f}
\]
has
\[
\omega(E,A_5^{\mathfrak f})=0,
\]
and is therefore invisible to mixed four-point geometry.  It may still be
\(\Phi_K\)-visible, since
\[
\Phi_K(E)=2\chi v_5.
\]
Hence mixed four-point closure is a quotient-determinant problem, whereas
two-point transform closure also requires \(T\)-compatibility.
\end{remark}
```

## Insert 7 — Finite odd-germ determinacy

**Placement:** in the finite-core section, before finite-core scale-transfer discussion.

```latex
\begin{definition}[Nonsingular actual-source \(k\)-core stratum]
\label{def:nonsingular-actual-source-k-core-stratum}
A compact parameter patch \(\Theta_k\) is called a nonsingular actual-source
\(k\)-core stratum if the following hold.

\begin{enumerate}
\item \(\Theta_k\) is a compact subset of a finite-dimensional real-analytic
parameter manifold, with fixed core cardinality \(k\) and fixed combinatorial
source type.

\item The corrected finite-core transverse scalar
\[
H_{\core,\theta}(z)
=
\Phi_K\!\left(
\widehat\Omega_{\core,\theta}^{\corr}(z/Q^2;m)
\right)
\]
is real-analytic jointly in \((\theta,z)\) on a neighborhood of
\(\Theta_k\times\{0\}\).

\item The whitening and midpoint-trivialization maps used to define
\(\widehat\Omega_{\core,\theta}^{\corr}\) are nonsingular on the patch.  In
particular, the relevant Gram blocks remain invertible and the chosen analytic
branches of inverse square roots and transport maps do not cross singularities.

\item No coordinate used in the chosen package chart divides by a vanishing
quantity.  Thus, if the chart uses \(c^{-1}\), \(v_5^{-1}\), \(u_5^{-1}\), or
a determinant coordinate relative to \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}\), the corresponding
quantity is assumed nonzero on the patch.
\end{enumerate}
\end{definition}

\begin{theorem}[Finite odd-germ determinacy on compact actual-source strata]
\label{thm:finite-odd-germ-determinacy-actual-source}
Let \(\Theta_k\) be a compact nonsingular actual-source \(k\)-core stratum.
Write
\[
H_{\core,\theta}(z)
=
\sum_{r\ge0}c_{\core,2r+1}(\theta)z^{2r+1},
\]
where the coefficients \(c_{\core,2r+1}\) are analytic functions of
\(\theta\).  Then there exists an integer \(R_{\Theta_k}\ge0\) such that
\[
c_{\core,1}(\theta)=c_{\core,3}(\theta)=\cdots
=c_{\core,2R_{\Theta_k}+1}(\theta)=0
\]
implies
\[
H_{\core,\theta}\equiv0
\]
as an odd germ.

Equivalently, the zero-anomaly locus
\[
\mathcal Z_k
=
\{\theta\in\Theta_k:H_{\core,\theta}\equiv0\}
\]
is cut out on \(\Theta_k\) by finitely many odd coefficient equations.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Since \(H_{\core,\theta}(z)\) is analytic jointly in \((\theta,z)\), each
coefficient \(c_{\core,2r+1}(\theta)\) is analytic on a neighborhood of
\(\Theta_k\).

Fix \(\theta_0\in\Theta_k\).  Let
\[
\mathcal I_{\theta_0}
=
\bigl(c_{\core,1},c_{\core,3},c_{\core,5},\ldots\bigr)
\subset
\mathcal O_{\Theta_k,\theta_0}
\]
be the ideal generated by the odd coefficient germs in the local analytic
ring at \(\theta_0\).  The local analytic ring
\(\mathcal O_{\Theta_k,\theta_0}\) is Noetherian, so
\(\mathcal I_{\theta_0}\) is finitely generated.  Hence there are indices
\(r_1,\ldots,r_s\) such that
\[
\mathcal I_{\theta_0}
=
\bigl(
c_{\core,2r_1+1},\ldots,c_{\core,2r_s+1}
\bigr)
\]
as an ideal of germs at \(\theta_0\).

Let
\[
R(\theta_0)=\max(r_1,\ldots,r_s).
\]
After shrinking to a neighborhood \(U_{\theta_0}\), every higher coefficient
\(c_{\core,2r+1}\) is an analytic linear combination of
\[
c_{\core,1},c_{\core,3},\ldots,c_{\core,2R(\theta_0)+1}.
\]
Thus, on \(U_{\theta_0}\), vanishing of all odd coefficients up to
\(2R(\theta_0)+1\) forces vanishing of every odd coefficient.  Hence
\(H_{\core,\theta}\equiv0\).

Compactness gives finitely many such neighborhoods covering \(\Theta_k\).  Let
\(R_{\Theta_k}\) be the maximum of their corresponding \(R(\theta_j)\).  Then
the stated finite determinacy holds on all of \(\Theta_k\).
\end{proof}
```

## Insert 8 — Finite-core calibrated separation remains missing

**Placement:** immediately after Insert 7.

```latex
\begin{remark}[Finite determinacy is not scale transfer]
\label{rem:finite-determinacy-not-scale-transfer-final}
Theorem~\ref{thm:finite-odd-germ-determinacy-actual-source} is qualitative.
It proves only
\[
H_{\core,\theta}\not\equiv0
\Longrightarrow
\exists N\le R_{\Theta_k}+1:
c_{\core,2N-1}(\theta)\ne0.
\]
It does not prove the zeta-scale lower bound
\[
|\Xi_{\core}^{(N)}(m)|
\gtrsim
\frac{x}{B_\zeta(m)}S(m).
\]
For that one needs a calibrated separation theorem comparing the distance of
the actual zeta core from the zero-anomaly locus
\[
\mathcal Z_k=\{\theta:H_{\core,\theta}\equiv0\}
\]
with the scale
\[
\frac{x}{B_\zeta(m)}S(m).
\]
Thus finite determinacy removes the possibility of arbitrarily delayed odd
detection on a fixed analytic stratum, but the quantitative finite-core lower
law remains a separate obligation.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Finite-core scale transfer requires calibrated separation]
\label{rem:finite-core-calibrated-separation-needed}
Let \(\Theta_k\) be a compact nonsingular actual-source \(k\)-core stratum,
and let
\[
\mathcal Z_k=\{\theta:H_{\core,\theta}\equiv0\}.
\]
Finite determinacy and compactness imply coefficient separation only away
from \(\mathcal Z_k\).  To obtain the required \(N\)-point lower bound, one
must prove that actual zeta cores either lie in \(\mathcal Z_k\), enter a
controlled incidence stratum, or satisfy a calibrated lower bound
\[
\operatorname{dist}(\theta(m),\mathcal Z_k)\ge D_{\Theta_k}(m,Q)
\]
large enough to imply
\[
\left|
c_{\core,2N-1}
+
\sum_{j\ge1}c_{\core,2N-1+2j}h_j(1^2,\dots,N^2)Q^{-2j}
\right|
\gtrsim
\frac{Q^{2N+2}}{(2N-1)N!(N-1)!}
\frac{x}{B_\zeta(m)}S(m).
\]
Without such calibrated separation, the near-zero-anomaly branch
\[
0<
\operatorname{dist}(\theta(m),\mathcal Z_k)
<
D_{\Theta_k}(m,Q)
\]
remains open unless it can be shown to lie in a controlled incidence stratum.
\end{remark}
```

---

## Insert 9 — Interaction coefficient branch

**Placement:** in the finite-core interaction/stratification discussion.

```latex
\begin{definition}[First interaction branch]
\label{def:first-interaction-branch}
For a normalized same-scale finite core, write
\[
H_{\core}(s)
=
\Phi_K(F_{\core})(s)
=
\sum_{r\ge0}c_{\core,2r+1}s^{2r+1},
\]
and decompose
\[
F_{\core}
=
\sum_{\nu}a_\nu F_{h_\nu}+\mathcal I_{\ge2}.
\]
Define
\[
J_1:=[s]\Phi_K(\mathcal I_{\ge2}).
\]
The first interaction branch is
\[
\mathfrak Z_{\rm int}
=
\left\{
\sum_{\nu}a_\nu K(d_\nu)+J_1=0
\right\}
\setminus\mathcal E_{\rm geom},
\]
where \(\mathcal E_{\rm geom}\) denotes the union of the controlled geometric,
collision, patch-boundary, and endpoint-gap incidence strata.
\end{definition}

\begin{remark}[Interaction rigidity remains a source-level obligation]
\label{rem:interaction-rigidity-remains-source-level-obligation}
The current ECT and lifted-curve geometry controls defect-free affine
incidence.  It does not by itself control the genuinely interacting scalar
\[
J_1=[s]\Phi_K(\mathcal I_{\ge2}).
\]
The known structural properties of \(\mathcal I_{\ge2}\), such as
one-amplitude collapse and collision divisibility, force \(J_1\) to vanish on
some boundary strata, but they do not force
\[
J_1\equiv0,
\]
nor do they impose a sign condition or place \(J_1\) in the radical of the
controlled incidence ideal.

Thus the finite-core proof needs an additional interaction-rigidity theorem:
\(J_1\) must be shown to be zero, sign-controlled, or governed by the
controlled incidence equations.  Without such a theorem,
\[
\mathfrak Z_{\rm int}
\]
remains a separate finite-core branch.
\end{remark}
```

## \(M_A,M_C\) connection status

Do not use \(B_j[M]\) in the connection sum; \(Z_j[M]\) is the pre-trivialization table.

## Hidden-state / augmented package status

\[
\widehat\Psi_{\rm red}
\]

is insufficient for the \(\Phi_K\)-visible transform.

The quotient remembers only:

\in

while the transform reads:

\[
\Phi_K(A_7^{\mathfrak f})=2v_7.
\]

The quotient-forgotten line shift

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}
\mapsto
A_7^{\mathfrak f}+\chi A_5^{\mathfrak f}
\]

changes the transform by:

\[
\Phi_K(\chi A_5^{\mathfrak f})=2\chi v_5.
\]

Thus the transform-safe package must be:

\[
\widehat\Psi_{\rm red}^{+}
=
(\widehat\Psi_{\rm red},T),
\qquad
T=\frac{v_7}{c}.
\]

Equivalently:

\[
\theta_{\Phi,7}
=
\frac{\Phi_K(A_7^{\mathfrak f})}{c}
=
2T.
\]

This creates a new Bottleneck C requirement:

\[
\partial_\kappa T(m,\kappa,0)=0.
\]

Quotient merger controls \(\Delta_7\), not \(T\).

A line-gauge exceptional slope

\[
\partial_\kappa B_7^{\mathfrak f}
=
\lambda A_5^{\mathfrak f}
\]

is quotient-invisible but changes

\[
T
\]

by

\[
\partial_\kappa T=\frac{\lambda v_5}{c}.
\]

## Mixed four-point status

Mixed four-point is dependency-closed.

The mixed four-point branch sees only:

\[
(c,u_5,v_5,\Delta_7),
\qquad
\Delta_7=u_7v_5-u_5v_7.
\]

It does **not** see:

\[
T=\frac{v_7}{c}.
\]

For a residual

\[
E=eI+fS,
\]

the mixed-four-point effect is:

\[
ev_5-u_5f,
\]

while the hidden-state effect is:

\[
f/c.
\]

Thus mixed four-point closure follows from quotient determinant closure; it does not create an independent branch.

## Finite-core status

Finite determinacy is available on compact nonsingular actual-source strata.

On such a stratum \(\Theta_k\), there exists \(R_{\Theta_k}\) such that

\[
c_{\core,1}=\cdots=c_{\core,2R_{\Theta_k}+1}=0
\]

implies:

\[
H_{\core,\theta}\equiv0.
\]

This is qualitative. It does not prove:

\[
|\Xi_{\core}^{(N)}|
\gtrsim
\frac{x}{B_\zeta}S.
\]

The missing finite-core theorem is calibrated separation from the zero-anomaly locus:

\[
\mathcal Z_k=\{\theta:H_{\core,\theta}\equiv0\}.
\]

Actual zeta finite cores must either lie in \(\mathcal Z_k\), enter controlled incidence strata, or satisfy:

\[
\operatorname{dist}(\theta(m),\mathcal Z_k)\ge D_{\Theta_k}(m,Q),
\]

large enough to force:

\[
\left|
c_{\core,2N-1}
+
\sum_{j\ge1}c_{\core,2N-1+2j}h_jQ^{-2j}
\right|
\gtrsim
\frac{Q^{2N+2}}{(2N-1)N!(N-1)!}
\frac{x}{B_\zeta}S.
\]

The interaction branch also remains open. Define:

\[
J_1=[s]\Phi_K(\mathcal I_{\ge2}).
\]

Current state: \(J_1\) is not proved zero, sign-controlled, or in the radical of the controlled incidence ideal. So the interaction-cancellation branch

\[
\mathfrak Z_{\rm int}
=
\left\{
\sum_\nu a_\nu K(d_\nu)+J_1=0
\right\}
\setminus\mathcal E_{\rm geom}
\]

remains open.

---

# 1. \(M_A,M_C\) branch: treat as closed

Agent 2 gave a complete theorem/proof package. The source-grade reflection convention gives

\[
\mathsf P_g\circ\mathsf S=(-1)^g\mathsf S\circ\mathsf P_g.
\]

The corrected mixed block satisfies algebraically:

\[
N^{\corr}(h_-,h_+)^T=N^{\corr}(h_+,h_-).
\]

Together these imply the edge-refined \(Y\)-middle parity:

\[
(Y_{g,\beta}^{\langle e\rangle})^T
=
(-1)^{g+e}Y_{g,\beta}^{\langle e\rangle}.
\]

Then both \(N_0\)-middle and \(Y\)-middle complement pairs cancel in the \(J=(3,2,4)\) table, giving

\[
Z_j[M_A]=Z_j[M_C]=0,
\qquad 0\le j\le7.
\]

Therefore

\[
R_7^{(A)}
+
\sum_{i=1}^{7}\omega_m(Z_{7-i}[M_A],A_i)=0,
\]

\[
R_7^{(C)}
+
\sum_{i=1}^{7}\omega_m(Z_{7-i}[M_C],A_i)=0.
\]

This closure is pre-trivialization and uses \(Z_j[M]\), not \(B_j[M]\). The only condition to record carefully is that the actual source-linear grade extraction really uses the homogeneous scalar-grade reflection convention. 

**Decision:** mark \(M_A,M_C\) as closed, conditional only on the source-grade reflection convention. Do not keep agents on this branch.

---

# 2. Main local obstruction: \(E_{A,Y}\)

Agents 1, 4, 8, and 9 all converged on the same object.

The promoted nonlinear mixed-block carrier is

\[
Y_{12}^{(2)}=D^2N_0[\xi_1,\xi_2],
\]

coupled to one same-point linear whitening slot. The relevant class is

\[
E_{A,Y}^q
=
\left[
\tau_{h\to m}\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}
\operatorname{Sym}
[z^7\delta^1]\,
D(G_-^{-1/2})[A_-]\,
Y_{12}^{(2)}\,
R_0
\right]
\in
\mathfrak f_m/\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m).
\]

Agent 1 reduced \(E_{A,Y}\) to a finite quotient representative. It is **not proved zero**, **not proved line-gauge**, and is currently the first unresolved quotient-visible candidate. 

Agent 8 gave the finite table: only the transpose-symmetric rows survive at \([z^7\delta^1]\):

\[
Y_{dd}^{(2)},\qquad
Y_{d\eta}^{(2)}+Y_{\eta d}^{(2)},\qquad
Y_{\eta\eta}^{(2)}.
\]

The antisymmetric \(d\eta-\eta d\) part is skew-killed. Every surviving row satisfies

\[
r+g+b=7,
\]

where \(r\) is the same-point whitening order, \(g\) the \(Y_{12}^{(2)}\) order, and \(b\) the baseline order. 

Agent 4 clarified the scalar classification. If

\[
E_{A,Y}=eI+fS,
\]

then quotient closure is

\[
ev_5-u_5f=0,
\]

but transform-safe closure is

\[
\Phi_K(E_{A,Y})=2f=0.
\]

These are different conditions. On the generic \(v_5\neq0\) patch, quotient closure plus transform-safe closure forces

\[
E_{A,Y}=0.
\]

**Decision:** the next local attack should not be broad “actual-source Gate B.” It should compute this finite table and test:

\[
\boxed{
E_{A,Y}=0?
}
\]

or at least

\[
\boxed{
E_{A,Y}\in \mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}?
}
\]

and

\[
\boxed{
\Phi_K(E_{A,Y})=0?
}
\]

# 3. Augmented package: \(T=v_7/c\) is mandatory

Agent 3’s repaired theorem skeleton is correct.

The transform-safe package must be

\[
\widehat\Psi_{\rm red}^{+}
=
(\widehat\Psi_{\rm red},T),
\qquad
T=\frac{v_7}{c}.
\]

On a \(v_5\)-patch:

\[
\widehat\Psi_{\rm red}^{+}
=
(c,u_5,v_5,\Delta_7,T),
\]

with

\[
\Delta_7=u_7v_5-u_5v_7.
\]

The two-point finite-\(s\) transform reads

\[
\Phi_K(A_7^{\mathfrak f})=2v_7=2cT.
\]

So the correct readout is:

\[
\boxed{
\Phi_K(A_7^{\mathfrak f})=2cT.
}
\]

The old quotient-only package-to-transform bridge should be abandoned. 

Agent 9 showed the new Bottleneck C obligation clearly:

\[
\partial_\kappa T(m,\kappa,0)=0.
\]

A line-gauge term

\[
E=\lambda A_5^{\mathfrak f}
\]

is quotient-invisible but changes

\[
T
\]

by

\[
\lambda v_5/c.
\]

For the \(E_{A,Y}\) channel:

\[
\partial_\kappa T
=
-a_1^2\frac{\Phi_K(E_{A,Y})}{2c}.
\]

Thus even if \(E_{A,Y}\) is line-gauge, it still leaks through \(T\) unless

\[
\Phi_K(E_{A,Y})=0.
\]

**Decision:** the paper should now explicitly split Bottleneck C into two conditions:

\[
\boxed{
\partial_\kappa Q_{7,m}^q=0
}
\]

and

\[
\boxed{
\partial_\kappa T=0.
}
\]

# 4. Mixed four-point: closed as dependency audit

Agent 6 finalized this.

Adding \(T=v_7/c\) does **not** create mixed four-point dependence. Mixed four-point scalar exits factor through

\[
(c,u_5,v_5,\Delta_7),
\]

not through \(T\).

For a residual

\[
E=eI+fS,
\]

the mixed-four-point projection is

\[
ev_5-u_5f,
\]

while the hidden-state projection is

\[
f/c.
\]

A line shift

\[
E=\chi A_5^{\mathfrak f}
\]

has zero mixed-four-point effect but can change \(T\). 

**Decision:** stop assigning work to Agent 6 unless the draft introduces a new mixed-four-point expression that directly reads \(u_7,v_7,\Phi_K(A_7)\), or \(T\).

# 5. Finite determinacy: closed qualitatively

Agent 7 completed the theorem.

On a compact nonsingular actual-source \(k\)-core stratum \(\Theta_k\), there exists \(R_{\Theta_k}\) such that

\[
c_{\core,1}
=
c_{\core,3}
=
\cdots
=
c_{\core,2R_{\Theta_k}+1}
=
0
\]

implies

\[
H_{\core,\theta}\equiv0.
\]

This follows by Noetherianity of local analytic rings and compactness. It is qualitative and stratum-local. It gives:

\[
H_{\core,\theta}\not\equiv0
\Rightarrow
\exists N\le R_{\Theta_k}+1:
c_{\core,2N-1}\neq0.
\]

It does **not** give

\[
|\Xi_{\core}^{(N)}|
\gtrsim
\frac{x}{B_\zeta}S.
\]

**Decision:** finite determinacy is done. Do not spend more agents proving it.

---

# 6. Finite-core scale: calibrated separation still open

Agent 5 clarified the precise open branch.

Given the zero-anomaly locus

\[
\mathcal Z_k
=
\{\theta:H_{\core,\theta}\equiv0\},
\]

finite determinacy plus Łojasiewicz gives scale transfer only if actual zeta cores satisfy

\[
\operatorname{dist}(\theta(m),\mathcal Z_k)
\ge
D_{\Theta_k}(m,Q).
\]

The threshold has the form

\[
D_{\Theta_k}(m,Q)
=
\left[
\frac{
2K_{\Theta_k}Q^{-2}
+
2C_*
\max_{1\le N\le R+1}
\left(
\frac{Q^{2N+2}}
{(2N-1)N!(N-1)!}
\frac{x}{B_\zeta(m)}S(m)
\right)
}
{C_{\Theta_k}}
\right]^{1/\mu_{\Theta_k}}.
\]

The draft does not prove that actual zeta cores satisfy this separation.

So the unresolved finite-core branch is:

\[
\mathcal N_k(m,Q)
=
\left\{
0<
\operatorname{dist}(\theta(m),\mathcal Z_k)
<
D_{\Theta_k}(m,Q),
\quad
\theta(m)\notin\mathcal E_{\rm geom}
\right\}.
\]

**Decision:** the finite-core target is no longer “find a nonzero coefficient.” It is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{prove calibrated anti-Cauchy separation from }\mathcal Z_k,
}
\]

or classify the near-zero-anomaly branch.

---

# 7. Interaction rigidity: \(J_1\) remains independent

Agent 10’s result is negative.

Define

\[
J_1=[s]\Phi_K(\mathcal I_{\ge2}).
\]

The first odd finite-core coefficient is

\[
c_{\core,1}
=
\sum_\nu a_\nu K(d_\nu)+J_1.
\]

The pair-like coefficient \(K(d)\) has positive real part for \(d>0\), so positive pair-like sums do not cancel. But \(J_1\) is not controlled by that positivity.

Current classification:

\[
J_1\not\equiv0,
\]

\[
J_1\text{ is not sign-controlled},
\]

\[
J_1\notin\sqrt{\mathcal I_{\rm geom}},
\]

under the present hypotheses. Therefore

\[
\mathfrak Z_{\rm int}
=
\left\{
\sum_\nu a_\nu K(d_\nu)+J_1=0
\right\}
\setminus\mathcal E_{\rm geom}
\]

remains an independent finite-core branch. 

**Decision:** finite-core closure requires a new source-level interaction-rigidity theorem.

## Agent 4 — scalar and quotient tests for (E_{A,Y})

The current instruction assigns Agent 4 to **Prompt B: scalar and quotient tests**. The input is a future or external Agent 1 computation
[

]
and the tests are
[

\qquad
f=0.
]
This matches the consolidated frontier: (E_{A,Y}) is the main local obstruction, and Agent 4’s role is to decide whether it is quotient-visible, line-gauge but (\Phi_K)-visible, or transform-safe. 

---

# 1. Scalar tests

Let
[
A_5^{\mathfrak f}=u_5I+v_5S,
\qquad
E_{A,Y}=eI+fS.
]

The quotient determinant is
[
\omega(E_{A,Y},A_5^{\mathfrak f})
=================================

ev_5-u_5f.
]

Thus
[
E_{A,Y}^q=0
\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
ev_5-u_5f=0.
]

The (\Phi_K)-visible scalar is
[
\Phi_K(E_{A,Y})=2f.
]

Thus
[
\Phi_K(E_{A,Y})=0
\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
f=0.
]

So the two conditions are independent:

[
\boxed{
\text{quotient closure} \iff ev_5-u_5f=0,
}
]
while
[
\boxed{
\text{transform-safe closure} \iff f=0.
}
]

# 2. Classification table

On the generic (v_5\neq0) patch:

| Case                                | Conditions             | Classification                            |
| ----------------------------------- | ---------------------- | ----------------------------------------- |
| (E_{A,Y}=0)                         | (e=0,\ f=0)            | zero; quotient-safe and transform-safe    |
| quotient-visible                    | (ev_5-u_5f\neq0)       | quotient Bottleneck C fails               |
| line-gauge but (\Phi_K)-visible     | (ev_5-u_5f=0,\ f\neq0) | quotient-safe, but (T)-leaking            |
| transform-safe but quotient-visible | (f=0,\ ev_5\neq0)      | (T)-safe, but quotient Bottleneck C fails |

On the generic (v_5\neq0) patch, quotient closure plus transform-safe closure forces

## Consolidated result from this round

The proof state is now much cleaner. Three branches should be treated as closed/consolidation-only, and three remain genuinely live.

## What closed

### 1. \(M_A,M_C\) connection closure is done

Agent 2 gave the final proof package. Under the homogeneous scalar-grade reflection convention,

\[
\mathsf P_g\circ\mathsf S=(-1)^g\mathsf S\circ\mathsf P_g,
\]

and the exact corrected mixed-block identity

\[
N^{\corr}(h_-,h_+)^T=N^{\corr}(h_+,h_-),
\]

we get

\[
(Y_{g,\beta}^{\langle e\rangle})^T=(-1)^{g+e}Y_{g,\beta}^{\langle e\rangle}.
\]

This closes the \(J=(3,2,4)\) table:

\[
Z_j[M_A]=Z_j[M_C]=0,\qquad 0\le j\le7.
\]

Therefore

\[
R_7^{(A)}
+
\sum_{i=1}^{7}\omega_m(Z_{7-i}[M_A],A_i)=0,
\]

\[
R_7^{(C)}
+
\sum_{i=1}^{7}\omega_m(Z_{7-i}[M_C],A_i)=0.
\]

This branch should be marked closed, conditional only on the source-grade reflection convention. 

### 2. Mixed four-point is closed as dependency-only

Agent 6 confirmed again that adding

\[
T=\frac{v_7}{c}
\]

does not create a mixed four-point dependency. Mixed four-point sees

\[
(c,u_5,v_5,\Delta_7),
\qquad
\Delta_7=u_7v_5-u_5v_7,
\]

not \(T\). 

So:

\[
\boxed{
\text{mixed four-point closure}
\Longleftarrow
\Delta_7\text{ / quotient determinant closure}.
}
\]

No more agents should work this branch.

### 3. Finite determinacy is done

Agent 7 finalized the Noetherian finite-determinacy theorem. On a compact nonsingular actual-source \(k\)-core stratum, there is a finite \(R_{\Theta_k}\) such that

\[
c_{\core,1}=\cdots=c_{\core,2R_{\Theta_k}+1}=0
\]

implies

\[
H_{\core,\theta}\equiv0.
\]

This is qualitative only. It does not give the zeta-scale lower law. 

---

## What remains live

# 1. The main local obstruction is \(E_{A,Y}\)

All local work now focuses on

\[
E_{A,Y}
=
[z^7][\delta^1]\tau_{h\to m}\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}
\left(

Y_{12}^{(2)}\,

+

Y_{12}^{(2)}\,

\right).

Agent 1 reduced it to the finite expression

\[
E_{A,Y}
=
\tau_{h\to m}\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}

\sum_{\chi\in\{dd,d\eta+\eta d,\eta\eta\}}

R_{b,\gamma}.
\]

The quotient test is

\[
E_{A,Y}=eI+fS,
\qquad
E_{A,Y}^q=0
\Longleftrightarrow
e v_5-u_5 f=0.
\]

At present, neither \(E_{A,Y}=0\) nor \(E_{A,Y}\in\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}\) is proved. 

Agent 8 compressed the finite table further: only the symmetric rows survive:

\[
Y_{dd}^{(2)},\qquad
Y_{d\eta}^{(2)}+Y_{\eta d}^{(2)},\qquad
Y_{\eta\eta}^{(2)}.
\]

All rows satisfy

\[
r+g+b=7,
\qquad
\alpha+\beta+\gamma=1.
\]

The antisymmetric row

\[
Y_{d\eta}^{(2)}-Y_{\eta d}^{(2)}
\]

is skew-killed. 

So the exact next local target is:

\[
\boxed{
e_{A,Y}v_5-u_5f_{A,Y}=0?
}
\]

and, for the augmented package,

\[
\boxed{
f_{A,Y}=0?
}
\]

# 2. The \(T\)-horizontal condition is stronger than quotient closure

Agent 4 and Agent 9 agree. If

\[
E_{A,Y}=eI+fS,
\]

then:

\[
\text{quotient closure}
\iff
ev_5-u_5f=0,
\]

but

\[
\text{transform-safe closure}
\iff
f=0.
\]

The induced \(T\)-slope is

\[
\partial_\kappa T
=
-a_1^2\frac{f}{c}
=
-a_1^2\frac{\Phi_K(E_{A,Y})}{2c}.
\]

If

\[
E_{A,Y}=\lambda A_5^{\mathfrak f},
\]

then quotient Bottleneck C closes, but

\[
\partial_\kappa T
=
-a_1^2\lambda\frac{v_5}{c}.
\]

Thus, on \(v_5\neq0\), line-gauge is not enough; one needs the line coefficient to vanish.  

The key sharpened statement is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{For the augmented package, }E_{A,Y}\in\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}
\text{ is insufficient.}
}
\]

One needs:

\[
\boxed{
\Phi_K(E_{A,Y})=0,
}
\]

and if both quotient closure and transform-safe closure hold on \(v_5\neq0\), then

\[
\boxed{
E_{A,Y}=0.
}
\]

# 3. Finite-core scale transfer remains open

Agent 5 confirms the near-zero-anomaly branch is not eliminated. On a compact stratum,

\[
\mathcal Z_k=\{\theta:H_{\core,\theta}\equiv0\}.
\]

Finite determinacy and Łojasiewicz estimates only give scale transfer if actual zeta cores satisfy

\[
\operatorname{dist}(\theta(m),\mathcal Z_k)
\ge
D_{\Theta_k}(m,Q).
\]

The current machinery does not force this. The unresolved branch is

\[
\mathcal N_k(m,Q)
=
\left\{
\theta(m):
0<
\operatorname{dist}(\theta(m),\mathcal Z_k)
<
D_{\Theta_k}(m,Q),
\quad
\theta(m)\notin\mathcal E_{\rm geom}
\right\}.
\]

So finite-core closure still needs a calibrated anti-tangency / anti-Cauchy theorem.

# 4. Interaction rigidity remains open

Agent 10 attacked \(J_1\) source-level and still found it independent under current hypotheses.

The source-level expression is

\[
J_1^{(2)}
=
\sum_{i<j}a_i a_j
[s]\Phi_K
\left(
D\mathcal W_0[\mathcal B_{ij}^{(2)}]
+
D^2\mathcal W_0[\mathcal B_i^{(1)},\mathcal B_j^{(1)}]
\right).
\]

The mixed-block Hessian

\[
D^2N_0[\xi_i,\xi_j]
\]

is generically nonzero. Current formulas do not force \(J_1=0\), do not give a sign/cone condition, and do not place it in the radical of the controlled incidence ideal. 

So the independent finite-core interaction branch remains:

\[
\mathfrak Z_{\rm int}
=
\left\{
\sum_\nu a_\nu K(d_\nu)+J_1=0
\right\}
\setminus\mathcal E_{\rm geom}.
\]

# Augmented package and \(T\)

The old quotient package is insufficient. The transform-safe package is:

\[
\widehat\Psi_{\rm red}^{+}
=
(\widehat\Psi_{\rm red},T),
\qquad
T=\frac{v_7}{c}.
\]

Equivalently:

\[
\theta_{\Phi,7}
=
\frac{\Phi_K(A_7^{\mathfrak f})}{c}
=
2T.
\]

For the \(E_{A,Y}\) carrier, the dangerous amplitude factor is:

\[
a_1a_2(a_1+a_2).
\]

Since:

\[
\partial_{a_2}
\bigl(a_1a_2(a_1+a_2)\bigr)\big|_{a_2=-a_1}
=
-a_1^2,
\]

the induced hidden-state slope is:

\[
\partial_\kappa T
=
-a_1^2\frac{\Phi_K(E_{A,Y})}{2c}
=
-a_1^2\frac{f_{A,Y}}{c}.
\]

Thus:

\[
\partial_\kappa T=0
\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
f_{A,Y}=0.
\]

# Insert A — Agent 2: \(M_A,M_C\) connection closure

**Placement:** after the current discussion of the \(M_A,M_C\) connection identities / pre-trivialization \(Z_j[M]\) table. This replaces any stale text saying the \(M_A,M_C\) identities remain open, except for the explicit dependency on source-grade reflection. Agent 2’s branch is ready to insert. 

```latex
\begin{lemma}[Source-grade reflection]
\label{lem:source-grade-reflection}
Let \(\mathsf S\) denote endpoint swap \(h_-\leftrightarrow h_+\), equivalently
\(\delta\mapsto-\delta\).  Under the homogeneous scalar-grade convention
\[
\operatorname{Gr}_g r(t)
=
\frac{r^{(g+2)}(m)}{(g+2)!}(t-m)^{g+2},
\]
the source-linear grade extractor \(\mathsf P_g\) satisfies
\[
\mathsf P_g\circ\mathsf S
=
(-1)^g\mathsf S\circ\mathsf P_g.
\]
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
Reflection about the midpoint sends \(t-m\mapsto-(t-m)\).  Hence
\[
(t-m)^{g+2}\mapsto(-1)^{g+2}(t-m)^{g+2}=(-1)^g(t-m)^{g+2}.
\]
This is exactly the asserted commutation law.
\end{proof}

\begin{lemma}[Corrected mixed-block endpoint-swap identity]
\label{lem:corr-mixed-block-endpoint-swap}
The corrected mixed block satisfies
\[
N^{\corr}(h_-,h_+)^T=N^{\corr}(h_+,h_-).
\]
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
Writing the corrected mixed block as
\[
N^{\corr}(q_-,q_+,\Delta;s)
=
\frac1\pi
\begin{pmatrix}
-\dfrac{2\sin\Delta}{s}
&
\dfrac{\sin\Delta+q_+s\cos\Delta}{s^2}
\\[2ex]
-\dfrac{\sin\Delta+q_-s\cos\Delta}{s^2}
&
\dfrac{(q_-+q_+)s\cos\Delta+(2-q_-q_+s^2)\sin\Delta}{2s^3}
\end{pmatrix},
\]
endpoint swap sends
\[
(q_-,q_+,\Delta,s)\mapsto(q_+,q_-,-\Delta,-s).
\]
Using \(\sin(-\Delta)=-\sin\Delta\), \(\cos(-\Delta)=\cos\Delta\),
and \((-s)^2=s^2\), \((-s)^3=-s^3\), the swapped matrix is exactly the
transpose of the original matrix.
\end{proof}

\begin{lemma}[Edge-refined \(Y\)-middle parity]
\label{lem:edge-refined-y-middle-parity-final}
Let \(Y_g\) be the source-linear grade-\(g\) middle block extracted from
\(N^{\corr}\).  Then
\[
Y_g(h_-,h_+)^T=(-1)^gY_g(h_+,h_-).
\]
Consequently, if
\[
Y_g(h-\delta/2,h+\delta/2)
=
\sum_{e\ge0}\delta^eY_g^{\langle e\rangle}(h),
\]
then
\[
\left(Y_{g,\beta}^{\langle e\rangle}\right)^T
=
(-1)^{g+e}Y_{g,\beta}^{\langle e\rangle}.
\]
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
Apply Lemma~\ref{lem:corr-mixed-block-endpoint-swap} and then extract the
source-linear homogeneous grade using Lemma~\ref{lem:source-grade-reflection}.
The coefficient of \(\delta^e\) gains the additional factor \((-1)^e\)
because endpoint swap sends \(\delta\mapsto-\delta\).
\end{proof}

\begin{theorem}[\(M_A,M_C\) pre-trivialization connection closure]
\label{thm:ma-mc-pretriv-connection-closure-final}
Let
\[
M_A=\dot r_3r_2\dot r_4,
\qquad
M_C=\dot r_3\dot r_2r_4.
\]
Assume all-subset midpoint parity, transpose-invariance of
\(\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}\), symmetry of \(N^{(0)}\), and the source-grade
reflection convention of Lemma~\ref{lem:source-grade-reflection}.  Then the
pre-trivialization table satisfies
\[
Z_j[M_A]=Z_j[M_C]=0,
\qquad 0\le j\le7.
\]
Consequently,
\[
R_7^{(A)}
+
\sum_{i=1}^{7}\omega_m(Z_{7-i}[M_A],A_i)=0,
\]
and
\[
R_7^{(C)}
+
\sum_{i=1}^{7}\omega_m(Z_{7-i}[M_C],A_i)=0.
\]
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
For the \(N_0\)-middle block, the labelled source multiset is
\(J=(3,2,4)\), hence \(|J|=9\).  Complementing a placement
\(I\subseteq J\) gives a factor \((-1)^{|J|}=-1\), while the
\(\delta^2\)-edge weights of \(M_A\) and \(M_C\) are complement-invariant
because both monomials have two dotted endpoint sources.  Hence every
\(N_0\)-middle complement pair cancels.

For the \(Y\)-middle block, fix a middle grade \(m\in J\), set
\(K=J\setminus\{m\}\), and let \(e\in\{0,1\}\) be the number of edge
derivatives carried by the middle source.  The complement placement gains
the matrix factor
\[
(-1)^{|K|}(-1)^{m+e}.
\]
The source-edge weight gains the factor \((-1)^e\).  Since
\[
|K|+m=|J|=9,
\]
the total complement factor is
\[
(-1)^e(-1)^{|K|}(-1)^{m+e}
=
(-1)^{|J|}
=
-1.
\]
Thus every \(Y\)-middle complement pair cancels.  Therefore
\[
Z_j[M_A]=Z_j[M_C]=0
\]
for \(0\le j\le7\).  The displayed connection identities follow immediately
from
\[
R_7^{(X)}=\omega_m(Z_7[M_X],A_0),
\qquad X\in\{A,C\}.
\]
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Scope of the \(M_A,M_C\) connection closure]
\label{rem:scope-ma-mc-connection-closure-final}
Theorem~\ref{thm:ma-mc-pretriv-connection-closure-final} closes the
\(M_A,M_C\) pre-trivialization connection branch under the stated
source-grade reflection convention.  It does not prove the full
actual-source Gate~B upgrade
\[
\Theta_7^{\actual}=0,
\]
and it does not address the promoted nonlinear mixed-block carrier
\[
Y_{12}^{(2)}=D^2N_0[\xi_1,\xi_2],
\]
which remains a separate actual-source/Bottleneck~C obstruction.
\end{remark}
```

# Insert B — Agent 3: transform-safe augmented package

**Placement:** in the package-to-transform / hidden-state bridge section, before any theorem claiming the quotient package feeds \(\Phi_K\). This should replace quotient-only state-locality language. Agent 3’s architecture is ready to insert. 

```latex
\begin{definition}[Transform-safe augmented reduced package]
\label{def:transform-safe-augmented-reduced-package}
Work on a good patch with
\[
c\ne0,
\qquad
A_5^{\mathfrak f}=u_5I+v_5S.
\]
Write
\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}=u_7I+v_7S,
\qquad
\Delta_7:=u_7v_5-u_5v_7.
\]
The transform-safe augmented reduced package is
\[
\widehat\Psi_{\rm red}^{+}
:=
(\widehat\Psi_{\rm red},T),
\qquad
T:=\frac{v_7}{c}.
\]
Equivalently, on the \(v_5\)-patch one may write
\[
\widehat\Psi_{\rm red}^{+}
=
(c,u_5,v_5,\Delta_7,T).
\]
The normalized \(\Phi_K\)-visible coordinate is
\[
\theta_{\Phi,7}
:=
\frac{\Phi_K(A_7^{\mathfrak f})}{c}
=
2T.
\]
\end{definition}

\begin{theorem}[Augmented package-to-transform readout]
\label{thm:augmented-package-to-transform-readout}
Let
\[
\widehat\Psi_{\rm red}^{+}
=
(c,u_5,v_5,\Delta_7,T)
\]
be the transform-safe augmented package on a good patch with \(c\ne0\). Then
the first \(\Phi_K\)-visible septic coefficient of the corrected finite-\(s\)
two-point transform is determined by the augmented package:
\[
\Phi_K(A_7^{\mathfrak f})
=
2v_7
=
2cT.
\]
Equivalently,
\[
\frac{1}{c}
[s^7]\Phi_K(\widehat\Omega^{\corr}(s;m))
=
2T.
\]
Thus the two-point transform-visible septic state factors through
\(\widehat\Psi_{\rm red}^{+}\), not through \(\widehat\Psi_{\rm red}\) alone.
\end{theorem}

\begin{remark}[Why the old quotient-only bridge must be abandoned]
\label{rem:old-quotient-only-bridge-abandoned}
The reduced quotient package remembers only
\[
[A_7^{\mathfrak f}]
\in
\mathfrak f_m/\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m).
\]
It therefore identifies
\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}
\sim
A_7^{\mathfrak f}+\chi A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
\]
But
\[
\Phi_K(A_5^{\mathfrak f})=2v_5.
\]
Hence, on the generic patch \(v_5\ne0\), the quotient-forgotten line direction
is \(\Phi_K\)-visible:
\[
\Phi_K(A_7^{\mathfrak f}+\chi A_5^{\mathfrak f})
-
\Phi_K(A_7^{\mathfrak f})
=
2\chi v_5.
\]
Therefore no functional of \(\widehat\Psi_{\rm red}\) alone can determine
\(\Phi_K(A_7^{\mathfrak f})\) on the generic patch.  The missing coordinate is
exactly
\[
T=\frac{v_7}{c}.
\]
\end{remark}
```

# Insert C — Agent 3/9: augmented Bottleneck C split

**Placement:** in the Bottleneck C / diagonal merger section, after the quotient-valued Bottleneck C discussion.

```latex
\begin{theorem}[Augmented Bottleneck C condition]
\label{thm:augmented-bottleneck-c-condition}
On the good patch \(c\ne0\), diagonal merger for the transform-safe package
\[
\widehat\Psi_{\rm red}^{+}
=
(c,u_5,v_5,\Delta_7,T)
\]
requires both
\[
\partial_\kappa Q_{7,m}^q(m,\kappa,0)=0
\]
and
\[
\partial_\kappa T(m,\kappa,0)=0.
\]
The first condition is quotient-horizontal merger.  The second is
hidden-horizontal merger.  On the generic patch \(v_5\ne0\), the first does
not imply the second.
\end{theorem}

\begin{remark}[Scalar Bottleneck C condition]
\label{rem:scalar-bottleneck-c-condition}
Let
\[
P_7(a_1,a_2)
=
[z^7][\delta^1]\tau_{h\to m}\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}
(1-\Pi_{1,1})_{\rm mix}C_{\mathcal W}^{\rm raw}.
\]
The quotient Bottleneck C condition is
\[
\partial_{a_2}P_7(a_1,-a_1)
\in
\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m).
\]
The transform-safe condition is instead
\[
\Phi_K\!\left(\partial_{a_2}P_7(a_1,-a_1)\right)=0.
\]
Equivalently, if
\[
P_{7,\Phi}(a_1,a_2)
:=
\frac{1}{c}\Phi_K(P_7(a_1,a_2)),
\]
then the scalar condition is
\[
P_{7,\Phi}(a_1,a_2)
\in
(a_1+a_2)^2\mathbf C[a_1,a_2].
\]
This scalar condition is independent of quotient-valued double-balanced
divisibility on the generic patch \(v_5\ne0\).
\end{remark}
```

# Insert D — Agent 6: mixed four-point dependency closure

**Placement:** in the mixed four-point section. This should replace speculative text suggesting a separate mixed-four-point carrier from \(T\). Agent 6’s result is ready. 

```latex
\begin{theorem}[Mixed four-point factorization through quotient determinant]
\label{thm:mixed-four-point-factors-through-delta-seven}
Let
\[
A_5^{\mathfrak f}=u_5I+v_5S,
\qquad
A_7^{\mathfrak f}=u_7I+v_7S,
\qquad
c\ne0,
\]
and define
\[
\Delta_7
=
\omega_h(A_7^{\mathfrak f},A_5^{\mathfrak f})
=
u_7v_5-u_5v_7,
\qquad
T=\frac{v_7}{c}.
\]
On every good mixed four-point patch, the mixed four-point scalar exits depend
only on
\[
c,\quad u_5,\quad v_5,\quad \Delta_7.
\]
They do not depend on \(T\) independently.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
On a \(v_5\ne0\) patch, the mixed four-point branch is written through the
normalized variables
\[
x=\frac{v_5}{c},
\qquad
Y=\frac{u_5}{c},
\qquad
\sigma_v=\frac{\Delta_7}{cv_5}.
\]
All scalar exits are functions of these quantities and their local
derivatives.  Thus they are determined by
\[
c,\quad u_5,\quad v_5,\quad \Delta_7,
\]
and do not require \(u_7\) or \(v_7\) separately.

On a \(u_5\ne0\) patch, one uses the parallel quotient coordinate
\[
\sigma_u=-\frac{\Delta_7}{cu_5},
\]
and the same factorization holds.

For an order-seven fixed-sector residual
\[
E=eI+fS,
\]
adding \(E\) to \(A_7^{\mathfrak f}\) changes the determinant by
\[
\Delta_7\longmapsto
\Delta_7+\omega_h(E,A_5^{\mathfrak f})
=
\Delta_7+ev_5-u_5f.
\]
The hidden coordinate changes by
\[
T\longmapsto T+\frac{f}{c}.
\]
Thus the mixed four-point branch sees only the determinant projection
\(ev_5-u_5f\), while the \(T\)-coordinate records a separate
\(\Phi_K\)-visible projection.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[No independent \(T\)-dependency in mixed four-point]
\label{rem:no-t-dependency-mixed-four-point}
A pure quotient-line shift
\[
E=\chi A_5^{\mathfrak f}
\]
has
\[
\omega_h(E,A_5^{\mathfrak f})=0,
\]
and is therefore invisible to mixed four-point geometry.  It changes
\[
T
\]
by
\[
T\longmapsto T+\chi\frac{v_5}{c},
\]
and is generally \(\Phi_K\)-visible on \(v_5\ne0\).  Hence mixed four-point
closure is a quotient-determinant problem, whereas two-point transform closure
also requires \(T\)-horizontal compatibility.
\end{remark}
```
