# Insert E — Agent 7: finite determinacy

**Placement:** in the finite-core section, before calibrated separation / finite-core lower transfer. Agent 7’s theorem is ready. 

```latex
\begin{definition}[Nonsingular actual-source \(k\)-core stratum]
\label{def:nonsingular-actual-source-k-core-stratum}
A compact parameter patch \(\Theta_k\) is called a nonsingular actual-source
\(k\)-core stratum if the following conditions hold.

\begin{enumerate}
\item \(\Theta_k\) is contained in a finite-dimensional real-analytic
parameter manifold with fixed core cardinality \(k\), fixed source
combinatorics, and fixed collision/blow-up chart.

\item The corrected finite-core transverse scalar
\[
H_{\core,\theta}(z)
=
\Phi_K\!\left(
\widehat\Omega_{\core,\theta}^{\corr}(z/Q^2;m)
\right)
\]
is real-analytic jointly in \((\theta,z)\) on a neighborhood of
\(\Theta_k\times\{0\}\).

\item The whitening, inverse-square-root, and midpoint-trivialization maps used
to define \(\widehat\Omega_{\core,\theta}^{\corr}\) are nonsingular and
analytic on the patch.

\item The chosen coordinate chart does not divide by a vanishing quantity.  In
particular, if the chart uses \(c^{-1}\), \(u_5^{-1}\), \(v_5^{-1}\), or a
determinant coordinate relative to \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}\), the corresponding
quantity is nonzero on the patch.
\end{enumerate}
\end{definition}

\begin{theorem}[Finite odd-germ determinacy on compact actual-source strata]
\label{thm:finite-odd-germ-determinacy-actual-source}
Let \(\Theta_k\) be a compact nonsingular actual-source \(k\)-core stratum.
Write
\[
H_{\core,\theta}(z)
=
\sum_{r\ge0}c_{\core,2r+1}(\theta)z^{2r+1}.
\]
Then there exists an integer \(R_{\Theta_k}\ge0\) such that
\[
c_{\core,1}(\theta)=c_{\core,3}(\theta)=\cdots
=c_{\core,2R_{\Theta_k}+1}(\theta)=0
\]
implies
\[
H_{\core,\theta}\equiv0
\]
as an odd germ.

Equivalently, the zero-anomaly locus
\[
\mathcal Z_k
=
\{\theta\in\Theta_k:H_{\core,\theta}\equiv0\}
\]
is cut out on \(\Theta_k\) by finitely many odd coefficient equations.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
By joint analyticity of \(H_{\core,\theta}(z)\), each coefficient
\[
c_{\core,2r+1}(\theta)
\]
is real-analytic on a neighborhood of \(\Theta_k\).

Fix \(\theta_0\in\Theta_k\).  Let
\[
\mathcal I_{\theta_0}
=
\bigl(c_{\core,1},c_{\core,3},c_{\core,5},\ldots\bigr)
\subset
\mathcal O_{\Theta_k,\theta_0}
\]
be the ideal generated by the odd coefficient germs in the local analytic ring
at \(\theta_0\).  The local analytic ring is Noetherian.  Hence
\(\mathcal I_{\theta_0}\) is finitely generated.  Therefore there are indices
\(r_1,\ldots,r_s\) such that
\[
\mathcal I_{\theta_0}
=
\bigl(
c_{\core,2r_1+1},\ldots,c_{\core,2r_s+1}
\bigr)
\]
as germs at \(\theta_0\).

Set
\[
R(\theta_0)=\max(r_1,\ldots,r_s).
\]
After shrinking to a neighborhood \(U_{\theta_0}\), every coefficient
\(c_{\core,2r+1}\) is an analytic linear combination of
\[
c_{\core,1},c_{\core,3},\ldots,c_{\core,2R(\theta_0)+1}.
\]
Thus, on \(U_{\theta_0}\), vanishing of all odd coefficients up to order
\(2R(\theta_0)+1\) forces every odd coefficient to vanish.  Hence
\(H_{\core,\theta}\equiv0\) as an odd germ.

The compactness of \(\Theta_k\) gives a finite subcover
\[
U_{\theta_1},\ldots,U_{\theta_M}.
\]
Taking
\[
R_{\Theta_k}
=
\max_{1\le j\le M}R(\theta_j)
\]
proves the claim uniformly on \(\Theta_k\).
\end{proof}
```

---

# Insert F — finite determinacy scope and handoff

**Placement:** immediately after Insert E.

```latex
\begin{remark}[Strata excluded from one finite-determinacy patch]
\label{rem:finite-determinacy-excluded-strata}
Theorem~\ref{thm:finite-odd-germ-determinacy-actual-source} is stratum-local.
The following loci must be separated before applying it.

\begin{enumerate}
\item \emph{Amplitude-drop strata:}
\[
a_j=0,
\]
where a \(k\)-core degenerates to a smaller core.

\item \emph{Collision strata:}
\[
h_i=h_j,
\]
unless a collision/blow-up coordinate chart has been chosen in which the
corrected source construction remains analytic.

\item \emph{Whitening singularities:} loci where the relevant Gram blocks lose
invertibility or the inverse-square-root branches cease to be analytic.

\item \emph{\(c=0\) strata:} these must be excluded from charts using
\[
T=\frac{v_7}{c}
\]
or any other \(c^{-1}\)-normalization.

\item \emph{\(A_5^{\mathfrak f}=0\) strata:} these are rank-jump loci for the
quotient line
\[
\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
\]

\item \emph{\(v_5=0\) and \(u_5=0\) patch boundaries:} these must be separated
when using the corresponding \(v_5\)-patch or \(u_5\)-patch coordinates.

\item \emph{Hidden-state rank jumps:} loci where the augmented package
coordinate
\[
T=\frac{v_7}{c}
\]
or the \(\Phi_K\)-visible lift ceases to be represented by the chosen analytic
chart.
\end{enumerate}

After separating these loci, finite odd-germ determinacy applies on each
compact nonsingular analytic stratum.
\end{remark}

\begin{corollary}[Coefficient floor away from the zero-anomaly locus]
\label{cor:coefficient-floor-away-from-zero-anomaly}
Let \(\Theta_k\) be a compact nonsingular actual-source \(k\)-core stratum, and
let \(R_{\Theta_k}\) be the finite-determinacy depth from
Theorem~\ref{thm:finite-odd-germ-determinacy-actual-source}.  Define
\[
\mathcal Z_k
=
\{\theta\in\Theta_k:H_{\core,\theta}\equiv0\}.
\]
For \(\eta>0\), set
\[
\Theta_{k,\eta}
=
\{\theta\in\Theta_k:
\operatorname{dist}(\theta,\mathcal Z_k)\ge\eta\}.
\]
Then there exists \(\gamma_\eta>0\) such that every
\(\theta\in\Theta_{k,\eta}\) satisfies
\[
\max_{0\le r\le R_{\Theta_k}}
|c_{\core,2r+1}(\theta)|
\ge
\gamma_\eta.
\]
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
The function
\[
D(\theta)
=
\max_{0\le r\le R_{\Theta_k}}
|c_{\core,2r+1}(\theta)|
\]
is continuous on \(\Theta_k\).  By
Theorem~\ref{thm:finite-odd-germ-determinacy-actual-source},
\[
D(\theta)=0
\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
\theta\in\mathcal Z_k.
\]
Thus \(D>0\) on the compact set \(\Theta_{k,\eta}\), and hence \(D\) has a
positive minimum there.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Finite determinacy is not zeta-scale transfer]
\label{rem:finite-determinacy-not-zeta-scale-transfer}
Theorem~\ref{thm:finite-odd-germ-determinacy-actual-source} is qualitative.
It proves only
\[
H_{\core,\theta}\not\equiv0
\Longrightarrow
\exists N\le R_{\Theta_k}+1:
c_{\core,2N-1}(\theta)\ne0.
\]
It does not prove
\[
|\Xi_{\core}^{(N)}(m)|
\gtrsim
\frac{x}{B_\zeta(m)}S(m).
\]
Nor does it provide a sign law, a tail-domination estimate for the filtered
\(N\)-point coefficient, or an explicit bound for \(R_{\Theta_k}\) depending
only on \(k\).

The remaining quantitative problem is to compare the actual zeta core's
distance from
\[
\mathcal Z_k
\]
with the calibration scale
\[
\frac{x}{B_\zeta(m)}S(m).
\]
That is the calibrated separation problem, not a consequence of
Noetherian finite determinacy.
\end{remark}

\begin{hypothesis}[Calibrated finite-core separation]
\label{hyp:calibrated-finite-core-separation}
Let \(\Theta_k\) be a compact nonsingular actual-source \(k\)-core stratum,
with zero-anomaly locus
\[
\mathcal Z_k
=
\{\theta:H_{\core,\theta}\equiv0\}.
\]
For actual zeta finite cores \(\theta(m)\), either
\[
\theta(m)\in\mathcal Z_k,
\]
or \(\theta(m)\) lies in a controlled incidence stratum, or else
\[
\operatorname{dist}(\theta(m),\mathcal Z_k)
\ge
D_{\Theta_k}(m,Q),
\]
where \(D_{\Theta_k}(m,Q)\) is large enough to force
\[
\left|
c_{\core,2N-1}
+
\sum_{j\ge1}
c_{\core,2N-1+2j}
h_j(1^2,\ldots,N^2)Q^{-2j}
\right|
\gtrsim
\frac{Q^{2N+2}}{(2N-1)N!(N-1)!}
\frac{x}{B_\zeta(m)}S(m)
\]
for some
\[
N\le R_{\Theta_k}+1.
\]
\end{hypothesis}
```

## Agent 4 — quotient and scalar tests for (E_{A,Y})

The current Agent 4 instruction is conditional on Agent 1 producing
[
E_{A,Y}=eI+fS.
]
Until (e,f) are computed, the best possible result is the decisive scalar reduction. The attached command states that the local problem has collapsed to computing or controlling exactly:
[
e_{A,Y}v_5-u_5f_{A,Y},
\qquad
f_{A,Y}.
]
It also gives the induced (T)-slope formula for this carrier. 

---

# 1. Two decisive tests

Let
[
A_5^{\mathfrak f}=u_5I+v_5S,
\qquad
E_{A,Y}=eI+fS.
]

The quotient obstruction is
[
Q_{A,Y}:=\omega(E_{A,Y},A_5^{\mathfrak f})
=ev_5-u_5f.
]

Therefore
[
\boxed{
E_{A,Y}^q=0
\Longleftrightarrow
Q_{A,Y}=ev_5-u_5f=0.
}
]

The transform-visible scalar is
[
\Phi_K(E_{A,Y})=2f.
]

Therefore
[
\boxed{
\Phi_K(E_{A,Y})=0
\Longleftrightarrow
f=0.
}
]

Thus quotient Bottleneck C and augmented (T)-horizontal Bottleneck C are logically distinct.

---

# 2. Classification

Given (E_{A,Y}=eI+fS), classify as follows.

## Case 1: fully safe

[
e=0,\qquad f=0.
]

Then
[
Q_{A,Y}=0,
\qquad
\Phi_K(E_{A,Y})=0.
]

So both quotient merger and (T)-horizontal merger close.

[
\boxed{
E_{A,Y}=0
\Rightarrow
\text{fully safe.}
}
]

---

## Case 2: quotient-visible

[
Q_{A,Y}=ev_5-u_5f\neq0.
]

Then quotient Bottleneck C fails.

Even if (f=0), the quotient obstruction remains:
[
Q_{A,Y}=ev_5.
]

So
[
\boxed{
Q_{A,Y}\neq0
\Rightarrow
\text{quotient Bottleneck C fails.}
}
]

---

## Case 3: line-gauge but (\Phi_K)-visible

[
Q_{A,Y}=0,
\qquad
f\neq0.
]

Then
[
E_{A,Y}\in\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f},
]
but
[
\Phi_K(E_{A,Y})=2f\neq0.
]

This closes quotient Bottleneck C but leaks through the augmented hidden coordinate (T).

Equivalently, write
[
E_{A,Y}=\lambda A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
]
Then
[
e=\lambda u_5,
\qquad
f=\lambda v_5.
]

So
[
Q_{A,Y}=0,
]
but
[
\Phi_K(E_{A,Y})=2\lambda v_5.
]

On the generic (v_5\neq0) patch, this vanishes only if
[
\lambda=0.
]

Thus
[
\boxed{
E_{A,Y}\in\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}
\text{ is not enough for the augmented package.}
}
]

---

## Case 4: (T)-safe but quotient-visible

[
f=0,
\qquad
Q_{A,Y}=ev_5\neq0.
]

Then
[
\Phi_K(E_{A,Y})=0,
]
but quotient Bottleneck C fails.

So
[
\boxed{
T\text{-horizontal closure does not imply quotient closure.}
}
]

---

# 3. Induced (T)-slope

The dangerous amplitude factor is
[
a_1a_2(a_1+a_2).
]

Since
[
\partial_{a_2}\bigl(a_1a_2(a_1+a_2)\bigr)
=========================================

a_1^2+2a_1a_2,
]
we get
[
\partial_{a_2}\bigl(a_1a_2(a_1+a_2)\bigr)\big|_{a_2=-a_1}
=========================================================

-a_1^2.
]

Therefore
[
\partial_\kappa T
=================

# -a_1^2\frac{\Phi_K(E_{A,Y})}{2c}

-a_1^2\frac{f}{c}.
]

If
[
E_{A,Y}=\lambda A_5^{\mathfrak f},
]
then
[
f=\lambda v_5,
]
and hence
[
\boxed{
\partial_\kappa T
=================

-a_1^2\lambda\frac{v_5}{c}.
}
]

So on the generic (v_5\neq0) patch:
[
\boxed{
\partial_\kappa T=0
\Longleftrightarrow
f=0.
}
]

If line-gauge is also known, then:
[
\boxed{
\partial_\kappa T=0
\Longleftrightarrow
E_{A,Y}=0.
}
]

---

# 4. What the augmented package requires

The quotient package only needs:
[
ev_5-u_5f=0.
]

The transform-safe augmented package needs:
[
f=0.
]

On the generic (v_5\neq0) patch, proving both requires:
[
E_{A,Y}=0.
]

Therefore the correct target is stronger than line-gauge:

[
\boxed{
\text{Augmented Bottleneck C requires full vanishing of }E_{A,Y}
\text{ on the generic line-gauge patch.}
}
]

The theorem-ready form is:

```latex
\begin{theorem}[Augmented safety test for the promoted mixed-block carrier]
\label{thm:augmented-safety-test-eay}
Let
\[
E_{A,Y}=eI+fS,
\qquad
A_5^{\mathfrak f}=u_5I+v_5S.
\]
Then quotient Bottleneck C for the promoted quadratic mixed-block carrier is
equivalent to
\[
ev_5-u_5f=0.
\]
The augmented \(T\)-horizontal condition is equivalent to
\[
f=0.
\]
Consequently, on the generic \(v_5\ne0\) patch, quotient closure together
with \(T\)-horizontal closure is equivalent to
\[
E_{A,Y}=0.
\]
\end{theorem}
```

Current status:

[
\boxed{
\text{Agent 4 is blocked only on the explicit Agent 1 computation of }(e,f).
}
]

Once (e,f) are known, the classification is immediate.

=====

# Agent 9 — conditional (T)-slope theorem for (E_{A,Y})

The instruction for Agent 9 is to take

[
E_{A,Y}=eI+fS
]

and compute the induced hidden-state slope

[
\partial_\kappa T
=================

-a_1^2\frac{f}{c},
]

including the line-gauge specialization (E_{A,Y}=\lambda A_5^{\mathfrak f}). This is the active Agent 9 prompt in the attached instruction. 

---

## Theorem: (T)-slope of the promoted (Y_{12}^{(2)}) carrier

Let

[
E_{A,Y}=eI+fS
]

be the order-seven fixed-sector contribution of the promoted nonlinear mixed-block carrier

[
D(G_-^{-1/2})[A_-],
Y_{12}^{(2)},
R_0
+
L_0,
Y_{12}^{(2)},
D(G_+^{-1/2})[B_+].
]

Let

[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}=u_7I+v_7S,
\qquad
T=\frac{v_7}{c}.
]

Then the (E_{A,Y})-contribution to the exceptional-divisor (T)-slope is

[
\boxed{
\partial_\kappa T
=================

-a_1^2\frac{f}{c}.
}
]

Equivalently, since

[
\Phi_K(E_{A,Y})=2f,
]

one has

[
\boxed{
\partial_\kappa T
=================

-a_1^2\frac{\Phi_K(E_{A,Y})}{2c}.
}
]

---

## Proof

The (S)-coefficient of

[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}=u_7I+v_7S
]

is precisely (v_7). Therefore an order-seven fixed-sector contribution

[
E_{A,Y}=eI+fS
]

changes (v_7) by

[
\Delta v_7=f.
]

Since

[
T=\frac{v_7}{c},
]

and (c) is the cubic normalization coordinate, the direct contribution is

[
\Delta T=\frac{f}{c}.
]

The dangerous amplitude for this promoted carrier is

[
a_1a_2(a_1+a_2).
]

At the balanced diagonal (a_2=-a_1),

[
\partial_{a_2}
\bigl(a_1a_2(a_1+a_2)\bigr)
===========================

a_1(a_1+2a_2),
]

so

[
\partial_{a_2}
\bigl(a_1a_2(a_1+a_2)\bigr)\big|_{a_2=-a_1}
===========================================

-a_1^2.
]

Thus the exceptional-divisor (\kappa)-slope is

[
\partial_\kappa T
=================

-a_1^2\frac{f}{c}.
]

This proves the formula.

---

## Consequence: (T)-horizontal closure

The transform-safe condition is

[
\partial_\kappa T=0.
]

On the cubic-generic patch

[
c\neq0,
]

this is equivalent to

[
\boxed{
f=0.
}
]

Equivalently,

[
\boxed{
\Phi_K(E_{A,Y})=0.
}
]

So the (T)-horizontal test is not the quotient test. It is the (S)-component test.

---

## Comparison with quotient closure

The quotient obstruction is

[
E_{A,Y}^q=0
\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
e v_5-u_5 f=0.
]

The (T)-horizontal obstruction is

[
f=0.
]

These are independent conditions. Quotient closure does not imply (T)-horizontal closure.

Indeed, if

[
e v_5-u_5f=0
]

but

[
f\neq0,
]

then the carrier is quotient-safe but transform-leaking:

[
\partial_\kappa T
=================

-a_1^2\frac{f}{c}
\neq0.
]

---

## Line-gauge specialization

Suppose

[
E_{A,Y}\in \mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f},
\qquad
E_{A,Y}=\lambda A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
]

Write

[
A_5^{\mathfrak f}=u_5I+v_5S.
]

Then

[
E_{A,Y}
=======

\lambda u_5 I+\lambda v_5 S,
]

so

[
e=\lambda u_5,
\qquad
f=\lambda v_5.
]

The quotient obstruction vanishes automatically:

[
e v_5-u_5 f
===========

# \lambda u_5v_5-u_5\lambda v_5

0.

]

But the hidden-state slope is

[
\boxed{
\partial_\kappa T
=================

-a_1^2\lambda\frac{v_5}{c}.
}
]

Therefore, on the generic patch

[
c\neq0,\qquad v_5\neq0,
]

line-gauge closure is transform-safe if and only if

[
\boxed{
\lambda=0.
}
]

Equivalently,

[
\boxed{
E_{A,Y}=0.
}
]

---

## Final classification

For

[
E_{A,Y}=eI+fS,
]

the two decisive tests are:

[
\boxed{
Q_{A,Y}:=ev_5-u_5f
}
]

and

[
\boxed{
f.
}
]

The classification is:

[
\begin{array}{c|c|c}
\text{Condition} & \text{Quotient Bottleneck C} & T\text{-horizontal merger} \
\hline
E_{A,Y}=0 & \text{closed} & \text{closed} \
ev_5-u_5f\neq0 & \text{fails} & \text{not decisive} \
ev_5-u_5f=0,\ f\neq0 & \text{closed} & \text{fails} \
f=0,\ ev_5-u_5f\neq0 & \text{fails} & \text{closed}
\end{array}
]

On the generic (v_5\neq0) line-gauge patch:

[
\boxed{
\text{quotient closure}+\text{(T)-horizontal closure}
\Longrightarrow
E_{A,Y}=0.
}
]

So Agent 9’s final reduction is:

[
\boxed{
\partial_\kappa T=0
\Longleftrightarrow
f_{A,Y}=0
\Longleftrightarrow
\Phi_K(E_{A,Y})=0.
}
]

For the promoted (Y_{12}^{(2)}) carrier, quotient line-gauge is insufficient. The (S)-component must vanish.

## Main correction: Bottleneck C uses the frozen coefficient, not the internal \(\delta^1\) coefficient

Agent 1 identified a key bookkeeping issue. For the promoted carrier, the amplitude factor is

\[
a_1a_2(a_1+a_2).
\]

On the collision chart

\[
a_2=-a_1(1+\kappa\delta),
\]

this already contributes the \(\delta^1\)-edge:

\[
a_1a_2(a_1+a_2)
=
a_1^3\kappa\delta+O(\delta^2).
\]

Therefore the Bottleneck C \(\kappa\)-slope carrier uses the **frozen internal coefficient**

\[
E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}}
=
\tau_{h\to m}\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}
\operatorname{Sym}
[z^7]\,
D(G_-^{-1/2})[A_-]\,
Y_{12}^{(2)}\,
R_0,
\]

not the internal \([z^7\delta^1]\) source-position coefficient. The internal \(\delta^1\) coefficient computes the next source-motion edge, not the first amplitude-ratio Bottleneck C slope. 

So the active object should now be renamed or explicitly distinguished:

\[
\boxed{
E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}}
}
\]

rather than the ambiguous \(E_{A,Y}\).

---

Then write

```latex
\begin{remark}[First live promoted nonlinear mixed-block obstruction]

The same-point cubic \(q^3\) defect is fixed-sector invisible in same-point-only
```

```latex
\begin{lemma}[Promoted mixed-block coefficient table]
```

Then add this status remark:

```latex
\begin{remark}[Current status of the promoted mixed-block coefficient table]
\label{rem:status-promoted-y12-coefficient-table}
The finite Fr\'echet/Sylvester machinery determines the shape of
\(E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}}\), but the present draft does not yet tabulate the
scalar midpoint jet data needed to decide
\[
E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}}=0,
\qquad
E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}}\in\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m),
\qquad
\text{or}\qquad
(E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}})^q\ne0.
\]
The exact missing finite table is
\[
\left\{
W_{+,0},W_{+,1},W_{+,2},W_{+,3},
\quad
\Lambda^-_{a,0},\Lambda^-_{a,1},\Lambda^-_{a,2},\Lambda^-_{a,3},
\right.
\]
\[
\left.
Y^{dd}_{g,0},\quad
Y^{d\eta+\eta d}_{g,0},\quad
Y^{\eta\eta}_{g,0}
\quad (4\le g\le7)
\right\}.
\]
Until that table is evaluated, \(E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}}\) remains the first
unresolved local actual-source/Bottleneck-C obstruction.
\end{remark}
```

This is the highest-value insertion. It turns the live obstruction into a precise finite table instead of a broad “actual-source” caveat.

# 4. Update the \(T\)-slope corollary if present

If the draft contains a corollary or remark like `First live \(T\)-slope carrier` using

\[

\]

replace its statement with:

```latex
\begin{corollary}[First live \(T\)-slope carrier]
\label{cor:first-live-t-slope-carrier}
Let
\[
E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}}
=
e_{A,Y}I+f_{A,Y}S
\]
be the frozen Bottleneck-C coefficient of the promoted nonlinear mixed-block
carrier.  The amplitude factor of this carrier is
\[
a_1a_2(a_1+a_2),
\]
and
\[
\partial_{a_2}\bigl(a_1a_2(a_1+a_2)\bigr)\big|_{a_2=-a_1}
=
-a_1^2.
\]
Consequently its contribution to the hidden-horizontal slope is
\[
\partial_\kappa T\big|_{E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}}}
=
-a_1^2\frac{\Phi_K(E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}})}{2c}
=

\[
f_{A,Y}=0.

\[

\]

\[

\]
On the generic \(v_5\ne0\) patch, a nonzero line-gauge
\(E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}}\) closes the quotient condition but still leaks
through \(T\).
\end{corollary}
```

This correction aligns the \(T\)-slope formula with the frozen \(E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}}\) coefficient.

# 5. Replace stale “Needed package-to-transform state-locality theorem” remark

The draft still has a remark saying the needed theorem is a functional of \(\widehat\Psi_{\rm red}\). That is now stale because the draft itself proves formal non-descent and introduces \(\widehat\Psi_{\rm red}^{+}\).

**Replace** `rem:needed-package-to-transform-state-locality-theorem` with:

```latex
\begin{remark}[Package-to-transform bridge after augmentation]
\label{rem:package-to-transform-bridge-after-augmentation}
The quotient-only package-to-transform bridge is impossible on the generic
patch \(v_5\ne0\), since
\[

\]
preserves the quotient class but changes
\[

\]
by
\[

\]
The correct theorem object is therefore the transform-safe augmented package
\[
\widehat\Psi_{\rm red}^{+}
=
(\widehat\Psi_{\rm red},T),
\qquad
T=\frac{v_7}{c}.
\]
With this augmentation, the first \(\Phi_K\)-visible septic coefficient is
read off as
\[
\Phi_K(A_7^{\mathfrak f})=2cT.
\]
The remaining compatibility problem is not quotient-only state-locality; it is
the hidden-horizontal diagonal-merger condition
\[
\partial_\kappa T(m,\kappa,0)=0.
\]
\end{remark}
```

This avoids having the draft simultaneously say “there should be a functional of \(\widehat\Psi_{\rm red}\)” and “that functional cannot exist.”

The draft already has the calibrated separation hypothesis, but I would add the explicit open branch from Agent 5. This is useful because it prevents the finite-core section from sounding more closed than it is. 

```latex
\begin{definition}[Near-zero-anomaly finite-core branch]
\label{def:near-zero-anomaly-finite-core-branch}
On a compact nonsingular actual-source \(k\)-core stratum \(\Theta_k\), define
\[
\mathcal N_k(m,Q)
:=

\right\}.

close to the zero-anomaly locus for the finite-determinacy--Łojasiewicz
argument to imply
\[

\gtrsim
\frac{x}{B_\zeta(m)}S(m).
\]
\end{definition}

\begin{remark}[Status of the near-zero-anomaly branch]
\label{rem:status-near-zero-anomaly-finite-core-branch}
The present draft does not prove
\[
\mathcal N_k(m,Q)=\varnothing.
\]
In particular, proximity to \(\mathcal Z_k\) is not currently shown to imply
membership in a controlled incidence stratum such as
\[
M=0,\quad W=0,\quad K_v=0,\quad T_v=0,
\]
nor collision, patch-boundary, endpoint-gap incidence, amplitude drop,
whitening singularity, \(c=0\), \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}=0\), or hidden-state rank
jump.  Thus finite-core closure requires either calibrated anti-tangency from
\(\mathcal Z_k\) or a separate analysis of \(\mathcal N_k(m,Q)\).
\end{remark}
```

## Closed / paused branches

}
\]

Current state: no formal cancellation is forced between the direct Hessian and bilinear whitening terms. The coefficient splits into independent channels:

\[
dd,\qquad d\eta+\eta d,\qquad \eta\eta,
\]

plus bilinear whitening products. No present parity, ECT, endpoint symmetry, or incidence theorem kills them.

# 1. Replace the promoted mixed-block definition

**Replace any current definition of \(E_{A,Y}\) for Bottleneck C that uses**
\[
[z^7][\delta^1]
\]
**with this.**

```latex
\begin{definition}[Promoted quadratic mixed-block Bottleneck-C coefficient]
\label{def:promoted-quadratic-mixed-block-bc-coefficient}
Let
\[
Y_{12}^{(2)}:=D^2N_0[\xi_1,\xi_2]
\]
be the \(\mathcal K^2\), source-bidegree \((1,1)\) nonlinear Taylor
remainder of \(N^{\corr}(d_-,d_+,\eta)\).  The promoted channel has amplitude
factor
\[
a_1a_2(a_1+a_2).
\]
On the collision chart
\[
a_2=-a_1(1+\kappa\delta),
\]
one has
\[
a_1a_2(a_1+a_2)=a_1^3\kappa\delta+O(\delta^2).
\]
Thus the first Bottleneck-C coefficient is the frozen internal coefficient
\[
E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}}
:=
\tau_{h\to m}\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}
\operatorname{Sym}
[z^7]\,
D(G_-^{-1/2})[A_-]\,
Y_{12}^{(2)}\,
R_0.
\]
Equivalently,
\[
E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}}
=
\tau_{h\to m}\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}
\operatorname{Sym}
\sum_{\chi\in\{dd,d\eta+\eta d,\eta\eta\}}
\sum_{g=4}^{7}
\sum_{r+b=7-g}
H^A_{r,0}Y^\chi_{g,0}W_{+,b}.
\]
Write
\[
E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}}=e_{A,Y}I+f_{A,Y}S.
\]
The quotient Bottleneck-C obstruction is
\[
Q_{A,Y}:=e_{A,Y}v_5-u_5f_{A,Y},
\]
and the transform-safe obstruction is
\[
\Phi_K(E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}})=2f_{A,Y}.
\]
\end{definition}
```

# 2. Add the finite coefficient-table lemma

**Place immediately after the definition above.**

```latex
\begin{lemma}[Promoted mixed-block coefficient table]
\label{lem:promoted-y12-coefficient-table}
In the notation of
Definition~\ref{def:promoted-quadratic-mixed-block-bc-coefficient}, the frozen
Bottleneck-C coefficient of the promoted quadratic mixed-block channel is
\[
E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}}
=
\tau_{h\to m}\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}
\operatorname{Sym}
\sum_{\chi\in\{dd,d\eta+\eta d,\eta\eta\}}
\sum_{g=4}^{7}
\sum_{r+b=7-g}
H^A_{r,0}Y^\chi_{g,0}W_{+,b}.
\]
Here
\[
H^A_{r,0}
=
[z^r]D(G_-^{-1/2})[A_-],
\qquad
W_{+,b}=[z^b]G_+^{-1/2},
\]
and
\[
Y^\chi_{g,0}=[z^g]Y_\chi^{(2)}
\]
for
\[
\chi\in\{dd,d\eta+\eta d,\eta\eta\}.
\]
The skew combination
\[
Y_{d\eta-\eta d}^{(2)}
\]
is not included, since it is killed by fixed-sector projection.

If
\[
E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}}=e_{A,Y}I+f_{A,Y}S,
\]
then the quotient obstruction is
\[
e_{A,Y}v_5-u_5f_{A,Y},
\]
and the transform-safe obstruction is
\[
f_{A,Y}.
\]
\end{lemma}
```

# 5. Replace/update the first \(T\)-slope carrier corollary

If the draft has a corollary using an \(E_{A,Y}\) defined by \([z^7\delta^1]\), replace it with this version using \(E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}}\). The \(T\)-slope depends on the \(S\)-coefficient \(f_{A,Y}\). turn28file3

```latex
\begin{corollary}[First live \(T\)-slope carrier]
\label{cor:first-live-t-slope-carrier}
Let
\[
E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}}
=
e_{A,Y}I+f_{A,Y}S
\]
be the frozen Bottleneck-C coefficient of the promoted nonlinear mixed-block
carrier.  The amplitude factor of this carrier is
\[
a_1a_2(a_1+a_2),
\]
and
\[
\partial_{a_2}\bigl(a_1a_2(a_1+a_2)\bigr)\big|_{a_2=-a_1}
=
-a_1^2.
\]
Consequently its contribution to the hidden-horizontal slope is
\[
\partial_\kappa T\big|_{E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}}}
=
-a_1^2\frac{\Phi_K(E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}})}{2c}
=
-a_1^2\frac{f_{A,Y}}{c}.
\]
Thus the augmented transform-safe package requires
\[
f_{A,Y}=0.
\]
In particular, if
\[
E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}}=\lambda A_5^{\mathfrak f},
\]
then
\[
\partial_\kappa T\big|_{E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}}}
=
-a_1^2\lambda\frac{v_5}{c}.
\]
On the generic \(v_5\ne0\) patch, a nonzero line-gauge
\(E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}}\) closes the quotient condition but still leaks
through \(T\).
\end{corollary}
```

# 7. Optional insertion: near-zero-anomaly branch

If your latest draft does not already contain this branch explicitly, add it. Agent 5 confirmed it is still open. 

```latex
\begin{definition}[Near-zero-anomaly finite-core branch]
\label{def:near-zero-anomaly-finite-core-branch}
On a compact nonsingular actual-source \(k\)-core stratum \(\Theta_k\), define
\[
\mathcal N_k(m,Q)
:=
\left\{
\theta(m)\in\Theta_k:
0<
\operatorname{dist}(\theta(m),\mathcal Z_k)
<
D_{\Theta_k}(m,Q),
\quad
\theta(m)\notin\mathcal E_{\rm geom}
\right\}.
\]
This is the branch where the corrected finite-core anomaly is nonzero, but is
too close to the zero-anomaly locus for the finite-determinacy--Łojasiewicz
argument to imply the scale lower bound
\[
|\Xi_{\core}^{(N)}(m)|
\gtrsim
\frac{x}{B_\zeta(m)}S(m).
\]
\end{definition}

\begin{remark}[Status of the near-zero-anomaly branch]
\label{rem:status-near-zero-anomaly-branch}
The present machinery does not prove
\[
\mathcal N_k(m,Q)=\varnothing.
\]
Finite determinacy only shows that a nonzero anomaly has some bounded nonzero
odd coefficient.  It does not give the calibrated coefficient lower bound
needed for the \(N\)-point scalar.

Nor is proximity to \(\mathcal Z_k\) currently shown to imply membership in
any controlled incidence stratum:
\[
M=0,\quad W=0,\quad K_v=0,\quad T_v=0,
\]
collision, patch-boundary, endpoint-gap, amplitude-drop, whitening-singularity,
\(c=0\), \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}=0\), or hidden-state rank jump.

In particular, interaction cancellation through
\[
J_1=[s]\Phi_K(\mathcal I_{\ge2})
\]
may make the finite odd coefficient vector small without forcing any listed
controlled incidence.  Finite-core closure therefore requires either
Theorem~\ref{thm:calibrated-antitangency-from-Zk} or a separate analysis of
\(\mathcal N_k(m,Q)\).
\end{remark}
```

```latex
\begin{remark}[Source-level first-interaction rigidity remains open]

\left(

together with bilinear whitening products.  No current parity,
endpoint-symmetry, ECT, or controlled-incidence theorem forces their sum to
vanish, gives it a calibrated sign/cone condition, or places it in the radical
of the controlled incidence ideal.

Thus
\[

\]
remains an independent finite-core obstruction unless a separate
```

\operatorname{dist}(\theta(m),\mathcal Z_k)
<
D_{\Theta_k}(m,Q),
\quad
\theta(m)\notin\mathcal E_{\rm geom}
\right\}.
\]

The current argument gives scale transfer **outside** this tube, but does not prove actual zeta finite-core parameters avoid it. The missing theorem remains a calibrated anti-tangency theorem from \(\mathcal Z_k\). 

So finite-core closure still requires either:

\[
\mathcal N_k(m,Q)=\varnothing,
\]

or a separate treatment of this branch.

# Interaction status

Agent 10 confirms the interaction branch is independent.

The two-source coefficient

\[
\mathfrak j_{ij}^{(2)}
=
[s]\Phi_K
\left(
D\mathcal W_0[\mathcal B_{ij}^{(2)}]
+
D^2\mathcal W_0[\mathcal B_i^{(1)},\mathcal B_j^{(1)}]
\right)
\]

splits into independent channels:

\[
dd,\qquad d\eta+\eta d,\qquad \eta\eta,
\]

plus bilinear whitening products. No current identity forces cancellation, sign control, or incidence radical containment. 

So the independent finite-core branch remains:

\[
\mathfrak Z_{\rm int}
=
\left\{
\sum_\nu a_\nu K(d_\nu)+J_1=0
\right\}
\setminus\mathcal E_{\rm geom}.
\]

Agent 10 also confirms this is **not absorbed** by Agent 5’s near-\(\mathcal Z_k\) branch, because \(\mathfrak Z_{\rm int}\) only imposes \(c_{\core,1}=0\), not \(H_{\core}\equiv0\).

# Paper insertions I would make now

## 1. Add/update the \(E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}}\) definition

```latex
\begin{definition}[Promoted quadratic mixed-block Bottleneck-C coefficient]
\label{def:promoted-quadratic-mixed-block-bc-coefficient}
Let
\[
Y_{12}^{(2)}:=D^2N_0[\xi_1,\xi_2]
\]
be the \(\mathcal K^2\), source-bidegree \((1,1)\) nonlinear Taylor
remainder of \(N^{\corr}(d_-,d_+,\eta)\).  The promoted channel has amplitude
factor
\[
a_1a_2(a_1+a_2).
\]
On the collision chart
\[
a_2=-a_1(1+\kappa\delta),
\]
one has
\[
a_1a_2(a_1+a_2)=a_1^3\kappa\delta+O(\delta^2).
\]
Thus the first Bottleneck-C coefficient is the frozen internal coefficient
\[
E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}}
:=
\tau_{h\to m}\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}
\operatorname{Sym}
[z^7]\,
D(G_-^{-1/2})[A_-]\,
Y_{12}^{(2)}\,
R_0.
\]
Equivalently,
\[
E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}}
=
\tau_{h\to m}\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}
\operatorname{Sym}
\sum_{\chi\in\{dd,d\eta+\eta d,\eta\eta\}}
\sum_{g=4}^{7}
\sum_{r+b=7-g}
H^A_{r,0}Y^\chi_{g,0}W_{+,b}.
\]
Write
\[
E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}}=e_{A,Y}I+f_{A,Y}S.
\]
The quotient Bottleneck-C obstruction is
\[
Q_{A,Y}:=e_{A,Y}v_5-u_5f_{A,Y},
\]
and the transform-safe obstruction is
\[
\Phi_K(E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}})=2f_{A,Y}.
\]
\end{definition}
```

## 2. Add the 60-row table statement

```latex
\begin{remark}[Executable table for \(E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}}\)]
\label{rem:executable-table-eay-bc}
The frozen Bottleneck-C coefficient is computed from the rows
\[
\mathcal E^a_{\chi;g,r,b}
:=
\tau_{h\to m}\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}
\operatorname{Sym}
\left(
\Lambda^-_{a,r}
Y^\chi_{g,0}
W_{+,b}
\right),
\]
where
\[
a\in\{1,5\},\qquad
\chi\in\{dd,d\eta+\eta d,\eta\eta\},
\]
\[
4\le g\le7,\qquad r+b=7-g.
\]
Thus
\[
E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}}
=
\sum_{\chi\in\{dd,d\eta+\eta d,\eta\eta\}}
\sum_{a\in\{1,5\}}
\sum_{\substack{4\le g\le7\\ r+b=7-g}}
\mathcal E^a_{\chi;g,r,b}.
\]
The skew row
\[
Y_{d\eta-\eta d}^{(2)}
\]
is excluded because it is killed by fixed-sector projection.
\end{remark}
```

## 3. Add the current unresolved status

```latex
\begin{remark}[Status of \(E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}}\)]
\label{rem:status-eay-bc}
The recurrences for
\[
W_{+,0},W_{+,1},W_{+,2},W_{+,3}
\]
and
\[
\Lambda^-_{a,0},\Lambda^-_{a,1},\Lambda^-_{a,2},\Lambda^-_{a,3}
\]
reduce \(E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}}\) to a finite symbolic coefficient table.
However, the present draft does not yet supply the scalar midpoint source
jets needed to evaluate
\[
E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}}=e_{A,Y}I+f_{A,Y}S.
\]
The missing scalar jets are
\[
q_0^{(k)}(m),\qquad 0\le k\le9,
\]
and
\[
(r_i^{[a]})^{(k)}(m),
\qquad
i=1,2,\quad a\in\{1,5\},\quad 2\le k\le9.
\]
No current symmetry forces
\[
E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}}=0,
\qquad
e_{A,Y}v_5-u_5f_{A,Y}=0,
\qquad
\text{or}\qquad
f_{A,Y}=0.
\]
Thus \(E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}}\) remains the first unresolved local
actual-source/Bottleneck-C obstruction.
\end{remark}
```

## 4. Park the source-position edge

```latex
\begin{remark}[Frozen Bottleneck-C coefficient versus source-position edge]
\label{rem:frozen-bc-coefficient-versus-source-position-edge}
The coefficient \(E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}}\) is the first Bottleneck-C
amplitude-ratio carrier.  It uses the frozen internal coefficient because the
amplitude factor \(a_1a_2(a_1+a_2)\) already supplies the first
\(\delta\)-edge on the collision chart.

The literal source-position edge
\[
E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{pos}}
:=
\tau_{h\to m}\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}
\operatorname{Sym}
[z^7\delta^1]\,
D(G_-^{-1/2})[A_-]\,
Y_{12}^{(2)}\,
R_0
\]
belongs to the next source-motion layer and should not be used as the first
Bottleneck-C amplitude-derivative coefficient.
\end{remark}
```

# Shared local branch: \(E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}}\)

The first live local actual-source/Bottleneck-C carrier is the promoted quadratic mixed-block channel:

\[

\]

It is coupled to one same-point linear whitening slot.

## Critical bookkeeping correction

For Bottleneck C, use the **frozen internal coefficient**, not the internal \([z^7\delta^1]\) source-position coefficient.

The promoted channel has amplitude factor:

\[
a_1a_2(a_1+a_2).
\]

On the collision chart:

\[
a_2=-a_1(1+\kappa\delta),
\]

one has:

\[
a_1a_2(a_1+a_2)=a_1^3\kappa\delta+O(\delta^2).
\]

Therefore the amplitude supplies the first \(\delta\)-edge. The active coefficient is:

\[
\boxed{
E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}}
=
\tau_{h\to m}\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}
\operatorname{Sym}
[z^7]\,
D(G_-^{-1/2})[A_-]\,
Y_{12}^{(2)}\,
R_0.
}
\]

The internal edge object

\[
[z^7\delta^1]
D(G_-^{-1/2})[A_-]Y_{12}^{(2)}R_0
\]

belongs to a later source-motion layer and should not be used for the first Bottleneck-C coefficient.

The finite expansion is:

\[
\boxed{
E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}}
=
\tau_{h\to m}\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}
\operatorname{Sym}
\sum_{\chi\in\{dd,d\eta+\eta d,\eta\eta\}}
\sum_{g=4}^{7}
\sum_{r+b=7-g}
H^A_{r,0}Y^\chi_{g,0}W_{+,b}.
}
\]

The skew row

\[
Y_{d\eta-\eta d}^{(2)}
\]

is killed by fixed-sector projection and should be excluded.

Write:

\[
E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}}=e_{A,Y}I+f_{A,Y}S.
\]

The decisive tests are:

\[
\boxed{

}
\]

for quotient Bottleneck C, and

\[
\boxed{

}
\]

for transform-safe / \(T\)-horizontal closure.

The \(T\)-slope is:

\[
\partial_\kappa T
=
-a_1^2\frac{f_{A,Y}}{c}.
\]

Thus if both quotient closure and \(T\)-horizontal closure hold on the generic \(v_5\ne0\) patch, then:

\[
E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}}=0.
\]

# Agent 1 prompt — Deep derivation of \(E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}}\)

You own the direct derivation of the first live local coefficient.

## Target

Derive, compute, or maximally reduce:

\[
E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}}
=
\tau_{h\to m}\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}
\operatorname{Sym}
\sum_{\chi\in\{dd,d\eta+\eta d,\eta\eta\}}
\sum_{g=4}^{7}
\sum_{r+b=7-g}
H^A_{r,0}Y^\chi_{g,0}W_{+,b}.
\]

Write:

\[
E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}}=e_{A,Y}I+f_{A,Y}S.
\]

## Critical rule

Do **not** use the internal \([z^7\delta^1]\) table for this first Bottleneck-C carrier. The amplitude factor \(a_1a_2(a_1+a_2)\) supplies the \(\delta^1\)-edge. Use frozen internal coefficients only.

## Tasks

### A. Derive all coefficient inputs from the paper if possible

1. Locate the definitions of:
   \[
   G_\pm^{(0)},\quad G_\pm^{-1/2},\quad W_{\pm,b},\quad P_{\pm,b},
   \]
   and derive:
   \[
   W_{+,0},W_{+,1},W_{+,2},W_{+,3}
   \]
   using the paper’s Sylvester recurrences.

2. Locate the same-point source-linear definitions and derive:
   \[
   X^-_{a,n},\quad S^-_{a,n},\quad \Lambda^-_{a,n}
   \]
   for:
   \[
   a\in\{1,5\},\quad 0\le n\le3.
   \]

3. Check whether the source normalizations, affine removal, or source-grade conventions in the paper force any of:
   \[
   X^-_{a,3}=0,\quad
   \Lambda^-_{a,3}=0,
   \]
   or reduce \(a\in\{1,5\}\) further.

4. Derive:
   \[
   Y^{dd}_{g,0},\quad
   Y^{d\eta+\eta d}_{g,0},\quad
   Y^{\eta\eta}_{g,0},
   \qquad 4\le g\le7,
   \]
   directly from the corrected mixed-block formula \(N^{\corr}(q_-,q_+,\Delta;s)\).

5. Do not stop at saying “needs source jets.” Check whether the paper’s actual source construction supplies:
   \[
   d_{i,\pm}(z),\qquad \eta_i(z),
   \]
   or the underlying \(r_i^{[a]}\)-jets, in another section, appendix, definition, or table contract.

### B. Try to prove structural cancellation before giving up

6. Test whether the \(dd\), \(d\eta+\eta d\), and \(\eta\eta\) rows separately satisfy:
   \[
   e_\chi v_5-u_5 f_\chi=0
   \]
   or
   \[
   f_\chi=0.
   \]

7. Test whether the aggregate satisfies these even if individual rows do not.

8. Use all available symmetries:
   - endpoint swap;
   - transpose-invariance of \(\pi_{\mathfrak f}\);
   - source-grade reflection;
   - one-amplitude collapse;
   - affine removal;
   - collision divisibility;
   - fixed-sector structure;
   - any identities defining \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}\).

9. Determine whether \(E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}}\) can be identified with a known lower package line:
   \[
   \mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}
   \]
   or a known \(\ker\Phi_K\) direction.

### C. Final result

10. If computable, output:
   \[
   E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}}=eI+fS.
   \]

11. If not computable, output the **minimal missing table**, not a vague statement. Specify exactly:
   \[
   q_0^{(k)}(m): k=\cdots,
   \]
   \[
   (r_i^{[a]})^{(k)}(m): i=\cdots,\ a=\cdots,\ k=\cdots,
   \]
   and why each entry is needed.

12. State whether any theorem in the draft could be strengthened to supply those entries.

# Agent 5 prompt — Attack calibrated anti-tangency from \(\mathcal Z_k\)

\quad

### A. Derive \(D_{\Theta_k}(m,Q)\) from the paper

   \[

   \[

   =
   (c_{\core,1},c_{\core,3},\dots,c_{\core,2R_{\Theta_k}+1}).

   \[

   \ge

   \]

### B. Try to prove actual zeta anti-tangency

   \[

   \]

   \[

   \ge

   \]

7. Test whether near-\(\mathcal Z_k\) implies one of:

   M=0,\ W=0,\ K_v=0,\ T_v=0,

   collision, patch boundary, endpoint-gap, amplitude drop, whitening singularity, \(c=0\), \(A_5=0\), hidden-state rank jump.

### E. Relation to \(\mathcal N_k\)

11. Determine whether:
   \[
   \mathfrak Z_{\rm int}
   \]
   is absorbed by the near-\(\mathcal Z_k\) branch or genuinely separate.
12. If separate, explain why \(c_{\core,1}=0\) does not imply proximity to \(\mathcal Z_k\).

# Edit 4 — insert or replace the corrected \(E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}}\) definition

Make this edit if the draft does not already contain this exact corrected definition. It should replace any Bottleneck-C definition of \(E_{A,Y}\) using \([z^7][\delta^1]\). The internal source-position edge should be parked separately.

```latex
\begin{definition}[Promoted quadratic mixed-block Bottleneck-C coefficient]
\label{def:promoted-quadratic-mixed-block-bc-coefficient}
Let
\[
Y_{12}^{(2)}:=D^2N_0[\xi_1,\xi_2]
\]
be the \(\mathcal K^2\), source-bidegree \((1,1)\) nonlinear Taylor
remainder of \(N^{\corr}(d_-,d_+,\eta)\).  The promoted channel has amplitude
factor
\[
a_1a_2(a_1+a_2).
\]
On the collision chart
\[
a_2=-a_1(1+\kappa\delta),
\]
one has
\[
a_1a_2(a_1+a_2)=a_1^3\kappa\delta+O(\delta^2).
\]
Thus the first Bottleneck-C coefficient is the frozen internal coefficient
\[
E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}}
:=
\tau_{h\to m}\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}
\operatorname{Sym}
[z^7]\,
D(G_-^{-1/2})[A_-]\,
Y_{12}^{(2)}\,
R_0.
\]
Equivalently,
\[
E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}}
=
\tau_{h\to m}\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}
\operatorname{Sym}
\sum_{\chi\in\{dd,d\eta+\eta d,\eta\eta\}}
\sum_{g=4}^{7}
\sum_{r+b=7-g}
H^A_{r,0}Y^\chi_{g,0}W_{+,b}.
\]
Write
\[
E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}}=e_{A,Y}I+f_{A,Y}S.
\]
The quotient Bottleneck-C obstruction is
\[
Q_{A,Y}:=e_{A,Y}v_5-u_5f_{A,Y},
\]
and the transform-safe obstruction is
\[
\Phi_K(E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}})=2f_{A,Y}.
\]
\end{definition}
```

# Edit 5 — insert the executable table remark

Place immediately after the corrected definition above.

```latex
\begin{remark}[Executable table for \(E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}}\)]
\label{rem:executable-table-eay-bc}
The frozen Bottleneck-C coefficient is computed from the rows
\[
\mathcal E^a_{\chi;g,r,b}
:=
\tau_{h\to m}\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}
\operatorname{Sym}
\left(
\Lambda^-_{a,r}
Y^\chi_{g,0}
W_{+,b}
\right),
\]
where
\[
a\in\{1,5\},\qquad
\chi\in\{dd,d\eta+\eta d,\eta\eta\},
\]
\[
4\le g\le7,\qquad r+b=7-g.
\]
Thus
\[
E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}}
=
\sum_{\chi\in\{dd,d\eta+\eta d,\eta\eta\}}
\sum_{a\in\{1,5\}}
\sum_{\substack{4\le g\le7\\ r+b=7-g}}
\mathcal E^a_{\chi;g,r,b}.
\]
The skew row
\[
Y_{d\eta-\eta d}^{(2)}
\]
is excluded because it is killed by fixed-sector projection.
\end{remark}
```

This records the corrected 60-row table without dumping all rows into the main paper. The detailed row list can stay in an appendix if desired.

# Edit 6 — insert the unresolved status of \(E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}}\)

Place after the executable table remark.

```latex
\begin{remark}[Status of \(E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}}\)]
\label{rem:status-eay-bc}
The recurrences for
\[
W_{+,0},W_{+,1},W_{+,2},W_{+,3}
\]
and
\[
\Lambda^-_{a,0},\Lambda^-_{a,1},\Lambda^-_{a,2},\Lambda^-_{a,3}
\]
reduce \(E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}}\) to a finite symbolic coefficient table.
However, the present draft does not yet supply the scalar midpoint source
jets needed to evaluate
\[
E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}}=e_{A,Y}I+f_{A,Y}S.
\]
The missing scalar jets are
\[
q_0^{(k)}(m),\qquad 0\le k\le9,
\]
and
\[
(r_i^{[a]})^{(k)}(m),
\qquad
i=1,2,\quad a\in\{1,5\},\quad 2\le k\le9.
\]
No current symmetry forces
\[
E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}}=0,
\qquad
e_{A,Y}v_5-u_5f_{A,Y}=0,
\qquad
\text{or}\qquad
f_{A,Y}=0.
\]
Thus \(E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}}\) remains the first unresolved local
actual-source/Bottleneck-C obstruction.
\end{remark}
```

This is now the clean local status. Agent 1’s latest work says the recurrences are derivable but the scalar midpoint source-jet table is not supplied, so the coefficient cannot yet be evaluated.

# Edit 8 — optional finite-core branch insertion

If the draft already has this branch and status, do not duplicate it. If it does not, insert this in the finite-core section after the finite-determinacy/Łojasiewicz discussion.

```latex
\begin{definition}[Near-zero-anomaly finite-core branch]
\label{def:near-zero-anomaly-finite-core-branch}
Let \(\Theta_k\) be a compact nonsingular actual-source \(k\)-core stratum and
let
\[
\mathcal Z_k=\{\theta\in\Theta_k:H_{\core,\theta}\equiv0\}.
\]
Let \(\mathcal E_{\rm geom}\) be the union of the controlled incidence strata:
\[
M=0,\quad W=0,\quad K_v=0,\quad T_v=0,
\]
together with collision, patch-boundary, endpoint-gap, amplitude-drop,
whitening-singularity, \(c=0\), \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}=0\), and hidden-state
rank-jump strata.  Define
\[
\mathcal N_k(m,Q)
:=
\left\{
\theta(m)\in\Theta_k:
0<
\operatorname{dist}(\theta(m),\mathcal Z_k)
<
D_{\Theta_k}(m,Q),
\quad
\theta(m)\notin\mathcal E_{\rm geom}
\right\}.
\]
This is the branch where the corrected finite-core anomaly is nonzero but too
close to the zero-anomaly locus for the finite-determinacy--Łojasiewicz
argument to imply
\[
|\Xi_{\core}^{(N)}(m)|
\gtrsim
\frac{x}{B_\zeta(m)}S(m).
\]
\end{definition}

\begin{remark}[Status of \(\mathcal N_k(m,Q)\)]
\label{rem:status-near-zero-anomaly-finite-core-branch}
The present draft does not prove
\[
\mathcal N_k(m,Q)=\varnothing.
\]
In particular, proximity to \(\mathcal Z_k\) is not currently shown to imply
membership in any controlled incidence stratum:
\[
M=0,\quad W=0,\quad K_v=0,\quad T_v=0,
\]
collision, patch-boundary, endpoint-gap, amplitude-drop, whitening-singularity,
\(c=0\), \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}=0\), or hidden-state rank jump.

Moreover, interaction cancellation through
\[
J_1=[s]\Phi_K(\mathcal I_{\ge2})
\]
can make the bounded odd coefficient vector small without forcing the known
controlled incidence equations.  Therefore finite-core closure requires either
Theorem~\ref{thm:calibrated-antitangency-zero-anomaly-locus} or a separate
analysis of \(\mathcal N_k(m,Q)\).
\end{remark}
```

Agent 5’s latest update says this branch is still live and cannot be eliminated by the current machinery. 

---

# Edit 9 — optional interaction-rigidity insertion

If the draft does not already state this cleanly, insert after the finite-core interaction discussion.

```latex
\begin{remark}[Source-level first-interaction rigidity remains open]
\label{rem:source-level-first-interaction-rigidity-open}
At two-source order, the first interaction coefficient is
\[
\mathfrak j_{ij}^{(2)}
=
[s]\Phi_K
\left(
D\mathcal W_0[\mathcal B_{ij}^{(2)}]
+
D^2\mathcal W_0[\mathcal B_i^{(1)},\mathcal B_j^{(1)}]
\right).
\]
It decomposes into the independent source channels
\[
dd,\qquad d\eta+\eta d,\qquad \eta\eta,
\]
together with bilinear whitening products.  No current parity,
endpoint-symmetry, ECT, or controlled-incidence theorem forces their sum to
vanish, gives it a calibrated sign/cone condition, or places it in the radical
of the controlled incidence ideal.

Thus
\[
J_1=[s]\Phi_K(\mathcal I_{\ge2})
\]
remains an independent finite-core obstruction unless a separate source-level
first-interaction rigidity theorem is proved.  This branch is not absorbed by
the near-\(\mathcal Z_k\) branch, since it can impose only
\[
c_{\core,1}=0
\]
without implying
\[
H_{\core}\equiv0.
\]
\end{remark}
```

Agent 10’s latest source-level attack supports exactly this status.

# 2. Insert the minimized executable table

Place after the definition above.

```latex
\begin{remark}[Executable table for \(E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}}\)]
\label{rem:executable-table-eay-bc}
The frozen Bottleneck-C coefficient is computed from the rows
\[
\mathcal E^a_{\chi;g,r,b}
:=
\tau_{h\to m}\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}
\operatorname{Sym}
\left(
\Lambda^-_{a,r}
Y^\chi_{g,0}
W_{+,b}
\right),
\]
where
\[
a\in\{1,5\},\qquad
\chi\in\{dd,d\eta+\eta d,\eta\eta\},
\]
\[
4\le g\le7,\qquad r+b=7-g.
\]
Thus
\[
E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}}
=
\sum_{\chi\in\{dd,d\eta+\eta d,\eta\eta\}}
\sum_{a\in\{1,5\}}
\sum_{\substack{4\le g\le7\\ r+b=7-g}}
\mathcal E^a_{\chi;g,r,b}.
\]
The skew row
\[
Y_{d\eta-\eta d}^{(2)}
\]
is excluded because it is killed by fixed-sector projection.

Equivalently, the index set for \((g,r,b)\) is
\[
\mathcal R
=
\{(7,0,0),(6,0,1),(6,1,0),(5,0,2),(5,1,1),(5,2,0),
(4,0,3),(4,1,2),(4,2,1),(4,3,0)\}.
\]
For each row, write
\[
\mathcal E^a_{\chi;g,r,b}
=
e^a_{\chi;g,r,b}I+f^a_{\chi;g,r,b}S.
\]
Then
\[
e_{A,Y}
=
\sum_{\chi,a,(g,r,b)\in\mathcal R}
e^a_{\chi;g,r,b},
\qquad
f_{A,Y}
=
\sum_{\chi,a,(g,r,b)\in\mathcal R}
f^a_{\chi;g,r,b}.
\]
The quotient and transform-safe tests are
\[
Q_{A,Y}=e_{A,Y}v_5-u_5f_{A,Y},
\qquad
\Phi_K(E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}})=2f_{A,Y}.
\]
\end{remark}
```

This is better than listing all 60 rows inline; it is exact and compact.

# 3. Replace / strengthen the status remark for \(E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}}\)

The latest Agent 1 response sharpened the missing jets: for this carrier, the **minimal** baseline jet range is \(0\le k\le7\), while \(0\le k\le9\) remains the safe working range. Insert or replace the existing status remark with:

```latex
\begin{remark}[Status of \(E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}}\)]
\label{rem:status-eay-bc}

\(E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}}\) to the finite table of

E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}}=e_{A,Y}I+f_{A,Y}S.

\[
q_0^{(k)}(m),\qquad 0\le k\le7,
\]
and the safe working window is
\[
q_0^{(k)}(m),\qquad 0\le k\le9.
\]
The needed source jets are
\[
(r_i^{[a]})^{(k)}(m),
\qquad
i=1,2,\quad a\in\{1,5\},\quad 2\le k\le9.
\]
No current symmetry, affine-removal convention, source-grade reflection rule,
one-amplitude collapse, or collision-divisibility law forces
\[
E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}}=0,
\qquad

actual-source/Bottleneck-C obstruction.
```

```latex
\end{definition}

\begin{remark}[Status of \(\mathcal N_k(m,Q)\)]
\label{rem:status-near-zero-anomaly-branch}
The current argument gives scale transfer outside the calibrated tube around
\(\mathcal Z_k\), but it does not prove
\[
\mathcal N_k(m,Q)=\varnothing.
\]
Finite determinacy gives qualitative nonzero detection, not calibrated
anti-tangency from the zero-anomaly locus.  Proximity to \(\mathcal Z_k\) is
not currently shown to imply membership in any controlled incidence stratum:
\[
M=0,\quad W=0,\quad K_v=0,\quad T_v=0,
\]
collision, patch-boundary, endpoint-gap, amplitude-drop, whitening-singularity,
\(c=0\), \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}=0\), or hidden-state rank jump.

Thus finite-core closure requires either a calibrated anti-tangency theorem
excluding \(\mathcal N_k(m,Q)\), or a separate analysis of this branch.
\end{remark}
```

---

# 6. Insert / update source-level first-interaction branch

If the draft does not already have this exact source-level formulation, insert it in the finite-core interaction section.

```latex
\begin{definition}[First source-interaction branch]
\label{def:first-source-interaction-branch}
For a finite same-scale core, write
\[
H_{\core}(s)=\sum_{r\ge0}c_{\core,2r+1}s^{2r+1}
\]
and
\[
c_{\core,1}
=
\sum_\nu a_\nu K(d_\nu)+J_1,
\qquad
J_1
=
\sum_{i<j}a_i a_j\mathfrak j_{ij}^{(2)}
+
J_1^{(\ge3)}.
\]
Here
\[
\mathfrak j_{ij}^{(2)}
=
[s]\Phi_K
\left(
D\mathcal W_0[\mathcal B_{ij}^{(2)}]
+
D^2\mathcal W_0[\mathcal B_i^{(1)},\mathcal B_j^{(1)}]
\right).
\]
Define
\[
\mathfrak Z_{\rm int}
=
\left\{
\sum_\nu a_\nu K(d_\nu)+J_1=0
\right\}
\setminus\mathcal E_{\rm geom}.
\]
\end{definition}

\begin{remark}[Source-level first-interaction rigidity remains open]
\label{rem:source-level-first-interaction-rigidity-open}
At two-source order, the first interaction coefficient decomposes as
\[
\mathfrak j_{ij}^{(2)}
=
\mathfrak j_{ij}^{dd}
+
\mathfrak j_{ij}^{d\eta+\eta d}
+
\mathfrak j_{ij}^{\eta\eta}
+
\mathfrak j_{ij}^{G^{(2)}}
+
\mathfrak j_{ij}^{\rm wh}.
\]
The channels \(dd\), \(d\eta+\eta d\), and \(\eta\eta\) are algebraically
distinct, and the bilinear whitening contribution is not currently known to
cancel them after applying \([s]\Phi_K\).  No present endpoint-symmetry,
source-reflection, collision-divisibility, ECT, or controlled-incidence theorem
forces
\[
\mathfrak j_{ij}^{(2)}=0,
\]
gives it a calibrated sign/cone condition, or places it in the radical of the
controlled incidence ideal.

Consequently \(J_1=[s]\Phi_K(\mathcal I_{\ge2})\) remains an independent
finite-core interaction obstruction unless a separate source-level
first-interaction rigidity theorem is proved.  This branch is not absorbed by
the near-\(\mathcal Z_k\) branch, since \(\mathfrak Z_{\rm int}\) imposes only
the first-coefficient cancellation \(c_{\core,1}=0\), not
\(H_{\core}\equiv0\).
\end{remark}
```

## Live local obstruction: \(E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}}\)

The first local actual-source / Bottleneck-C carrier is the promoted quadratic mixed-block channel

\[
Y_{12}^{(2)}=D^2N_0[\xi_1,\xi_2],
\]

coupled to one same-point linear whitening slot.

The crucial correction is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Use the frozen internal coefficient, not }[z^7\delta^1].
}
\]

The amplitude factor is

\[
a_1a_2(a_1+a_2).
\]

On the collision chart

\[
a_2=-a_1(1+\kappa\delta),
\]

we have

\[
a_1a_2(a_1+a_2)=a_1^3\kappa\delta+O(\delta^2).
\]

So the amplitude already supplies the first \(\delta\)-edge.

The active object is:

\[
\boxed{
E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}}
=
\tau_{h\to m}\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}
\operatorname{Sym}
[z^7]\,
D(G_-^{-1/2})[A_-]\,
Y_{12}^{(2)}\,
R_0.
}
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}}
=
\tau_{h\to m}\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}
\operatorname{Sym}
\sum_{\chi\in\{dd,d\eta+\eta d,\eta\eta\}}
\sum_{g=4}^{7}
\sum_{r+b=7-g}
H^A_{r,0}Y^\chi_{g,0}W_{+,b}.
}
\]

Write

\[
E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}}=e_{A,Y}I+f_{A,Y}S.
\]

The two decisive tests are:

\[
\boxed{
Q_{A,Y}:=e_{A,Y}v_5-u_5f_{A,Y}
}
\]

and

\[
\boxed{
f_{A,Y}.
}
\]

Quotient Bottleneck-C closure requires

\[
Q_{A,Y}=0.
\]

Transform-safe / \(T\)-horizontal closure requires

\[
f_{A,Y}=0.
\]

The induced \(T\)-slope is

\[
\partial_\kappa T
=
-a_1^2\frac{f_{A,Y}}{c}.
\]

So on the generic \(v_5\ne0\) patch, if both quotient closure and \(T\)-horizontal closure hold, then

\[
E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}}=0.
\]

The finite table currently uses:

\[
W_{+,0},W_{+,1},W_{+,2},W_{+,3},
\]

\[
\Lambda^-_{a,0},\Lambda^-_{a,1},\Lambda^-_{a,2},\Lambda^-_{a,3},
\qquad a\in\{1,5\},
\]

\[
Y^{dd}_{g,0},\quad
Y^{d\eta+\eta d}_{g,0},\quad
Y^{\eta\eta}_{g,0},
\qquad 4\le g\le7.
\]

Earlier agents say the scalar midpoint source jets likely needed are

\[
q_0^{(k)}(m),\qquad 0\le k\le7
\]

or safely

\[
0\le k\le9,
\]

and

\[
(r_i^{[a]})^{(k)}(m),
\qquad
i=1,2,\quad a\in\{1,5\},\quad 2\le k\le9.
\]

But your job is to **try to derive these from the paper**, not merely repeat that they are missing.

# 1. Local obstruction: \(E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}}\)

Agent 1 and Agent 8 converge.

The active coefficient is:

\[
E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}}
=
\tau_{h\to m}\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}
\operatorname{Sym}
\sum_{\chi\in\{dd,d\eta+\eta d,\eta\eta\}}
\sum_{g=4}^{7}
\sum_{r+b=7-g}
H^A_{r,0}Y^\chi_{g,0}W_{+,b}.
\]

The source-position edge table is not the first Bottleneck-C carrier. The amplitude factor

\[
a_1a_2(a_1+a_2)
\]

already supplies the first \(\delta\)-edge, so the correct coefficient is the frozen one. turn35file2

The finite table is now completely specified. The active rows are:

\[
a\in\{1,5\},
\qquad
\chi\in\{dd,d\eta+\eta d,\eta\eta\},
\]

\[
4\le g\le7,
\qquad
r+b=7-g.
\]

The row is:

\[
\mathcal E^a_{\chi;g,r,b}
=
\tau_{h\to m}\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}
\operatorname{Sym}
\left(
\Lambda^-_{a,r}
Y^\chi_{g,0}
W_{+,b}
\right).
\]

The skew row

\[
Y_{d\eta-\eta d}^{(2)}
\]

is removed. No further row reduction is currently justified. 

The decisive scalars remain:

\[

\]

\[

\]

\[
f_{A,Y}.
\]

Quotient Bottleneck C requires:

\[
Q_{A,Y}=0.
\]

The transform-safe / \(T\)-horizontal condition requires:

\[
f_{A,Y}=0.
\]

On the generic \(v_5\ne0\) patch, both together force:

\[
E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}}=0.
\]

## What is now known

The transfer-side machinery is derivable:

\[
W_{+,0..3},
\qquad
\Lambda^-_{a,0..3},
\qquad
Y^\chi_{4..7,0}
\]

are all recursively computable once the relevant scalar midpoint jets are given. turn35file2

## What is still missing

The current draft does not determine the actual scalar midpoint source jets needed to evaluate the table:

\[
q_0^{(k)}(m),
\qquad 0\le k\le9,
\]

and

\[
(r_i^{[a]})^{(k)}(m),
\qquad
i=1,2,\quad a\in\{1,5\},\quad 2\le k\le9.
\]

Agent 1 sharpened this further: the problem is not just that a table is absent; the existing source normalizations do not force the desired cancellation. Affine removal removes too little, source-grade reflection gives parity but not vanishing, one-amplitude collapse gives the amplitude factor but not matrix cancellation, and fixed-sector projection keeps the symmetric rows. 

So the correct missing local theorem is one of these:

\[
\boxed{
E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}}=0
}
\]

or, weaker but still useful,

\[
\boxed{
Q_{A,Y}=0
\quad\text{and}\quad
f_{A,Y}=0.
}
\]

A quotient-only theorem

\[
Q_{A,Y}=0
\]

would not be enough for the augmented transform-safe package, because it can still leak through \(T\).

\[
\operatorname{dist}(\theta(m),\mathcal Z_k)
\gtrsim
\left(\frac{x}{B_\zeta(m)}S(m)\right)^{1/(\mu_{\Theta_k}(R+3))}
\]

up to constants/exponents depending on the exact optimization. This is not supplied by compactness, finite determinacy, same-scale normalization, zero-spacing, endpoint-gap controls, or finite-\(N\) positivity. 

The needed theorem can be stated either geometrically:

\[
\operatorname{dist}(\theta(m),\mathcal Z_k)
\ge
D_{\Theta_k}(m,Q),
\]

or more directly as a coefficient lower theorem:

\[
\max_N
\left|
c_{\core,2N-1}
+
\sum_{j\ge1}
c_{\core,2N-1+2j}h_jQ^{-2j}
\right|
\gtrsim
\frac{Q^{2N+2}}{(2N-1)N!(N-1)!}
\frac{x}{B_\zeta}S.
\]

The coefficient version is closer to what the \(N\)-point argument actually needs.

---

# 3. Interaction branch: still independent

Agent 10 again pushed the source-level attack and found no cancellation, no cone law, and no incidence containment for

\[
\mathfrak j_{ij}^{(2)}
=
[s]\Phi_K
\left(
D\mathcal W_0[\mathcal B_{ij}^{(2)}]
+
D^2\mathcal W_0[\mathcal B_i^{(1)},\mathcal B_j^{(1)}]
\right).
\]

The obstruction is already visible in the \(dd\)-sector. The corrected mixed-block Hessian contains a live term of the form

\[
-\frac{\sin\Delta_0}{2\pi s}
\left(
d_{i,-}d_{j,+}+d_{j,-}d_{i,+}
\right),
\]

and whitening can move diagonal content into the \(\Phi_K\)-visible channel. No present identity forces the direct Hessian contribution to cancel the bilinear whitening contribution. turn35file3

The interaction branch is:

\[
\mathfrak Z_{\rm int}
=
\left\{
\sum_\nu a_\nu K(d_\nu)+J_1=0
\right\}
\setminus\mathcal E_{\rm geom}.
\]

It is not absorbed by \(\mathcal N_k(m,Q)\). The reason is that \(\mathfrak Z_{\rm int}\) imposes only

\[
c_{\core,1}=0,
\]

whereas

\[
\mathcal Z_k
\]

requires the full finite-determinacy coefficient vector to vanish. One can have

\[
H_{\core}(s)=c_{\core,3}s^3+O(s^5),
\qquad
c_{\core,3}\ne0,
\]

while lying on \(\mathfrak Z_{\rm int}\). turn35file3

---

# Strategic next move

I would stop running broad agents. The current state calls for **two focused theorem attacks**.

## Attack A — local scalar closure for \(E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}}\)

The target should not be “derive the table” anymore. That has been done structurally. The target should be:

\[
\boxed{
E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}}=0
}
\]

or at least

\[
\boxed{
Q_{A,Y}=0
\quad\text{and}\quad
f_{A,Y}=0.
}
\]

The agents should try to prove a **promoted mixed-block scalar closure theorem**, not merely ask again for the source jets.

The theorem to attack:

```latex
\begin{theorem}[Promoted mixed-block Bottleneck-C scalar closure]
For the promoted mixed-block Bottleneck-C coefficient
\[
E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}}
=
\tau_{h\to m}\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}
\operatorname{Sym}
\sum_{a,\chi,g,r,b}
A_a\Lambda^-_{a,r}Y^\chi_{g,0}W_{+,b},
\]
one has
\[
E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}}=0.
\]
Equivalently, on the generic \(v_5\ne0\) patch,
\[
e_{A,Y}v_5-u_5f_{A,Y}=0
\quad\text{and}\quad
f_{A,Y}=0.
\]
\end{theorem}
```

If this theorem fails, the local proof attempt likely fails unless a new correction package cancels this channel.

## Attack B — finite-core obstruction split

The finite-core branch should now be split cleanly into two **independent** attacks:

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal N_k(m,Q)
}
\]

and

\[
\boxed{
\mathfrak Z_{\rm int}.
}
\]

Do not let agents conflate them.

For \(\mathcal N_k\), attack coefficient-scale anti-tangency.

For \(\mathfrak Z_{\rm int}\), attack source-level first-interaction rigidity.

## Consolidated verdict

This round materially sharpened the attack. It did **not** close a new theorem, but it reduced each live branch to a much more specific mathematical obstruction.

The current frontier is now:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Local: prove or refute endpoint-diagonal realization / parity closure for }E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}}.
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Finite-core: prove radial sampled anti-smallness / coefficient non-concentration.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Interaction: prove conditional definiteness or incidence control for the }dd\text{-kernel.}
}

# 1. Local branch: \(E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}}\)

The local agents pushed the \(E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}}\) obstruction much further. Earlier, the live object was the whole 60-row table. Now the best possible closure route is a parity/source-realization theorem.

The key conditional result is:

\[
\boxed{
\eta^\Delta=O(\delta)
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}}=0.
}
\]

Here

\[
\eta^\Delta=\frac{\eta_+-\eta_-}{2}.
\]

If the endpoint displacements \(\eta_+,\eta_-\) are evaluations of the **same analytic source-motion field** at \(h+\delta/2\) and \(h-\delta/2\), then

\[
\eta^\Delta
=
\frac{\delta}{2}\eta'(h)+O(\delta^3),
\]

so

\[
[\delta^0]\eta^\Delta=0.
\]

That kills the parity-bad frozen subchannels

\[
d\eta^\Delta+\eta^\Delta d,
\qquad
\eta^\Sigma\eta^\Delta,
\]

leaving only even-background channels. Since every active row satisfies

\[
r+b+g=7,
\]

the row becomes reflection-odd and is killed by fixed-sector symmetrization. That would prove

\[
E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}}=0,
\qquad
Q_{A,Y}=0,
\qquad
f_{A,Y}=0,
\qquad
\partial_\kappa T=0.
\]

But this is still conditional. The agents did **not** find, in the current proof state, a theorem guaranteeing that the endpoint displacement variables are co-moving in this sense. If \(\eta_+\) and \(\eta_-\) are independent frozen endpoint variables, then the parity-bad channels can survive and produce a quotient-visible and \(T\)-visible obstruction. 

So the local target is no longer “evaluate the 60-row table.” The next target is:

\[
\boxed{
[\delta^0]\eta^\Delta=0
\text{ for all active source directions.}
}
\]

Equivalently, prove the endpoint-diagonal source-realization theorem.

There is also an indexing correction: some older prompts used \(a\in\{1,5\}\), but the newer local attack notes that the draft’s finite Fréchet primitive table uses indices \(a=2,\dots,6\), and the first actual \(dd\)-row obstruction involves \(a=2\). Future local work should align with the draft’s actual source-index convention, not the older shorthand. 

---

# 2. Finite-core branch: radial anti-smallness is the irreducible issue

Agent 5 pushed the anti-tangency branch through several formulations: distance to \(\mathcal Z_k\), coefficient non-concentration, normal-cone approach, collar exclusion, adaptive \(Q\), and projective detection.

The useful reduction is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{projective detection is essentially handled by finite determinacy;}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{the remaining issue is radial sampled separation / anti-smallness.}
}
\]

Using the finite-determinacy coefficient norm

\[
\|H_{\core,\theta}\|_{\rm fd}
=
\max_{0\le r\le R_{\Theta_k}}
|c_{\core,2r+1}(\theta)|,
\]

some bounded \(N\) detects every nonzero projective direction once \(Q\) is large enough. Thus the projective tangent-cone issue is not the main blocker. The remaining theorem needed is a lower bound of the form

\[
\|H_{\core,\theta(m)}\|_{\rm fd}
\gtrsim
\max_{1\le N\le R_{\Theta_k}+1}
\left(
\frac{Q^{2N+2}}
{(2N-1)N!(N-1)!}
\frac{x}{B_\zeta(m)}S(m)
\right)
\]

outside

\[
\mathcal Z_k\cup\mathcal E_{\rm geom}.
\]

Equivalently, in coefficient form, the proof needs:

\[
\max_N |F_N(\theta(m),Q)|
\gtrsim
\max_N
\frac{Q^{2N+2}}
{(2N-1)N!(N-1)!}
\frac{x}{B_\zeta(m)}S(m).
\]

This is a sampled non-concentration theorem for actual zeta finite-core parameters. It does not follow from compactness, finite determinacy, zero spacing, endpoint-gap control, or positivity of the \(N\)-point kernel. 

Adaptive \(Q\) only changes the exponent. It does not remove the need for radial anti-smallness. If

\[
Z(m)=\frac{x}{B_\zeta(m)}S(m),
\]

then a typical optimized condition has the shape

\[
\operatorname{dist}(\theta(m),\mathcal Z_k)
\gtrsim
Z(m)^{1/(\mu_{\Theta_k}(R_{\Theta_k}+3))}.
\]

So the finite-core branch is now:

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal N_k^{\rm rad}(m,Q):
0<\|H_{\core,\theta(m)}\|_{\rm fd}
\ll
\text{calibrated }N\text{-point scale}.
}
\]

---

# 3. Interaction branch: \(dd\)-kernel rigidity is the core obstruction

Agent 10 pushed the interaction branch very far. The \(dd\)-sector remains live under increasingly favorable assumptions:

1. arbitrary normal gauge;
2. common Gram-source compatibility;
3. rank-one transverse source locking;
4. balanced amplitudes;
5. separation-only residual kernel;
6. finite-\(k\) centered kernel testing.

The important conclusion is:

\[
\boxed{
\mathfrak j_{ij}^{dd}
\text{ remains a genuine independent obstruction.}
}
\]

Whitening cancels radial normalization terms, but leaves the transverse cross-source inner product

\[
\langle x_i^\perp,y_j^\perp\rangle.
\]

Even if the source is rank-one locked, the interaction reduces to

\[
\mathfrak j_{ij}^{dd}
=
\alpha_i\beta_j\mathcal K_{dd}(m),
\]

which is not forced to vanish, does not have fixed sign because of signed amplitudes, and is not shown to lie in the controlled incidence ideal. 

Even under the best-case separation kernel form

\[
\mathfrak j_{ij}^{dd}=K_{dd}(u_i-u_j;m),
\]

balanced amplitudes do not close the branch. A centered \(k\times k\) kernel matrix must be one-sided on

\[
\mathbf 1^\perp,
\]

but this is a genuine spectral condition. For \(k=3\), one already needs inequalities comparing values like

\[
K_{dd}(1;m)
\quad\text{and}\quad
K_{dd}(2;m).
\]

Analyticity, symmetry, collision divisibility, and pair-like positivity do not imply those inequalities. 

So the interaction target has sharpened to:

\[
\boxed{
\text{prove conditional definiteness / centered-kernel spectral rigidity for }K_{dd},
}
\]

or prove that the signature-changing loci are controlled incidence.

---

\ll

```text
\[

\gtrsim
\max_{1\le N\le R_{\Theta_k}+1}

\frac{Q^{2N+2}}
{(2N-1)N!(N-1)!}
\frac{x}{B_\zeta(m)}S(m)
\right)

outside
\[
\mathcal Z_k\cup\mathcal E_{\rm geom}.
\]

Here
\[
\|H_{\core,\theta}\|_{\rm fd}
=

|c_{\core,2r+1}(\theta)|.

Tasks:

\[

\|H_{\core,\theta(m)}\|_{\rm fd}
\ge \text{calibrated scale}.
\]
3. Test whether zero-spacing, endpoint gaps, same-scale normalization, discreteness of zeros, \(S(m)\), \(B_\zeta(m)\), or known zeta-side estimates imply this bound.
4. Test adaptive \(Q\): derive the best possible exponent if \(Q\) is chosen optimally.
5. If the theorem cannot be proved, formulate the exact bad branch:

\mathcal N_k^{\rm rad}(m,Q)
=
\left\{
\theta(m)\notin\mathcal Z_k\cup\mathcal E_{\rm geom}:
0<\|H_{\core,\theta(m)}\|_{\rm fd}
```

# Agent FC-B — interaction / centered \(dd\)-kernel spectral rigidity

This agent attacks the **mechanism that can make coefficients small**, especially the interaction term:

\[
J_1=[s]\Phi_K(\mathcal I_{\ge2}).
\]

They should focus on the \(dd\)-sector and conditional definiteness.

Prompt:

```text
You are attacking the finite-core interaction rigidity branch, especially the centered \(dd\)-kernel.

Do not work on general radial anti-smallness except to explain how this branch can feed it.

Target:
Control
\[
J_1=[s]\Phi_K(\mathcal I_{\ge2}),
\]
especially the two-source \(dd\)-component
\[
\mathfrak j_{ij}^{dd}.
\]

Assume the most favorable reduction if useful:
\[
\mathfrak j_{ij}^{dd}
=
K_{dd}(u_i-u_j;m),
\qquad
K_{dd}(t)=K_{dd}(-t),
\qquad
K_{dd}(0)=0.
\]

Tasks:
1. Derive the centered finite-core quadratic form:
\[
J_{dd}^{(2)}
=
\sum_{i<j}a_i a_j K_{dd}(u_i-u_j;m),
\qquad
\sum_i a_i=0.
\]
2. For \(k=3\), take
\[
u=(-1,0,1),
\]
write
\[
A=K_{dd}(1;m),
\qquad
B=K_{dd}(2;m),
\]
and derive the sign/PSD condition on the balanced subspace.
3. Check whether the paper’s source formula for \(K_{dd}\) implies this condition, e.g. a relation like
\[
A\ge B/4
\]
up to phase/sign convention.
4. If not, test whether the signature-changing locus is controlled incidence:
\[
M=0,\ W=0,\ K_v=0,\ T_v=0,
\]
collision, endpoint-gap, patch-boundary, amplitude drop, whitening singularity, \(c=0\), \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}=0\), or hidden-rank jump.
5. Extend to general \(k\): formulate the needed spectral condition for
\[
P\mathcal K P,
\qquad
P=I-\frac1k\mathbf 1\mathbf 1^\top.
\]
6. If spectral rigidity is unavailable, define the independent branch:
\[
\mathfrak Z_{\rm int}^{dd}
=
\left\{
\sum_\nu a_\nu K(d_\nu)
+
\sum_{i<j}a_i a_jK_{dd}(u_i-u_j;m)
=0
\right\}
\setminus \mathcal E_{\rm geom}.
\]

Deliverable:
A conditional-definiteness theorem, an incidence-containment theorem, or a precise centered-kernel obstruction branch.
```

---

# Why this split is correct

Agent FC-A asks:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Can actual zeta finite-core germs be too small?}
}
\]

Agent FC-B asks:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Can interaction terms cause that smallness?}
}
\]

So FC-A is global/radial; FC-B is structural/mechanistic.

If FC-B proves interaction rigidity, FC-A’s job becomes easier. If FC-B fails, FC-A must carry \(\mathfrak Z_{\rm int}^{dd}\) as a mechanism feeding radial smallness.

I would not run two agents on radial anti-smallness at the same time. That will mostly produce the same negative compactness/Łojasiewicz analysis again.

The goal is to attack the three live mathematical blockers from independent angles, not to produce more status notes.

---

# Shared background for all agents

We are attacking the latest RH proof draft mathematically. Do **not** do paper-editing unless you find a theorem, counterexample, or precise missing lemma. Work from the current paper and the following consolidated state.

Closed or paused branches:

\[
\boxed{M_A,M_C\text{ connection closure is done.}}
\]

\[
\boxed{\text{Mixed four-point is dependency-closed.}}
\]

\[
\boxed{\text{Qualitative finite odd-germ determinacy is done.}}
\]

The three live blockers are now:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Local blocker: }E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Finite-core blocker: radial sampled anti-smallness}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Interaction blocker: }J_1=[s]\Phi_K(\mathcal I_{\ge2})
}
\]

## I. Local blocker: \(E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}}\)

The first live local actual-source / Bottleneck-C carrier is the promoted quadratic mixed-block Hessian

\[
Y_{12}^{(2)}=D^2N_0[\xi_1,\xi_2].
\]

The active coefficient is **not** the internal source-position \([z^7\delta^1]\) coefficient. The amplitude factor

\[
a_1a_2(a_1+a_2)
\]

already supplies the first \(\delta\)-edge on the collision chart

\[
a_2=-a_1(1+\kappa\delta),
\]

because

\[
a_1a_2(a_1+a_2)=a_1^3\kappa\delta+O(\delta^2).
\]

Therefore the active coefficient is the **frozen** Bottleneck-C coefficient

\[
E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}}
=
\tau_{h\to m}\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}
\operatorname{Sym}
[z^7]\,
D(G_-^{-1/2})[A_-]\,
Y_{12}^{(2)}
R_0.
\]

Equivalently,

\[
E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}}
=
\tau_{h\to m}\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}
\operatorname{Sym}
\sum_{\chi\in\{dd,d\eta+\eta d,\eta\eta\}}
\sum_{g=4}^{7}
\sum_{r+b=7-g}
H^A_{r,0}Y^\chi_{g,0}W_{+,b}.
\]

Write

\[
E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}}=e_{A,Y}I+f_{A,Y}S.
\]

The two decisive scalar tests are:

\[
Q_{A,Y}=e_{A,Y}v_5-u_5f_{A,Y},
\]

and

\[
f_{A,Y}.
\]

Quotient Bottleneck-C closure requires

\[
Q_{A,Y}=0.
\]

The augmented transform-safe / \(T\)-horizontal condition requires

\[
f_{A,Y}=0,
\]

because

\[
\partial_\kappa T
=
-a_1^2\frac{f_{A,Y}}{c}.
\]

On the generic \(v_5\ne0\) patch, quotient closure plus \(T\)-horizontal closure forces

\[
E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}}=0.
\]

The old 60-row table has been reduced structurally, but not evaluated. Later local attacks found a possible parity closure route: if the endpoint-displacement separation component

\[
\eta^\Delta:=\frac{\eta_+-\eta_-}{2}
\]

vanishes at the frozen face,

\[
[\delta^0]\eta^\Delta=0,
\]

then the parity-bad frozen subchannels

\[
d\eta^\Delta+\eta^\Delta d,
\qquad
\eta^\Sigma\eta^\Delta
\]

vanish, where

\[
\eta^\Sigma:=\frac{\eta_++\eta_-}{2}.
\]

Then only even-background channels remain; since every active row satisfies

\[
r+b+g=7,
\]

each row is reflection-odd and killed by fixed-sector symmetrization. This would prove

\[
E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}}=0.
\]

However, the current draft state does **not yet prove** that endpoint displacement sources are co-moving / endpoint-diagonal:

\[
\eta_{i,+}=\eta_i(h+\delta/2),
\qquad
\eta_{i,-}=\eta_i(h-\delta/2).
\]

If instead \(\eta_+\) and \(\eta_-\) are independent frozen endpoint variables, then \([\delta^0]\eta^\Delta\) can survive, and \(E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}}\) can be quotient-visible and \(T\)-visible. 

Also note a source-index warning. Some older prompts used \(a\in\{1,5\}\), but the latest finite Fréchet primitive table appears to use indices \(a=2,\dots,6\), and a concrete \(dd\)-row obstruction involved \(a=2\). Agents must align notation with the paper’s actual finite Fréchet index convention before drawing conclusions. 

---

## II. Finite-core blocker: radial sampled anti-smallness

Qualitative finite determinacy is done. On a compact nonsingular actual-source \(k\)-core stratum \(\Theta_k\), there exists \(R_{\Theta_k}\) such that

\[
c_{\core,1}=\cdots=c_{\core,2R_{\Theta_k}+1}=0
\]

implies

\[
H_{\core,\theta}\equiv0.
\]

Define the finite-determinacy norm

\[
\|H_{\core,\theta}\|_{\rm fd}
=
\max_{0\le r\le R_{\Theta_k}}
|c_{\core,2r+1}(\theta)|.
\]

The latest finite-core attack showed that **projective detection is basically handled**: once \(Q\) is large enough, some bounded \(N\) detects this finite-determinacy norm up to \(O(Q^{-2})\) tail error. Thus the real remaining issue is **radial size**, not direction. 

The missing theorem is a sampled radial lower bound for actual zeta finite-core parameters:

\[
\|H_{\core,\theta(m)}\|_{\rm fd}
\gtrsim
\max_{1\le N\le R_{\Theta_k}+1}
\left(
\frac{Q^{2N+2}}
{(2N-1)N!(N-1)!}
\frac{x}{B_\zeta(m)}S(m)
\right),
\]

outside

\[
\mathcal Z_k\cup\mathcal E_{\rm geom},
\]

where

\[
\mathcal Z_k=\{\theta:H_{\core,\theta}\equiv0\}.
\]

Equivalently, using a filtered coefficient

\[
F_N(\theta,Q)
=
c_{\core,2N-1}(\theta)
+
\sum_{j\ge1}
c_{\core,2N-1+2j}(\theta)
h_j(1^2,\dots,N^2)Q^{-2j},
\]

the proof needs

\[
\max_N |F_N(\theta(m),Q)|
\gtrsim
\max_N
\left(
\frac{Q^{2N+2}}
{(2N-1)N!(N-1)!}
\frac{x}{B_\zeta(m)}S(m)
\right).
\]

This is a sampled coefficient non-concentration theorem for actual zeta core parameters. Compactness, finite determinacy, zero-spacing, endpoint-gap controls, and \(N\)-point positivity do not imply it. Adaptive \(Q\) only changes exponents; it does not remove the need for anti-smallness. 

The unresolved branch is:

\[
\mathcal N_k^{\rm rad}(m,Q)
=
\left\{
\theta(m)\notin\mathcal Z_k\cup\mathcal E_{\rm geom}:
0<\|H_{\core,\theta(m)}\|_{\rm fd}
<
\text{calibrated scale}
\right\}.
\]

---

## III. Interaction blocker: \(J_1=[s]\Phi_K(\mathcal I_{\ge2})\)

The first interaction branch remains independent. At two-source order,

\[
J_1^{(2)}
=
\sum_{i<j}a_i a_j\mathfrak j_{ij}^{(2)},
\]

where

\[
\mathfrak j_{ij}^{(2)}
=
[s]\Phi_K
\left(
D\mathcal W_0[\mathcal B_{ij}^{(2)}]
+
D^2\mathcal W_0[\mathcal B_i^{(1)},\mathcal B_j^{(1)}]
\right).
\]

The hardest concrete channel is the \(dd\)-sector. After increasingly favorable reductions, it remains live under:

\[
\text{normal gauge},
\]

\[
\text{common Gram-source compatibility},
\]

\[
\text{rank-one transverse source locking},
\]

\[
\text{balanced amplitudes},
\]

\[
\text{separation-only residual kernel}.
\]

In a Gram-compatible normal form, whitening removes radial normalization terms but leaves a transverse cross-source inner product

\[
\langle x_i^\perp,y_j^\perp\rangle.
\]

Rank-one locking reduces this to a scalar kernel but does not force vanishing or a sign law. Balanced amplitudes do not control the residual kernel unless it has conditional definiteness. 

Under the most favorable separation-kernel reduction,

\[
\mathfrak j_{ij}^{dd}=K_{dd}(u_i-u_j;m),
\]

where

\[
K_{dd}(t)=K_{dd}(-t),
\qquad
K_{dd}(0)=0,
\]

one still needs the centered kernel matrix

\[
\mathcal K_{ij}=K_{dd}(u_i-u_j;m)
\]

to be one-sided on the balanced subspace

\[
\mathbf 1^\perp.
\]

For \(k=3\), with

\[
u=(-1,0,1),
\]

let

\[
A=K_{dd}(1;m),
\qquad
B=K_{dd}(2;m).
\]

One-sidedness already imposes a nontrivial inequality such as

\[
A\ge \frac14 B
\]

up to phase/sign convention. Analyticity, symmetry, collision divisibility, pair-like positivity, and same-scale compactness do not imply this. 

Thus the interaction target is now:

\[
\boxed{
\text{prove centered }dd\text{-kernel spectral rigidity / conditional definiteness,}
}
\]

or show that signature-changing loci are controlled incidence.

---

# Deployment: two agents per live problem

We will attack each live problem from two different angles.

# Local Agent 1 — endpoint-diagonal realization attack

```text
You are attacking the local obstruction \(E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}}\) through the endpoint-diagonal realization route.

Background:
The active Bottleneck-C carrier is the frozen coefficient
\[
E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}}
=
\tau_{h\to m}\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}
\operatorname{Sym}
[z^7]D(G_-^{-1/2})[A_-]Y_{12}^{(2)}R_0.
\]
Do not use the internal \([z^7\delta^1]\) table. The amplitude
\[
a_1a_2(a_1+a_2)
\]
already supplies the first \(\delta\)-edge on
\[
a_2=-a_1(1+\kappa\delta).
\]

Target:
Prove or refute
\[
[\delta^0]\eta_i^\Delta=0,
\qquad
\eta_i^\Delta=\frac{\eta_{i,+}-\eta_{i,-}}{2},
\]
for every active source direction \(\xi_i\) entering
\[
Y_{12}^{(2)}=D^2N_0[\xi_1,\xi_2].
\]

Tasks:
1. Locate the actual paper definitions of \(\eta_{i,+},\eta_{i,-},d_{i,+},d_{i,-}\), and the source-motion variables used in \(N^{\corr}\).
2. Determine whether \(\eta_{i,+}\) and \(\eta_{i,-}\) are evaluations of one analytic source-motion field:
\[
\eta_{i,+}=\eta_i(h+\delta/2),
\qquad
\eta_{i,-}=\eta_i(h-\delta/2).
\]
3. If yes, prove
\[
\eta_i^\Delta=O(\delta),
\]
and therefore prove the parity-bad frozen subchannels vanish:
\[
Y^{d\eta^\Delta+\eta^\Delta d}_{g,0}=0,
\qquad
Y^{\eta^\Sigma\eta^\Delta}_{g,0}=0.
\]
Then conclude
\[
E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}}=0.
\]
4. If no, identify the exact surviving parity-bad source component. Determine whether it can carry \(S\)-projection and hence \(T\)-leakage.
5. Align notation with the actual finite Fréchet index convention in the paper. Do not rely on older shorthand \(a\in\{1,5\}\) if the draft uses \(a=2,\dots,6\).

Deliverable:
Either a proof of endpoint-diagonal source realization and local closure, or a concrete parity-bad survivor.
```

# Local Agent 2 — direct Hessian parity / odd-background audit

```text
You are attacking \(E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}}\) through direct parity audit of the promoted Hessian.

Background:
The possible closure route is:
\[
\mathscr R(Y^\chi_{g,0})=(-1)^gY^\chi_{g,0}
\]
for every surviving frozen Hessian channel
\[
\chi\in\{dd,d\eta+\eta d,\eta\eta\}.
\]
If this holds, then every active row has sign
\[
(-1)^{r+b+g}=(-1)^7=-1,
\]
so fixed-sector symmetrization kills the carrier:
\[
E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}}=0.
\]

Target:
Inspect the actual corrected mixed block
\[
N^{\corr}(q_-,q_+,\Delta;s)
\]
and determine whether the frozen Hessian \(D^2N_0[\xi_1,\xi_2]\) has any odd-background surviving terms.

Tasks:
1. Decompose each surviving channel
\[
dd,\quad d\eta+\eta d,\quad \eta\eta
\]
into source-reflection grades \(p_1,p_2\) and background order \(\ell\):
\[
Y^\chi_{g,0}=\sum_{p_1+p_2+\ell=g}Y^\chi_{p_1,p_2,\ell}.
\]
2. Prove or refute that every nonzero surviving summand has
\[
\ell\equiv0\pmod2.
\]
3. For \(\eta\)-channels, split endpoint displacement into midpoint and separation components:
\[
\eta^\Sigma=\frac{\eta_++\eta_-}{2},
\qquad
\eta^\Delta=\frac{\eta_+-\eta_-}{2}.
\]
Audit whether \(d\eta^\Delta+\eta^\Delta d\) or \(\eta^\Sigma\eta^\Delta\) survives in the frozen coefficient.
4. If all odd-background pieces vanish, prove
\[
E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}}=0.
\]
5. If some odd-background piece survives, give the minimal surviving term and compute whether it can contribute to \(f_{A,Y}\) or \(Q_{A,Y}\).

Deliverable:
A proof of no odd-background frozen Hessian support, or a concrete odd-background survivor.
```

# Finite-Core Agent 1 — radial sampled anti-smallness

```text
You are attacking finite-core radial sampled anti-smallness.

Do not work on \(J_1\)-kernel spectral rigidity except as a possible mechanism feeding radial smallness.
```
