```text
Finite determinacy gives the finite-determinacy norm
\[
\|H_{\core,\theta}\|_{\rm fd}
=
\max_{0\le r\le R_{\Theta_k}}|c_{\core,2r+1}(\theta)|.
\]
Projective detection by bounded \(N\)-point coefficients is essentially handled after \(Q^{-2}\)-tail control. The remaining issue is radial size.

Target:
Prove or refute
\[
\|H_{\core,\theta(m)}\|_{\rm fd}
\gtrsim
\max_{1\le N\le R_{\Theta_k}+1}
\left(
\frac{Q^{2N+2}}
{(2N-1)N!(N-1)!}
\frac{x}{B_\zeta(m)}S(m)
\right)
\]
outside
\[
\mathcal Z_k\cup\mathcal E_{\rm geom}.
\]

Tasks:
1. Confirm the projective detection proposition:
for \(Q\) large enough, some bounded \(N\le R_{\Theta_k}+1\) has
\[
|F_N(\theta,Q)|\ge c\|H_{\core,\theta}\|_{\rm fd}.
\]
2. Then focus entirely on radial lower bounds for actual samples:
\[
\theta(m)\notin\mathcal Z_k\cup\mathcal E_{\rm geom}
\Rightarrow
\|H_{\core,\theta(m)}\|_{\rm fd}\ge \text{calibrated scale}.
\]
3. Test whether zero spacing, endpoint gaps, same-scale normalization, discreteness of zeta zeros, \(S(m)\), \(B_\zeta(m)\), or known zeta-side estimates imply this.
4. Re-check adaptive \(Q\): derive the optimal exponent and determine exactly when feasible \(Q\) exists.
5. If no proof exists, formulate the minimal bad branch
\[
\mathcal N_k^{\rm rad}(m,Q)
=
\left\{
\theta(m)\notin\mathcal Z_k\cup\mathcal E_{\rm geom}:
0<\|H_{\core,\theta(m)}\|_{\rm fd}<\text{calibrated scale}
\right\}.
\]

Deliverable:
A radial sampled anti-smallness theorem, or a theorem-ready unresolved radial branch.
```

```text
\[

5. Formulate the sharpest coefficient-small bad branch:
\[
\mathcal N_k^{\rm coef}(m,Q)
=
```

# Interaction Agent 1 — \(dd\)-kernel spectral rigidity

```text
You are attacking the interaction branch through the finite-\(k\) centered \(dd\)-kernel.

Known:
The interaction term
\[
J_1=[s]\Phi_K(\mathcal I_{\ge2})
\]
has a live \(dd\)-sector. Even under favorable reductions, we may get
\[
\mathfrak j_{ij}^{dd}=K_{dd}(u_i-u_j;m),
\]

\[
K_{dd}(t)=K_{dd}(-t),
\qquad
K_{dd}(0)=0.
\]

Target:
Prove or refute that the centered kernel matrix
\[
\mathcal K_{ij}=K_{dd}(u_i-u_j;m)
\]
is one-sided on the balanced subspace
\[
\mathbf 1^\perp.
\]

Tasks:
1. Start with \(k=3\), \(u=(-1,0,1)\).
Let
\[
A=K_{dd}(1;m),
\qquad
B=K_{dd}(2;m).
\]
Derive the sign condition on the balanced subspace. Check whether the paper’s source formula implies it.
2. Test Taylor models:
\[
K_{dd}(t)=t^2,\quad t^4,\quad t^2+\epsilon t^4.
\]
Use them to understand which coefficient signs are needed.
3. Determine whether same-scale compactness or pair-like positivity implies the centered kernel sign condition. If not, explain why.
4. Extend to general finite \(k\): formulate the spectral condition for
\[
P\mathcal K P,
\qquad
P=I-\frac1k\mathbf 1\mathbf 1^\top.
\]
5. If no theorem exists, formulate the required finite-core centered \(dd\)-kernel spectral rigidity theorem.

Deliverable:
A conditional-definiteness theorem, or a precise centered-kernel spectral obstruction.
```

# Interaction Agent 2 — source-level \(dd\)-rigidity / incidence containment

```text
You are attacking \(J_1\) through source-level \(dd\)-rigidity and incidence containment.

Do not assume a separation-only kernel unless you derive it from the paper. Start from the actual source-level expression
\[
\mathfrak j_{ij}^{(2)}
=
[s]\Phi_K
\left(
D\mathcal W_0[\mathcal B_{ij}^{(2)}]
+
D^2\mathcal W_0[\mathcal B_i^{(1)},\mathcal B_j^{(1)}]
\right).
\]

Target:
Determine whether the \(dd\)-sector is zero, sign-controlled, or contained in the controlled incidence radical.

Tasks:
1. Work in normal gauge and derive the \(dd\)-sector of the second variation explicitly:
\[
\mathcal C_{ij,dd}^{(2)}
=
D\mathcal W_0[\mathcal B_{ij,dd}^{(2)}]
+
D^2\mathcal W_0[\mathcal B_{i,d}^{(1)},\mathcal B_{j,d}^{(1)}].
\]
2. Interpret whitening geometrically: identify the radial normalization terms that cancel and the transverse cross-source inner product that survives.
3. Test whether actual zeta source directions are constrained enough to force transverse \(dd\)-orthogonality:
\[
\langle x_i^\perp,y_j^\perp\rangle=0.
\]
4. If not, test rank-one locking:
\[
x_i^\perp=\alpha_i u_-,
\qquad
y_j^\perp=\beta_j u_+.
\]
Does this imply zero, fixed sign, or incidence containment? If no, explain why signed amplitudes still allow cancellation.
5. Test whether the \(dd\)-sector lies in the radical of the controlled incidence ideal:
\[
M,W,K_v,T_v,
\]
collision, endpoint-gap, patch-boundary, amplitude drop, whitening singularity, \(c=0\), \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}=0\), hidden-rank jump.
6. If no, formulate the independent branch
\[
\mathfrak Z_{\rm int}^{dd}
=
\left\{
\sum_\nu a_\nu K(d_\nu)+
\sum_{i<j}a_i a_j\mathfrak j_{ij}^{dd}=0
\right\}
\setminus\mathcal E_{\rm geom}.
\]

Deliverable:
A source-level \(dd\)-interaction rigidity theorem, incidence-containment theorem, or independent interaction branch.
```

# Coordination rules

The two local agents should compare only on the question:

\[
[\delta^0]\eta^\Delta=0?
\]

If Local Agent 1 proves endpoint-diagonal source realization, Local Agent 2 should use it to close parity. If Local Agent 2 finds an odd-background survivor independent of \(\eta^\Delta\), that refutes the endpoint-diagonal route.

The two finite-core agents should stay split:

\[
\text{FC1: radial norm size}
\]

\[
\text{FC2: sampled coefficient non-concentration}
\]

They should not both repeat compactness / finite determinacy.

The two interaction agents should stay split:

\[
\text{INT1: centered kernel spectral condition}
\]

\[
\text{INT2: source-level orthogonality/incidence}
\]

They meet only if INT2 derives a separation kernel \(K_{dd}\), which INT1 can then test spectrally.

## Consolidated verdict

This round sharpened all three live blockers. It did **not** close a theorem.

The main update is local: **endpoint-diagonal realization is not enough anymore**. Local Agent 2 found an odd-background frozen \(\eta\eta\) Hessian survivor directly inside the corrected mixed block \(N^{\corr}(q_-,q_+,\Delta;s)\), independent of the \(\eta^\Delta\) endpoint-separation issue. So even if Local Agent 1 later proves \([\delta^0]\eta^\Delta=0\), \(E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}}\) is still not closed unless this \(\eta\eta\) odd-background term is killed by a separate fixed-sector cancellation theorem.

# 1. Local branch: the new blocker is \(\eta\eta\) odd-background cancellation

Local Agent 1 confirmed the conditional route:

\[
[\delta^0]\eta^\Delta=0
\quad\Rightarrow\quad
\text{parity-bad endpoint-separation terms vanish.}
\]

But that theorem is not proved from the current source definitions. If \(\eta_+\) and \(\eta_-\) are independent frozen endpoint variables, then \(d\eta^\Delta+\eta^\Delta d\) and \(\eta^\Sigma\eta^\Delta\) can survive and leak through \(S\). 

Local Agent 2 found something stronger: the corrected mixed block itself contains an odd-background \(\eta\eta\) Hessian term. In particular, from

\[
N_{12}
=
\frac{\sin\Delta+q_+s\cos\Delta}{s^2},
\]

twice differentiating in \(\Delta\) gives

\[
\partial_\Delta^2 N_{12}\big|_0
=
-\frac{\sin\Delta_0}{s^2}
-
\frac{q_{0,+}\cos\Delta_0}{s}.
\]

Since \(\sin\Delta_0\) is odd and \(s^2\) is even, the term

\[
-\frac{\sin\Delta_0}{s^2}\eta_i\eta_j
\]

is an odd-background frozen \(\eta\eta\) survivor. It lands in the active \(\eta\eta\) channel, not the killed \(d\eta-\eta d\) channel. 

So the local target should now be:

\[
\boxed{
\tau_{h\to m}\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}
\operatorname{Sym}
\left(
\Lambda^-_{a,r}
\left[\partial_\Delta^2N_0\right]_{\eta\eta,\mathrm{odd}}
W_{+,b}
\right)=0
}
\]

for every active row \(r+b+g=7\).

This is more specific than the previous \(E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}}=0\) target and more urgent than the endpoint-diagonal route.

## Next local deployment

Run two local agents as follows:

```text
\operatorname{Sym}
\left(
\Lambda^-_{a,r}
\left[\partial_\Delta^2N_0\right]_{\eta\eta,\mathrm{odd}}
W_{+,b}
\right)=0
\]
for all active rows \(r+b+g=7\).

Start from
\[
N_{12}=\frac{\sin\Delta+q_+s\cos\Delta}{s^2},
\qquad
N_{21}=-\frac{\sin\Delta+q_-s\cos\Delta}{s^2}.
\]

Tasks:
1. Compute the full \((1,2)/(2,1)\) \(\eta\eta\) odd-background block, including the \(q_{\pm}\cos\Delta_0/s\) companions.
2. Apply endpoint transpose, \(\operatorname{Sym}\), \(\tau_{h\to m}\), and \(\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}\).
3. Determine whether the \(-\sin\Delta_0/s^2\) term cancels with the \(q_{\pm}\cos\Delta_0/s\) terms after fixed-sector projection.
4. If it does not cancel, compute whether it has nonzero \(S\)-projection or nonzero quotient determinant.

Deliverable:
A proof of fixed-sector cancellation of the odd \(\eta\eta\) block, or a concrete \(S\)-/quotient-visible survivor.
```

### Local B — endpoint-diagonal source realization

Keep this agent, but lower priority. It still matters for the \(d\eta^\Delta+\eta^\Delta d\) and \(\eta^\Sigma\eta^\Delta\) subchannels, but it no longer closes the whole local branch alone.

```text
Attack endpoint-diagonal source realization.

Target:
\[
[\delta^0]\eta_i^\Delta=0,
\qquad
\eta_i^\Delta=\frac{\eta_{i,+}-\eta_{i,-}}2.
\]

Prove from the paper’s source definitions that
\[
\eta_{i,+}=\eta_i(h+\delta/2),
\qquad
\eta_{i,-}=\eta_i(h-\delta/2)
\]
for one analytic co-moving source-motion field \(\eta_i(t)\).

If true, conclude that the endpoint-separation subchannels
\[
d\eta^\Delta+\eta^\Delta d,
\qquad
\eta^\Sigma\eta^\Delta
\]
do not contribute to the frozen \(E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}}\).

If false, produce the explicit parity-bad endpoint source component and determine whether it can contribute to \(f_{A,Y}\).
```

---

# 2. Finite-core branch: radial sampled anti-smallness is the irreducible blocker

FC1 and FC2 agree. Projective detection is basically done: with the finite-determinacy norm

\[
\|H_{\core,\theta}\|_{\rm fd}
=
\max_{0\le r\le R_{\Theta_k}}|c_{\core,2r+1}(\theta)|,
\]

some bounded \(N\) detects a nonzero germ once \(Q^{-2}\)-tail error is controlled. The real missing input is a **radial lower bound** on the size of the actual zeta finite-core germ. 

The needed theorem is:

\[
\|H_{\core,\theta(m)}\|_{\rm fd}
\gtrsim
\max_{1\le N\le R_{\Theta_k}+1}
\left(
\frac{Q^{2N+2}}
{(2N-1)N!(N-1)!}
\frac{x}{B_\zeta(m)}S(m)
\right)
\]

outside

\[
\mathcal Z_k\cup\mathcal E_{\rm geom}.
\]

FC2 restates the same obstruction in coefficient-sampling form: the actual zeta sample map \(m\mapsto\theta(m)\) must avoid the analytic small-value sets

\[
\max_N |F_N(\theta(m),Q)|<\Lambda(m,Q).
\]

Zero spacing, discreteness of zeros, compactness, and Remez/Łojasiewicz volume estimates do not give the required pointwise exclusion. 

So the finite-core branch is now:

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal N_k^{\rm rad}
\quad\text{or equivalently}\quad
\mathcal N_k^{\rm coef}.
}
\]

No need to run two agents on finite determinacy or projective detection again.

## Next finite-core deployment

Split them like this:

### Finite-Core A — arithmetic/sampling non-concentration

```text
Attack sampled coefficient non-concentration for actual zeta core parameters.

Target:
\[
\max_{1\le N\le R_{\Theta_k}+1}|F_N(\theta(m),Q)|
\ge
\Lambda(m,Q)
\]
outside
\[
\mathcal Z_k\cup\mathcal E_{\rm geom}.
\]

Do not re-prove finite determinacy or projective detection.

Tasks:
1. Search for any arithmetic/distribution/separation theorem in the draft that constrains the actual sample map \(m\mapsto\theta(m)\) relative to analytic small-value sets.
2. Test whether zero-spacing plus endpoint-gap controls can imply a lower bound for \(F_N\), not just collision avoidance.
3. If not, formulate the exact Diophantine/sampling theorem needed.
4. State whether a weaker density theorem would be enough for the global RH exclusion. If not, explain why the proof needs pointwise exclusion.

Deliverable:
A sampled coefficient non-concentration theorem, or a precise statement that the proof requires a new pointwise arithmetic separation theorem.
```

### Finite-Core B — mechanisms feeding radial smallness

```text
Attack mechanisms that can make \(\|H_{\core,\theta(m)}\|_{\rm fd}\) small outside controlled incidence.

Target:
Identify whether interaction cancellation, especially \(J_1\), can drive
\[
0<\|H_{\core,\theta(m)}\|_{\rm fd}\ll \Lambda(m,Q)
\]
without entering \(\mathcal E_{\rm geom}\).

Tasks:
1. Analyze how \(J_1=[s]\Phi_K(\mathcal I_{\ge2})\) enters \(c_{\core,1}\).
2. Determine whether similar interaction terms can affect higher finite-determinacy coefficients.
3. Test whether smallness of the finite vector
\[
(c_{\core,1},c_{\core,3},\ldots,c_{\core,2R+1})
\]
forces any controlled incidence.
4. If not, define the mechanism branch feeding \(\mathcal N_k^{\rm rad}\).

Deliverable:
Either a mechanism-to-incidence theorem, or a precise interaction-fed radial-smallness branch.
```

---

# 3. Interaction branch: \(dd\)-kernel rigidity is still independent

INT1 and INT2 agree from different angles.

INT1 shows that even under the favorable separation-kernel reduction

\[
\mathfrak j_{ij}^{dd}=K_{dd}(u_i-u_j;m),
\]

one still needs a centered spectral theorem for the matrix

\[
\mathcal K_{ij}=K_{dd}(u_i-u_j;m)
\]

on the balanced subspace \(\mathbf 1^\perp\). Already at \(k=3\), with \(u=(-1,0,1)\), the condition depends on

\[
A=K_{dd}(1;m),
\qquad
B=K_{dd}(2;m),
\]

and requires a nontrivial inequality like

\[
A\ge B/4
\]

up to sign/phase convention. This is not implied by evenness, analyticity, collision divisibility, same-scale compactness, or pair-like positivity. 

INT2 shows that before even assuming separation-only form, the source-level \(dd\)-interaction contains a transverse cross-source inner product

\[
\langle x_i^\perp,y_j^\perp\rangle
\]

left after whitening removes radial components. This transverse fiber angle is invisible to one-pair/lifted-curve incidence data, so the current incidence package does not control it. 

So the interaction blocker is now two-layered:

\[
\boxed{
\text{source-level transverse \(dd\)-fiber rigidity}
}
\]

and, if that reduces to a separation kernel,

\[
\boxed{
\text{centered \(dd\)-kernel spectral rigidity}.
}
\]

## Next interaction deployment

### Interaction A — source-level transverse fiber rigidity

```text
Attack the source-level transverse \(dd\)-fiber obstruction.

Target:
Control or eliminate
\[
\langle x_i^\perp,y_j^\perp\rangle
\]
inside \(\mathfrak j_{ij}^{dd}\).

Tasks:
1. Work from the normal-gauge whitened second variation.
2. Identify exactly how \(\langle x_i^\perp,y_j^\perp\rangle\) enters \([s]\Phi_K\).
3. Test whether the paper’s one-pair incidence data
\[
M,W,K_v,T_v
\]
or endpoint-gap/patch conditions determine this transverse angle.
4. Test rank-one locking:
\[
x_i^\perp=\alpha_i u_-,
\qquad
y_j^\perp=\beta_j u_+.
\]
Does it force zero, sign, or incidence containment after signed amplitudes \(a_i a_j\)?
5. If not, formulate the exact fiberwise transverse \(dd\)-rigidity theorem needed.

Deliverable:
A proof of transverse \(dd\)-orthogonality/sign/incidence control, or an independent fiber-angle obstruction.
```

### Interaction B — centered-kernel spectral theorem

```text
Attack the centered \(dd\)-kernel spectral theorem.

Assume the favorable reduction:
\[
\mathfrak j_{ij}^{dd}=K_{dd}(u_i-u_j;m),
\quad
K_{dd}(t)=K_{dd}(-t),
\quad
K_{dd}(0)=0.
\]

Target:
Prove or refute one-sidedness of
\[
P\mathcal K P,
\qquad
\mathcal K_{ij}=K_{dd}(u_i-u_j;m),
\qquad
P=I-\frac1k\mathbf1\mathbf1^\top.
\]

Tasks:
1. Start with \(k=3\), \(u=(-1,0,1)\).
2. Write \(A=K_{dd}(1;m)\), \(B=K_{dd}(2;m)\), and derive the exact PSD/NSD condition.
3. Check whether the paper’s source formula implies the required inequality between \(A\) and \(B\).
4. If not, determine whether the signature-changing locus is controlled incidence.
5. Extend to general \(k\).

Deliverable:
A centered-kernel spectral rigidity theorem, incidence-containment theorem, or a concrete spectral obstruction branch.
```

# Bottom line

The attack has narrowed to three precise missing theorem families:

## Local

\[
\boxed{
\tau\pi_{\mathfrak f}\operatorname{Sym}
\left(
\Lambda^-_{a,r}
[\partial_\Delta^2N_0]_{\eta\eta,\mathrm{odd}}
W_{+,b}
\right)=0
}
\]

plus, secondarily,

\[
\boxed{
[\delta^0]\eta^\Delta=0.
}
\]

## Finite-core

\[
\boxed{
\|H_{\core,\theta(m)}\|_{\rm fd}
\ge
\text{calibrated sampled scale}
}
\]

or equivalently sampled coefficient non-concentration.

## Interaction

\[
\boxed{
\langle x_i^\perp,y_j^\perp\rangle
\text{ is zero/sign-controlled/incidence-controlled}
}
\]

or, under separation reduction,

\[
\boxed{
P\mathcal K P
\text{ is one-sided or signature changes are controlled incidence}.
}
\]

That is the current proof frontier.

This round is significant. It does **not** close a branch, but it **kills one promising local closure route** and sharpens all three live blockers.

# 1. Local branch: endpoint-diagonal realization is not enough

Previously, the best local hope was:

\[
[\delta^0]\eta^\Delta=0
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}}=0.
\]

Local B confirms that this endpoint-diagonal theorem is **not currently proved**. If \(\eta_{i,+}\) and \(\eta_{i,-}\) are evaluations of one analytic field, then

\[
\eta_i^\Delta=\frac{\eta_{i,+}-\eta_{i,-}}2=O(\delta),
\]

so the frozen endpoint-separation subchannels vanish. But the current source definitions do not force this; independent frozen endpoint displacement data would still allow \(d\eta^\Delta+\eta^\Delta d\) and \(\eta^\Sigma\eta^\Delta\) to survive. 

However, Local A found a more serious issue: **even if endpoint-diagonal realization were proved, the local branch still would not close.** The corrected mixed block itself contains an odd-background frozen \(\eta\eta\) Hessian survivor. Starting from

\[
N_{12}=\frac{\sin\Delta+q_+s\cos\Delta}{s^2},
\qquad
N_{21}=-\frac{\sin\Delta+q_-s\cos\Delta}{s^2},
\]

twice differentiating in \(\Delta\) yields an odd off-diagonal block

\[
\left[\partial_\Delta^2N_0\right]_{\eta\eta,\mathrm{odd}}
=
\left(
\frac{\sin\Delta_0}{s^2}
+
\frac{q_e\cos\Delta_0}{s}
\right)J,
\qquad
J=
\begin{pmatrix}
0&-1\\
1&0
\end{pmatrix}.
\]

The companion \(q_\pm\cos\Delta_0/s\) term does **not** cancel it; it combines into the coefficient

\[
A_o=\frac{\sin\Delta_0}{s^2}+\frac{q_e\cos\Delta_0}{s},
\]

which is generically nonzero on a good phase patch. 

After multiplying by symmetric same-point and right whitening matrices

\[
L=
\begin{pmatrix}
a&c\\
c&d
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
W=
\begin{pmatrix}
u&w\\
w&v
\end{pmatrix},
\]

the fixed-sector projection gives

\[
\pi_{\mathfrak f}\operatorname{Sym}(L A_oJ W)
=
A_o\Bigl(
[c(u-v)+w(d-a)]I
+
[ud-av]S
\Bigr).
\]

The \(S\)-coefficient

\[
A_o(ud-av)
\]

is generically nonzero. Therefore this block can produce

\[
f_{A,Y}\neq0,
\]

so

\[
\partial_\kappa T=-a_1^2\frac{f_{A,Y}}{c}\neq0.
\]

It can also be quotient-visible because for a pure \(S\)-survivor,

\[
Q_{A,Y}=e v_5-u_5f=-u_5f,
\]

which is nonzero on a generic \(u_5\neq0\) patch. 

## Updated local target

The local problem is no longer primarily the 60-row table, nor just endpoint-diagonal realization. The main local theorem now needed is:

\[
\boxed{
\tau_{h\to m}\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}
\operatorname{Sym}
\left(
\Lambda^-_{a,r}
\left[
\left(
\frac{\sin\Delta_0}{s^2}
+
\frac{q_e\cos\Delta_0}{s}
\right)J
\right]_{g}
W_{+,b}
\right)=0
}
\]

for every active row

\[
r+b+g=7.
\]

Endpoint-diagonal realization remains useful, but only for the endpoint-separation subchannels. It does **not** handle this scalar \(\Delta\)-Hessian \(\eta\eta\) odd-background survivor.

---

# 2. Finite-core branch: radial/sample non-concentration remains open

FC1 confirms the finite-core problem has reduced to **radial sampled anti-smallness**. Projective detection is available: if

\[
\|H_{\core,\theta}\|_{\rm fd}
=
\max_{0\le r\le R_{\Theta_k}}
|c_{\core,2r+1}(\theta)|,
\]

then for \(Q\) large enough, some bounded \(N\) satisfies

\[
|F_N(\theta,Q)|
\ge
\frac12
\|H_{\core,\theta}\|_{\rm fd}.
\]

So direction/projection is not the main issue. The missing theorem is a **size** theorem:

\[
\|H_{\core,\theta(m)}\|_{\rm fd}
\gtrsim
\max_{1\le N\le R_{\Theta_k}+1}
\left(
\frac{Q^{2N+2}}
{(2N-1)N!(N-1)!}
\frac{x}{B_\zeta(m)}S(m)
\right)
\]

outside

\[
\mathcal Z_k\cup\mathcal E_{\rm geom}.
\]

Adaptive \(Q\) improves the exponent but still requires a radial lower bound. 

FC2 reaches the same conclusion from the sampling side. The finite-core coefficient functions

\[
F_N(\theta,Q)
=
c_{\core,2N-1}(\theta)
+
\sum_{j\ge1}
c_{\core,2N-1+2j}(\theta)
h_j(1^2,\dots,N^2)Q^{-2j}
\]

define analytic small-value sets. The proof needs a pointwise exclusion:

\[
\max_N |F_N(\theta(m),Q)|
\ge
\Lambda(m,Q),
\]

where

\[
\Lambda(m,Q)
=
C_*
\max_N
\left(
\frac{Q^{2N+2}}
{(2N-1)N!(N-1)!}
\frac{x}{B_\zeta(m)}S(m)
\right).
\]

Zero spacing, endpoint gaps, discreteness of zeros, compactness, and Remez/Łojasiewicz volume bounds do not imply such pointwise sampled non-concentration. 

FCB also identifies a mechanism for failure: interaction terms may cancel the pair-like/one-body finite vector. Writing

\[
C_{\rm fd}(\theta)
=
P_{\rm fd}(\theta)+J_{\rm fd}(\theta),
\]

smallness can occur through

\[
J_{\rm fd}(\theta)
\approx
-P_{\rm fd}(\theta),
\]

without forcing controlled incidence. This is the interaction-fed radial-smallness branch. 

## Updated finite-core target

The theorem needed is:

\[
\boxed{
\theta(m)\notin\mathcal Z_k\cup\mathcal E_{\rm geom}
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\max_N |F_N(\theta(m),Q)|\ge \Lambda(m,Q).
}
\]

Equivalently:

\[
\boxed{
\theta(m)\notin\mathcal Z_k\cup\mathcal E_{\rm geom}
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\|H_{\core,\theta(m)}\|_{\rm fd}
\ge \text{calibrated scale}.
}
\]

Without it, the unresolved branch is:

\[
\mathcal N_k^{\rm coef}(m,Q)
=
\left\{
\theta(m)\notin\mathcal Z_k\cup\mathcal E_{\rm geom}:
\max_N |F_N(\theta(m),Q)|<\Lambda(m,Q)
\right\}.
\]

---

# 3. Interaction branch: \(dd\)-fiber/spectral rigidity remains independent

Interaction A shows the source-level obstruction is not just “unknown coefficients.” In normal gauge, whitening removes radial terms but leaves the transverse cross-source inner product

\[
\langle x_i^\perp,y_j^\perp\rangle.
\]

One-pair incidence data

\[
M,\ W,\ K_v,\ T_v
\]

and endpoint/patch data may constrain norms or one-pair quantities, but they do not determine the relative transverse fiber angle. In a transverse fiber, \(\langle x_i^\perp,y_j^\perp\rangle\) can vary while one-pair norms remain fixed. Rank-one locking reduces this to

\[
\alpha_i\beta_j\langle u_-,u_+\rangle,
\]

but still does not imply zero, sign control, or incidence containment because signed amplitudes \(a_i a_j\) can reverse signs. 

Interaction B then assumes the favorable reduction

\[
\mathfrak j_{ij}^{dd}
=
K_{dd}(u_i-u_j;m),
\qquad
K_{dd}(t)=K_{dd}(-t),
\qquad
K_{dd}(0)=0,
\]

and still finds no closure. For \(k=3\), with

\[
u=(-1,0,1),
\]

define

\[
A=K_{dd}(1;m),
\qquad
B=K_{dd}(2;m).
\]

On balanced amplitudes \(a=(x,y,-x-y)\), the quadratic form is

\[
J_{dd}
=
-Bx^2-Bxy-Ay^2.
\]

One-sidedness requires the matrix

\[
\begin{pmatrix}
B&B/2\\
B/2&A
\end{pmatrix}
\]

to be semidefinite. In the real negative-type convention this requires

\[
B\ge0,\qquad A\ge0,\qquad A\ge \frac{B}{4}.
\]

Analyticity, evenness, collision divisibility, same-scale compactness, and pair-like positivity do not imply this. For example,

\[
K_{dd}(t)=t^4
\]

already violates the quadratic sign condition. 

## Updated interaction target

There are now two equivalent-looking but distinct missing theorem routes:

### Source-level route

\[
\boxed{
\langle x_i^\perp,y_j^\perp\rangle
\text{ is zero, sign-controlled, or incidence-controlled.}
}
\]

### Centered-kernel route

\[
\boxed{
P\operatorname{Re}(e^{-i\theta_0}\mathcal K)P
\text{ is semidefinite on }\mathbf 1^\perp,
}
\]

or all signature-changing loci of \(P\mathcal KP\) lie in \(\mathcal E_{\rm geom}\).

Absent one of these, the branch

\[
\mathfrak Z_{\rm int}^{dd}
=
\left\{
\sum_\nu a_\nu K(d_\nu)
+
\sum_{i<j}a_i a_j\mathfrak j_{ij}^{dd}=0
\right\}
\setminus\mathcal E_{\rm geom}
\]

remains independent.

# 1. Local branch: the lead obstruction is now the odd \(\eta\eta\) block

Local A found a concrete surviving row. The odd off-diagonal \(\eta\eta\) Hessian block is

\[
\left[\partial_\Delta^2N_0\right]_{\eta\eta,\mathrm{odd}}
=
A_oJ,
\qquad
A_o=
\frac{\sin\Delta_0}{s^2}
+
\frac{q_e\cos\Delta_0}{s},
\]

with

\[
J=
\begin{pmatrix}
0&-1\\
1&0
\end{pmatrix}.
\]

The companion \(q_e\cos\Delta_0/s\) term does **not** cancel the \(\sin\Delta_0/s^2\) term; near a good phase patch it reinforces it:

\[
A_o\sim \frac{2q_0}{s}+O(s).
\]

The concrete active row is

\[
\boxed{
(a,r,g,b)=(2,0,7,0),
\qquad
\chi=\eta\eta_{\mathrm{odd}}.
}
\]

Using the actual finite Fréchet source index \(a=2\), Local A derives

\[
\Lambda^-_{2,0}
=
-\frac{1}{24\pi q^3}E_{22}.
\]

For a diagonal right whitening block

\[
W_{+,0}=\begin{pmatrix}u&0\\0&v\end{pmatrix},
\]

the row contributes

\[
\mathcal E^{2}_{\eta\eta;7,0,0}
=
\ell \nu_{\eta\eta,7}u\,S.
\]

Thus, generically,

\[
f_{A,Y}\neq0,
\]

so

\[
\partial_\kappa T
=
-a_1^2\frac{f_{A,Y}}{c}
\neq0.
\]

On a generic \(u_5\neq0\) patch, the quotient determinant also fails:

\[
Q_{A,Y}=-u_5f_{A,Y}\neq0.
\]

This means the local closure is **not structurally proved** and now hinges on a very specific odd-\(\eta\eta\) row cancellation theorem. 

Local B confirms the endpoint-diagonal cleanup remains unproved:

\[
[\delta^0]\eta_i^\Delta=0
\]

would follow if

\[
\eta_{i,+}=\eta_i(h+\delta/2),
\qquad
\eta_{i,-}=\eta_i(h-\delta/2),
\]

but the current source definitions do not force this. If endpoint data are independent, \(d\eta^\Delta+\eta^\Delta d\) and \(\eta^\Sigma\eta^\Delta\) can survive and leak through \(S\). However, Local B also correctly notes that even if endpoint-diagonal realization is proved, it no longer closes the whole local problem, because the scalar \(\Delta\)-Hessian \(\eta\eta\) odd-background block remains independent. 

## Updated local target

The next local attack should focus on:

\[
\boxed{
\tau_{h\to m}\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}
\operatorname{Sym}
\left(
\Lambda^-_{2,0}
\left[
\left(
\frac{\sin\Delta_0}{s^2}
+
\frac{q_e\cos\Delta_0}{s}
\right)J
\eta_i\eta_j
\right]_{7}
W_{+,0}
\right)=0.
}
\]

Equivalently, prove one of:

\[
\nu_{\eta\eta,7}=0,
\]

\[
\Lambda^-_{2,0}=0,
\]

or a fixed-sector cancellation against other active rows.

At present, none is proved.

---

# 2. Finite-core branch: sampled coefficient non-concentration remains open

Finite-Core A confirms the needed theorem is pointwise sampled coefficient non-concentration.

For

\[
F_N(\theta,Q)
=
c_{\core,2N-1}(\theta)
+
\sum_{j\ge1}
c_{\core,2N-1+2j}(\theta)
h_j(1^2,\dots,N^2)Q^{-2j},
\]

the proof needs

\[
\boxed{
\max_N |F_N(\theta(m),Q)|
\ge
\Lambda(m,Q)
}
\]

outside

\[
\mathcal Z_k\cup\mathcal E_{\rm geom},
\]

where

\[
\Lambda(m,Q)
=
C_*
\max_N
\left(
\frac{Q^{2N+2}}
{(2N-1)N!(N-1)!}
\frac{x}{B_\zeta(m)}S(m)
\right).
\]

Zero-spacing, endpoint gaps, compactness, discreteness of zeros, and Remez/Łojasiewicz volume estimates do not give this pointwise exclusion. They control collision, boundary, or measure-type smallness, not analytic coefficient cancellation at actual sampled zeta configurations. 

Finite-Core B identifies the mechanism that can feed this branch:

\[
C_{\rm fd}(\theta)
=
P_{\rm fd}(\theta)+J_{\rm fd}(\theta).
\]

The interaction vector

\[
J_{\rm fd}
=
(J_1,J_3,\ldots,J_{2R+1})
\]

can formally cancel the pair-like vector:

\[
J_{\rm fd}\approx -P_{\rm fd}.
\]

This can make

\[
0<
\|C_{\rm fd}(\theta)\|_\infty
<
\Lambda(m,Q)
\]

without forcing controlled incidence. This is the interaction-fed radial-smallness branch:

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal N_k^{\rm int-rad}(m,Q).
}
\]

The missing theorem is therefore stronger than \(J_1\)-rigidity alone. It must control the whole finite vector

\[
(P_1+J_1,\ P_3+J_3,\ldots,P_{2R+1}+J_{2R+1}).
\]

## Updated finite-core target

The theorem needed is:

\[
\boxed{
\theta(m)\notin \mathcal Z_k\cup\mathcal E_{\rm geom}
\Rightarrow
\max_N |F_N(\theta(m),Q)|\ge\Lambda(m,Q).
}
\]

Or, mechanistically:

\[
\boxed{
\|P_{\rm fd}(\theta(m))+J_{\rm fd}(\theta(m))\|_\infty
\ge
\Lambda(m,Q).
}
\]

At present, this is not available.

---

# 3. Interaction branch: \(dd\)-rigidity remains independent

Interaction A isolates the source-level obstruction:

\[
\boxed{
\langle x_i^\perp,y_j^\perp\rangle.
}
\]

In normal gauge, whitening removes radial components but leaves this transverse cross-source inner product. One-pair incidence data

\[
M,\ W,\ K_v,\ T_v
\]

can constrain one-pair quantities or norms, but they do not determine the relative transverse fiber angle between \(x_i^\perp\) and \(y_j^\perp\). Rank-one locking reduces the interaction to

\[
\alpha_i\beta_j\langle u_-,u_+\rangle,
\]

but still gives neither zero, nor sign control, nor incidence containment because signed amplitudes \(a_i a_j\) can cancel the pair-like positive channel. 

Interaction B assumes the most favorable separation-kernel reduction

\[
\mathfrak j_{ij}^{dd}
=
K_{dd}(u_i-u_j;m),
\qquad
K_{dd}(t)=K_{dd}(-t),
\qquad
K_{dd}(0)=0,
\]

and still finds no closure. For \(k=3\), with

\[
u=(-1,0,1),
\]

let

\[
A=K_{dd}(1;m),
\qquad
B=K_{dd}(2;m).
\]

On balanced vectors \(a=(x,y,-x-y)\),

\[
J_{dd}
=
-Bx^2-Bxy-Ay^2.
\]

One-sidedness requires

\[
\begin{pmatrix}
B&B/2\\
B/2&A
\end{pmatrix}
\]

to be semidefinite. In the real negative-type convention this requires

\[
B\ge0,\qquad A\ge0,\qquad A\ge\frac{B}{4}.
\]

Analyticity, evenness, collision divisibility, same-scale compactness, and pair-like positivity do not imply this. The signature-changing locus

\[
K_{dd}(1;m)=\frac14K_{dd}(2;m)
\]

is also not among the currently controlled incidence equations. 

## Updated interaction target

The branch remains:

\[
\boxed{
\mathfrak Z_{\rm int}^{dd}
=
\left\{
\sum_\nu a_\nu K(d_\nu)
+
\sum_{i<j}a_i a_j\mathfrak j_{ij}^{dd}
=0
\right\}
\setminus\mathcal E_{\rm geom}.
}
\]

It can be closed only by proving one of:

\[
\langle x_i^\perp,y_j^\perp\rangle=0,
\]

a cone/sign theorem compatible with signed amplitudes,

\[
\mathfrak j_{ij}^{dd}\in\sqrt{\mathcal I_{\rm geom}},
\]

or, under the separation-kernel reduction, centered-kernel spectral rigidity:

\[
P\operatorname{Re}(e^{-i\theta_0}\mathcal K)P
\]

is semidefinite on \(\mathbf 1^\perp\), or its signature-changing loci are controlled incidence.

---

| Finite-core radial branch | still open | sampled coefficient non-concentration missing |
| Interaction-fed radial branch | still open | \(J_{\rm fd}\approx-P_{\rm fd}\) not ruled out |
| \(dd\)-interaction | still open | transverse fiber angle / centered kernel spectrum uncontrolled |
| \(M_A,M_C\) | closed | no action |
| Mixed four-point | dependency-closed | no action |
| Finite determinacy | qualitative theorem done | no action |

## Assistant (2026-04-25 13:44:23)

_Thought for 7s_

The agent round meaningfully sharpened the situation. It did **not** close a branch. It identifies one local obstruction as a concrete row-level survivor and pushes the finite-core / interaction blockers into sharper theorem forms.

## 1. Local branch: now blocked at one explicit scalar

The lead local obstruction is no longer broad \(E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}}\). It is the concrete top row

\[
\mathcal E^{2}_{\eta\eta;7,0,0}.
\]

Local A has pushed this hard and found a specific \(S\)-visible survivor. The row is governed by

\[
\Lambda^-_{2,0}
\left[
\left(
\frac{\sin\Delta_0}{s^2}
+
\frac{q_-\cos\Delta_0}{s}
\right)
\eta_i\eta_j
\right]_{7}
W_{+,0}.
\]

With

\[
\Lambda^-_{2,0}
=
-\frac{1}{24\pi q^3}E_{22},
\]

the \(S\)-coefficient is

\[
f_{\eta\eta}^{\mathrm{top}}
=
-\frac{u}{24\pi q^3}\nu_{21,7},
\]

where

\[
\nu_{21,7}
=
[z^7]\left[
\left(
\frac{\sin\Delta_0}{s^2}
+
\frac{q_-\cos\Delta_0}{s}
\right)\eta_i\eta_j
\right].
\]

Under the favorable phase-gap integral model, this reduces to

\[
\nu_{21,7}
=
\frac{1}{Q^{14}}
\left[
\frac{q_0}{480}
(\rho_{i,2}\rho_{j,4}+\rho_{i,4}\rho_{j,2})
+
\frac{1}{144}
\left(
\frac{q_0''}{6}-\frac{2q_0^3}{3}
\right)
\rho_{i,2}\rho_{j,2}
\right].
\]

For the homogeneous source \(r(u)=u^2\), with \(q_0''=0\), this is nonzero:

\[
\nu_{21,7}
=
-\frac{q_0^3}{216Q^{14}}.
\]

So the local row survives under affine removal, endpoint symmetry, source-grade parity, the frozen Bottleneck-C bookkeeping, and the actual \(a=2,r=0\) Fréchet row. This is a serious obstruction, not bookkeeping noise. 

Local B sharpened the endpoint-separation issue. If \(N^{\corr}\) is truly formulated only in \((q_-,q_+,\Delta;s)\), then \(\eta^\Delta\)-style endpoint-separation channels are not intrinsic to the displayed mixed block. If endpoint fields are separately introduced, endpoint-diagonal realization is still an extra theorem. Either way, endpoint cleanup does **not** affect the lead scalar \(\eta\eta\) row. 

**Local conclusion:**

\[
\boxed{
\text{The local proof now requires cancellation of } \nu_{21,7}
\text{ or a correction term.}
}
\]

The missing theorem is no longer “endpoint-diagonal realization.” It is one of:

\[
\nu_{21,7}=0,
\]

or full top-row \(S\)-cancellation after summing all active rows,

\[
\sum_{\mathrm{top}\ \eta\eta} f_{\eta\eta}^{\mathrm{top}}=0,
\]

or a new correction package cancelling this row.

---

## 2. Finite-core branch: now a finite-vector non-concentration problem

Finite-Core A and B agree: finite determinacy and projective detection are not the problem. For \(Q\) large enough,

\[
\max_N |F_N(\theta,Q)|
\asymp
\|H_{\core,\theta}\|_{\rm fd}.
\]

The live problem is radial size:

\[
\theta(m)\notin\mathcal Z_k\cup\mathcal E_{\rm geom}
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\|H_{\core,\theta(m)}\|_{\rm fd}
\gtrsim
\Lambda(m,Q),
\]

where

\[
\Lambda(m,Q)
=
C_*
\max_{1\le N\le R_{\Theta_k}+1}
\left(
\frac{Q^{2N+2}}
{(2N-1)N!(N-1)!}
\frac{x}{B_\zeta(m)}S(m)
\right).
\]

Finite-Core A also shows this cannot be derived from compactness, finite determinacy, zero-spacing, endpoint-gap regularity, or Remez/Łojasiewicz volume estimates. A formal model can satisfy all current controlled nondegeneracy conditions while having

\[
0<\|C_{\rm fd}\|_\infty<\Lambda(m,Q).
\]

So this is a genuinely new pointwise sampled non-concentration input. 

Finite-Core B sharpens the mechanism. Write

\[
C_{\rm fd}=P_{\rm fd}+J_{\rm fd}.
\]

The obstruction is now best viewed as **interaction-angle cancellation** or **hidden transverse Gram-state cancellation**:

\[
J_{\rm fd}\approx -P_{\rm fd}.
\]

B pushed this through rank, fiber, and Gram-feasibility formulations. The controlled geometric data

\[
M,W,K_v,T_v
\]

do not determine the transverse cross-Gram data feeding \(J_{\rm fd}\). Therefore the branch persists unless the paper proves fiberwise interaction rigidity, cone separation, or sampled anti-concentration along controlled-data fibers. 

**Finite-core conclusion:**

\[
\boxed{
\text{The live finite-core theorem is finite-vector non-concentration: }
\|P_{\rm fd}+J_{\rm fd}\|_\infty\ge \Lambda(m,Q).
}
\]

A useful sharpened bad branch is:

\[
\mathcal N_k^{\rm align}(m,Q)
=
\left\{
\theta(m)\notin\mathcal Z_k\cup\mathcal E_{\rm geom}:
0<
\|P_{\rm fd}(\theta(m))+J_{\rm fd}(\theta(m))\|_\infty
<
\Lambda(m,Q)
\right\}.
\]

This is the finite-core branch to carry forward.

---

## 3. Interaction branch: now a transverse-covariance / conditional-definiteness problem

Interaction A shows the \(dd\)-interaction is not controlled by one-pair geometry. In normal gauge, whitening removes radial terms but leaves the transverse feature inner product:

\[
\langle x_i^\perp,y_j^\perp\rangle.
\]

Even if the endpoint transverse fibers are canonically identified by a jet-frame curve, this becomes a transported covariance kernel

\[
C(t_i,t_j)=\langle \gamma'(t_i)^\perp,\gamma'(t_j)^\perp\rangle,
\]

not zero. After collision weighting, the kernel is of the form

\[
K_{ij}^{dd}=(u_i-u_j)^2\langle v(u_i),v(u_j)\rangle.
\]

A PSD covariance kernel is still insufficient: the collision factor introduces an indefinite term unless a strong feature-balance condition holds. In particular,

\[
Q_{dd}(a)
=
2\left\langle
\sum_i a_i u_i^2v_i,\sum_j a_jv_j
\right\rangle
-
2\left\|
\sum_i a_i u_iv_i
\right\|^2.
\]

The first term has no fixed sign unless one proves transverse feature-balance. Moment constraints like \(\sum a_i=0\) or \(\sum a_i u_i=0\) are not enough. 

Interaction B analyzes the best-case separation-kernel reduction:

\[
\mathfrak j_{ij}^{dd}=K_{dd}(u_i-u_j;m).
\]

This route now requires a full conditional-definiteness / spectral-measure theorem. The \(k=3\) test gives value inequalities; the \(k=4\) test adds finite-difference inequalities; the general moment test forces an all-order hierarchy. Even alternating Taylor signs are insufficient; one needs a positive spectral-measure / moment-Hankel condition. Near collision, the first nonquadratic coefficient already has a required sign condition. 

**Interaction conclusion:**

\[
\boxed{
\text{The }dd\text{-interaction remains live unless one proves conditional definiteness or feature-balance rigidity.}
}
\]

The missing theorem is now best stated as one of:

\[
P\,\operatorname{Re}(e^{-i\theta_0}\mathcal K)\,P
\text{ is semidefinite on }\mathbf 1^\perp,
\]

or

\[
K_{dd}(t)
\text{ has a positive spectral-measure representation,}
\]

or

\[
\sum_i a_i v(u_i)=0
\text{ / feature-balance on every admissible core,}
\]

or every signature-change locus is controlled incidence.

None is currently available.

---

The local obstruction looks like an actual defect. The next local agent should not re-check endpoint diagonalization. It should ask whether the package definition is missing a correction term that cancels

\[
\mathcal E^{2}_{\eta\eta;7,0,0}.
\]

Prompt:

```text

\[
f_{\eta\eta}^{\rm top}
=
-\frac{u}{24\pi q^3}\nu_{21,7}.
\]

Assume \(\nu_{21,7}\) is generically nonzero. Search the paper’s corrected-package construction for any omitted second-order phase-gap correction, connection correction, normalization term, or source-bidegree projection that should contribute an opposite top-row \(S\)-coefficient.

Do not try to prove endpoint-diagonal realization. Do not rederive the row. Treat the row as a live defect and look for the missing correction mechanism.

Deliverable:
Either an explicit cancelling correction term, or a proof that the current package cannot close Bottleneck C without adding one.
```

## B. Finite-core: formulate the exact anti-concentration theorem as a dependency

This branch is now too large to solve by local algebra. The next agent should turn it into a formal dependency of the proof, not keep re-proving insufficiency.

```text
\[

Deliverable:
A theorem-dependency block: assumption, implication proof, and exact remaining missing input.
```

The interaction branch only has one real closure route left: derive a spectral representation or show the actual \(K_{dd}\) lacks one.

Prompt:

```text
Attack the actual \(dd\)-kernel \(K_{dd}\), not abstract models.

Target:
Does the actual source formula for \(K_{dd}\) have a conditionally one-sided representation:
\[
\operatorname{Re}(e^{-i\theta_0}K_{dd}(t;m))
=
\alpha(m)t^2+\int(1-\cos(t\xi))\,d\mu_m(\xi)
\]
or its negative?

Compute the first nonquadratic coefficient \(\kappa_{2m}\) of the actual \(K_{dd}\) if possible. Check the near-collision sign condition:
if \(\operatorname{Re}(e^{-i\theta_0}\kappa_2)>0\), then the first nonquadratic coefficient must have the opposite sign.

Deliverable:
Either a positive spectral representation, or an explicit coefficient-level obstruction showing the centered \(dd\)-kernel cannot be conditionally one-sided.
```

which is nonzero on a good phase patch. This survives affine removal, endpoint symmetry, source-grade parity, and the frozen Bottleneck-C bookkeeping.

## 3. Interaction: no conditional definiteness from current \(dd\)-kernel structure

The two interaction agents also converge.

One route tries to derive a positive spectral representation for the actual \(dd\)-kernel. Under the favorable transported covariance form,

\[
K_{dd}(t;m)
=
t^2
\left\langle
v\!\left(m+\frac t2\right),
v\!\left(m-\frac t2\right)
\right\rangle,
\]

the first nonquadratic coefficient is

\[
\kappa_4
=
\frac14
\left(
\langle v_0,v_2\rangle-\langle v_1,v_1\rangle
\right).
\]

A conditionally one-sided representation would require, after phase rotation,

\[
\operatorname{Re}(e^{-i\theta_0}\kappa_4)\le 0
\quad
\text{when}
\quad
\operatorname{Re}(e^{-i\theta_0}\kappa_2)>0.
\]

The current source geometry does not prove this. Even if a normalized-frame condition made the first sign favorable, a full spectral-measure theorem would still be needed for all higher coefficients. 

The other interaction response attacks the covariance-weighted form directly:

\[
K_{ij}^{dd}
=
(u_i-u_j)^2\langle v_i,v_j\rangle.
\]

For balanced amplitudes \(\sum_i a_i=0\),

\[
Q_{dd}(a)
=
2\left\langle
\sum_i a_i u_i^2v_i,\sum_j a_jv_j
\right\rangle
-
2\left|
\sum_i a_i u_iv_i
\right|^2.
\]

The second term is one-sided, but the first term is indefinite unless one proves the **feature-balance condition**

\[
\sum_i a_i v_i=0.
\]

Ordinary amplitude balance does not imply feature balance. Rank-one locking also does not solve it unless \(\sum_i a_i\lambda_i=0\). Thus the \(dd\)-interaction remains sign-indefinite unless a feature-balance, cone, spectral-representation, or incidence-containment theorem is added. 

So the interaction branch has also stabilized:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Need feature-balance rigidity or positive spectral representation for }K_{dd}.
}
\]

Without that, the branch

\[
\mathfrak Z_{\rm int}^{dd}
=
\left\{
\sum_\nu a_\nu K(d_\nu)
+
\sum_{i,j}a_i a_j
(u_i-u_j)^2\langle v_i,v_j\rangle
=0
\right\}
\setminus\mathcal E_{\rm geom}
\]

remains live.

# 3. Interaction: feature-balance / spectral positivity still missing

The interaction agents also converge.

The actual \(dd\)-interaction has the covariance-weighted form

\[
K_{ij}^{dd}
=
(u_i-u_j)^2\langle v_i,v_j\rangle,
\qquad
v_i=v(u_i).
\]

For balanced amplitudes

\[
\sum_i a_i=0,
\]

the quadratic form is

\[
Q_{dd}(a)
=
2\left\langle
\sum_i a_i u_i^2v_i,\sum_j a_jv_i
\right\rangle
-
2\left|
\sum_i a_i u_iv_i
\right|^2.
\]

More carefully, the first term involves

\[
\sum_j a_jv_j.
\]

The second term is one-sided, but the first term is indefinite unless one has feature balance:

\[
\sum_i a_iv_i=0.
\]

Ordinary amplitude balance does **not** imply feature balance. Rank-one locking also does not imply it unless the weights are constant or satisfy an extra weighted-balance theorem. 

The spectral-representation route also remains unproved. Under

\[
K_{dd}(t;m)
=
t^2
\left\langle
v\!\left(m+\frac t2\right),
v\!\left(m-\frac t2\right)
\right\rangle,
\]

the first nonquadratic coefficient is

\[
\kappa_4
=
\frac14
\left(
\langle v_0,v_2\rangle-\langle v_1,v_1\rangle
\right).
\]

Conditional one-sidedness would require, after phase rotation,

\[
\operatorname{Re}(e^{-i\theta_0}\kappa_4)\le0
\quad
\text{when}
\quad
\operatorname{Re}(e^{-i\theta_0}\kappa_2)>0.
\]

The current source geometry does not prove this; nor does it prove the all-order moment/Hankel positivity needed for a positive spectral representation. 

So the interaction branch remains:

\[
\mathfrak Z_{\rm int}^{dd}
=
\left\{
\sum_\nu a_\nu K(d_\nu)
+
\sum_{i,j}a_i a_j
(u_i-u_j)^2\langle v_i,v_j\rangle
=0
\right\}
\setminus\mathcal E_{\rm geom}.
\]

To close it, the proof needs one of:

\[
\boxed{\sum_i a_iv_i=0\text{ for all admissible balanced cores,}}
\]

\[
\boxed{K_{dd}\text{ has a positive/negative spectral representation,}}
\]

or

\[
\boxed{\text{all feature-balance/spectral-sign failures lie in }\mathcal E_{\rm geom}.}
\]

None is currently derived.

The finite-core and interaction branches are now formal dependencies, but the immediate bottleneck is local: whether the \(\Theta_\pm\)-normal package can be made coherent.

# 1. Local package result

The local defect remains:

\[
f_{\eta\eta}^{\rm top}
=
-\frac{u}{24\pi q^3}\nu_{21,7},
\]

where

\[
\nu_{21,7}
=
[z^7]\left[
\left(
\frac{\sin\Delta_0}{s^2}
+
\frac{q_-\cos\Delta_0}{s}
\right)
\eta_i\eta_j
\right].
\]

The existing package mechanisms do **not** cancel this row: source-bidegree projection keeps it, amplitude normalization only rescales, midpoint trivialization is invertible, connection correction is post-edge, and quotienting cannot remove \(T\)-visible \(S\)-leakage. Therefore the current package cannot prove Bottleneck C or \(T\)-horizontal closure at this row. 

A scalar reparametrization of \(\Delta\) is insufficient, because flattening \(N_{12}\) and \(N_{21}\) requires different second-order coefficients when \(q_+\neq q_-\). The only coherent repair proposed is to use off-diagonal numerator variables:

\[
\Theta_+=\sin\Delta+q_+s\cos\Delta,
\qquad
\Theta_-=\sin\Delta+q_-s\cos\Delta.
\]

Then

\[
N_{12}=\frac{\Theta_+}{s^2},
\qquad
N_{21}=-\frac{\Theta_-}{s^2},
\]

so the off-diagonal entries are affine in \(\Theta_\pm\), and the dangerous pure off-diagonal \(\eta\eta\) Hessian disappears. 

The subsequent audit says this is coherent **as a conditional redesign**:

\[
\Theta_+\mapsto-\Theta_-,
\qquad
\Theta_-\mapsto-\Theta_+
\]

under endpoint swap, so endpoint-transpose covariance is preserved. The off-diagonal odd-\(\eta\eta\) top row is indeed cancelled. Source-bidegree and amplitude bookkeeping can remain coherent, and source-linear gates should survive because first variations are unchanged. 

But the audit also identifies new obligations:

1. diagonal \(\eta\eta\) terms in \(N_{11},N_{22}\) must be rechecked;
2. Gate B actual-source realization must be reproved in \(\Theta_\pm\)-normal form;
3. \(M_A,M_C\) connection closure must be restated/rechecked in \(\Theta_\pm\)-coordinates;
4. the augmented hidden coordinate must become

\[
T^\Theta=\frac{v_7^\Theta}{c},
\]

computed **after** the normal-form correction;
5. \(\Theta_\pm\) must be treated as constrained normal coordinates induced by \((q_-,q_+,\Delta)\), not as free independent variables. 

## Local conclusion

\[
\boxed{
\text{Adopt }\Theta_\pm\text{ as the leading repair candidate, but audit it as a new package.}
}
\]

Do not pretend it is already proved.

---

# 2. Finite-core result

The finite-core agents agree: carry this branch as a formal dependency.

Define

\[
C_{\rm fd}
=
(c_{\core,1},c_{\core,3},\ldots,c_{\core,2R_{\Theta_k}+1})
=
P_{\rm fd}+J_{\rm fd}.
\]

The missing theorem is:

\[
\theta(m)\notin\mathcal Z_k\cup\mathcal E_{\rm geom}
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\|P_{\rm fd}(\theta(m))+J_{\rm fd}(\theta(m))\|_\infty
\ge
\Lambda(m,Q),
\]

where

\[
\Lambda(m,Q)
=
C_*
\max_{1\le N\le R_{\Theta_k}+1}
\left(
\frac{Q^{2N+2}}
{(2N-1)N!(N-1)!}
\frac{x}{B_\zeta(m)}S(m)
\right).
\]

If assumed, projective detection plus \(Q^{-2}\)-tail control gives some bounded \(N\) such that

\[
|\Xi_{\core}^{(N)}(m)|
\gtrsim
\frac{x}{B_\zeta(m)}S(m).
\]

So this branch is now exactly:

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal N_k^{\rm align}(m,Q)=\varnothing.
}
\]

It should be recorded as a named dependency, not repeatedly attacked through finite determinacy. turn46file3

---

# 3. Interaction result

The interaction branch remains independent.

Under the covariance-weighted \(dd\)-model,

\[
K_{ij}^{dd}
=
(u_i-u_j)^2\langle v_i,v_j\rangle,
\]

balanced amplitudes \(\sum_i a_i=0\) give

\[
Q_{dd}(a)
=
2\left\langle
\sum_i a_i u_i^2v_i,\sum_j a_jv_j
\right\rangle
-
2\left|
\sum_i a_i u_iv_i
\right|^2.
\]

The second term is one-sided. The first is indefinite unless the feature-balance condition

\[
\sum_i a_iv_i=0
\]

holds. Ordinary amplitude balance does not imply this; rank-one locking also does not unless the feature weights are constant or separately balanced. 

The spectral route also fails under current assumptions. If

\[
K_{dd}(t;m)
=
t^2
\left\langle
v\!\left(m+\frac t2\right),
v\!\left(m-\frac t2\right)
\right\rangle,
\]

then

\[
\kappa_4
=
\frac14
\left(
\langle v_0,v_2\rangle-\langle v_1,v_1\rangle
\right).
\]

Conditional one-sidedness would require a sign/moment condition on \(\kappa_4\) and all higher coefficients. The current source geometry does not supply this. 

So the interaction branch remains:

\[
\boxed{
\mathfrak Z_{\rm int}^{dd}
\text{ is live unless feature-balance, spectral positivity, or incidence containment is proved.}
}
\]

---

# Recommended next prompts

```text

\[
\Theta_+=\sin\Delta+q_+s\cos\Delta,\qquad

\]
cancel the known off-diagonal defect
\[
\mathcal E^{2}_{\eta\eta;7,0,0}.
\]

\[

\]
\[

\frac{(q_-+q_+)s\cos\Delta+(2-q_-q_+s^2)\sin\Delta}{2s^3}
\]
produce any order-\(\le7\) fixed-sector \(S\)-component after the same-point whitening slot and right whitening.

Tasks:
1. Compute the \(\eta\eta\) Hessians of \(N_{11},N_{22}\).
```

```text
affine in the off-diagonal numerator variables.

Target:
```

```text
\]
still holds.
```

# Shared background for new agents

We are no longer in broad proof-audit mode. The proof currently has one urgent local package issue and two global dependencies.

Closed / do not reopen unless you find an actual contradiction:

\[
M_A,M_C\text{ connection closure is done.}
\]

\[
\text{Mixed four-point is dependency-closed.}
\]

\[
\text{Qualitative finite odd-germ determinacy is done.}
\]

The current live issues are:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Local package repair via }\Theta_\pm\text{ normal form}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Finite-core sampled vector non-concentration}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
dd\text{-interaction feature-balance / spectral-positivity}
}
\]

The immediate agents are being assigned to the **local \(\Theta_\pm\) repair**, so this handoff emphasizes what they need beyond the paper.

---

# 1. Why the current local package fails

The current corrected package fails locally at a concrete promoted \(\eta\eta\) top row:

\[
\mathcal E^{2}_{\eta\eta;7,0,0}.
\]

The row contributes an \(S\)-component

\[
f_{\eta\eta}^{\rm top}
=
-\frac{u}{24\pi q^3}\nu_{21,7},
\]

where

\[
\nu_{21,7}
=
[z^7]\left[
\left(
\frac{\sin\Delta_0}{s^2}
+
\frac{q_-\cos\Delta_0}{s}
\right)
\eta_i\eta_j
\right].
\]

Under the favorable phase-gap integral model,

\[
\eta_i(s)=\int_{-s/2}^{s/2}r_i(u)\,du,
\qquad
r_i(u)=\rho_{i,2}u^2+\rho_{i,4}u^4+\cdots,
\]

one gets

\[
\nu_{21,7}
=
\frac{1}{Q^{14}}
\left[
\frac{q_0}{480}
(\rho_{i,2}\rho_{j,4}+\rho_{i,4}\rho_{j,2})
+
\frac{1}{144}
\left(
\frac{q_0''}{6}-\frac{2q_0^3}{3}
\right)
\rho_{i,2}\rho_{j,2}
\right].
\]

For the homogeneous source

\[
r_i=r_j=u^2,
\qquad
q_0''=0,
\]

this gives

\[
\nu_{21,7}
=
-\frac{q_0^3}{216Q^{14}},
\]

which is nonzero on a good patch \(q_0\ne0\). This survives affine removal, endpoint symmetry, source-grade parity, and frozen Bottleneck-C bookkeeping. 

The existing package mechanisms do **not** cancel this row:

\[
\text{source-bidegree projection keeps the promoted degree-three carrier,}
\]

\[
\text{amplitude normalization only rescales it,}
\]

\[
\text{midpoint trivialization is invertible on a good patch,}
\]

\[
\text{connection correction is post-edge and cannot cancel the raw frozen coefficient,}
\]

\[
\text{quotienting is insufficient because the augmented package needs }f_{A,Y}=0.
\]

Thus, in the current package, Bottleneck C and \(T\)-horizontal closure fail at this row unless a new source-jet identity proves \(\nu_{21,7}=0\), or the package is modified with a genuine counterterm. 

---

# 2. Why a scalar \(\Delta\)-reparametrization is insufficient

A tempting repair is to replace \(\Delta\) by a scalar nonlinear coordinate

\[
\Delta=\Theta+\frac12 c\Theta^2+O(\Theta^3).
\]

For an entry \(N_{\alpha\beta}(\Delta)\),

\[
\partial_\Theta^2N_{\alpha\beta}
=
\partial_\Delta^2N_{\alpha\beta}
+
c\,\partial_\Delta N_{\alpha\beta}.
\]

To flatten the \((2,1)\)-entry one needs

\[
c=c_-=
\frac{\sin\Delta_0+q_-s\cos\Delta_0}
{\cos\Delta_0-q_-s\sin\Delta_0}.
\]

To flatten the \((1,2)\)-entry one needs

\[
c=c_+=
\frac{\sin\Delta_0+q_+s\cos\Delta_0}
{\cos\Delta_0-q_+s\sin\Delta_0}.
\]

Generically,

\[
q_+\ne q_-,
\qquad
c_+\ne c_-.
\]

So a single scalar phase-gap coordinate cannot simultaneously flatten both off-diagonal entries while preserving endpoint-transpose symmetry. 

---

# 3. The \(\Theta_\pm\) repair candidate

The only plausible local repair found so far is to use **off-diagonal numerator normal coordinates**:

\[
\Theta_+
=
\sin\Delta+q_+s\cos\Delta,
\qquad
\Theta_-
=
\sin\Delta+q_-s\cos\Delta.
\]

Then the off-diagonal entries become

\[
N_{12}^{\Theta}=\frac{\Theta_+}{s^2},
\qquad
N_{21}^{\Theta}=-\frac{\Theta_-}{s^2}.
\]

These are affine in \(\Theta_\pm\), hence

\[
D^2_{\Theta_+}N_{12}^{\Theta}=0,
\qquad
D^2_{\Theta_-}N_{21}^{\Theta}=0.
\]

Therefore the pure off-diagonal \(\eta\eta\) Hessian vanishes in this normal form, and the specific old defect

\[
\mathcal E^{2}_{\eta\eta;7,0,0,\mathrm{off}}
\]

is cancelled. 

Endpoint-transpose covariance is consistent if the swap convention is

\[
\Theta_+\longleftrightarrow-\Theta_-.
\]

Indeed, under endpoint swap,

\[
s\mapsto -s,\quad
\Delta\mapsto-\Delta,\quad
q_+\leftrightarrow q_-,
\]

so

\[
\Theta_+\mapsto-\Theta_-,
\qquad
\Theta_-\mapsto-\Theta_+.
\]

Thus

\[
N_{12}=\frac{\Theta_+}{s^2}
\mapsto
\frac{-\Theta_-}{s^2}
=
N_{21}.
\]

So the repair is endpoint-transpose covariant. 

---

# 4. What \(\Theta_\pm\) does **not** automatically solve

The \(\Theta_\pm\) repair is **not** a harmless coordinate relabeling. It is a new package unless one proves the discarded off-diagonal curvature is gauge.

The variables \(\Theta_\pm\) are built from one scalar \(\Delta\) and two endpoint slopes \(q_\pm\). They are not free independent variables. They must be treated as constrained normal coordinates induced by

\[
(q_-,q_+,\Delta)
\longmapsto
(q_-,q_+,\Theta_-,\Theta_+),
\]

with

\[
\Theta_\pm=\sin\Delta+q_\pm s\cos\Delta.
\]

If the package treats \(\Theta_\pm\) as independent variables without preserving this constraint, it may no longer represent the actual finite-\(s\) zeta-side mixed block. 

The \(\Theta_\pm\) repair also does **not** automatically handle diagonal entries:

\[
N_{11}=-\frac{2\sin\Delta}{s},
\]

\[
N_{22}
=
\frac{(q_-+q_+)s\cos\Delta+(2-q_-q_+s^2)\sin\Delta}{2s^3}.
\]

The diagonal entries still have \(\Delta\)-Hessians. In the old top-row obstruction, the \(S\)-leak came from the off-diagonal \((2,1)\)-entry because

\[
\Lambda^-_{2,0}\propto E_{22}
\]

selected the second row. Diagonal Hessian terms behave differently and on a diagonal \(W_{+,0}\) patch contribute only diagonally, but in a general non-diagonal \(W_{+,0}\) patch they can mix into \(S\). Therefore diagonal \(\eta\eta\) terms must be audited separately. 

---

# 5. What likely survives under \(\Theta_\pm\)

The previous audit suggests the following, but agents must verify rather than assume.

## Gate A

Gate A is source-linear / homogeneous scalar-grade. The \(\Theta_\pm\) correction starts at second order in the phase-gap source; it kills a quadratic \(\eta\eta\) Hessian. It should not alter source-linear first-variation tables.

So Gate A should survive **if** the first-order source convention is unchanged. 

## \(M_A,M_C\) connection closure

The \(M_A,M_C\) connection closure relied on source-linear mixed-block swap/parity. The \(\Theta_\pm\) normal form preserves endpoint swap if

\[
\Theta_+\mapsto-\Theta_-.
\]

At the linear level,

\[
\delta\Theta_\pm
=
(\cos\Delta_0-q_\pm s\sin\Delta_0)\delta\Delta
+
s\cos\Delta_0\,\delta q_\pm.
\]

Therefore

\[
\delta N_{12}=\frac{\delta\Theta_+}{s^2}
\]

matches the old first variation of \(N_{12}\), and similarly for \(N_{21}\). Thus \(Y\)-middle parity should survive, but the parity lemma must be restated in \(\Theta_\pm\)-coordinates. 

## Source-bidegree and amplitude bookkeeping

The correction changes the matrix coefficient, not the amplitude polynomial. The promoted degree-three amplitude pattern

\[
a_1a_2(a_1+a_2)
\]

is still the same. Source-bidegree and amplitude bookkeeping can remain coherent, but actual-source realization must be rewritten in the \(\Theta_\pm\) normal form. 

---

# 6. What must be reproved under \(\Theta_\pm\)

The agents must treat this as a new package and reprove:

\[
\boxed{
\text{diagonal }\eta\eta\text{ safety}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate B actual-source realization through ordinary order }7
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
M_A,M_C\text{ source-linear parity in }\Theta_\pm\text{-coordinates}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{the augmented transform coordinate }T^\Theta
}
\]

The old actual-source obstruction is removed only if the normal-form correction is part of the definition of the corrected package **before** forming

\[
C_{\mathcal W}^{\rm raw}.
\]

Thus Gate B does not break automatically, but its actual-source realization must be reproved. 

---

# 7. \(T^\Theta\): the most important bookkeeping point

The old hidden coordinate was

\[
T=\frac{v_7}{c}.
\]

But the old package fails because the row contributes an \(S\)-component and changes \(v_7\), giving

\[
\partial_\kappa T=-a_1^2\frac{f}{c}\ne0.
\]

With the \(\Theta_\pm\)-normal package, \(v_7\) must be computed **after** the normal-form correction. Therefore the repaired hidden coordinate must be

\[
T^\Theta:=\frac{v_7^\Theta}{c}.
\]

The package-to-transform bridge must be stated for the corrected finite-\(s\) scalar germ in \(\Theta\)-normal form. If \(T\) is computed before the correction, the old leak remains. 

Agents should not use old \(T\) and new \(E^{\Theta}\) in the same theorem.

---

# 8. Finite-core dependency background

This is not the immediate local package task, but agents should know the global proof state.

The finite-core branch is now a formal dependency. Define

\[
C_{\rm fd}
=
(c_{\core,1},c_{\core,3},\ldots,c_{\core,2R_{\Theta_k}+1})
=
P_{\rm fd}+J_{\rm fd}.
\]

The missing theorem is sampled vector non-concentration:

\[
\theta(m)\notin\mathcal Z_k\cup\mathcal E_{\rm geom}
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\|P_{\rm fd}(\theta(m))+J_{\rm fd}(\theta(m))\|_\infty
\ge
\Lambda(m,Q),
\]

where

\[
\Lambda(m,Q)
=
C_*
\max_{1\le N\le R_{\Theta_k}+1}
\left(
\frac{Q^{2N+2}}
{(2N-1)N!(N-1)!}
\frac{x}{B_\zeta(m)}S(m)
\right).
\]

If this is assumed, projective detection and \(Q^{-2}\)-tail control imply the required \(N\)-point lower bound

\[
|\Xi_{\core}^{(N)}(m)|
\gtrsim
\frac{x}{B_\zeta(m)}S(m)
\]

for some bounded \(N\). turn46file3

The live bad branch is

\[
\mathcal N_k^{\rm align}(m,Q)
=
\left\{
\theta(m)\notin\mathcal Z_k\cup\mathcal E_{\rm geom}:
0<
\|P_{\rm fd}+J_{\rm fd}\|_\infty
<
\Lambda(m,Q)
\right\}.
\]

This should be carried as a formal dependency, not re-attacked via finite determinacy.

---

# 9. Interaction dependency background

The \(dd\)-interaction remains independent unless the proof gains feature-balance or spectral positivity.

The actual covariance-weighted model is

\[
K_{ij}^{dd}
=
(u_i-u_j)^2\langle v_i,v_j\rangle.
\]

For balanced amplitudes,

\[
\sum_i a_i=0,
\]

the quadratic form is

\[
Q_{dd}(a)
=
2\left\langle
\sum_i a_i u_i^2v_i,\sum_j a_jv_j
\right\rangle
-
2\left|
\sum_i a_i u_iv_i
\right|^2.
\]

The second term is one-sided. The first term is indefinite unless one proves feature balance:

\[
\sum_i a_iv_i=0.
\]

Ordinary amplitude balance does not imply feature balance. Rank-one locking only changes the missing condition to

\[
\sum_i a_i\lambda_i=0.
\]

Unit normalization of \(v(u)\) also does not give conditional definiteness; a unit curve can violate the required spectral sign at order \(t^6\). turn46file5

Thus the interaction branch remains

\[
\mathfrak Z_{\rm int}^{dd}
=
\left\{
\sum_\nu a_\nu K(d_\nu)
+
\sum_{i,j}a_i a_j
(u_i-u_j)^2\langle v_i,v_j\rangle
=0
\right\}
\setminus\mathcal E_{\rm geom}.
\]

This matters globally, but the immediate local \(\Theta_\pm\) agents probably do not need to attack it unless their work touches finite-core \(J_{\rm fd}\).

---

# 10. Recommended agent framing

The three new agents should not re-audit the old \(\nu_{21,7}\) row. They should assume:

\[
\boxed{
\text{old package fails at }\mathcal E^{2}_{\eta\eta;7,0,0}.
}
\]

They should ask whether the \(\Theta_\pm\)-normal package is a valid replacement.

The handoff targets:

## Agent 1: diagonal \(\eta\eta\) audit

Needs to know:

\[
\Theta_\pm\text{ cancels only off-diagonal }\eta\eta.
\]

It does not touch \(N_{11},N_{22}\). The main risk is diagonal Hessian entries mixing into \(S\) through non-diagonal \(W_{+,0}\).

## Agent 2: Gate B actual-source audit

Needs to know:

\[
\Theta_\pm\text{ preserves first variations but changes nonlinear actual-source realization.}
\]

Gate A likely survives. Gate B actual-source must be reproved because the old actual-source obstruction is removed only if \(\Theta_\pm\) correction is included before \(C_{\mathcal W}^{\rm raw}\).

## Agent 3: \(T^\Theta\) bridge

Needs to know:

must replace old \(T\). The bridge must use the corrected finite-\(s\) scalar germ after the \(\Theta_\pm\) normal-form correction.

## Consolidated verdict

The \(\Theta_\pm\) repair is **not yet a valid completed repair**. It cancels the known off-diagonal odd-\(\eta\eta\) row only if treated as a **new corrected-package normal form**, not as a coordinate relabeling of the physical block.

The three checks sharpen the required work:

\Theta_\pm\text{ kills the old off-diagonal top row, but diagonal }\eta\eta\text{ terms create a shifted obstruction.}
}
\]

\[

\text{Gate B does not automatically survive: constrained-source curvature reintroduces the old residual.}
}

\[
\boxed{
T^\Theta\text{ is algebraically coherent only for the redesigned package; physical compatibility remains unproved.}
}
\]

---

# 1. Agent 1: diagonal \(\eta\eta\) terms are not automatically safe

Agent 1 found:

\[
[z^7]Y^{\eta\eta}_{\mathrm{diag}}=0,
\]

so the exact old top row

\[
\mathcal E^2_{\eta\eta;7,0,0}
\]

does **not** reappear from \(N_{11},N_{22}\).

But the diagonal Hessian starts one order earlier, at ordinary order \(6\), and can feed the septic table through one odd whitening coefficient:

\[
\mathcal D^{\mathrm{diag}}_{\eta\eta;7}
=
\tau_{h\to m}\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}\operatorname{Sym}
\left(
\Lambda^-_{\bullet,1}Y^{\eta\eta,\mathrm{diag}}_6W_{+,0}
+
\Lambda^-_{\bullet,0}Y^{\eta\eta,\mathrm{diag}}_6W_{+,1}
\right).
\]

The diagonal Hessian is not fixed-sector invisible in general. If

\[
Y=\operatorname{diag}(A,B),
\quad
L=
\begin{pmatrix}
\ell_{11}&\ell_{12}\\
\ell_{12}&\ell_{22}
\end{pmatrix},
\quad
W=
\begin{pmatrix}
w_{11}&w_{12}\\
w_{12}&w_{22}
\end{pmatrix},
\]

then the \(S\)-coordinate of \(\pi_{\mathfrak f}(LYW)\) contains

\[
f
=
\frac12
\left[
A(\ell_{11}w_{12}+\ell_{12}w_{11})
+
B(\ell_{12}w_{22}+\ell_{22}w_{12})
\right].
\]

So diagonal \(\eta\eta\) terms can become \(S\)-visible when \(W_{+,0}\) or the odd whitening coefficients are non-diagonal. 

**Implication:** the \(\Theta_\pm\) repair removes the off-diagonal defect but leaves a new diagonal safety theorem:

\[
\boxed{
\pi_S
\operatorname{Sym}
\left(
\Lambda^-_{\bullet,1}Y^{\eta\eta,\mathrm{diag}}_6W_{+,0}
+
\Lambda^-_{\bullet,0}Y^{\eta\eta,\mathrm{diag}}_6W_{+,1}
\right)=0.
}
\]

Without that, the repaired package is still locally incomplete.

---

# 2. Agent 2: Gate B does not survive automatically

Agent 2 found the central issue with \(\Theta_\pm\).

The first variations are unchanged. For

\[
\Theta_\sigma=\sin\Delta+q_\sigma s\cos\Delta,
\]

one has

\[
\delta\Theta_\sigma
=
(\cos\Delta_0-q_{\sigma,0}s\sin\Delta_0)\delta\Delta
+
s\cos\Delta_0\,\delta q_\sigma.
\]

So source-linear tables used in Gate A and the source-linear parts of Gate B survive.

But the second variations are not unchanged. The actual source does not supply free affine \(\Theta_\pm\). It supplies constrained variables:

\[
\Theta_\pm=\sin\Delta+q_\pm s\cos\Delta.
\]

For two source directions,

\[
\delta_{ij}^2\Theta_\sigma
=
A_\sigma\eta_{ij}
+
sC\,\chi_{\sigma,ij}
-
\Theta_{\sigma,0}\eta_i\eta_j
-
sS(\chi_{\sigma,i}\eta_j+\chi_{\sigma,j}\eta_i).
\]

Therefore the induced second off-diagonal block is

\[
\mathcal Y^{\Theta}_{ij}
=
\begin{pmatrix}
0 & \delta_{ij}^2\Theta_+/s^2\\
-\delta_{ij}^2\Theta_-/s^2 & 0
\end{pmatrix}.
\]

In the pure \(\eta\eta\) case,

\[
\delta_{ij}^2\Theta_\sigma=-\Theta_{\sigma,0}\eta_i\eta_j,
\]

so

\[
\delta_{ij}^2N_{21}^{\Theta,\mathrm{actual}}
=
\left(
\frac{\sin\Delta_0}{s^2}
+
\frac{q_-\cos\Delta_0}{s}
\right)\eta_i\eta_j.
\]

That is precisely the old residual. 

**Implication:** \(\Theta_\pm\) only fixes the row if the package **declares** \(\Theta_\pm\) to be affine normal source coordinates before forming the raw package. If \(\Theta_\pm\) is merely a coordinate change of the actual source functor, the old curvature returns via the chain rule.

So Gate B now needs a new hypothesis/theorem:

\[
\boxed{
D^2_{\mathrm{source}}\Theta_\pm
\text{ has no order-\(\le7\) fixed-sector contribution after raw Gate B projection.}
}
\]

Equivalently, prove

\[
\mathcal R_7^\Theta=0
\]

for the curvature channels

\[
A_\sigma\eta_{ij},
\quad
sC\,\chi_{\sigma,ij},
\quad
-\Theta_{\sigma,0}\eta_i\eta_j,
\quad
-sS(\chi_{\sigma,i}\eta_j+\chi_{\sigma,j}\eta_i).
\]

Without this, Gate B actual-source closure remains open.

---

# 3. Agent 3: \(T^\Theta\) is coherent only as corrected-package readout

Agent 3 confirms the algebra:

Define

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f,\Theta}
=
u_7^\Theta I+v_7^\Theta S,
\qquad
T^\Theta=\frac{v_7^\Theta}{c}.
\]

Then

\[
\Phi_K(A_7^{\mathfrak f,\Theta})
=
2v_7^\Theta
=
2cT^\Theta.
\]

So the readout theorem is algebraically fine.

But the crucial issue is physical compatibility. If \(\Theta_\pm\) is only a coordinate relabeling, the old second-source curvature appears through

\[
-\frac{1}{s^2}D^2_{\mathrm{source}}\Theta_-.
\]

So the repair works only if \(\Theta_\pm\)-normal form is part of the **definition of the corrected raw package before forming**

\[
C_{\mathcal W}^{\rm raw,\Theta}.
\]

Otherwise

\[
T^\Theta
\]

is just the old \(T\) in disguised coordinates and the old leak remains. 

The missing compatibility theorem is:

\[
[z^7]\Phi_K
\left(
\widehat\Omega_\zeta^{\corr}(z;m)
-
\widehat\Omega^{\corr,\Theta}(z;m)
\right)
=
0,
\]

or else the difference must be explicitly included in \(T^\Theta\).

---

# Current status of the \(\Theta_\pm\) repair

The repair is **coherent as a formal redesigned package**, but not as a proved repair of the original physical transform.

The unresolved obligations are now precise:

## A. Diagonal safety

\[
\pi_S
\operatorname{Sym}
\left(
\Lambda^-_{\bullet,1}Y^{\eta\eta,\mathrm{diag}}_6W_{+,0}

for

-
\widehat\Omega^{\corr,\Theta}
\right)
=0,

or include the difference in the definition of \(T^\Theta\).

# Strategic assessment

The \(\Theta_\pm\) proposal is now weaker than it initially looked.

It cancels the off-diagonal Hessian only under a **formal affine-normal-source convention**. But the actual constrained source functor reintroduces the same old \(\eta\eta\) curvature through

\[
D^2_{\mathrm{source}}\Theta_\pm.
\]

So there are two possible paths:

## Path 1 — formal corrected-package redesign

Declare \(\Theta_\pm\) affine normal variables in the package, then prove the redesigned package still represents the physical transform up to the needed septic \(\Phi_K\) readout.

This requires the physical compatibility theorem.

## Path 2 — actual-source proof

Keep \(\Theta_\pm\) induced from \((q_\pm,\Delta)\). Then the old residual returns. In this path, \(\Theta_\pm\) does **not** repair the local package unless \(\mathcal R_7^\Theta=0\) is proved by a full aggregate cancellation.

At present, neither path is complete.

# 1. Agent A: actual constrained \(\Theta_\pm\) source curvature reintroduces the old obstruction

Agent A proves the key no-go for interpreting \(\Theta_\pm\) as an actual source-coordinate change.

The constrained second variation is

\[
\delta_{ij}^2\Theta_\sigma
=
A_\sigma\eta_{ij}
+
sC_0\chi_{\sigma,ij}
-
\Theta_{\sigma,0}\eta_i\eta_j
-
sS_0(\chi_{\sigma,i}\eta_j+\chi_{\sigma,j}\eta_i).
\]

Therefore the lower-left off-diagonal source-curvature entry includes

\[
\frac{\Theta_{-,0}}{s^2}\eta_i\eta_j
+
\frac{S_0}{s}(\chi_{-,i}\eta_j+\chi_{-,j}\eta_i).
\]

The first term is exactly the old obstruction integrand:

\[
\frac{\Theta_{-,0}}{s^2}\eta_i\eta_j
=
\left(
\frac{\sin\Delta_0}{s^2}
+
\frac{q_-\cos\Delta_0}{s}
\right)\eta_i\eta_j.
\]

In the homogeneous scalar test

\[
r_i=r_j=u^2,\qquad q_0''=0,
\]

the \(\chi\eta\) channel does not cancel this; the septic coefficient is

\[
[z^7]F_{21}(z/Q^2)
=
\frac{q_0^3}{216Q^{14}}\neq0.
\]

So under the actual constrained-source interpretation,

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal R_7^\Theta\neq0.
}
\]

The \(\Theta_\pm\) repair only works if \(\Theta_\pm\) are declared **affine source variables** in a redesigned package. It does not work as a coordinate relabeling of

\[
(q_-,q_+,\Delta).

# 2. Agent B: diagonal \(\eta\eta\) safety also fails

does vanish by parity. But the diagonal Hessian starts at order \(6\), and with one odd same-point whitening coefficient it creates a septic \(S\)-visible shifted row:

\left(

+
\Lambda^-_{\bullet,0}Y^{\eta\eta,\mathrm{diag}}_6W_{+,1}
\right).

In the constant-baseline homogeneous test, with

\[
r_i=r_j=u^2,\qquad q_0\neq0,
\]

Agent B computes

=

\operatorname{diag}

\frac{q_0}{72},

\right),

and using the actual same-point Fréchet row

\Lambda^-_{2,1}

\qquad
\lambda=
\frac{\alpha\beta}{4\pi Q(p_1+p_2)},

gets a nonzero \(S\)-coefficient:

# 3. Agent C: \(T^\Theta\) is not physically valid unless the removed curvature is carried

Agent C confirms the algebraic readout:

\widehat\Omega_\zeta^{\corr}
-
\widehat\Omega^{\corr,\Theta}
\right).
}

Equivalently, if the mismatch has fixed-sector form

\[
D_7^\Theta=\alpha_7^\Theta I+\beta_7^\Theta S,

T^{\Theta,\phys}
=
T^\Theta+\frac{\beta_7^\Theta}{c}.
\]

So the physical Bottleneck C condition is

\[
\partial_\kappa T^{\Theta,\phys}=0,
\]

not merely

\[
\partial_\kappa T^\Theta=0.

```text
=
```

\quad (n<7).

+

Ignoring any untracked remainder,

=

\]

Thus subtracting the residual from the formal package does not eliminate it from the physical hidden coordinate. It only moves it. 

A second redesign agent states the no-go sharply: any transform-faithful local correction \(K_7\) that cancels the known residual must have nonzero fixed-sector \(S\)-component; therefore

\[

generically. But preserving the physical \(T\)-readout would require

\right),

The current computations point the other way: \(\beta_{\loc}^\Theta\) is explicitly nonzero in the homogeneous good-patch tests.

```text
\beta_{\loc}^\Theta
```

## Consolidated verdict

The three passes agree:

\[
\boxed{
\partial_\kappa\!\left(\frac{\beta_{\loc}^{\Theta}}{c}\right)\neq0
}
\]

in a legitimate homogeneous good-patch model. Therefore there is **no aggregate cancellation theorem** for the currently identified physical edge term.

This closes the \(\Theta_\pm\) normal-form repair attempt negatively, unless a new, currently absent, zeta-specific identity is added.

---

# 1. What was tested

After the formal \(\Theta_\pm\)-normal package subtracts the local residual, the physical hidden coordinate is still

\[
T^{\phys}
=
T^\star+\frac{\beta_{\loc}^{\Theta}}{c},
\]

where

\[
\beta_{\loc}^{\Theta}
=
\beta_{\off}^{\Theta}
+
\beta_{\diag}^{\Theta}
+
\beta_{\companions}^{\Theta}.
\]

The only remaining possible local closure was:

\[
\partial_\kappa\left(\frac{\beta_{\loc}^{\Theta}}{c}\right)=0.
\]

The agents tested this directly.

---

# 2. Why the \(\kappa\)-test reduces to the physical edge coefficient

The promoted amplitude carrier is still

\[
a_1a_2(a_1+a_2).
\]

Along

\[
a_2=-a_1+\kappa,
\]

one has

\[
a_1a_2(a_1+a_2)
=
-a_1^2\kappa+a_1\kappa^2,
\]

so

\[
\left.
\partial_\kappa
\bigl(a_1a_2(a_1+a_2)\bigr)
\right|_{\kappa=0}
=
-a_1^2.
\]

Since the carrier vanishes at \(\kappa=0\), differentiating \(1/c\) contributes nothing at the edge. Thus

\[
\left.
\partial_\kappa\left(\frac{\beta_{\loc}^{\Theta}}{c}\right)
\right|_{\kappa=0}
=
-\frac{a_1^2}{c_0}B_{\loc}^{\Theta},
\]

where \(B_{\loc}^{\Theta}\) is the frozen physical edge coefficient. So the condition is exactly

\[
B_{\loc}^{\Theta}=0.
\]

turn54file2

---

# 3. Off-diagonal contribution remains nonzero

The actual constrained \(\Theta_\pm\)-source curvature contributes through

\[
\frac{\Theta_{-,0}}{s^2}\eta_i\eta_j
+
\frac{S_0}{s}
(\chi_{-,i}\eta_j+\chi_{-,j}\eta_i).
\]

In the homogeneous good-patch test

\[
r_i=r_j=u^2,
\qquad
q_0''=0,
\]

the lower-left septic coefficient is

\[
[z^7]F_{21}(z/Q^2)
=
\frac{q_0^3}{216Q^{14}}\neq0.
\]

With the same top-row normalization, this yields a nonzero off-diagonal \(S\)-coefficient, e.g.

\[
B_{\off}^{\Theta}
=
-\frac{u}{5184\pi Q^{14}}
\]

in one normalization, or equivalently a nonzero coefficient proportional to

\[
\frac{u q_0^3}{q^3Q^{14}}.
\]

The normalization/sign conventions differ across agents, but the invariant conclusion is the same:

\[
\boxed{
B_{\off}^{\Theta}\neq0.
}
\]

turn54file1turn54file2

---

# 4. Diagonal shifted contribution is also nonzero and cannot structurally cancel it

The shifted diagonal septic row gives

\[
B_{\diag}^{\Theta}
=
-\frac{\lambda}{2\pi Q^{12}}
\left(
\frac{q_0\alpha}{72}
+
\frac{q_0^3\beta}{864}
\right),
\]

with

\[
\lambda=
\frac{\alpha\beta}{4\pi Q(p_1+p_2)}.
\]

In one simplified normalization this becomes

\[
B_{\diag}^{\Theta}
=
-\frac{\sqrt3}{1152\,Q^{13}q_0^2},
\]

again nonzero on a good patch. 

Crucially, the diagonal and off-diagonal pieces have different \(Q\)-homogeneity:

\[
B_{\off}^{\Theta}=O(Q^{-14}),
\qquad
B_{\diag}^{\Theta}=O(Q^{-13}).
\]

Therefore they cannot cancel as a formal identity in \(Q\). At most they could accidentally cancel at isolated parameter values, which is useless for a proof-level local identity. turn54file1

One pass also gives a robust small-parameter argument: by scaling the diagonal whitening coefficients

\[
\alpha=\varepsilon\alpha_0,
\qquad
\beta=\varepsilon\beta_0,
\]

the diagonal contribution becomes \(O(\varepsilon^3)\), while the off-diagonal contribution stays nonzero. Hence

\[
B_{\loc}^{\Theta}
=
B_{\off}^{\Theta}
+
O(\varepsilon^3)
\neq0
\]

for sufficiently small nonzero \(\varepsilon\). 

---

# 5. Labelled summation, transpose, and companions do not rescue it

The agents also checked the usual escape routes.

The labelled-source sum cannot force cancellation: take all labels zero except the one active pair \(i,j\) with

\[
r_i=r_j=u^2.
\]

The \((i,j)\) and \((j,i)\) terms are symmetric and add rather than cancel. 

Endpoint transpose does not cancel the off-diagonal term; this obstruction was already known to survive endpoint symmetry and fixed-sector bookkeeping. 

Right/left companions are coefficient-dependent and can be suppressed or made small in the same local model while preserving the nonzero off-diagonal term. Thus no universal aggregate identity is available. 

---

# 6. Final local conclusion

The physical edge obstruction survives:

\[
\boxed{
\left.
\partial_\kappa
\left(
\frac{\beta_{\loc}^{\Theta}}{c}
\right)
\right|_{\kappa=0}
\neq0.
}
\]

One explicit model gives

\[
\left.
\partial_\kappa
\left(
\frac{\beta_{\loc}^{\Theta}}{c}
\right)
\right|_{\kappa=0}
=
\frac{1}{c}
\left(
\frac{1}{5184\pi Q^{14}}
+
\frac{13}{13824\pi^2Q^{13}}
\right)
\neq0
\]

in a normalized specialization. Another gives the robust form

\[
\left.
\partial_\kappa
\left(
\frac{\beta_{\loc}^{\Theta}}{c}
\right)
\right|_{\kappa=0}
=
-\frac{a_1^2u q_0^3}
{5184\pi c_0q^3Q^{14}}
+
O(\varepsilon^3)
\neq0.
\]

The exact constants vary with normalization conventions, but the nonvanishing conclusion is stable. turn54file1turn54file2

\]

\boxed{
\partial_\kappa(\beta_{\loc}^{\Theta}/c)=0.
}

The agents have now produced explicit good-patch models where this identity fails. So the honest status is stronger:
