# Insert 1 — local \(\Theta_\pm\) no-go

**Placement:** after the current discussion of the \(\Theta_\pm\)-normal package / local Bottleneck-C repair attempt. If the draft already has a \(\Theta_\pm\) section, append this as the final “status/no-go” subsection.

This captures the latest result: a formal \(\Theta_\pm\) counterterm package can hide the defect in a redesigned package, but it cannot remove the **physical** \(T\)-visible obstruction. The key point is that the physical coordinate must carry the removed edge residual back as \(\beta_{\loc}^{\Theta}/c\), and the latest homogeneous good-patch tests show \(\partial_\kappa(\beta_{\loc}^{\Theta}/c)\ne0\). turn53file1turn54file0turn54file1turn54file2

```latex
\begin{definition}[\(\Theta\)-local physical edge residual]
\label{def:theta-local-physical-edge-residual}
Let
\[
R_{\off,7}^{\Theta}
\]
denote the septic fixed-sector residual produced by the actual constrained
source curvature of the off-diagonal numerator variables
\[
\Theta_\pm=\sin\Delta+q_\pm s\cos\Delta.
\]
Let
\[
R_{\diag,7}^{\Theta}
\]
denote the shifted diagonal \(\eta\eta\) septic residual
\[
\pi_{\mathfrak f}
\operatorname{Sym}
\left(
\Lambda^-_{\bullet,1}Y^{\eta\eta,\diag}_6W_{+,0}
+
\Lambda^-_{\bullet,0}Y^{\eta\eta,\diag}_6W_{+,1}
\right).
\]
Define the total local physical edge residual by
\[
R_{\loc,7}^{\Theta}
:=
R_{\off,7}^{\Theta}
+
R_{\diag,7}^{\Theta}.
\]
Write
\[
R_{\loc,7}^{\Theta}
=
\alpha_{\loc}^{\Theta}I+\beta_{\loc}^{\Theta}S.
\]
The scalar \(\beta_{\loc}^{\Theta}\) is the \(\Phi_K\)-visible physical edge
residual left by the \(\Theta_\pm\)-normal local package.
\end{definition}

\begin{remark}[The \(\Theta_\pm\)-normal package is formal, not physical]
\label{rem:theta-normal-package-formal-not-physical}
A formal septic-normal package may be defined by subtracting
\(R_{\loc,7}^{\Theta}\) from the raw \(\Theta\)-normal package:
\[
C_{\mathcal W}^{\raw,\star}
:=
C_{\mathcal W}^{\raw,\Theta}
-
z^7\tau_{m\to h}^{-1}R_{\loc,7}^{\Theta}.
\]
This changes only the septic nonlinear layer and leaves lower ordinary orders
and source-linear tables unchanged.

However, the physical finite-\(s\) transform has not lost the residual.
The physical septic coefficient is
\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f,\phys}
=
A_7^{\mathfrak f,\star}
+
R_{\loc,7}^{\Theta}
+
R_{\rem,7}^{\Theta},
\]
where \(R_{\rem,7}^{\Theta}\) denotes any further untracked mismatch.
Ignoring the possible further mismatch, the physical hidden coordinate is
therefore
\[
T^{\phys}
=
T^\star+\frac{\beta_{\loc}^{\Theta}}{c}.
\]
Thus a formal normal-form package can move the local edge residual out of the
package coefficient, but it cannot remove it from the physical transform
readout.
\end{remark}

\begin{proposition}[No transform-faithful septic normal-form repair]
\label{prop:no-transform-faithful-septic-normal-form-repair}
Let \(K_7\) be a local septic normal-form correction satisfying the following
four conditions:
\begin{enumerate}
\item \(K_7\) is invisible below ordinary order \(7\);
\item \(K_7\) is source-quadratic, hence does not alter the source-linear
Gate~A, Gate~B, or \(M_A,M_C\) connection tables;
\item \(K_7\) cancels the local septic residual
\[
R_{\loc,7}^{\Theta}
=
\alpha_{\loc}^{\Theta}I+\beta_{\loc}^{\Theta}S;
\]
\item the physical \(\Phi_K\)-readout is unchanged, so no correction term is
added back into the physical hidden coordinate.
\end{enumerate}
Then necessarily
\[
\beta_{\loc}^{\Theta}=0.
\]
Consequently, on any good patch where
\[
\beta_{\loc}^{\Theta}\ne0,
\]
no such transform-faithful local normal-form correction exists.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
To cancel \(R_{\loc,7}^{\Theta}\), the correction \(K_7\) must contain the
fixed-sector component
\[
-\beta_{\loc}^{\Theta}S.
\]
But preserving the physical \(\Phi_K\)-readout without adding a correction to
the hidden coordinate requires
\[
[z^7]\Phi_K(K_7)=0.
\]
Since
\[
\Phi_K(S)=2,
\]
the \(S\)-component of \(K_7\) contributes
\[
-2\beta_{\loc}^{\Theta}
\]
to the septic \(\Phi_K\)-readout. Hence readout preservation forces
\[
\beta_{\loc}^{\Theta}=0.
\]
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[Physical edge obstruction survives in a good-patch model]
\label{prop:theta-physical-edge-obstruction-good-patch}
There exists a homogeneous good-patch local coefficient model for which
\[
\left.
\partial_\kappa
\left(
\frac{\beta_{\loc}^{\Theta}}{c}
\right)
\right|_{\kappa=0}
\ne0.
\]
In particular, no aggregate cancellation theorem for
\[
\beta_{\loc}^{\Theta}
\]
is supported by the current coefficient calculus.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
The promoted edge amplitude remains
\[
a_1a_2(a_1+a_2).
\]
Along
\[
a_2=-a_1+\kappa
\]
one has
\[
a_1a_2(a_1+a_2)
=
-a_1^2\kappa+a_1\kappa^2,
\]
and hence
\[
\left.
\partial_\kappa
\bigl(a_1a_2(a_1+a_2)\bigr)
\right|_{\kappa=0}
=
-a_1^2.
\]
Since the edge carrier itself vanishes at \(\kappa=0\), differentiating
\(1/c\) contributes nothing at \(\kappa=0\). Therefore
\[
\left.
\partial_\kappa
\left(
\frac{\beta_{\loc}^{\Theta}}{c}
\right)
\right|_{\kappa=0}
=
-\frac{a_1^2}{c_0}B_{\loc}^{\Theta},
\]
where \(B_{\loc}^{\Theta}\) is the frozen local physical edge coefficient.

Now take the homogeneous source model
\[
r_i=r_j=u^2,\qquad q_0''=0,
\]
on a good patch with
\[
u\,q_0\,q\,Q\,c_0\ne0.
\]
The constrained off-diagonal \(\Theta_\pm\)-source curvature contributes a
nonzero lower-left septic coefficient. In the normalization of the
off-diagonal top row this gives
\[
B_{\off}^{\Theta,\hom}
=
\frac{u q_0^3}{5184\pi q^3Q^{14}}
\ne0.
\]
The shifted diagonal term has the form
\[
B_{\diag}^{\Theta,\hom}
=
-\frac{\lambda}{2\pi Q^{12}}
\left(
\frac{q_0\alpha}{72}
+
\frac{q_0^3\beta}{864}
\right),
\qquad
\lambda=
\frac{\alpha\beta}{4\pi Q(p_1+p_2)}.
\]
Choose
\[
\alpha=\varepsilon\alpha_0,\qquad
\beta=\varepsilon\beta_0,
\]
with \(\varepsilon\ne0\) sufficiently small and \(p_1+p_2\ne0\).  Then
\[
B_{\diag}^{\Theta,\hom}=O(\varepsilon^3),
\]
while \(B_{\off}^{\Theta,\hom}\) remains nonzero. Therefore
\[
B_{\loc}^{\Theta,\hom}
=
B_{\off}^{\Theta,\hom}
+
B_{\diag}^{\Theta,\hom}
+
B_{\companions}^{\Theta,\hom}
\ne0
\]
for sufficiently small \(\varepsilon\), after including the companion terms
already accounted for by endpoint symmetrization and the local fixed-sector
aggregation. Hence
\[
\left.
\partial_\kappa
\left(
\frac{\beta_{\loc}^{\Theta}}{c}
\right)
\right|_{\kappa=0}
=
-\frac{a_1^2}{c_0}B_{\loc}^{\Theta,\hom}
\ne0.
\]
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Status of the \(\Theta_\pm\)-normal repair]
\label{rem:status-theta-normal-repair}
The \(\Theta_\pm\)-normal form is useful as an obstruction-isolating device:
it identifies the physical septic edge residual
\[
\beta_{\loc}^{\Theta}.
\]
It does not close local Bottleneck~C.  A formal package may be constructed so
that
\[
\partial_\kappa T^\star=0,
\]
but the physical hidden coordinate is
\[
T^{\phys}
=
T^\star+\frac{\beta_{\loc}^{\Theta}}{c}.
\]
Thus the transform-safe physical Bottleneck~C condition is
\[
\partial_\kappa
\left(
T^\star+\frac{\beta_{\loc}^{\Theta}}{c}
\right)=0.
\]
The homogeneous good-patch model of
Proposition~\ref{prop:theta-physical-edge-obstruction-good-patch} shows that
the second term is not currently zero.  Therefore local Bottleneck~C cannot be
closed by \(\Theta_\pm\)-normal coordinates or septic normal-form counterterms
alone.
\end{remark}
```

# Insert 2 — finite-core dependency block

**Placement:** in the finite-core section, after the finite determinacy / projective detection discussion. If the draft already has a weaker near-\(\mathcal Z_k\) branch, add this as the sharper current dependency.

This captures the exact current dependency: finite determinacy and projective detection are done, but the proof still needs pointwise sampled vector non-concentration for \(C_{\rm fd}=P_{\rm fd}+J_{\rm fd}\). turn56file2turn56file3turn56file4turn56file9

```latex
\begin{definition}[Finite-determinacy vector and sampled scale]
\label{def:finite-determinacy-vector-and-sampled-scale}
On a compact nonsingular actual-source \(k\)-core stratum \(\Theta_k\), let
\[
C_{\rm fd}(\theta)
=
(c_{\core,1},c_{\core,3},\ldots,c_{\core,2R_{\Theta_k}+1})(\theta)
\]
be the finite-determinacy coefficient vector.  We decompose it as
\[
C_{\rm fd}(\theta)
=
P_{\rm fd}(\theta)+J_{\rm fd}(\theta),
\]
where \(P_{\rm fd}\) is the pair-like or one-body finite vector and
\[
J_{\rm fd}
=
(J_1,J_3,\ldots,J_{2R_{\Theta_k}+1}),
\qquad
J_{2r+1}=[s^{2r+1}]\Phi_K(\mathcal I_{\ge2}),
\]
is the finite interaction vector.

For \(1\le N\le R_{\Theta_k}+1\), define
\[
F_N(\theta,Q)
=
c_{\core,2N-1}(\theta)
+
\sum_{j\ge1}
c_{\core,2N-1+2j}(\theta)
h_j(1^2,\ldots,N^2)Q^{-2j}.
\]
Set
\[
\Lambda(m,Q)
=
C_*
\max_{1\le N\le R_{\Theta_k}+1}
\left(
\frac{Q^{2N+2}}
{(2N-1)N!(N-1)!}
\frac{x}{B_\zeta(m)}S(m)
\right).
\]
\end{definition}

\begin{theorem}[Sampled finite-core vector non-concentration]
\label{thm:sampled-finite-core-vector-nonconcentration}
Let \(\Theta_k\) be a compact nonsingular actual-source \(k\)-core stratum.
Every actual zeta finite-core parameter
\[
\theta(m)\in\Theta_k
\]
satisfies at least one of the following:
\[
\theta(m)\in\mathcal Z_k,
\]
\[
\theta(m)\in\mathcal E_{\rm geom},
\]
or
\[
\|P_{\rm fd}(\theta(m))+J_{\rm fd}(\theta(m))\|_\infty
\ge
\Lambda(m,Q).
\]
\end{theorem}

\begin{lemma}[Finite-core lower transfer from sampled vector non-concentration]
\label{lem:finite-core-lower-transfer-from-svnc}
Assume Theorem~\ref{thm:sampled-finite-core-vector-nonconcentration}.  Assume
also bounded-depth projective detection: for \(Q\ge Q_0(\Theta_k)\), every
\(\theta\notin\mathcal Z_k\) admits some \(1\le N\le R_{\Theta_k}+1\) such that
\[
|F_N(\theta,Q)|
\ge
c_0\|C_{\rm fd}(\theta)\|_\infty.
\]
Then every actual zeta finite-core sample
\[
\theta(m)\notin\mathcal Z_k\cup\mathcal E_{\rm geom}
\]
has some \(1\le N\le R_{\Theta_k}+1\) satisfying
\[
|\Xi_{\core}^{(N)}(m)|
\ge
c
\frac{x}{B_\zeta(m)}S(m).
\]
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
Choose \(N\) by projective detection.  Since
\[
C_{\rm fd}=P_{\rm fd}+J_{\rm fd},
\]
Theorem~\ref{thm:sampled-finite-core-vector-nonconcentration} gives
\[
|F_N(\theta(m),Q)|
\ge
c_0\Lambda(m,Q).
\]
By definition of \(\Lambda(m,Q)\),
\[
\Lambda(m,Q)
\ge
C_*
\frac{Q^{2N+2}}
{(2N-1)N!(N-1)!}
\frac{x}{B_\zeta(m)}S(m).
\]
Substitute this into
\[
\Xi_{\core}^{(N)}(m)
=
(-1)^{N+1}
(2N-1)N!(N-1)!
Q^{-(2N+2)}
F_N(\theta(m),Q).
\]
The claimed bound follows.
\end{proof}

\begin{definition}[Finite-core alignment-small branch]
\label{def:finite-core-alignment-small-branch}
Let
\[
C_{\rm fd}=P_{\rm fd}+J_{\rm fd}.
\]
Define
\[
\mathcal N_k^{\rm align}(m,Q)
\]
to be the set of actual zeta finite-core parameters
\[
\theta(m)\in\Theta_k\setminus(\mathcal Z_k\cup\mathcal E_{\rm geom})
\]
such that
\[
0<
\|P_{\rm fd}(\theta(m))+J_{\rm fd}(\theta(m))\|_\infty
<
\Lambda(m,Q).
\]
Equivalently, Theorem~\ref{thm:sampled-finite-core-vector-nonconcentration}
asserts
\[
\mathcal N_k^{\rm align}(m,Q)=\varnothing.
\]
\end{definition}

\begin{remark}[Why finite determinacy and spacing do not prove sampled non-concentration]
\label{rem:finite-determinacy-spacing-not-sampled-nonconcentration}
Theorem~\ref{thm:sampled-finite-core-vector-nonconcentration} is not a
consequence of qualitative finite determinacy, compactness, discreteness of
zeros, pairwise zero-spacing, endpoint-gap control, or
Remez--{\L}ojasiewicz volume estimates.  Those tools control exact vanishing,
collision, boundary behavior, or measure-smallness of analytic tubes.  The
finite-core lower transfer requires a pointwise exclusion:
\[
\theta(m)\notin
\left\{
\max_N |F_N(\theta,Q)|<\Lambda(m,Q)
\right\}
\]
for every actual zeta finite-core sample outside
\(\mathcal Z_k\cup\mathcal E_{\rm geom}\).

The interaction vector \(J_{\rm fd}\) gives a concrete mechanism for failure:
\[
J_{\rm fd}(\theta(m))\approx -P_{\rm fd}(\theta(m))
\]
can make \(C_{\rm fd}=P_{\rm fd}+J_{\rm fd}\) nonzero but smaller than the
calibrated scale without forcing any currently listed controlled incidence.
Thus sampled vector non-concentration is a genuine arithmetic or
source-level anti-cancellation input.
\end{remark}
```

# Insert 3 — \(dd\)-interaction dependency/status

**Placement:** in the finite-core interaction / \(J_1\) section, after the first-interaction discussion.

This records the stabilized interaction branch: feature balance or conditional spectral positivity is required; it is not currently derived. turn56file14turn56file16

```latex
\begin{definition}[\(dd\)-interaction branch]
\label{def:dd-interaction-branch}
In the covariance-weighted \(dd\)-interaction model, write
\[
K_{ij}^{dd}
=
(u_i-u_j)^2\langle v_i,v_j\rangle,
\qquad
v_i=v(u_i).
\]
The associated centered \(dd\)-interaction branch is
\[
\mathfrak Z_{\rm int}^{dd}
=
\left\{
\sum_\nu a_\nu K(d_\nu)
+
\sum_{i,j}a_i a_j
(u_i-u_j)^2\langle v_i,v_j\rangle
=0
\right\}
\setminus\mathcal E_{\rm geom}.
\]
This branch represents cancellation of the first finite-core coefficient by
the \(dd\)-interaction without forcing the full odd germ to vanish.
\end{definition}

\begin{remark}[Feature balance is stronger than amplitude balance]
\label{rem:feature-balance-stronger-than-amplitude-balance}
For balanced amplitudes
\[
\sum_i a_i=0,
\]
the covariance-weighted \(dd\)-quadratic form satisfies
\[
Q_{dd}(a)
=
2\left\langle
\sum_i a_i u_i^2v_i,\sum_j a_jv_j
\right\rangle
-
2\left|
\sum_i a_i u_iv_i
\right|^2.
\]
The second term is one-sided.  The first term has no fixed sign unless one has
the feature-balance condition
\[
\sum_i a_iv_i=0.
\]
Ordinary amplitude balance does not imply feature balance.  Even rank-one
locking
\[
v_i=\lambda_i v_0
\]
only changes the missing condition to
\[
\sum_i a_i\lambda_i=0.
\]
Thus the \(dd\)-interaction remains sign-indefinite unless feature balance,
cone control, or incidence containment is proved.
\end{remark}

\begin{theorem}[Feature-balance or spectral positivity for the \(dd\)-interaction]
\label{thm:feature-balance-or-spectral-positivity-dd-needed}
On each compact nonsingular same-scale finite-core patch away from the
controlled degeneracy set, let \(v(u)\) be the transverse \(dd\)-source feature
after same-side whitening normalization.  To close the \(dd\)-interaction
branch, one needs at least one of the following:
\begin{enumerate}
\item \emph{Feature balance:}
\[
\sum_i a_i v(u_i)=0
\]
for every admissible balanced finite core \(\sum_i a_i=0\);

\item \emph{Conditional spectral rigidity:} the reduced kernel
\[
K_{dd}(t;m)
=
t^2
\left\langle
v\!\left(m+\frac t2\right),
v\!\left(m-\frac t2\right)
\right\rangle
\]
admits, after phase rotation, a conditionally one-sided spectral
representation, or its negative;

\item \emph{Incidence containment:} all feature-balance failures and centered
kernel signature-changing loci lie in the controlled incidence set
\(\mathcal E_{\rm geom}\).
\end{enumerate}
Absent one of these inputs, the branch
\[
\mathfrak Z_{\rm int}^{dd}
\]
remains independent.
\end{theorem}
```

```latex
\begin{remark}[Current proof frontier after the \(\Theta_\pm\) audit]
\label{rem:current-proof-frontier-after-theta-audit}
The present proof state is as follows.

\begin{enumerate}
\item The current local Bottleneck-C strategy fails under the physical
readout.  The \(\Theta_\pm\)-normal form can define a formal septic package,
but the physical hidden coordinate is
\[
T^{\phys}
=
T^\star+\frac{\beta_{\loc}^{\Theta}}{c}.
\]
The homogeneous good-patch model gives
\[
\left.
\partial_\kappa
\left(
\frac{\beta_{\loc}^{\Theta}}{c}
\right)
\right|_{\kappa=0}
\ne0.
\]
Thus local Bottleneck~C cannot be closed by \(\Theta_\pm\)-normal coordinates
or septic normal-form counterterms alone.

\item The finite-core lower-transfer branch is reduced to the sampled vector
non-concentration dependency
\[
\mathcal N_k^{\rm align}(m,Q)=\varnothing.
\]
Assuming this dependency, bounded-depth projective detection gives the needed
\(N\)-point lower bound.

\item The \(dd\)-interaction branch remains independent unless feature balance,
conditional spectral positivity, or incidence containment is proved for the
covariance-weighted interaction kernel.
\end{enumerate}

Consequently, the next local progress requires a new physical edge identity
not contained in the current package:
\[
\partial_\kappa(\beta_{\loc}^{\Theta}/c)=0,
\]
or a different local mechanism entirely.
\end{remark}
```

## Insert 2 — closed \(M_A,M_C\) connection branch

```latex
\subsection{Closed branch: \(M_A,M_C\) connection closure}
\label{subsec:closed-ma-mc-connection-closure}

Let
\[
M_A=\dot r_3r_2\dot r_4,
\qquad
M_C=\dot r_3\dot r_2r_4.
\]
Under the homogeneous scalar-grade reflection convention,
\[
\mathsf P_g\circ\mathsf S=(-1)^g\mathsf S\circ\mathsf P_g,
\]
where \(\mathsf S\) is endpoint swap, the corrected mixed block satisfies
\[
N^{\corr}(h_-,h_+)^T=N^{\corr}(h_+,h_-).
\]
Consequently, for the source-linear middle block \(Y_g\),
\[
Y_g(h_-,h_+)^T=(-1)^gY_g(h_+,h_-).
\]
Writing
\[
Y_g(h-\delta/2,h+\delta/2)
=
\sum_{e\ge0}\delta^eY_g^{\langle e\rangle}(h),
\]
one obtains the edge-refined parity
\[
\left(Y_{g,\beta}^{\langle e\rangle}\right)^T
=
(-1)^{g+e}Y_{g,\beta}^{\langle e\rangle}.
\]

This parity closes the labelled \(J=(3,2,4)\) pre-trivialization table:
\[
Z_j[M_A]=Z_j[M_C]=0,
\qquad
0\le j\le7.
\]
Therefore the connection identities
\[
R_7^{(A)}
+
\sum_{i=1}^{7}\omega_m(Z_{7-i}[M_A],A_i)=0,
\]
and
\[
R_7^{(C)}
+
\sum_{i=1}^{7}\omega_m(Z_{7-i}[M_C],A_i)=0
\]
hold under the stated source-grade reflection convention.

Thus the \(M_A,M_C\) connection branch is no longer a live obstruction.
```

## Insert 3 — frozen \(E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}}\) definition and status

Place after the closed branch, under a subsection such as “Live local obstruction.” This corrects the major bookkeeping issue: Bottleneck C uses the frozen coefficient, not the internal source-position \([z^7\delta^1]\) coefficient. turn59file9turn59file13

```latex
\subsection{Live local obstruction: the frozen promoted mixed-block coefficient}
\label{subsec:live-local-obstruction-eay-bc}

The first live local actual-source/Bottleneck~C carrier is the promoted
quadratic mixed-block channel
\[
Y_{12}^{(2)}:=D^2N_0[\xi_1,\xi_2].
\]
It is coupled to one same-point linear whitening slot.  The promoted channel
has amplitude factor
\[
a_1a_2(a_1+a_2).
\]
On the collision chart
\[
a_2=-a_1(1+\kappa\delta),
\]
one has
\[
a_1a_2(a_1+a_2)=a_1^3\kappa\delta+O(\delta^2).
\]
Thus the amplitude already supplies the first \(\delta\)-edge.  Therefore the
first Bottleneck~C coefficient is the frozen internal coefficient
\[
E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}}
:=
\tau_{h\to m}\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}
\operatorname{Sym}
[z^7]\,
D(G_-^{-1/2})[A_-]\,
Y_{12}^{(2)}\,
R_0.
\]
Equivalently,
\[
E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}}
=
\tau_{h\to m}\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}
\operatorname{Sym}
\sum_{\chi\in\{dd,d\eta+\eta d,\eta\eta\}}
\sum_{g=4}^{7}
\sum_{r+b=7-g}
H^A_{r,0}Y^\chi_{g,0}W_{+,b}.
\]
Write
\[
E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}}=e_{A,Y}I+f_{A,Y}S.
\]
The quotient Bottleneck~C obstruction is
\[
Q_{A,Y}:=e_{A,Y}v_5-u_5f_{A,Y}.
\]
The transform-safe obstruction is
\[
\Phi_K(E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}})=2f_{A,Y}.
\]

For comparison, the literal source-position edge
\[
E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{pos}}
:=
\tau_{h\to m}\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}
\operatorname{Sym}
[z^7\delta^1]\,
D(G_-^{-1/2})[A_-]\,
Y_{12}^{(2)}\,
R_0
\]
belongs to the next source-motion layer.  It is not the first
Bottleneck~C amplitude-derivative coefficient.
```

```latex
\begin{remark}[Executable table for \(E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}}\)]
\label{rem:executable-table-eay-bc-current}
The frozen Bottleneck~C coefficient is computed from the rows

\mathcal E^a_{\chi;g,r,b}
:=

\Lambda^-_{a,r}Y^\chi_{g,0}W_{+,b}

\]

4\le g\le7,

E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}}
=

\mathcal E^a_{\chi;g,r,b}.
\]

Y_{d\eta-\eta d}^{(2)}
\]
is excluded because it is killed by fixed-sector projection.
\end{remark}
```

```latex
\begin{remark}[Status of the frozen promoted mixed-block coefficient]
\label{rem:status-eay-bc-current}
The finite Fr\'echet--Sylvester recurrences reduce

does not supply the scalar midpoint source-jet data needed to evaluate
\[
E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}}=e_{A,Y}I+f_{A,Y}S.
\]
The required scalar data include, safely,
\[
q_0^{(k)}(m),
\qquad
0\le k\le9,

and

(r_i^{[a]})^{(k)}(m),
\qquad
i=1,2,\quad a\in\{1,5\},\quad 2\le k\le9.

\]
through the orders contributing to

Y^{dd}_{g,0},
\qquad

e_{A,Y}v_5-u_5f_{A,Y}=0,

nor
```

## Insert 4 — scalar classification and \(T\)-slope for \(E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}}\)

Place immediately after Insert 3. This captures the Agent 4/9 conclusion that quotient closure and transform-safe closure are different. turn59file17

```latex
\begin{lemma}[Scalar tests for the frozen promoted mixed-block coefficient]
\label{lem:scalar-tests-eay-bc}
Let
\[
E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}}=eI+fS,
\qquad
A_5^{\mathfrak f}=u_5I+v_5S.
\]
Then quotient Bottleneck~C for the promoted mixed-block carrier is equivalent
to
\[
ev_5-u_5f=0.
\]
The transform-safe \(T\)-horizontal condition is equivalent to
\[
f=0.
\]
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
The quotient line is
\[
\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
\]
Thus
\[
E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}}\in \mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}
\]
is equivalent, on a good patch, to the vanishing of the determinant
\[
ev_5-u_5f.
\]
On the other hand,
\[
\Phi_K(I)=0,
\qquad
\Phi_K(S)=2.
\]
Hence
\[
\Phi_K(E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}})=2f,
\]
so the transform-safe condition is exactly \(f=0\).
\end{proof}

\begin{corollary}[First live \(T\)-slope carrier]
\label{cor:first-live-t-slope-carrier-current}
The amplitude factor of the promoted carrier is
\[
a_1a_2(a_1+a_2),
\]
and
\[
\partial_{a_2}\bigl(a_1a_2(a_1+a_2)\bigr)\big|_{a_2=-a_1}
=
-a_1^2.
\]
Therefore
\[
\partial_\kappa T\big|_{E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}}}
=
-a_1^2\frac{\Phi_K(E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}})}{2c}
=
-a_1^2\frac{f}{c}.
\]
If
\[
E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}}=\lambda A_5^{\mathfrak f},
\]
then
\[
\partial_\kappa T\big|_{E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}}}
=
-a_1^2\lambda\frac{v_5}{c}.
\]
Thus, on the generic patch \(v_5\ne0\), a nonzero line-gauge
\(E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}}\) closes the quotient condition but still leaks
through \(T\).
\end{corollary}
```

## Insert 5 — \(\Theta_\pm\) no-go / physical edge obstruction

This is the major progress after the frozen \(E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}}\) bookkeeping. Place this in a subsection after the \(\Theta_\pm\)-normal-form discussion. It should replace any optimistic claim that \(\Theta_\pm\) repairs the local branch. The transcript records that formal \(\Theta_\pm\) packages can hide the obstruction, but the physical hidden coordinate carries it back; explicit homogeneous good-patch models give \(\partial_\kappa(\beta_{\loc}^\Theta/c)\ne0\). turn59file3turn59file4turn59file5turn59file6turn59file7turn59file8

```latex
\subsection{No-go for the \(\Theta_\pm\)-normal repair}
\label{subsec:no-go-theta-normal-repair}

The off-diagonal numerator variables
\[
\Theta_+=\sin\Delta+q_+s\cos\Delta,
\qquad
\Theta_-=\sin\Delta+q_-s\cos\Delta
\]
make the off-diagonal entries formally affine:
\[
N_{12}^{\Theta}=\frac{\Theta_+}{s^2},
\qquad
N_{21}^{\Theta}=-\frac{\Theta_-}{s^2}.
\]
As a formal normal package this cancels the original off-diagonal
\(\eta\eta\) Hessian row.  It does not, however, close the physical
Bottleneck~C obstruction.

\begin{definition}[\(\Theta\)-local physical edge residual]
\label{def:theta-local-physical-edge-residual}
Let
\[
R_{\off,7}^{\Theta}
\]
be the septic fixed-sector residual produced by the actual constrained source
curvature of the off-diagonal variables \(\Theta_\pm\).  Let
\[
R_{\diag,7}^{\Theta}
\]
be the shifted diagonal \(\eta\eta\) septic residual
\[
\pi_{\mathfrak f}
\operatorname{Sym}
\left(
\Lambda^-_{\bullet,1}Y^{\eta\eta,\diag}_6W_{+,0}
+
\Lambda^-_{\bullet,0}Y^{\eta\eta,\diag}_6W_{+,1}
\right).
\]
Define
\[
R_{\loc,7}^{\Theta}
:=
R_{\off,7}^{\Theta}+R_{\diag,7}^{\Theta}.
\]
Write
\[
R_{\loc,7}^{\Theta}
=
\alpha_{\loc}^{\Theta}I+\beta_{\loc}^{\Theta}S.
\]
The scalar \(\beta_{\loc}^{\Theta}\) is the \(\Phi_K\)-visible physical edge
residual left by the \(\Theta_\pm\)-normal package.
\end{definition}

\begin{remark}[Constrained \(\Theta_\pm\) variables reintroduce curvature]
\label{rem:constrained-theta-reintroduces-curvature}
The variables \(\Theta_\pm\) are not free affine source variables in the
physical finite-\(s\) block.  They are constrained by
\[
\Theta_\sigma=\sin\Delta+q_\sigma s\cos\Delta.
\]
For two source variations,
\[
D_{\source}^2\Theta_\sigma
=
A_\sigma\eta_{ij}
+sC\,\chi_{\sigma,ij}
-\Theta_{\sigma,0}\eta_i\eta_j
-sS(\chi_{\sigma,i}\eta_j+\chi_{\sigma,j}\eta_i).
\]
In the pure \(\eta\eta\) channel, this gives
\[
D_{\source}^2N_{21}^{\Theta,\actual}
=
\left(
\frac{\sin\Delta_0}{s^2}
+
\frac{q_-\cos\Delta_0}{s}
\right)\eta_i\eta_j,
\]
which is the old off-diagonal source-curvature obstruction.  Thus the
\(\Theta_\pm\)-normal form is not a physical coordinate relabeling that
removes the obstruction; it is a formal package subtraction unless this
curvature is carried back into the physical readout.
\end{remark}

\begin{proposition}[No transform-faithful septic normal-form repair]
\label{prop:no-transform-faithful-septic-normal-form-repair}
Let \(K_7\) be a local septic normal-form correction satisfying:
\begin{enumerate}
\item \(K_7\) is invisible below ordinary order \(7\);
\item \(K_7\) is source-quadratic, hence does not alter source-linear Gate~A,
Gate~B, or the \(M_A,M_C\) connection tables;
\item \(K_7\) cancels the local septic residual
\[
R_{\loc,7}^{\Theta}
=
\alpha_{\loc}^{\Theta}I+\beta_{\loc}^{\Theta}S;
\]
\item the physical \(\Phi_K\)-readout is unchanged, so no correction is added
back into the physical hidden coordinate.
\end{enumerate}
Then necessarily
\[
\beta_{\loc}^{\Theta}=0.
\]
Consequently, on any good patch where \(\beta_{\loc}^{\Theta}\ne0\), no such
transform-faithful local normal-form correction exists.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
To cancel \(R_{\loc,7}^{\Theta}\), the correction \(K_7\) must contain the
fixed-sector component
\[
-\beta_{\loc}^{\Theta}S.
\]
But preserving the physical \(\Phi_K\)-readout without adding a correction to
the hidden coordinate requires
\[
[z^7]\Phi_K(K_7)=0.
\]
Since \(\Phi_K(S)=2\), this forces
\[
\beta_{\loc}^{\Theta}=0.
\]
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[Physical edge obstruction survives in a good-patch model]
\label{prop:theta-physical-edge-obstruction-good-patch}
There exists a homogeneous good-patch local coefficient model for which
\[
\left.
\partial_\kappa
\left(
\frac{\beta_{\loc}^{\Theta}}{c}
\right)
\right|_{\kappa=0}
\ne0.
\]
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
The edge amplitude carrier is
\[
a_1a_2(a_1+a_2).
\]
Along
\[
a_2=-a_1+\kappa
\]
one has
\[
a_1a_2(a_1+a_2)=-a_1^2\kappa+a_1\kappa^2,
\]
and hence
\[
\left.
\partial_\kappa
\bigl(a_1a_2(a_1+a_2)\bigr)
\right|_{\kappa=0}
=
-a_1^2.
\]
Since \(\beta_{\loc}^{\Theta}(0)=0\), differentiating \(1/c\) contributes
nothing at \(\kappa=0\).  Thus
\[
\left.
\partial_\kappa
\left(
\frac{\beta_{\loc}^{\Theta}}{c}
\right)
\right|_{\kappa=0}
=
-\frac{a_1^2}{c_0}B_{\loc}^{\Theta},
\]
where \(B_{\loc}^{\Theta}\) is the frozen physical edge coefficient.

Take a homogeneous source model
\[
r_i=r_j=u^2,
\qquad
q_0''=0,
\]
on a good patch with
\[
u\,q_0\,q\,Q\,c_0\ne0.
\]
The constrained off-diagonal \(\Theta_\pm\)-source curvature contributes a
nonzero fixed-sector \(S\)-coefficient.  In the top-row normalization this
has leading form
\[
B_{\off}^{\Theta,\hom}
=
\frac{u q_0^3}{5184\pi q^3Q^{14}}.
\]
The shifted diagonal term has the form
\[
B_{\diag}^{\Theta,\hom}
=
-\frac{\lambda}{2\pi Q^{12}}
\left(
\frac{q_0\alpha}{72}
+
\frac{q_0^3\beta}{864}
\right),
\qquad
\lambda=
\frac{\alpha\beta}{4\pi Q(p_1+p_2)}.
\]
Choosing
\[
\alpha=\varepsilon\alpha_0,\qquad
\beta=\varepsilon\beta_0,
\]
with \(\varepsilon\ne0\) sufficiently small gives
\[
B_{\diag}^{\Theta,\hom}=O(\varepsilon^3),
\]
while \(B_{\off}^{\Theta,\hom}\) remains nonzero.  Therefore
\[
B_{\loc}^{\Theta,\hom}
=
B_{\off}^{\Theta,\hom}
+
O(\varepsilon^3)
\ne0
\]
for sufficiently small \(\varepsilon\), and the claimed derivative is nonzero.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Status of the \(\Theta_\pm\)-normal repair]
\label{rem:status-theta-normal-repair}
A formal septic package may subtract \(R_{\loc,7}^{\Theta}\) and thereby make
the formal package horizontal.  But the physical hidden coordinate is then
\[
T^{\phys}
=
T^\star+\frac{\beta_{\loc}^{\Theta}}{c}.
\]
Thus the transform-safe physical Bottleneck~C condition is
\[
\partial_\kappa
\left(
T^\star+\frac{\beta_{\loc}^{\Theta}}{c}
\right)=0.
\]
Proposition~\ref{prop:theta-physical-edge-obstruction-good-patch} shows that
the second term is not currently zero.  Therefore local Bottleneck~C cannot be
closed by \(\Theta_\pm\)-normal coordinates or septic normal-form counterterms
alone.  The remaining local route would require a new physical edge identity
\[
\partial_\kappa(\beta_{\loc}^{\Theta}/c)=0
\]
not present in the current package calculus.
\end{remark}
```

## Insert 6 — finite-core sampled vector dependency

If the paper already has a near-zero branch, this sharper block can replace it or follow it. It records the current exact dependency, not just qualitative finite determinacy. turn59file18

```latex
\subsection{Finite-core sampled vector non-concentration}
\label{subsec:finite-core-sampled-vector-nonconcentration}

Let \(\Theta_k\) be a compact nonsingular actual-source \(k\)-core stratum.
Define the finite-determinacy vector
\[
C_{\rm fd}(\theta)
=
(c_{\core,1},c_{\core,3},\ldots,c_{\core,2R_{\Theta_k}+1})(\theta).
\]
Decompose it as
\[
C_{\rm fd}(\theta)=P_{\rm fd}(\theta)+J_{\rm fd}(\theta),
\]
where \(P_{\rm fd}\) is the pair-like or one-body finite vector and
\[
J_{\rm fd}
=
(J_1,J_3,\ldots,J_{2R_{\Theta_k}+1}),
\qquad
J_{2r+1}=[s^{2r+1}]\Phi_K(\mathcal I_{\ge2}),
\]
is the finite interaction vector.

For \(1\le N\le R_{\Theta_k}+1\), define
\[
F_N(\theta,Q)
=
c_{\core,2N-1}(\theta)
+
\sum_{j\ge1}
c_{\core,2N-1+2j}(\theta)
h_j(1^2,\ldots,N^2)Q^{-2j}.
\]
Set
\[
\Lambda(m,Q)
=
C_*
\max_{1\le N\le R_{\Theta_k}+1}
\left(
\frac{Q^{2N+2}}
{(2N-1)N!(N-1)!}
\frac{x}{B_\zeta(m)}S(m)
\right).
\]

\begin{theorem}[Sampled finite-core vector non-concentration, needed]
\label{thm:sampled-finite-core-vector-nonconcentration-needed}
For every actual zeta finite-core parameter
\[
\theta(m)\in\Theta_k,
\]
one needs the following alternative:
\[
\theta(m)\in\mathcal Z_k,
\]
or
\[
\theta(m)\in\mathcal E_{\rm geom},
\]
or
\[
\|P_{\rm fd}(\theta(m))+J_{\rm fd}(\theta(m))\|_\infty
\ge
\Lambda(m,Q).
\]
\end{theorem}

\begin{definition}[Interaction-aligned finite-core branch]
\label{def:interaction-aligned-finite-core-branch}
Define
\[
\mathcal N_k^{\rm align}(m,Q)
\]
to be the set of actual zeta finite-core parameters
\[
\theta(m)\in\Theta_k\setminus(\mathcal Z_k\cup\mathcal E_{\rm geom})
\]
such that
\[
0<
\|P_{\rm fd}(\theta(m))+J_{\rm fd}(\theta(m))\|_\infty
<
\Lambda(m,Q).
\]
Equivalently, Theorem~\ref{thm:sampled-finite-core-vector-nonconcentration-needed}
asserts
\[
\mathcal N_k^{\rm align}(m,Q)=\varnothing.
\]
\end{definition}

\begin{lemma}[Lower transfer from sampled vector non-concentration]
\label{lem:finite-core-lower-transfer-from-svnc-current}
Assume Theorem~\ref{thm:sampled-finite-core-vector-nonconcentration-needed}.
Assume also bounded-depth projective detection: for \(Q\ge Q_0(\Theta_k)\),
every \(\theta\notin\mathcal Z_k\) admits some
\(1\le N\le R_{\Theta_k}+1\) such that
\[
|F_N(\theta,Q)|
\ge
c_0\|C_{\rm fd}(\theta)\|_\infty.
\]
Then every actual zeta finite-core sample
\[
\theta(m)\notin\mathcal Z_k\cup\mathcal E_{\rm geom}
\]
has some \(1\le N\le R_{\Theta_k}+1\) satisfying
\[
|\Xi_{\core}^{(N)}(m)|
\ge
c
\frac{x}{B_\zeta(m)}S(m).
\]
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
Choose \(N\) by projective detection.  Since
\[
C_{\rm fd}=P_{\rm fd}+J_{\rm fd},
\]
Theorem~\ref{thm:sampled-finite-core-vector-nonconcentration-needed} gives
\[
|F_N(\theta(m),Q)|
\ge
c_0\Lambda(m,Q).
\]
By the definition of \(\Lambda(m,Q)\),
\[
\Lambda(m,Q)
\ge
C_*
\frac{Q^{2N+2}}
{(2N-1)N!(N-1)!}
\frac{x}{B_\zeta(m)}S(m).
\]
Substituting this into
\[
\Xi_{\core}^{(N)}(m)
=
(-1)^{N+1}
(2N-1)N!(N-1)!
Q^{-(2N+2)}
F_N(\theta(m),Q)
\]
gives the asserted lower bound.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Status of the finite-core branch]
\label{rem:status-finite-core-branch-current}
Finite odd-germ determinacy supplies qualitative detection on compact
nonsingular strata.  It does not supply the sampled vector lower bound in
Theorem~\ref{thm:sampled-finite-core-vector-nonconcentration-needed}.  The
live finite-core obstruction is calibrated interaction alignment:
\[
J_{\rm fd}(\theta(m))\approx -P_{\rm fd}(\theta(m)),
\]
making \(C_{\rm fd}=P_{\rm fd}+J_{\rm fd}\) nonzero but smaller than the
\(N\)-point scale \(\Lambda(m,Q)\), without entering any currently listed
controlled incidence stratum.
\end{remark}
```

## Insert 7 — \(dd\)-interaction / feature-balance dependency

Place in the finite-core interaction section. This is the final stabilized interaction branch from the transcript. turn59file16

```latex
\subsection{\(dd\)-interaction feature-balance obstruction}
\label{subsec:dd-interaction-feature-balance-obstruction}

In the covariance-weighted \(dd\)-interaction model, write
\[
K_{ij}^{dd}
=
(u_i-u_j)^2\langle v_i,v_j\rangle,
\qquad
v_i=v(u_i).
\]
For balanced amplitudes
\[
\sum_i a_i=0,
\]
the associated quadratic form is
\[
Q_{dd}(a)
=
2\left\langle
\sum_i a_i u_i^2v_i,\sum_j a_jv_j
\right\rangle
-
2\left|
\sum_i a_i u_iv_i
\right|^2.
\]
The second term is one-sided.  The first term has no fixed sign unless one has
feature balance:
\[
\sum_i a_iv_i=0.
\]
Ordinary amplitude balance does not imply feature balance.  Even rank-one
locking
\[
v_i=\lambda_i v_0
\]
only changes the missing condition to
\[
\sum_i a_i\lambda_i=0.
\]

\begin{definition}[\(dd\)-interaction branch]
\label{def:dd-interaction-branch-current}
The centered \(dd\)-interaction branch is
\[
\mathfrak Z_{\rm int}^{dd}
=
\left\{
\sum_\nu a_\nu K(d_\nu)
+
\sum_{i,j}a_i a_j
(u_i-u_j)^2\langle v_i,v_j\rangle
=0
\right\}
\setminus\mathcal E_{\rm geom}.
\]
\end{definition}

\begin{theorem}[Feature balance or spectral positivity, needed]
\label{thm:feature-balance-or-spectral-positivity-needed-current}
On each compact nonsingular same-scale finite-core patch away from the
controlled degeneracy set, let \(v(u)\) be the transverse \(dd\)-source feature
after same-side whitening normalization.  To close the \(dd\)-interaction
branch, one needs at least one of the following:
\begin{enumerate}
\item \emph{Feature balance:}
\[
\sum_i a_i v(u_i)=0
\]
for every admissible balanced finite-core amplitude vector
\(\sum_i a_i=0\);

\item \emph{Conditional spectral rigidity:} the reduced kernel
\[
K_{dd}(t;m)
=
t^2
\left\langle
v\!\left(m+\frac t2\right),
v\!\left(m-\frac t2\right)
\right\rangle
\]
admits, after phase rotation, a conditionally one-sided spectral
representation, or its negative;

\item \emph{Incidence containment:} all feature-balance failures and centered
kernel signature-changing loci lie in the controlled incidence set
\(\mathcal E_{\rm geom}\).
\end{enumerate}
Absent one of these inputs, the branch
\[
\mathfrak Z_{\rm int}^{dd}
\]
remains independent.
\end{theorem}
```

```latex
\begin{remark}[Current proof frontier after the local package audits]

The current proof frontier is as follows.

reflection convention.

\item The promoted quadratic mixed-block Bottleneck~C coefficient
\[
E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}}
\]
is the first unresolved local actual-source coefficient.  The quotient test is
\[
e_{A,Y}v_5-u_5f_{A,Y}=0,
\]
and the transform-safe test is
\[
f_{A,Y}=0.
\]

\item The \(\Theta_\pm\)-normal form and septic normal-form counterterms do
not close the physical local obstruction.  They can move the obstruction into
a formal package, but the physical hidden coordinate carries it back through
\[
T^{\phys}
=
T^\star+\frac{\beta_{\loc}^{\Theta}}{c}.
\]
The known good-patch models have
\[
\partial_\kappa(\beta_{\loc}^{\Theta}/c)\ne0.
\]

\item The finite-core lower-transfer branch is reduced to sampled vector
non-concentration:
\[
\mathcal N_k^{\rm align}(m,Q)=\varnothing.
\]

\item The \(dd\)-interaction branch remains independent unless feature
balance, conditional spectral positivity, or incidence containment is proved.
\end{enumerate}
\end{remark}
```

# Edit 1 — mark sampled finite-core vector non-concentration as a dependency, not a proved theorem

## Why

If the current draft has:

```latex
\begin{theorem}[Sampled finite-core vector non-concentration]
\label{thm:sampled-finite-core-vector-nonconcentration}
...
\end{theorem}
```

then it reads as proved. But the current proof state is that this is a **needed input / dependency**, not established. The attached transcript repeatedly identifies this as the missing pointwise sampled non-concentration theorem, not a consequence of finite determinacy, spacing, or Łojasiewicz volume estimates. turn61file17

## Exact edit

**Find:**

```latex
\begin{theorem}[Sampled finite-core vector non-concentration]
\label{thm:sampled-finite-core-vector-nonconcentration}
Let \(\Theta_k\) be a compact nonsingular actual-source \(k\)-core stratum.
Every actual zeta finite-core parameter
\[
\theta(m)\in\Theta_k
\]
satisfies at least one of the following:
\[
\theta(m)\in\mathcal Z_k,
\]
\[
\theta(m)\in\mathcal E_{\rm geom},
\]
or
\[
\|P_{\rm fd}(\theta(m))+J_{\rm fd}(\theta(m))\|_\infty
\ge
\Lambda(m,Q).
\]
\end{theorem}
```

**Replace with:**

```latex
\begin{hypothesis}[Sampled finite-core vector non-concentration]
\label{hyp:sampled-finite-core-vector-nonconcentration}
Let \(\Theta_k\) be a compact nonsingular actual-source \(k\)-core stratum.
Every actual zeta finite-core parameter
\[
\theta(m)\in\Theta_k
\]
satisfies at least one of the following:
\[
\theta(m)\in\mathcal Z_k,
\]
\[
\theta(m)\in\mathcal E_{\rm geom},
\]
or
\[
\|P_{\rm fd}(\theta(m))+J_{\rm fd}(\theta(m))\|_\infty
\ge
\Lambda(m,Q).
\]
\end{hypothesis}
```

If the paper does **not** define a `hypothesis` environment, use this instead:

```latex
\begin{theorem}[Sampled finite-core vector non-concentration, needed]
\label{thm:sampled-finite-core-vector-nonconcentration-needed}
...
\end{theorem}
```

but I strongly prefer the `hypothesis` version if available.

## Follow-up reference edits

Replace references to:

```latex
Theorem~\ref{thm:sampled-finite-core-vector-nonconcentration}
```

with:

```latex

```

In particular, update:


to:

```latex
such that

\ge
c_0\|C_{\rm fd}(\theta)\|_\infty.
\]
Then every actual zeta finite-core sample
\[
\theta(m)\notin\mathcal Z_k\cup\mathcal E_{\rm geom}
\]
has some \(1\le N\le R_{\Theta_k}+1\) satisfying
\[

\ge
c
\frac{x}{B_\zeta(m)}S(m).
\]
\end{lemma}
```

And update the branch definition ending from:

```latex

asserts
\[
\mathcal N_k^{\rm align}(m,Q)=\varnothing.
```

to:

```latex
asserts

\mathcal N_k^{\rm align}(m,Q)=\varnothing.
```

# Edit 3 — clarify that the \(\Theta_\pm\) no-go does not supersede the frozen \(E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}}\) table

## Why

The consolidated section now contains both:

\[
E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}}
\]

as the first unresolved frozen Bottleneck-C coefficient, and the \(\Theta_\pm\) no-go. These are compatible, but a reader may think the \(\Theta_\pm\) no-go supersedes all \(E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}}\) work. It does not. The no-go says normal-form counterterms do not physically eliminate the local obstruction. The frozen coefficient table still names the concrete local Bottleneck-C coefficient.

## Exact insertion

**Place immediately after** `\label{rem:status-theta-normal-repair}` remark, or immediately before `\subsection{Finite-core sampled vector non-concentration}` if that follows the \(\Theta_\pm\) subsection.

```latex
\begin{remark}[\(\Theta_\pm\) no-go versus the frozen Bottleneck-C coefficient]
\label{rem:theta-nogo-versus-frozen-bc-coefficient}
The no-go result for the \(\Theta_\pm\)-normal repair does not replace the
frozen coefficient
\[
E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}}.
\]
Rather, it says that normal-form coordinates or septic counterterms cannot
make the physical transform-safe Bottleneck-C obstruction disappear.  The
canonical local coefficient to compute remains
\[
E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}}
=
e_{A,Y}I+f_{A,Y}S,
\]
with quotient test
\[
e_{A,Y}v_5-u_5f_{A,Y}=0
\]
and transform-safe test
\[
f_{A,Y}=0.
\]
The \(\Theta_\pm\) audit shows that if one removes a visible septic residual
from a formal package, the same residual must be carried by the physical
hidden coordinate.  Thus it is an obstruction-isolation result, not a
replacement for the \(E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}}\) finite table.
\end{remark}
```

```latex
\begin{remark}[Current local obstruction: odd-background \(\eta\eta\) top row]
\label{rem:current-local-obstruction-etaeta-top-row}
After correcting the Bottleneck-C bookkeeping, the first local actual-source
obstruction is no longer merely an unevaluated broad finite table.  The
current leading row is the frozen odd-background \(\eta\eta\) top row
\[
\mathcal E^{2}_{\eta\eta;7,0,0}.
\]
It is governed by
\[
\Lambda^-_{2,0}
\left[
\left(
\frac{\sin\Delta_0}{s^2}
+
\frac{q_-\cos\Delta_0}{s}
\right)
\eta_i\eta_j
\right]_{7}
W_{+,0},
\]
where
\[
\Lambda^-_{2,0}
=
-\frac{1}{24\pi q^3}E_{22}.
\]
Writing
\[
\nu_{21,7}
:=
[z^7]\left[
\left(
\frac{\sin\Delta_0}{s^2}
+
\frac{q_-\cos\Delta_0}{s}
\right)
\eta_i\eta_j
\right],
\]
the top-row \(S\)-coefficient is
\[
f_{\eta\eta}^{\rm top}
=
-\frac{u}{24\pi q^3}\nu_{21,7}.
\]
Thus the local branch is now binary: either prove a zeta-specific identity
\[
\nu_{21,7}=0,
\]
or add a principled second-order phase-gap correction/counterterm cancelling
this row.  Endpoint-diagonal source realization, even if proved, removes only
endpoint-separation subchannels and does not by itself close this scalar
\(\Delta\)-Hessian \(\eta\eta\) survivor.
\end{remark}
```

# Edit 4 — insert the concrete odd-\(\eta\eta\) top-row subsection

**Where:** insert immediately after

```latex

\label{cor:first-live-t-slope-carrier-current}
...
\end{corollary}
```

and before the \(\Theta_\pm\) no-go subsection.

**Insert:**

```latex
\subsection{Concrete odd-\(\eta\eta\) top-row obstruction}
\label{subsec:concrete-odd-etaeta-top-row-obstruction}

The local package audits isolate a concrete top-row survivor inside the frozen
Bottleneck~C coefficient.  The relevant row is
\[
\mathcal E^{2}_{\eta\eta;7,0,0}
=
\tau_{h\to m}\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}
\operatorname{Sym}
\left(
\Lambda^-_{2,0}
\left[
\left(
\frac{\sin\Delta_0}{s^2}
+
\frac{q_-\cos\Delta_0}{s}
\right)
J\,\eta_i\eta_j
\right]_{7}
W_{+,0}
\right),
\]
where
\[
J=
\begin{pmatrix}
0&-1\\
1&0
\end{pmatrix}.
\]
This is the actual finite Fr\'echet source index \(a=2\), not the older
shorthand \(a\in\{1,5\}\).

The row comes from the \((2,1)\)-off-diagonal entry
\[
N_{21}
=
-\frac{\sin\Delta+q_-s\cos\Delta}{s^2}.
\]
Twice differentiating in the scalar phase-gap variable \(\Delta\) gives
\[
\partial_\Delta^2N_{21}\big|_0
=
\frac{\sin\Delta_0}{s^2}
+
\frac{q_-\cos\Delta_0}{s}.
\]
Thus the odd-background \(\eta\eta\) block is not an endpoint-separation
artifact.  It is a scalar \(\Delta\)-Hessian term.

For the active finite Fr\'echet row one has
\[
\Lambda^-_{2,0}
=
-\frac{1}{24\pi q^3}E_{22}.
\]
If
\[
W_{+,0}
=
\begin{pmatrix}
u&w\\
w&v
\end{pmatrix},
\]
then
\[
\pi_{\mathfrak f}\operatorname{Sym}
\left(
\Lambda^-_{2,0}JW_{+,0}
\right)
=
-\frac{1}{24\pi q^3}(wI+uS).
\]
Consequently, if
\[
\nu_{21,7}
:=
[z^7]\left[
\left(
\frac{\sin\Delta_0}{s^2}
+
\frac{q_-\cos\Delta_0}{s}
\right)\eta_i\eta_j
\right],
\]
then this row contributes
\[
\mathcal E^{2}_{\eta\eta;7,0,0}
=
-\frac{\nu_{21,7}}{24\pi q^3}(wI+uS),
\]
up to the harmless good-patch transport \(\tau_{h\to m}\).  In particular,
\[
f_{\eta\eta}^{\top}
=
-\frac{u}{24\pi q^3}\nu_{21,7}.
\]

Under the favorable phase-gap integral model,
\[
\nu_{21,7}
=
\frac{1}{Q^{14}}
\left[
\frac{q_0}{480}
(\rho_{i,2}\rho_{j,4}+\rho_{i,4}\rho_{j,2})
+
\frac{1}{144}
\left(
\frac{q_0''}{6}
-
\frac{2q_0^3}{3}
\right)
\rho_{i,2}\rho_{j,2}
\right].
\]
For the homogeneous source \(r(u)=u^2\), with \(q_0''=0\), this gives
\[
\nu_{21,7}
=
-\frac{q_0^3}{216Q^{14}},
\]
which is nonzero on a good phase patch.

Therefore the row is generically \(T\)-visible:
\[
\partial_\kappa T
=
-a_1^2\frac{f_{\eta\eta}^{\top}}{c}
\ne0.
\]
It is also quotient-visible on a generic \(u_5\ne0\) patch; for example, if
\(w=0\), then
\[
Q_{\eta\eta}^{\top}
=
-u_5 f_{\eta\eta}^{\top}.
\]

\begin{remark}[Endpoint cleanup does not remove this row]
Endpoint-diagonal realization, if proved, removes only endpoint-separation
subchannels such as
\[
d\eta^\Delta+\eta^\Delta d,
\qquad
\eta^\Sigma\eta^\Delta.
\]
It does not remove the scalar \(\eta\eta\) term above, since that term comes
from \(\partial_\Delta^2N_0[\eta_i,\eta_j]\).  Thus the older route
\[
[\delta^0]\eta^\Delta=0
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}}=0
\]
is no longer sufficient.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[No existing package mechanism cancels the row]
The present package mechanisms do not cancel
\(\mathcal E^{2}_{\eta\eta;7,0,0}\):
source-bidegree projection does not remove the promoted degree-three amplitude
pattern \(a_1a_2(a_1+a_2)\); amplitude normalization only rescales the row;
midpoint trivialization is invertible on a good patch; connection correction is
post-edge and cannot cancel a raw frozen coefficient; and quotienting is
insufficient because the augmented transform-safe package requires the
\(S\)-component itself to vanish.
\end{remark}

Thus the local branch is in the following binary state.  Either one proves a
new source-jet identity
\[
\nu_{21,7}=0,
\]
or one proves a full top-row \(S\)-cancellation
\[
\sum_{\mathrm{top}\ \eta\eta} f_{\eta\eta}^{\top}=0,
\]
or one adds a new second-order phase-gap correction/counterterm cancelling this
row.  Without one of these inputs, the current corrected package does not close
Bottleneck~C or the \(T\)-horizontal condition at this row.
```

This is the most important substantive insertion. It reflects the latest local-agent result: the lead obstruction is now a row-level survivor, not merely a missing table.

```latex
After extracting the frozen Bottleneck-C matrix coefficient, the remaining
amplitude derivative is the derivative of
\[
a_1a_2(a_1+a_2)
\]
in the transverse amplitude direction at the balanced point \(a_2=-a_1\).

\[
\kappa_{\amp}:=a_2+a_1,

\[
a_1a_2(a_1+a_2)
```

# Edit 10 — add finite-core dependency clarification

**Where:** immediately after the proof of

```latex
\begin{lemma}[Finite-core lower transfer from sampled vector non-concentration]
\label{lem:finite-core-lower-transfer-from-svnc-current}
```

**Insert:**

```latex
\begin{remark}[Why sampled vector non-concentration is the exact finite-core dependency]
\label{rem:why-svnc-is-exact-finite-core-dependency}
Lemma~\ref{lem:finite-core-lower-transfer-from-svnc-current} separates the
finite-core problem into a qualitative part and a sampled-size part.  The
qualitative part is finite odd-germ determinacy: on a compact nonsingular
actual-source stratum,
\[
C_{\rm fd}(\theta)=0
\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
H_{\core,\theta}\equiv0.
\]
Together with bounded-depth \(Q^{-2}\)-tail control, this gives projective
detection of every nonzero finite-core germ by some
\[
1\le N\le R_{\Theta_k}+1.
\]
What remains is the sampled finite-vector lower bound
\[
\|C_{\rm fd}(\theta(m))\|_\infty
=
\|P_{\rm fd}(\theta(m))+J_{\rm fd}(\theta(m))\|_\infty
\ge
\Lambda(m,Q)
\]
outside
\[
\mathcal Z_k\cup\mathcal E_{\rm geom}.
\]
Equivalently, the remaining finite-core branch is the interaction-aligned
small-vector branch
\[
\mathcal N_k^{\rm align}(m,Q).
\]
Thus any further finite-core proof must either prove
Hypothesis~\ref{hyp:sampled-finite-core-vector-nonconcentration}, or add an
independent theorem forcing \(P_{\rm fd}+J_{\rm fd}\)-smallness into a
controlled incidence stratum.
\end{remark}
```

# Edit 12 — add feature-balance and rank-one locking lemmas

**Where:** in `subsec:dd-interaction-feature-balance-obstruction`, after the paragraph explaining \(Q_{dd}(a)\), before `def:dd-interaction-branch-current`.

**Insert:**

```latex
\begin{lemma}[Feature balance is stronger than amplitude balance]
\label{lem:feature-balance-stronger-than-amplitude-balance}
Suppose that, for a fixed finite core,
\[
\sum_i a_i v_i=0
\]
for every balanced amplitude vector
\[
\sum_i a_i=0.
\]
Then
\[
v_1=v_2=\cdots=v_k.
\]
Thus ordinary amplitude balance implies feature balance only when the
transverse \(dd\)-features are constant on the core.
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
Take \(a=e_i-e_j\).  Then \(\sum_\ell a_\ell=0\), so feature balance gives
\(v_i-v_j=0\).  Since \(i,j\) are arbitrary, all \(v_i\) are equal.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Rank-one locking does not close feature balance]
\label{rem:rank-one-locking-does-not-close-feature-balance}
If
\[
v_i=\lambda_i v_0,
\]
then feature balance becomes
\[
\sum_i a_i\lambda_i=0.
\]
This is not implied by
\[
\sum_i a_i=0
\]
unless the weights \(\lambda_i\) are constant on the core.  Thus rank-one
transverse locking merely transfers the missing condition from the vector
features \(v_i\) to the scalar weights \(\lambda_i\).
\end{remark}
```

---

# Edit 13 — add transported-kernel Taylor obstruction

**Where:** in the same `dd`-interaction subsection, after `def:dd-interaction-branch-current` and before the needed-input remark.

**Insert:**

```latex
\begin{definition}[Transported \(dd\)-kernel Taylor coefficients]
\label{def:transported-dd-kernel-taylor}
Assume the favorable transported-feature reduction
\[
K_{dd}(t;m)
=
t^2
\left\langle
v\!\left(m+\frac t2\right),
v\!\left(m-\frac t2\right)
\right\rangle.
\]
Write
\[
v(m+h)
=
v_0+h v_1+\frac{h^2}{2}v_2+O(h^3).
\]
Then
\[
K_{dd}(t;m)
=
\kappa_2t^2+\kappa_4t^4+O(t^6),
\]
where
\[
\kappa_2=\langle v_0,v_0\rangle,
\]
and
\[
\kappa_4
=
\frac14
\left(
\langle v_0,v_2\rangle-\langle v_1,v_1\rangle
\right).
\]
\end{definition}

\begin{remark}[First Taylor obstruction to \(dd\)-kernel conditional definiteness]
\label{rem:first-taylor-obstruction-dd-conditional-definiteness}
A positive spectral representation of the form
\[
\operatorname{Re}(e^{-i\theta_0}K_{dd}(t;m))
=
\alpha(m)t^2+\int_{\mathbb R}(1-\cos(t\xi))\,d\mu_m(\xi),
\qquad
\mu_m\ge0,
\]
or its negative, imposes sign restrictions on the Taylor coefficients.  In
particular, if the phase is chosen so that
\[
\operatorname{Re}(e^{-i\theta_0}\kappa_2)>0,
\]
then the first nonquadratic coefficient must satisfy
\[
\operatorname{Re}(e^{-i\theta_0}\kappa_4)\le0.
\]
By Definition~\ref{def:transported-dd-kernel-taylor}, this requires
\[
\operatorname{Re}
\left(
e^{-i\theta_0}
\left(
\langle v_0,v_2\rangle-\langle v_1,v_1\rangle
\right)
\right)
\le0.
\]
The current one-pair incidence package does not prove this transverse
feature-curvature inequality, nor the higher moment/Hankel positivity
conditions needed for a full positive spectral representation.
\end{remark}
```

# Edit 14 — optional unit-feature no-go

If you want to include the strongest negative example from the interaction agent, add this after Edit 13.

```latex
\begin{proposition}[Unit transported feature curves need not be spectrally positive]
\label{prop:unit-feature-curve-not-spectrally-positive}
Let
\[
v(u)=(\cos\phi(u),\sin\phi(u))
\]
be a unit transported transverse feature curve, and set
\[
K_{dd}(t)=
t^2
\left\langle
v\!\left(\frac t2\right),
v\!\left(-\frac t2\right)
\right\rangle.
\]
If
\[
\phi(u)=au+bu^3,
\]
then
\[
K_{dd}(t)
=
t^2
-\frac{a^2}{2}t^4
+
\left(
\frac{a^4}{24}-\frac{ab}{4}
\right)t^6
+
O(t^8).
\]
Consequently, even unit normalization of the transverse feature curve does
not imply the coefficient signs required by a conditionally one-sided spectral
representation.  In the negative-type convention, after
\(\kappa_2>0\) and \(\kappa_4\le0\), one still needs
\[
\kappa_6
=
\frac{a^4}{24}-\frac{ab}{4}
\ge0,
\]
which fails whenever
\[
b>\frac{a^3}{6}.
\]
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Since
\[
\left\langle
v\!\left(\frac t2\right),
v\!\left(-\frac t2\right)
\right\rangle
=
\cos\left(
\phi\!\left(\frac t2\right)-\phi\!\left(-\frac t2\right)
\right),
\]
and
\[
\phi\!\left(\frac t2\right)-\phi\!\left(-\frac t2\right)
=
at+\frac b4t^3,
\]
we have
\[
K_{dd}(t)=t^2\cos\left(at+\frac b4t^3\right).
\]
Expanding the cosine through order \(t^6\) gives the stated formula.
\end{proof}
```

This is optional because it is a concrete model example; the Taylor obstruction remark is enough for the main paper if you prefer less no-go material.

---

# Edit 15 — strengthen the dd-interaction needed-input remark

**Where:** replace the current `rem:feature-balance-or-spectral-positivity-dd-needed` with:

```latex
\begin{remark}[Needed input for the \(dd\)-interaction branch]
\label{rem:feature-balance-or-spectral-positivity-dd-needed}
On each compact nonsingular same-scale finite-core patch away from the
controlled degeneracy set, let \(v(u)\) be the transverse \(dd\)-source feature
after same-side whitening normalization.  To close the \(dd\)-interaction
branch, one needs at least one of the following:
\begin{enumerate}
\item \emph{Feature balance:}
\[
\sum_i a_i v(u_i)=0
\]
for every admissible balanced finite-core amplitude vector
\[
\sum_i a_i=0.
\]
By Lemma~\ref{lem:feature-balance-stronger-than-amplitude-balance}, this is
much stronger than ordinary amplitude balance.

\item \emph{Conditional spectral rigidity:} the reduced kernel
\[
K_{dd}(t;m)
=
t^2
\left\langle
v\!\left(m+\frac t2\right),
v\!\left(m-\frac t2\right)
\right\rangle
\]
admits, after phase rotation, a conditionally one-sided spectral
representation, or its negative:
\[
\operatorname{Re}(e^{-i\theta_0}K_{dd}(t;m))
=
\alpha(m)t^2+
\int_{\mathbb R}(1-\cos(t\xi))\,d\mu_m(\xi),
\qquad
\alpha(m)\ge0,\quad \mu_m\ge0,
\]
or the negative of such a kernel.  At minimum this route requires the Taylor
coefficient sign condition of
Remark~\ref{rem:first-taylor-obstruction-dd-conditional-definiteness}.  If
Proposition~\ref{prop:unit-feature-curve-not-spectrally-positive} is included,
it shows that unit normalization of \(v(u)\) alone is insufficient.

\item \emph{Incidence containment:} all feature-balance failures and centered
kernel signature-changing loci lie in the controlled incidence set
\(\mathcal E_{\rm geom}\).
\end{enumerate}
Absent one of these inputs, the branch
\[
\mathfrak Z_{\rm int}^{dd}
\]
remains independent.  In particular, pair-like positivity of the one-body
kernel is not by itself a centered-kernel spectral theorem for the
covariance-weighted \(dd\)-interaction.
\end{remark}
```

If you skip optional Edit 14, remove the sentence referencing `prop:unit-feature-curve-not-spectrally-positive`.

# Shared background for all agents

We are resuming the RH proof attack from the latest draft and the latest local / finite-core / interaction audits. We are **not** paper-editing in this round. The goal is to prove, refute, or sharply reduce the remaining mathematical obstructions.

The working state is now much narrower than before:

\[
\boxed{
\text{The main local obstruction is the concrete odd-\(\eta\eta\) top row.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{The main finite-core obstruction is sampled vector non-concentration.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{The main interaction obstruction is \(dd\)-feature balance / spectral rigidity.}
}
\]

Do not reopen closed branches unless you find an actual contradiction in the draft.

---

## 1. Branches that should be treated as closed or paused

### 1.1 \(M_A,M_C\) connection closure

The \(M_A,M_C\) branch is closed, conditional only on the homogeneous source-grade reflection convention. The relevant monomials were

\[
M_A=\dot r_3r_2\dot r_4,
\qquad
M_C=\dot r_3\dot r_2r_4.
\]

The source-grade reflection law is

\[
\mathsf P_g\circ\mathsf S=(-1)^g\mathsf S\circ\mathsf P_g.
\]

Together with the corrected mixed-block swap identity

\[
N^{\corr}(h_-,h_+)^T=N^{\corr}(h_+,h_-),
\]

this gives the edge-refined parity

\[
\left(Y_{g,\beta}^{\langle e\rangle}\right)^T
=
(-1)^{g+e}Y_{g,\beta}^{\langle e\rangle}.
\]

Hence the pre-trivialization table closes:

\[
Z_j[M_A]=Z_j[M_C]=0,\qquad 0\le j\le7.
\]

Therefore

\[
R_7^{(A)}
+
\sum_{i=1}^{7}\omega_m(Z_{7-i}[M_A],A_i)=0,
\]

and

\[
R_7^{(C)}
+
\sum_{i=1}^{7}\omega_m(Z_{7-i}[M_C],A_i)=0.
\]

Agents should not work on \(M_A,M_C\) unless they are specifically challenging the homogeneous source-grade reflection convention.

---

### 1.2 Mixed four-point branch

The mixed four-point branch is dependency-closed. It factors through

\[
(c,u_5,v_5,\Delta_7),
\qquad
\Delta_7=u_7v_5-u_5v_7.
\]

It does **not** independently read the hidden coordinate

\[
T=\frac{v_7}{c}.
\]

For a fixed-sector residual

\[
E=eI+fS,
\]

the mixed-four-point effect is

\[
ev_5-u_5f,
\]

while the hidden-state effect is

\[
\frac{f}{c}.
\]

Thus a line shift

\[
E=\chi A_5^{\mathfrak f}
\]

is mixed-four-point invisible but can be \(\Phi_K\)-visible. Mixed four-point should not get more agents unless the quotient determinant architecture changes.

---

### 1.3 Finite odd-germ determinacy

Finite odd-germ determinacy is done on compact nonsingular actual-source \(k\)-core strata. There is a finite \(R_{\Theta_k}\) such that

\[
c_{\core,1}=\cdots=c_{\core,2R_{\Theta_k}+1}=0
\]

implies

\[
H_{\core,\theta}\equiv0.
\]

This is qualitative. It does **not** imply the calibrated \(N\)-point lower bound

\[
|\Xi_{\core}^{(N)}|
\gtrsim
\frac{x}{B_\zeta}S.
\]

Do not spend agent cycles re-proving finite determinacy. The live finite-core work is quantitative.

---

## 2. The local Bottleneck-C obstruction

The first live local actual-source / Bottleneck-C carrier is the promoted quadratic mixed-block channel

\[
Y_{12}^{(2)}=D^2N_0[\xi_1,\xi_2],
\]

coupled to one same-point linear whitening slot.

The key bookkeeping correction remains:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Use the frozen internal coefficient, not the internal \([z^7\delta^1]\) source-position coefficient.}
}
\]

The amplitude of the promoted channel is

\[
a_1a_2(a_1+a_2).
\]

On the collision chart

\[
a_2=-a_1(1+\kappa\delta),
\]

one has

\[
a_1a_2(a_1+a_2)=a_1^3\kappa\delta+O(\delta^2).
\]

So the amplitude supplies the first \(\delta\)-edge. The active coefficient is

\[
E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}}
=
\tau_{h\to m}\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}
\operatorname{Sym}
[z^7]\,
D(G_-^{-1/2})[A_-]\,
Y_{12}^{(2)}\,
R_0.
\]

Equivalently,

\[
E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}}
=
\tau_{h\to m}\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}
\operatorname{Sym}
\sum_{\chi\in\{dd,d\eta+\eta d,\eta\eta\}}
\sum_{g=4}^{7}
\sum_{r+b=7-g}
H^A_{r,0}Y^\chi_{g,0}W_{+,b}.
\]

The source-position edge

\[
[z^7\delta^1]\,
D(G_-^{-1/2})[A_-]\,
Y_{12}^{(2)}\,
R_0
\]

belongs to a later source-motion layer. It is not the first Bottleneck-C amplitude-derivative coefficient.

Write

\[
E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}}
=
e_{A,Y}I+f_{A,Y}S.
\]

The quotient test is

\[
Q_{A,Y}
=
e_{A,Y}v_5-u_5f_{A,Y}.
\]

The transform-safe / \(T\)-horizontal test is

\[
f_{A,Y}=0,
\]

because

\[
\Phi_K(E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}})=2f_{A,Y}.
\]

The corresponding hidden-state slope is

\[
\partial_\kappa T
=
-a_1^2\frac{f_{A,Y}}{c}.
\]

Thus:

\[
E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}}=0
\quad\Rightarrow\quad
\text{quotient and \(T\)-horizontal closure both hold.}
\]

\[
Q_{A,Y}=0,\quad f_{A,Y}\ne0
\quad\Rightarrow\quad
\text{quotient closure holds, but \(T\) leaks.}
\]

\[
Q_{A,Y}\ne0
\quad\Rightarrow\quad
\text{quotient Bottleneck~C fails.}
\]

---

## 3. The concrete local survivor: odd-\(\eta\eta\) top row

The latest local work sharpened the broad \(E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}}\) table to a concrete top-row obstruction:

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal E^{2}_{\eta\eta;7,0,0}.
}
\]

This row uses the actual finite Fréchet source index

\[
a=2.
\]

Older shorthand such as

\[
a\in\{1,5\}
\]

is stale. The active Bottleneck-C source-linear index set should be read as

\[
\mathcal A_{\mathrm{BC}}\subseteq\{2,3,4,5,6\},
\qquad
2\in\mathcal A_{\mathrm{BC}}.
\]

The concrete row is governed by

\[
\Lambda^-_{2,0}
\left[
\left(
\frac{\sin\Delta_0}{s^2}
+
\frac{q_-\cos\Delta_0}{s}
\right)
\eta_i\eta_j
\right]_7
W_{+,0}.
\]

The finite Fréchet coefficient is

\[
\Lambda^-_{2,0}
=
-\frac{1}{24\pi q^3}E_{22}.
\]

Define

\[
\nu_{21,7}
:=
[z^7]\left[
\left(
\frac{\sin\Delta_0}{s^2}
+
\frac{q_-\cos\Delta_0}{s}
\right)
\eta_i\eta_j
\right].
\]

Then, on a diagonal leading right-whitening patch,

\[
W_{+,0}=\operatorname{diag}(u,v),
\]

the \(S\)-coefficient of the row is

\[
f_{\eta\eta}^{\rm top}
=
-\frac{u}{24\pi q^3}\nu_{21,7}.
\]

In the favorable phase-gap integral model,

\[
\nu_{21,7}
=
\frac{1}{Q^{14}}
\left[
\frac{q_0}{480}
(\rho_{i,2}\rho_{j,4}+\rho_{i,4}\rho_{j,2})
+
\frac{1}{144}
\left(
\frac{q_0''}{6}
-
\frac{2q_0^3}{3}
\right)
\rho_{i,2}\rho_{j,2}
\right].
\]

For the homogeneous source

\[
r(u)=u^2,
\qquad
q_0''=0,
\]

this becomes

\[
\nu_{21,7}
=
-\frac{q_0^3}{216Q^{14}},
\]

which is generically nonzero on a good patch.

So the current local obstruction is no longer merely “evaluate a finite table.” The concrete row-level issue is:

\[
\boxed{
\nu_{21,7}=0?
}
\]

or, failing that,

\[
\boxed{
\sum_{\mathrm{top}\ \eta\eta}f_{\eta\eta}^{\rm top}=0?
}
\]

or a new physical correction/counterterm.

Endpoint-diagonal source realization, even if proved, only removes endpoint-separation subchannels such as

\[
d\eta^\Delta+\eta^\Delta d,
\qquad
\eta^\Sigma\eta^\Delta.
\]

It does **not** remove the scalar \(\Delta\)-Hessian \(\eta\eta\) row above.

---

## 4. \(\Theta_\pm\) normal form: no-go status

The \(\Theta_\pm\) normal form is no longer a primary repair path.

It can make the off-diagonal entries formally affine by setting

\[
\Theta_+=\sin\Delta+q_+s\cos\Delta,
\qquad
\Theta_-=\sin\Delta+q_-s\cos\Delta,
\]

so that

\[
N_{12}^{\Theta}=\frac{\Theta_+}{s^2},
\qquad
N_{21}^{\Theta}=-\frac{\Theta_-}{s^2}.
\]

But physically \(\Theta_\pm\) are constrained by \((q_-,q_+,\Delta)\), so source curvature reappears unless one subtracts it as a formal counterterm.

A formal septic package can hide the obstruction, but the physical hidden coordinate carries it back:

\[
T^{\phys}
=
T^\star+\frac{\beta_{\loc}^{\Theta}}{c}.
\]

Good-patch models show

\[
\partial_\kappa\left(\frac{\beta_{\loc}^{\Theta}}{c}\right)\ne0.
\]

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
\Theta_\pm\text{ normal coordinates / septic counterterms do not close physical Bottleneck~C.}
}
\]

Theta work should resume only if looking for a genuinely physical correction term that cancels the row without being reintroduced through \(T^{\phys}\). Otherwise, theta agents should be paused.

---

## 5. Finite-core sampled vector branch

The finite-core branch is now a pointwise sampled non-concentration problem.

Define

\[
C_{\rm fd}
=
(c_{\core,1},c_{\core,3},\ldots,c_{\core,2R_{\Theta_k}+1})
=
P_{\rm fd}+J_{\rm fd}.
\]

For \(1\le N\le R_{\Theta_k}+1\), define

\[
F_N(\theta,Q)
=
c_{\core,2N-1}(\theta)
+
\sum_{j\ge1}
c_{\core,2N-1+2j}(\theta)
h_j(1^2,\ldots,N^2)Q^{-2j}.
\]

The calibrated scale is

\[
\Lambda(m,Q)
=
C_*
\max_{1\le N\le R_{\Theta_k}+1}
\left(
\frac{Q^{2N+2}}
{(2N-1)N!(N-1)!}
\frac{x}{B_\zeta(m)}S(m)
\right).
\]

The needed pointwise non-concentration input is:

\[
\theta(m)\notin \mathcal Z_k\cup\mathcal E_{\rm geom}
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\|P_{\rm fd}(\theta(m))+J_{\rm fd}(\theta(m))\|_\infty
\ge
\Lambda(m,Q).
\]

The unresolved branch is

\[
\mathcal N_k^{\rm align}(m,Q)
=
\left\{
\theta(m)\notin\mathcal Z_k\cup\mathcal E_{\rm geom}:
0<
\|P_{\rm fd}(\theta(m))+J_{\rm fd}(\theta(m))\|_\infty
<
\Lambda(m,Q)
\right\}.
\]

This is the sharp branch. Older distance-to-\(\mathcal Z_k\) formulations, such as

\[
\mathcal N_k^{\rm geom}(m,Q),
\]

are geometric sufficient routes, not the current sharp dependency.

Finite determinacy, compactness, pairwise zero spacing, endpoint gaps, discreteness, and Remez--Łojasiewicz volume estimates do not prove sampled non-concentration. They control qualitative vanishing, boundary/collision behavior, or small-value volume. The proof requires pointwise exclusion of actual zeta samples.

---

## 6. Interaction branch: \(dd\)-feature balance / spectral rigidity

The interaction branch is no longer just “\(J_1\) uncontrolled.” It has sharpened to the \(dd\)-feature-balance / conditional-spectral problem.

In the covariance-weighted \(dd\)-interaction model,

\[
K_{ij}^{dd}
=
(u_i-u_j)^2\langle v_i,v_j\rangle.
\]

For balanced amplitudes

\[
\sum_i a_i=0,
\]

the quadratic form has the structure

\[
Q_{dd}(a)
=
2\left\langle
\sum_i a_i u_i^2v_i,\sum_j a_jv_j
\right\rangle
-
2\left|
\sum_i a_i u_iv_i
\right|^2.
\]

The second term is one-sided. The first term has no fixed sign unless one has feature balance:

\[
\sum_i a_i v_i=0.
\]

Ordinary amplitude balance does not imply feature balance. In fact, if

\[
\sum_i a_i v_i=0
\]

for every balanced amplitude vector, then the features must be constant:

\[
v_1=\cdots=v_k.
\]

Rank-one locking

\[
v_i=\lambda_i v_0
\]

does not solve the problem unless

\[
\sum_i a_i\lambda_i=0.
\]

The spectral route is also nontrivial. Under the transported-kernel form

\[
K_{dd}(t;m)
=
t^2
\left\langle
v\!\left(m+\frac t2\right),
v\!\left(m-\frac t2\right)
\right\rangle,
\]

with

\[
v(m+h)=v_0+hv_1+\frac{h^2}{2}v_2+O(h^3),
\]

one gets

\[
K_{dd}(t;m)
=
\kappa_2t^2+\kappa_4t^4+O(t^6),
\]

where

\[
\kappa_2=\langle v_0,v_0\rangle,
\]

and

\[
\kappa_4
=
\frac14
\left(
\langle v_0,v_2\rangle-\langle v_1,v_1\rangle
\right).
\]

A conditionally one-sided spectral representation imposes sign restrictions on \(\kappa_4\) and higher coefficients. Current one-pair incidence geometry does not prove these conditions.

The unresolved \(dd\)-interaction branch is:

\[
\mathfrak Z_{\rm int}^{dd}
=
\left\{
\sum_\nu a_\nu K(d_\nu)
+
\sum_{i,j}a_i a_j
(u_i-u_j)^2\langle v_i,v_j\rangle
=0
\right\}
\setminus \mathcal E_{\rm geom}.
\]

---

# RH proof attack handover — current state and next priorities

## 0. Executive summary

We are no longer in broad paper-edit or coefficient-hunting mode. The proof attempt has been narrowed to a small number of precise mathematical obstructions.

The most important current fact is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{The local Bottleneck-C obstruction has sharpened to a concrete odd-\(\eta\eta\) top row.}
}
\]

That row is

\[
\mathcal E^{2}_{\eta\eta;7,0,0},
\]

with \(S\)-coefficient

\[
f_{\eta\eta}^{\rm top}
=
-\frac{u}{24\pi q^3}\nu_{21,7}.
\]

In the favorable phase-gap integral model,

\[
\nu_{21,7}
=
\frac{1}{Q^{14}}
\left[
\frac{q_0}{480}
(\rho_{i,2}\rho_{j,4}+\rho_{i,4}\rho_{j,2})
+
\frac{1}{144}
\left(
\frac{q_0''}{6}
-
\frac{2q_0^3}{3}
\right)
\rho_{i,2}\rho_{j,2}
\right].
\]

For the homogeneous source

\[
r(u)=u^2,
\qquad
q_0''=0,
\]

this gives

\[
\nu_{21,7}
=
-\frac{q_0^3}{216Q^{14}},
\]

which is generically nonzero on a good patch. This is now the most important local obstruction. turn64file4

The current proof state is therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Local proof strategy lives or dies on cancelling this row or proving it inadmissible.}
}
\]

The finite-core and interaction branches remain important, but they are downstream unless the local package survives.

# 1. Branches that should be treated as closed

## 1.1 Gate A

Gate A is accepted as aggregate-closed under the active homogeneous scalar-grade convention.

Do not reopen Gate A unless attacking the convention itself.

Gate A closure means the leading homogeneous cubic non-\((1,1)\) sector is no longer a live obstruction. Earlier live-looking families such as

\[
L_2N_0R_1+L_1N_0R_2,
\]

and

\[
L_3N_0R_0+L_0N_0R_3
\]

are treated as aggregate fixed-sector cancellations, not termwise vanishing.

## 1.2 \(M_A,M_C\) connection closure

This branch is closed, conditional only on the source-grade reflection convention.

The residual monomials were

\[
M_A=\dot r_3r_2\dot r_4,
\qquad
M_C=\dot r_3\dot r_2r_4.
\]

The key identity is source-grade reflection:

\[
\mathsf P_g\circ\mathsf S=(-1)^g\mathsf S\circ\mathsf P_g,
\]

together with the corrected mixed-block swap identity:

\[
N^{\corr}(h_-,h_+)^T=N^{\corr}(h_+,h_-).
\]

This gives the edge-refined \(Y\)-middle parity

\[
\left(Y_{g,\beta}^{\langle e\rangle}\right)^T
=
(-1)^{g+e}Y_{g,\beta}^{\langle e\rangle}.
\]

Therefore the pre-trivialization table closes:

\[
Z_j[M_A]=Z_j[M_C]=0,
\qquad 0\le j\le7.
\]

So the connection identities

\[
R_7^{(A)}
+
\sum_{i=1}^{7}\omega_m(Z_{7-i}[M_A],A_i)=0,
\]

and

\[
R_7^{(C)}
+
\sum_{i=1}^{7}\omega_m(Z_{7-i}[M_C],A_i)=0
\]

are closed. This should not get more agent time unless the source-grade reflection convention is challenged.

## 1.3 Mixed four-point branch

The mixed four-point branch is dependency-closed.

Mixed four-point scalar exits factor through

\[
(c,u_5,v_5,\Delta_7),
\qquad
\Delta_7=u_7v_5-u_5v_7.
\]

They do not depend independently on

\[
T=\frac{v_7}{c}.
\]

For a fixed-sector residual

\[
E=eI+fS,
\]

the mixed-four-point effect is

\[
ev_5-u_5f,
\]

whereas the hidden-state / \(\Phi_K\)-visible effect is

\[
\frac{f}{c}.
\]

Thus a line shift

\[
E=\chi A_5^{\mathfrak f}
\]

is mixed-four-point invisible but can be \(\Phi_K\)-visible.

Do not assign more agents to mixed four-point unless a new formula appears that directly reads \(u_7,v_7,\Phi_K(A_7)\), or \(T\).

## 1.4 Finite odd-germ determinacy

Finite determinacy is done on compact nonsingular actual-source \(k\)-core strata.

There exists \(R_{\Theta_k}\) such that

\[
c_{\core,1}=\cdots=c_{\core,2R_{\Theta_k}+1}=0
\]

implies

\[
H_{\core,\theta}\equiv0.
\]

This is a qualitative result only. It does not imply the calibrated lower bound

\[
|\Xi_{\core}^{(N)}|
\gtrsim
\frac{x}{B_\zeta}S.
\]

Do not re-prove finite determinacy. The remaining finite-core problem is quantitative sampled non-concentration.

# 2. The corrected local Bottleneck-C bookkeeping

The first live local actual-source / Bottleneck-C carrier is the promoted quadratic mixed-block channel:

\[
Y_{12}^{(2)}=D^2N_0[\xi_1,\xi_2],
\]

coupled to one same-point linear whitening slot.

The critical bookkeeping correction is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Use the frozen internal coefficient, not the internal \([z^7\delta^1]\) source-position coefficient.}
}
\]

The promoted channel has amplitude

\[
a_1a_2(a_1+a_2).
\]

On the collision chart

\[
a_2=-a_1(1+\kappa\delta),
\]

one has

\[
a_1a_2(a_1+a_2)
=
a_1^3\kappa\delta+O(\delta^2).
\]

So the amplitude already supplies the first \(\delta\)-edge.

The active coefficient is therefore

\[
E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}}
=
\tau_{h\to m}\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}
\operatorname{Sym}
[z^7]\,
D(G_-^{-1/2})[A_-]\,
Y_{12}^{(2)}\,
R_0.
\]

Equivalently,

\[
E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}}
=
\tau_{h\to m}\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}
\operatorname{Sym}
\sum_{\chi\in\{dd,d\eta+\eta d,\eta\eta\}}
\sum_{g=4}^{7}
\sum_{r+b=7-g}
H^A_{r,0}Y^\chi_{g,0}W_{+,b}.
\]

The literal internal source-position edge

\[
[z^7\delta^1]\,
D(G_-^{-1/2})[A_-]\,
Y_{12}^{(2)}
R_0
\]

belongs to a later source-motion layer. It should not be treated as the first Bottleneck-C carrier.

Write

\[
E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}}=e_{A,Y}I+f_{A,Y}S.
\]

The quotient Bottleneck-C test is

\[
Q_{A,Y}
=
e_{A,Y}v_5-u_5f_{A,Y}.
\]

The transform-safe / \(T\)-horizontal test is

\[
f_{A,Y}=0,
\]

because

\[
\Phi_K(E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}})=2f_{A,Y}.
\]

The induced hidden-state slope is

\[
\partial_\kappa T
=
-a_1^2\frac{f_{A,Y}}{c}.
\]

Thus:

\[
E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}}=0
\Rightarrow
\text{quotient and \(T\)-horizontal closure both hold.}
\]

\[
Q_{A,Y}=0,\quad f_{A,Y}\ne0
\Rightarrow
\text{quotient closure holds, but \(T\) leaks.}
\]

\[
Q_{A,Y}\ne0
\Rightarrow
\text{quotient Bottleneck-C fails.}
\]

The row is governed by

:=

+

\eta_i\eta_j

\]

Then, on a diagonal leading right-whitening patch

\[
W_{+,0}=\operatorname{diag}(u,v),

the \(S\)-coefficient is

\[
f_{\eta\eta}^{\rm top}
=
-\frac{u}{24\pi q^3}\nu_{21,7}.
\]

In the favorable phase-gap integral model,

\[
\nu_{21,7}
=

For the homogeneous source

# 4. \(\Theta_\pm\) no-go status

The \(\Theta_\pm\) normal form is no longer a high-priority repair path.

It defines

\[
\Theta_+=\sin\Delta+q_+s\cos\Delta,
\qquad
\Theta_-=\sin\Delta+q_-s\cos\Delta,
\]

so that formally

\[
N_{12}^{\Theta}=\frac{\Theta_+}{s^2},
\qquad
N_{21}^{\Theta}=-\frac{\Theta_-}{s^2}.
\]

This makes the off-diagonal entries affine in formal \(\Theta_\pm\)-coordinates.

However, physically \(\Theta_\pm\) are constrained by \((q_-,q_+,\Delta)\). Their source curvature reappears unless one subtracts it as a formal counterterm.

A formal septic package can hide the residual, but the physical hidden coordinate carries it back:

\[
T^{\phys}
=
T^\star+\frac{\beta_{\loc}^{\Theta}}{c}.
\]

Good-patch models show

\[
\partial_\kappa
\left(
\frac{\beta_{\loc}^{\Theta}}{c}
\right)
\ne0.
\]

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
\Theta_\pm\text{ normal coordinates or septic counterterms do not close physical Bottleneck-C.}
}
\]

A theta agent should only be kept if looking for a genuinely physical correction already present in the finite-\(s\) transform. Otherwise, pause theta work.

F_N(\theta,Q)
=

+

h_j(1^2,\ldots,N^2)Q^{-2j}.

The calibrated scale is

\Lambda(m,Q)
=
C_*
\max_{1\le N\le R_{\Theta_k}+1}

{(2N-1)N!(N-1)!}
\frac{x}{B_\zeta(m)}S(m)

\theta(m)\notin \mathcal Z_k\cup\mathcal E_{\rm geom}
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\|P_{\rm fd}(\theta(m))+J_{\rm fd}(\theta(m))\|_\infty
\ge

# 6. Interaction branch: \(dd\)-feature balance / spectral rigidity

The interaction branch is no longer just “\(J_1\) is uncontrolled.” It has sharpened to feature balance and spectral positivity.

In the covariance-weighted \(dd\)-interaction model,

\[
K_{ij}^{dd}
=
(u_i-u_j)^2\langle v_i,v_j\rangle.
\]

For balanced amplitudes

\[
\sum_i a_i=0,
\]

the quadratic form has the structure

\[
Q_{dd}(a)
=
2\left\langle
\sum_i a_i u_i^2v_i,\sum_j a_jv_j
\right\rangle
-
2\left|
\sum_i a_i u_iv_i
\right|^2.
\]

The second term is one-sided. The first term has no fixed sign unless feature balance holds:

\[
\sum_i a_i v_i=0.
\]

Ordinary amplitude balance does not imply feature balance. In fact, if

\[
\sum_i a_i v_i=0
\]

for every balanced amplitude vector, then

\[
v_1=\cdots=v_k.
\]

Rank-one locking

\[
v_i=\lambda_i v_0
\]

only reduces the missing condition to

\[
\sum_i a_i\lambda_i=0.
\]

The spectral route is also nontrivial. Under the transported-kernel form

\[
K_{dd}(t;m)
=
t^2
\left\langle
v\!\left(m+\frac t2\right),
v\!\left(m-\frac t2\right)
\right\rangle,
\]

with

\[
v(m+h)
=
v_0+hv_1+\frac{h^2}{2}v_2+O(h^3),
\]

one obtains

\[
K_{dd}(t;m)=\kappa_2t^2+\kappa_4t^4+O(t^6),
\]

where

\[
\kappa_2=\langle v_0,v_0\rangle,
\]

and

\[
\kappa_4
=
\frac14
\left(
\langle v_0,v_2\rangle-\langle v_1,v_1\rangle
\right).
\]

A conditionally one-sided spectral representation imposes sign restrictions on \(\kappa_4\) and higher coefficients. Current one-pair incidence geometry does not prove these sign conditions.

The unresolved \(dd\)-interaction branch is

\[
\mathfrak Z_{\rm int}^{dd}
=
\left\{
\sum_\nu a_\nu K(d_\nu)
+
\sum_{i,j}a_i a_j
(u_i-u_j)^2\langle v_i,v_j\rangle
=0
\right\}
\setminus \mathcal E_{\rm geom}.
\]

\kappa_2,\quad \kappa_4,\quad \kappa_6
\]

for the actual \(v\). Determine whether the sign pattern required for conditional spectral positivity is forced.

---

# 8. Priority order

## Priority 1 — local row survival

\[
\mathcal E^{2}_{\eta\eta;7,0,0}
\]

This is the most important branch. If it survives, the current local package fails.

## Priority 2 — interaction rigidity

This may control both finite-core alignment and possible global escape routes.

## Priority 3 — sampled vector non-concentration

Essential globally, but less urgent if the local package fails.

## Priority 4 — theta repair

Low probability after the no-go. Keep one escape-hatch agent only.

---

# Final tactical summary

The next attack should focus on the question:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Is the concrete odd-\(\eta\eta\) top row physically cancelled?}
}
\]

If the answer is no, the current local proof strategy fails.

```latex
\begin{remark}[Current local obstruction: odd-background \(\eta\eta\) top row]
\label{rem:current-local-obstruction-etaeta-top-row}
After correcting the Bottleneck-C bookkeeping, the first local actual-source

current leading row is the frozen odd-background \(\eta\eta\) top row
\[

\]

\[
\Lambda^-_{2,0}

\left(
\frac{\sin\Delta_0}{s^2}
+
\frac{q_-\cos\Delta_0}{s}
\right)
\eta_i\eta_j
\right]_{7}
W_{+,0},

\]

\nu_{21,7}

\left(
\frac{\sin\Delta_0}{s^2}
+
\frac{q_-\cos\Delta_0}{s}
\right)
\eta_i\eta_j
\right],
\]
the top-row \(S\)-coefficient is

f_{\eta\eta}^{\rm top}

\[
\nu_{21,7}=0,
\]
or add a principled second-order phase-gap correction/counterterm cancelling
```

# Edit 4 — insert the concrete odd-\(\eta\eta\) top-row obstruction subsection

and before:

